# CLAUDE.md

Canonical project context for VihuStudio. Read this first before making any change.

## Product Vision

- Preserve what is real.
- Beautify originals rather than replacing them.
- VihuStudio is a non-destructive visual storytelling studio.

## Core Principles

- Visual controls for visual properties.
- Text controls for textual properties.
- Reusable components over one-off implementations.
- Editor UI should only contain controls that improve the active workflow.
- Metadata should not occupy permanent workspace.
- Architecture changes require explicit approval.
- Repository is the source of truth.

## Current Status

### Frozen (Version 1.0)

- Workspace
- Project Management
- Persistence
- Page Management (Sprint 8.2 drag-and-drop reorder + trimmed context menu)
- Theme Engine (Sprint 9.2 — sits atop `ThemeRegistry`, not a hardcoded array; every public method keeps its pre-9.2 signature; Sprint 9.3 adds `getActiveArtworkTheme(Id)` / `applyArtworkTheme` alongside, same signature-preservation discipline)
- Theme Registry / Theme Library (Sprint 9.2 — Theme Library Foundation: `js/themeRegistry.js` merges Official + Imported themes into one catalog behind `get(id) / list() / getCatalog()`; `.vtheme` package format — plain JSON, `{manifest, theme, assets}` — validated on import with friendly failures, never crashes; duplicate-id imports prompt Replace / Keep Both / Cancel; imported themes persist to `localStorage`, official themes ship with the app; architecture is additive-ready for Theme Creator / Theme Editor / Theme Export / Community Themes without another redesign — none of those ship in 9.2)
- Artwork Themes (Sprint 9.3 — second theme type on the same registry, `manifest.type: 'story'|'artwork'`, missing/invalid `type` normalizes to `'story'` so every pre-9.3 package keeps loading with zero migration; controls ONLY how a child's picture is presented — background / frame / paper / caption / shadow / lighting / composition — NEVER touches artwork pixels; layered into the existing Sprint 6.5/6.5.1 Picture Border system as one more `_resolveBorder` fallback layer, not a parallel rendering engine; opt-in, no default, a "None" tile clears it; five Official Artwork Themes — Museum Gallery · Sketchbook · Watercolor Portfolio · Classroom Display · Scrapbook; Theme Library shows Story Themes / Artwork Themes as two sections in the same modal)
- Dynamic Theme Workspace (Sprint 9.4 — an optional `theme.editor` block, resolved by the new `js/workspaceBuilder.js`, decides which presentational controls the right-side designer shows, in what order, per theme; editor-only — never touches rendering. Single active-workspace-theme rule, no merging: an active Artwork Theme's `editor` governs Slide/Frame/Holder if present, otherwise the Story Theme's does. Slide = Page Designer's Story tab (Decorations, theme-gated; Background/Title stay core, always shown); Frame = Card Designer's Frame Look + Frame Style groups inside the Picture section (`frameStyle`/`fill`/`border`/`radius`/`shadow`, plus new `paper`/`mat`); Holder = Card Designer's Picture/Text/Sticker sections' presentation controls (`presentation`/`artworkFrame`/`lighting`/`caption` for Image, `typography`/`alignment` for Text, `stickerShadow` for Sticker — all additive to the always-present manipulation controls). Five official themes ship an `editor` block (Storybook Classic, Comic, Museum Gallery, Sketchbook, Watercolor Portfolio); Adventure/Minimal/Classroom Display/Scrapbook have none and fall back to today's fixed control set unchanged — the real backward-compatibility proof)
- Theme Language v2 (Sprint 9.5 — new `js/themePresets.js` registry adds a Presentation Preset layer that resolves Presentation Preset → Theme Overrides → System Defaults, so a theme can name creative intent (`presentation:'gallery'`) instead of spelling out every low-level field; does not redesign Theme Registry / Theme Engine / Workspace Builder. A Story Theme opts in with an optional `slide` block (page-furniture defaults — panelStyle/footerStyle/pageNumber/bookTitle*/handle*/decorations, read by `ThemeEngine._defaultOptionsFor`) and/or an optional `holder` block (Picture Holder look defaults — cornerRadius/padding/shadow/fill, the sprint's "Frame" scope; named `holder` to match the existing `themeOptions.holder` schema and avoid colliding with the pre-existing `theme.frame` field, which is the book's outer frame COLOR, an unrelated concept). An Artwork Theme's existing `presentation` field (Sprint 9.3) now resolves through `HOLDER_PRESETS.image` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_artworkBorder`. `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s Presentation control sources its options from `ThemePresets.listHolderPresets` instead of a hardcoded list, and a theme with a `presentation` but no `editor` block gets a non-empty control list from that preset's `editorControls` metadata. Storybook Classic's `slide`/`holder` presets reproduce its pre-9.5 hardcoded values exactly (byte-identical render verified) so the app's default theme has zero regression; Museum Gallery / Sketchbook / Watercolor Portfolio are refactored to the shorthand form, Comic gets richer `slide`/`holder` presets, Classroom Display / Scrapbook are untouched — all backward compatible, no migration required)
- Museum Gallery Theme Support (Sprint 9.6 — Phase 2, Official Theme Collection kickoff. Museum Gallery is the reference implementation; the engine only grew where this one theme needed it, nothing speculative. New capabilities, all additive: (1) **Folder-based `.vtheme` packages** — `js/zipReader.js` (dependency-free ZIP reader, `DecompressionStream('deflate-raw')`) lets `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile` accept a real zipped package (manifest+theme `.vtheme`, `metadata.json`, `preview.png`/`thumbnail.png`, `layouts/` `frames/` `layer-packs/` `assets/`) alongside the untouched legacy flat-JSON path; `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` ships as a real importable package proving zero app-code changes are needed after import. (2) **Slide layout presets** — `theme.layouts` (Portrait/Landscape/Square/Wide/Quote/Full Bleed) resolves the Frame rect via `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveLayout`/`_panelRectFor`, replacing the hardcoded PANEL_X/Y/W/H; `portrait` is byte-identical to the old fixed rect so every theme without `layouts` (everything but Museum Gallery) is unaffected. `holders:1` on every preset reserves — but doesn't yet build — multi-Holder layouts (Diptych/Triptych are a deliberate future sprint, not bolted on here). (3) **Frame Variations** — `theme.frameVariations` (named artwork-field bundles: Classic White Mat, Warm Ivory, Natural Linen, Floating Frame, Black Matte, Gold Accent, Dark Gallery), chosen per-card and resolved as one more override layer on the Sprint 9.5 preset ladder; this is also where Sprint 9.4's per-card Holder controls (Presentation/Frame/Lighting/Caption/Paper/Mat), written since 9.4 but never rendered, finally activate. (4) **Holder "Original" mode** — `ImageViewEngine`'s third mode alongside Fit/Fill (natural pixel size, zoom still applies on top); a universal core control (`_setMode` in `js/cardDesigner.js`), not theme-gated. (5) **The Layer System** — `js/layerEngine.js`, a small generic engine (layer = `{type:text|sticker|decoration, target:slide|frame|holder|element, anchor, zIndex, visible, ...}`) with zero canvas code of its own (SlideRenderer supplies the draw primitives); Museum Gallery's 5-layer pack (Museum Caption, Page Number, Handle, Gallery Spotlight, Wax Seal) is the only consumer this sprint — Page Number/Handle are declarative-only entries (no `text` payload) since they keep rendering via the pre-existing `_drawHandle`/`_drawPageNumber`, never duplicated. (6) **Rich theme metadata** — optional manifest fields (`purpose`/`mood`/`bestFor`/`notRecommendedFor`/`themeIcon`/`previewImage`), shown in the Theme Library picker card when present; `ThemeRegistry.registerOfficial` copies them from an official theme's own object onto its auto-derived manifest. (7) **Global packs** — Social + Shape sticker categories added to `js/stickerLibrary.js`'s existing extensible catalog (no architecture change), and `js/emojiPicker.js` wires an insert-emoji control onto every Text Element content field via `js/pageDesigner.js`'s shared `_makeTextInput`. Every change verified byte-identical-render-safe for themes that don't opt in)
- Museum Gallery Fidelity (Sprint 9.7 — matched Museum Gallery against the approved Design Board; visual fidelity, not new functionality, extending the theme language only where the board demanded it. (1) **Frame Variations carry real values** — `matWidth`/`frameThickness`/`borderColor`/`wallTone` on each variation (not just enum lookups); `frameThickness>0` finally enables the artwork border stroke (`lineEnabled` was hardcoded off for every artwork theme through 9.6); `wallTone` is the gallery-room paint colour, a Slide-level concept distinct from the mat, resolved independently of the image-gated Picture Border pipeline (`_resolveWallTone`) so it applies even on image-less pages (Quote). Base "Classic White" values live on `js/themePresets.js`'s `gallery` preset so the variation itself can stay an empty override. (2) **Layouts are compositions, not just rects** — a layout preset's `composition` (`'below'` default, `'right'` for Wide, `'quote'` for Quote) decides where the Museum Caption sits and whether the Frame/Holder pipeline runs at all; Quote drops the Frame entirely for a centered, word-wrapped quote + attribution (`_drawQuoteText`), Wide moves the caption beside the Frame (`_captionRectFor`) instead of below it. (3) **Museum Caption composes real fields** — `slide.metadata.artworkTitle/artist/age/date`, rendered as a two-line museum label (`_drawMuseumCaption`) via the Layer Engine's `museumCaption` text source; edited through a new `museumCaption` Workspace control (Title/Artist/Age/Date, each with emoji insertion). (4) **Handle/Page Number position + colour are theme-drivable** — a Layer Pack entry's optional `position` field pins Handle/Page Number to a corner regardless of the Story Theme's own default (Museum Gallery: page number bottom-left, handle bottom-right, matching the board); a wall-tone luminance check (`_chromeTextColor`) keeps that text legible against both light and dark gallery walls without hardcoding one mood. Every change verified against a live render comparison with the board and byte-identical for themes that don't opt in)
- Theme Designer (Sprint 8.4.2 — Book Style · Branding · Typography · Colours · Picture Holder Defaults · Page Layout · Decorations · Navigation; sub-options ride on `themeOptions` and reach the renderer via `ThemeEngine.resolveTheme()`)
- Card Designer (Sprint 8.4.3 — explicit Theme → Card inheritance: header note + per-section "Theme / This Page" badge; Picture Holder · Picture · Sticker · Text · Decoration sections — every object follows the same Object Designer interaction model)
- Page Designer (📖 Story / 📘 Cover / 🪝 Hook / 🏁 End roles; per-role content editors; per-element checklist with Visibility / Lock / Reset)
- Sticker Studio (15 categories, search, favorites + recents, 241 stickers; insertions land in the Card Designer's Sticker section)
- Picture Studio (temporary preparation modal — Crop / Rotate / Flip / Auto Enhance / Fit-Fill / Reset / Before-After; bake-on-Apply through the canonical SlideRenderer path)
- Publish Studio (Sprint 9.0 — five-stage flow: 📖 Read My Story → ✨ Almost Ready → 🎯 Choose Story Destination → 📕 Publishing → 🎉 Celebration; destination-driven — Story Book (Digital / Print-ready PDF via `js/pdfWriter.js`), Story Carousel (Instagram Portrait / Square PNGs; ZIP for multi-page via `js/zipWriter.js`), Story Reel (Coming Soon, plug-in-ready via `StoryDestinations.register()`); WYSIWYE holds byte-identically between the editor canvas and Carousel Portrait PNG)
- WYSIWYE Rendering (Sprint 9.0.2 + 9.1.2 — `SlideRenderer.init(canvas, opts)` accepts `{dpr}`, defaults to `window.devicePixelRatio`; `#previewCanvas` is CSS-fluid so the display fills the preview column up to native 1080 CSS px; the editor and the published Carousel Portrait PNG are byte-identical for the same slide — `SHA-256=86e6910993d29932`; `SlideRenderer.buildPayload` stamps the *resolved* theme so Theme Designer overrides reach every render surface; hit-testing reads canonical size via `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize()`)
- Story Destinations Registry (Sprint 9.0.4 — `StoryDestinations.list / find / findFormat / register / validate` — future destinations plug in from outside `storyDestinations.js` without editing PublishStudio; documented interface contract in the module header)
- Theme Designer Global Behaviour (Sprint 9.1.3 — Theme changes propagate to every page + every thumbnail + publish output immediately; NO object selection required; `_invalidateThumbnails` clears every slide's cache, `buildPayload` uses `resolveTheme()` so Typography / Colours overrides reach the renderer through the payload)
- Publishing Language (Sprint 9.1.4 — Export terminology is removed from the editor UI entirely; `📖 Publish` is the only publishing CTA; page context menu carries the six child-friendly actions: Publish This Page · Duplicate Page · Move Page Up · Move Page Down · Add Blank Page After · Delete Page; `PublishStudio.open({slides:[oneSlide]})` accepts a single-page slice for the Publish This Page flow)
- Universal Object Consistency (Frame · Sticker · Decoration · Text-Holder · Background all share Select / Move / Resize / Rotate / Layer / Lock / Delete primitives via the `slide.metadata.elementOverrides` bag)
- Universal Object Selection (Sprint 8.4.1 — any object click switches to the Card Designer, expands the matching section, and smoothly scrolls it into view; one `SCENE_TYPE_TO_SECTION` mapping covers every selectable element type)
- Picture Holder Completion (Sprint 8.4.4 — Selection · Free Move · Free W/H Resize · Rotation · Layer · Lock · Delete on the holder; Border / Corner Radius / Shadow shared with the Picture section's Frame Look + Frame Style; the picture inside the holder remains independently editable — Zoom / Move / Replace / Fit / Fill)
- Creation Experience V1 / Child First Studio (Sprint 10.0 — a Studio UX layer only; Theme Engine / Theme Registry / Theme Builder / Theme Import / Theme Library / rendering / the Slide→Frame→Holder→Element containership are all untouched. New product model — Creation Type → Theme → Representation → Editor → Context Editing — sits in front of the existing editor: `js/creationFlow.js` is a full-screen, hardcoded 3-step wizard (Creation Type cards → compatible Theme cards → Representation cards) shown on every fresh boot (no saved session) via `js/app.js`'s session-bootstrap IIFE; restoring a saved session skips it entirely. Only Story (`storybook-classic`) and Artwork Showcase (`museum-gallery`) are real this sprint — Quote Design / Poems show a "Coming Soon" card rather than a half-working editor. A Theme with Representations (Museum Gallery: Showcase→`landscape`, Portrait→`portrait`, Quote→`quote`, mapped to its existing `theme.layouts` ids) shows Step 3; a Theme with none (Storybook Classic) skips straight to the editor. Selecting a Representation only ever writes to fields the runtime already reads — `slide.metadata.layout`, `AppState.project.artworkTheme`/`.theme` — via `PageOps.addBefore(0)` + `ThemeEngine.applyArtworkTheme`/`applyTheme`, so nothing downstream needed to change. `js/contextPanel.js` replaces the permanent tab bar + always-visible accordion sections with one selection-driven panel — CardDesigner / PageDesigner / StickerStudio / WorkspaceBuilder are mounted exactly as before (untouched internally) and keep doing all the real work; ContextPanel only (a) hides the tab bar + each section's accordion chrome via a `context-panel-mode` CSS class, and (b) toggles which existing `[data-card-section]` / tab-content is visible, driven by a small hook added to `js/app.js`'s existing `_setSelectedTextElement`/`_setSelectedSceneElement`/`showSlide`. Nothing selected shows Representation info + Change Representation + a Caption/Quote editor (Museum Gallery's existing Title/Artist/Age/Date or Quote/Attribution fields, rebuilt as simple bound inputs since the original WorkspaceBuilder-managed controls live inside a section this view doesn't reparent from) + a reused Page Background colour control + Add a Sticker (temporarily reveals the existing Sticker Studio tab). Two spec states have no independent hit-target in the current architecture and were deliberately simplified rather than requiring new hit-testing: Artwork and Frame selection show together as one "Your Picture" view (Fit/Fill/Original/Bigger↔Smaller/Move plus Frame Look/Frame Style/Frame Variation — all already inside CardDesigner's 'image' section, since Story-role pages have no SceneEngine scene element and the separate 'frame' ("Picture Holder") section only ever applies to Cover/Hook/End pages); "Replace Artwork" / "Crop / Rotate" are new, small, additive actions (`PictureStudio.open` reused as-is) since replacing an already-placed picture in place didn't exist before this sprint — uploading always created a new page. Title/Description/Metadata selection is one grouped Caption editor in the default view rather than three independently clickable canvas fields.)
- Theme Driven Representations (Sprint 10.1 / TB-4.7 — Studio no longer hardcodes any theme's Representations; `js/creationFlow.js` and `js/contextPanel.js` read them live off the active theme. A theme now carries a flat `supportedCreationTypes` array (sibling to `layouts`/`frameVariations`, e.g. Museum Gallery `['artwork']`, Storybook Classic `['story']`) deciding which Creation Types it's offered under in Step 2 — Creation Types themselves (`js/creationFlow.js`'s `CREATION_TYPES`) stay a small hardcoded list per this sprint's own scope, only theme↔type *compatibility* became data. A Creation Type with zero compatible registered themes shows "Coming Soon" immediately (no empty theme grid) instead of a fabricated placeholder theme object. Each theme's own `representations` array (Museum Gallery: Showcase/Portrait/Quote, unchanged behaviourally from 9.6/9.7's `theme.layouts` ids) is what Step 3 and "Change Representation" render — each entry's `id`/`name`/`description`/`thumbnail`/`supportedCreationTypes`/`layout`/`defaultFrame`/`defaultLayerPack`/`background`/`actions` (§8 of `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`); `actions` (`editCaption`/`editQuote`) is what `js/contextPanel.js` now checks instead of a hardcoded `layout==='quote'` test to decide which field group to show. Theme Builder gained an optional `representations/` folder (validated — duplicate ids, `layout`/`defaultFrame` reference checks — and compiled into `theme.representations`, mirroring `layouts/`/`frames/`/`layer-packs/` exactly); `js/themeEngine.js`'s zip-import path collects the same folder on import. `docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md` documents the compiled shape. Verified end-to-end including a literal "rename a Representation on the live theme object, watch Studio's UI update with zero code changes" proof — the sprint's own success metric, exercised directly.)
- Official Theme 001 — Museum Gallery (Sprint 10.2 — authoring only, no Studio/Theme Builder/Compiler/Theme Engine/Context Panel/runtime redesign. Museum Gallery is removed entirely from `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `OFFICIAL_ARTWORK_THEMES` array — it no longer exists as in-code Studio data at all — and re-authored as a real Theme Project at `theme-projects/MuseumGallery/` (manifest.json/metadata.json/theme.json + `layouts/`/`frames/`/`layer-packs/`/`representations/`, every field value transcribed unchanged from the removed in-code entry). Theme Builder loads/validates/compiles it with zero errors into `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` (replacing the older Sprint-9.6 zip-format file with the canonical flat `{manifest,theme,assets}` package — see TB-4.6/TB-4.7). Trimmed to exactly the 3 Layouts (Landscape/Portrait/Quote) the 3 Representations (Showcase/Portrait/Quote) actually use — Wide/Square/Full Bleed existed in the old in-code version but were never reachable through the Context Panel (Studio only ever initializes a page from a Representation), so they were not re-authored; no `assets/` folder, since every Frame field is an enum resolved to a drawn canvas routine, not a raster image. `theme.json`'s `supportedCreationTypes:["artwork","artwork-collection"]` — "artwork-collection" is a forward-compatible reservation with no matching Creation Type card yet (Creation Types themselves stay Studio's small hardcoded list per Sprint 10.1's own scope). Museum Gallery now reaches Studio only through the ordinary Import Theme flow (`source:'imported'`, not `'official'`) — proven end-to-end: fresh boot with nothing imported shows zero `museum-gallery` theme and "Artwork Showcase" renders Coming Soon; importing `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` makes Creation Flow Step 2/3 and Context Panel's "Change Representation" show Museum Gallery / Showcase-Portrait-Quote exactly as before, with zero Studio code changes required — the sprint's own success metric, exercised directly rather than merely claimed.)
- Studio Arrival Experience (Sprint 11.0 — implements the canonical "Studio Creation Journey V1" storyboard's first two screens; a restyle and re-flow of the Sprint 10.0/10.1 wizard, not a Workspace/Context Editing/Theme Engine/Theme Builder/Theme Registry/Publish Flow/Studio Runtime change. Three permanent canon documents were written before any code and were later corrected in place as the storyboard was clarified, rather than left stale: `docs/STUDIO_DESIGN_CANON.md` (visual/emotional identity — a fixed warm-cream/paper-white watercolor palette independent of the app's own light/dark toggle, illustration style, spacing/interaction/motion philosophy, a "never look like Canva/PowerPoint/Figma/dashboards" list), `docs/STUDIO_CREATION_JOURNEY_V1.md` (Screen 1 → Screen 2 → Workspace → Workspace Context States → Publish, each stage's purpose/entry/exit/intent/objects-shown/hidden, product behaviour only), and `docs/STUDIO_SCREEN_2_INFORMATION_ARCHITECTURE.md` (Screen 2's full IA, v1.1); `js/creationFlow.js` implements those documents rather than redefining them. Screen 1 ("Choose What To Create") shows six storyboard-worded cards — Tell a Story / Showcase My Artwork / Create Quotes / Write a Poem / Make a Greeting Card / More Ideas — in a fixed 4-column grid (4+2 wrap, not an auto-fill grid) against a full-bleed illustrated "Story Meadow" (`.creation-scene` in `index.html`: sky gradient, sun glow, paper-grain SVG noise, drifting clouds, twinkling stars, rolling hills, grass, trees, swaying flowers, flying birds, fluttering butterflies, a drifting kite, a distant castle, and a wooden signpost reading "Your adventure starts here ♥" — pure CSS/emoji, no binary assets, `aria-hidden` and `pointer-events:none`). Screen 2 ("Choose Your Creative World") is a two-column master/detail layout, not a stacked wizard: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_renderWorldScreen` builds a LEFT `.creation-flow-sources-panel` containing a **Vihu Worlds** row (official themes, horizontally scrolling with a scroll-chevron affordance) and a **World Library** row (imported themes, ending in an **Add New World** card) — World Sources only, nothing else — feeding a RIGHT **Selected World Preview** panel (large hero artwork, name, description, a "🌿 Begin With 🌿" Representation-card picker, Start Creating) as the single detail component every World — regardless of source — is read about and acted through; selecting any card from either row only ever repaints the Preview, never spawns a second picker. Add New World appears twice, both wired to the same import flow — a header-level button beside the heading, and the World Library row's own last card — reusing `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile` unchanged; a newly imported World is auto-selected and its Preview painted immediately, no restart, no reload. A Creation Type with zero compatible themes is never a dead end (closing the exact gap raised after Sprint 10.2): the Vihu Worlds row is simply omitted and the World Library row's Add New World card is always present, with the Preview showing a plain "add a world to get started" prompt instead of a separate "Coming Soon" screen — there is no such screen. The Story Meadow scene stays mounted behind Screen 2, just faded (`.creation-flow-overlay.step2 .creation-scene{opacity:.55}`; the Screen-1-only signpost hides outright there instead of lingering faintly). The Context Panel's "Change Representation" shortcut is deliberately kept on its own lightweight render path (`_renderChangeRepresentationScreen`) — Representation grid only, no World Sources panel, no Add New World — since the active World is already fixed from the editor and Sprint 10.1's exact behavior there was out of this sprint's scope. Because the overlay's own background is no longer opaque (the meadow shows through it), the app header — a sibling of `#app`, so untouched by the pre-existing `body.creation-flow-active #app{display:none}` rule — gained its own `body.creation-flow-active` hide rule; the dev build-info footer instead got a raised `z-index` so it keeps showing crisply in the corner throughout the flow, per explicit product direction to keep build info visible while still in dev mode.)
- Product Asset System (Foundation — a documentation and repository-organization sprint only; no Studio/Theme Engine/Theme Builder/runtime change. Establishes the permanent split between **Product Assets** (owned by VihuStudio, reusable across the whole product, versioned under `assets/` at the repo root) and **World Assets** (owned by an individual World, packaged only inside that World's own `.vtheme`, never stored under `assets/`) — the two must never be duplicated into each other. `assets/` gained its full permanent folder structure — `brand/`, `illustrations/{creation,source}/`, `environments/{story-meadow,open-sky,clouds,butterflies,flowers,paper-boats}/`, `ui/{buttons,cards,frames,textures,shadows}/`, `icons/{navigation,actions,status}/`, `stickers/`, `placeholders/` — every folder carrying a README (purpose/ownership/expected asset types/naming convention/example usage), which doubles as that folder's git placeholder. Five canonical docs were added: `docs/PRODUCT_ASSETS.md` (the split itself + rules), `docs/PRODUCT_ILLUSTRATIONS.md` (reserves the six Creation Type illustrations — Tell a Story/Showcase My Artwork/Create Quotes/Write a Poem/Greeting Cards/More Coming Soon — as a permanent, reused-never-regenerated family, mapped to `js/creationFlow.js`'s existing `CREATION_TYPES` ids), `docs/ENVIRONMENTS.md` (documents Story Meadow's *existing* CSS/emoji implementation's palette/lighting/composition/motion as its permanent identity, and reserves Open Sky's identity for when it's built), `docs/ASSET_GUIDELINES.md` (illustration production style — hand-painted/watercolour/storybook/paper-texture, never corporate/enterprise/dashboard/flat-SaaS — cross-referenced with `docs/STUDIO_DESIGN_CANON.md` so the two never drift apart), and `docs/WORLD_ASSET_CONTRACT.md` (reserves an `assets/{hero,thumbnail,<representation-id>}.webp` packaging convention for Worlds, explicitly reconciled against the already-shipped `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`/`docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md` contract — today's real `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png`-at-project-root mechanism is left untouched, and the gap between it and this convention's ideal is named rather than glossed over). No artwork was created; the pre-existing `assets/icons/logo.png` was left in place untouched.)
- Screen 2 — World Selection & Preview Experience (Sprint 11.1 — implements Screen 2 only; no Workspace/Context Panel/Theme Engine/Theme Builder/Compiler/Publish/Creation Flow Step 1 change. Replaces the Sprint 11.0/11.1-prior click-to-select Page Style grid (checkmarks, a "🌿 Begin With 🌿" heading, a World name/description block) with the storyboard's actual model: **the Preview IS the layout selector**. `js/creationFlow.js`'s `paintPreview` now renders a compact World-identity heading (icon + name, non-interactive) followed by `.creation-flow-carousel` — a horizontally scrollable, scroll-snap carousel with one large slide per entry in `theme.representations` (each slide showing that layout's own art/icon, name, description) — with Start Creating living directly beneath it. There is no independent selection state: a scroll listener (`requestAnimationFrame`-debounced) computes the centred slide index from `scrollLeft`, drives the dot indicator and arrow-disabled state, and Start Creating always reads whichever index is current at click time, writing that slide's `layout` to `slide.metadata.layout` exactly as before — swiping the carousel and pressing the button are the entire interaction, matching the sprint's explicit "no radio buttons, no dropdown, no second selection system" mandate. A World with zero Representations (Storybook Classic, today) still renders exactly one slide — a synthetic `{__isDefault:true}` entry standing in for the World's own single layout — so `Start Creating` always has something to act on and the carousel is never skipped; `_finish` treats that synthetic slide as "no representation" (unchanged behaviour). `_repCard` (the small click-to-select card) and `_renderChangeRepresentationScreen` (the Context Panel's "Change Representation" shortcut) are deliberately untouched — a new, separate `_carouselSlide` builder serves only the Screen 2 Preview, so Change Representation keeps its pre-11.1 click-to-select behaviour exactly as Sprint 10.1 shipped it, since that surface is out of this sprint's declared scope. World Library's heading glyph corrected to 📚 (from 📖) to match the storyboard exactly. Verified end-to-end via Playwright, including the specific case of pressing Start Creating after arrow-navigating to a non-first slide and confirming the *visible* slide's layout — not the first one — is what gets applied.)
- Official World Platform — Museum Gallery Reference Implementation (Sprint 11.2 — establishes the permanent World Platform architecture: a World is content, Studio is a runtime, and the Studio never invents content a World's package doesn't declare. Museum Gallery's Theme Project source moved from `theme-projects/MuseumGallery/` to its permanent home `official-worlds/MuseumGallery/` — the repository convention (`docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §0) every future Official World's source lives under — and was recompiled through the unmodified Theme Builder tool with zero errors, producing a byte-identical `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` to before the move, proving the relocation didn't touch a privileged pipeline because there isn't one. Screen 2's Preview carousel (Sprint 11.1) had its one remaining fabrication removed: the synthetic single-slide `{__isDefault:true}` representation invented for a World with zero `theme.representations` is gone: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `paintPreview` now renders the carousel only when the package actually declares Representations, and for a World with none (Storybook Classic, a pre-existing legacy gap never touched by this sprint) shows no carousel and an honest "This world has no page styles to preview yet" message instead — Start Creating still works, creating the page with no layout override, since that's a real, already-supported code path, not fabricated data. `docs/WORLD_ASSET_CONTRACT.md` gained a permanent Import Parity rule, quoted verbatim from this sprint's ticket: "An Official World is considered complete only when its compiled .vtheme package can be imported into a clean installation of VihuStudio and provides exactly the same creation experience as when shipped with the product" — there is no runtime distinction between an Official World and an Imported World; the package is the product. A full codebase audit (`js/`, `renderer/`) confirmed zero hardcoded World/Theme special-casing of any kind — every existing `switch`/`if` keyed on a string is a generic, theme-authorable enum (border design, paper, lighting, caption style, scene background, UI section id) that any World's package can set, never a specific World's id or name; the only "hardcoded" theme id anywhere is `storybook-classic` as the pre-existing default new-project Story Theme, an unrelated legacy concept predating and orthogonal to Artwork Theme/World identity. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: a fresh boot has zero `museum-gallery` anywhere until imported; importing `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` via Add New World renders exactly the 3 carousel slides the package declares (Showcase/Portrait/Quote, real descriptions, no `__isDefault` artifact anywhere in the DOM); the imported record's `source` is plain `'imported'` — no privileged "official" flag; and Storybook Classic's zero-representation path shows the honest empty state with Start Creating still functional.)
- World Builder Foundation — Product Reset (Sprint B1.0 — retires the old Theme Compiler dashboard entirely and replaces it with **World Builder**, a creative, visual-first application per the approved World Builder Storyboard. `tools/theme-builder/` was renamed to `tools/world-builder/` (`git mv`, history preserved); its dashboard UI (`js/app.js`, `js/router.js`, `js/ui.js`, `js/state.js`, `js/eventBus.js`, `css/theme-builder.css`) is deleted outright — not evolved, not preserved behind a flag. What survives, unchanged and audited to have zero dependency on the removed dashboard machinery, are the compile/validate engines as internal services under `tools/world-builder/js/services/` (`projectLoader.js`, `validator.js`, `builder.js`, and a trimmed `constants.js` keeping only `THEME_TYPES`/`DEFAULT_THEME_TYPE`/`LAYOUT_ASPECTS`/`LAYER_TYPES`/`LAYER_TARGETS` — the dashboard-only `PAGES`/`EVENTS`/`VALIDATION_STATES`/`BUILD_STATES` enums retired with the UI that used them); `tools/world-builder/verify/goldenBuild.js` (all 30 assertions) now drives them directly through a new, non-user-facing `services-harness.html` instead of clicking dashboard buttons, proving the retirement didn't lose the regression coverage. Four permanent Architecture Locks are established in the new `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md`: **LOCK 01** the Runtime (Studio) only ever consumes a compiled `.vtheme`, indifferent to whether it came from World Builder or a raw file (Sprint 11.2's Import Parity rule, unbroken); **LOCK 02** the Builder owns Projects (editable, Builder-owned, meaningless to Studio), the Runtime owns World Packages (immutable once built) — nothing holds both roles; **LOCK 03** a New World is born valid — the instant a creator picks a template, a complete World Project already satisfying the new `docs/WORLD_PROJECT_CONTRACT.md` is generated, no empty-project or "finish setup" state ever shown; **LOCK 04** the Builder is visual-first — no JSON editors, no folder browsers, no developer terminology surfaced anywhere in Builder UI copy. `docs/WORLD_PROJECT_CONTRACT.md` defines a **World Project** as Builder-owned data (not a filesystem folder) persisted to `localStorage` — deliberately isomorphic in shape to the existing Theme Project Contract (`README.md`/`manifest.json`/`metadata.json`/`theme.json`/`layouts/`/`representations/`/`frames/`/`layer-packs/`/`assets/`, plus a new per-project `docs/WORLD_SPEC.md` + `docs/WORLD_ASSET_SPEC.md`) so a future Build stage can feed it to the same unmodified `validator.js`/`builder.js` with no translation layer. Only two screens are implemented, both new: **Screen 1 (Welcome)** — one primary Create New World CTA, a "My World Projects" list rendering live from the new `js/projectStore.js` (localStorage-backed, same pattern as `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `_persistImported`/`_loadImported`, explicitly no GitHub/cloud sync per this sprint's own instruction), and a static, non-interactive "Explore Worlds" section (Official/Community/Templates — informational only, no behaviour behind it this sprint); **Screen 2 (Choose a Template)** — six template cards (Artwork Gallery/Storybook/Quotes/Sketchbook/Greeting Cards/Blank World) rendered from the new `js/templates.js`, where clicking a card immediately calls `WorldTemplates.generate(id)` + `ProjectStore.create()` and returns to Screen 1 with the new draft visible — no wizard, no dialog, no manual folder/JSON step. Each template's generated World Project carries real starter content matching its creative intent (e.g. Artwork Gallery: Showcase/Portrait/Quote representations mirroring Museum Gallery's own shape; Storybook: Cover/Story/Ending representations, entirely new illustrative content that does not touch the pre-existing in-code `storybook-classic` runtime theme; Blank World: zero representations, deliberately demonstrating the contract's own optionality). New `css/world-builder.css` matches the storyboard's warm/watercolor aesthetic (`docs/STUDIO_DESIGN_CANON.md` palette — cream paper, rounded cards, gold reserved for the single primary action) — no dashboard styling anywhere. Builder Workspace/Validation UI/Build UI/Publish/AI Assistance/Official World Authoring/Community Publishing are explicitly out of scope and not implemented. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: no developer terminology (JSON/manifest/schema/Validate/Build Status) appears anywhere in the rendered UI; all 6 templates generate a complete, contract-satisfying World Project (every required file present) and persist correctly to `localStorage`; `goldenBuild.js`'s pre-existing 30 assertions still pass unchanged, proving the retained services are untouched by the UI reset.)
- World Builder Workspace Foundation (Sprint B1.1 — implements the permanent Builder Workspace from the approved World Builder Storyboard: Screen 3, the home of all World editing from here on. Two Screen 1/2 refinements land first: the "My World Projects" empty state changes from an absence-framed message to "✨ Your worlds will appear here. Create your first world to begin your journey."; the project card becomes a horizontal thumbnail+name+"draft · edited Xh ago" list row wired to actually open a Project (previously inert); each of Screen 2's 6 template cards gains a short creator-facing blurb (e.g. Artwork Gallery: "Showcase paintings, drawings and photography beautifully."); and — the Template Rule — selecting a template no longer regenerates the Project and returns to Screen 1: it opens the Builder Workspace on the new Project immediately, since "the Builder edits a World Project, never a Template." The Workspace itself (`tools/world-builder/index.html`'s new `#wb-screen-workspace`, `css/world-builder.css`'s ~400 new lines, `js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s workspace half) is one screen with three permanent regions matching the storyboard exactly: a Header (World Project's own name — "Untitled World" if unrenamed, never the template name — + Draft Saved status; Preview/Settings/Save/overflow are present but inert this sprint); left Builder Navigation (Overview/Representations/Layouts/Frames/Layer Packs/Assets/Validation/Build/Publish — nine fixed items, selecting one only swaps the Context Panel, never opens a new page, exactly like Studio's own object-selection model); a center Live Preview that never disappears regardless of Navigation state — per LOCK 01 this is an illustrative mockup built from the Project's own data (icon/name/tagline/aspect-ratio/frame colour), not Studio's Runtime renderer reused inside the Builder; and one permanent right Context Panel reused by every state. New `js/projectModel.js` is the single accessor/mutator layer over a Project's file map (`manifest.json`/`metadata.json`/`theme.json`/`layouts/*.json`/`frames/*.json`/`representations/all.json`) that every Context Panel renderer reads and writes through, so the file-map shape stays a private detail; every edit calls `ProjectStore.save()` immediately (no separate save step for Project data). Three real states are implemented: **Overview** (World Name/Tagline/Description/Publisher/Version/Creation Types/Thumbnail/Hero Image — Thumbnail/Hero Image show placeholders with an inert "Change" button since Asset uploading is out of scope; all edits write through immediately and the Header's World Name updates live); **Representations** (list + "+ Add Representation," Name/Description/Default Layout/Default Frame/Layer Pack/Supported Actions — `editCaption`/`editQuote` toggle chips — for the selected one, changes repaint the Live Preview); **Layouts** (list + "+ Add Layout," Layout Name/Aspect/Holder Area [a static diagram, no functional drag this sprint]/Caption Position/Padding/Spacing/Alignment for the selected one, Aspect changes resize the Live Preview immediately). The remaining six Navigation items (Frames/Layer Packs/Assets/Validation/Build/Publish) are safely stubbed — each shows its icon, name, and "Coming in the next sprint." in the Context Panel while Navigation and the Live Preview stay fully functional, never a dead or broken nav item. `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full "The Builder Workspace" section (the three-region diagram, Navigation, the Live Preview's LOCK-01-compliant illustrative nature, and the State System's one-renderer-per-Navigation-item design) and an updated Sprint status table; `docs/WORLD_PROJECT_CONTRACT.md` gained an "Automatic World Project creation" section documenting the `WorldTemplates.generate` → `ProjectStore.create` → Workspace-opens-immediately pipeline and the Template Rule. Frame editing, Layer Pack editing, Asset uploading, the Validation engine, the Build engine, Publishing, and AI assistance are explicitly out of scope and not implemented. Verified end-to-end via Playwright (46+ assertions): empty-state copy, all 6 template descriptions present, template selection opens the Workspace directly with the real World Project name (not the template title), all 9 Navigation items present in order, Overview edits (World Name) update the Header/localStorage/manifest.json/metadata.json immediately and in sync, Representations list/select/rename/add all work and repaint the Live Preview selector, Layouts aspect/padding edits persist to the layout's own JSON and resize the Live Preview, all 6 stub states show the correct title and "Coming in the next sprint." with the Live Preview still visible, zero developer terminology anywhere in the Workspace, the Home button returns to Welcome with the renamed Project visible, clicking a Project card reopens the Workspace on that Project, a zero-Representation Project (Blank World) shows a helpful empty hint instead of crashing, and `goldenBuild.js`'s pre-existing 30 assertions still pass unchanged.)
- First Official World Platform Validation (Sprint B2.0 — completes every remaining Builder Workspace state and proves the whole pipeline end-to-end by producing Museum Gallery as the first Official World authored entirely through World Builder, with zero manual JSON/folder editing. **Frames**: full CRUD (create/duplicate/rename/delete/reorder via `ProjectModel`) plus a property editor (Thickness/Padding/Inset/Border Color/Wall Tone/Shadow/Corner Radius/Default Margin), live in the Preview. **Layer Packs**: multiple named packs (Builder-only organization — the compiled Runtime still merges every `layer-packs/*.json` file into one flat array per `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §7, unchanged), a real Default Layer Pack control writing the previously-reserved `theme.json.defaultLayerPack` field, and a per-layer editor (Type/Target/Anchor/Position/Offset X-Y/Z-Index/Text Source/visibility/lock/reorder). **Assets**: entirely generated from new `docs/WORLD_ASSET_SPEC.md` (a canonical per-slot schema — id/displayName/category/purpose/required/formats/recommendedDimensions/recommendedResolution/usedBy/previewType/validationRules) and its Builder-readable mirror `js/assetSpec.js` — seven categories (Identity required; Frames dynamic per authored Frame; Textures/Decorations/Icons/Fonts/Backgrounds optional), real file upload (`FileReader` → data URI, the same embedding convention `builder.js` already used), live completion tracking. **Validation** and **Build** now run the real, unmodified `js/services/validator.js`/`builder.js` via new `js/projectCompiler.js` — an adapter that populates the services' own global `projectLoader` singleton from an in-memory World Project (every `project.files[path]` becomes a real `Blob`), making good on the Sprint B1.0 promise that Build would need "no translation layer"; Validation reports pass/warning/error grouped by category, Build produces a genuine `{manifest,theme,assets}` package stored as `project.lastBuild`. **Publish**: Export Package and Official World both trigger a real download of exactly the Build-produced package; Community World is an honest inert placeholder. Overview gained World Id/Icon/Purpose/Mood fields and a real Creation Types toggle (all previously template-frozen or read-only), and README.md now regenerates from current Name/Tagline/Description instead of staying frozen at template-creation content; Layouts gained a Composition field (`below`/`right`/`quote`). Producing Museum Gallery for real surfaced and fixed four platform bugs, none cosmetic: Layouts were missing the required `name` field (`validator.js` rejects this, but nothing before this sprint had ever run real Validation to notice); a Frame Variation's presentation fields were flat instead of nested under `fields` per `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §6 (compiled "successfully" but the runtime's resolver would never read them correctly); renaming a World in Overview never updated `theme.json.name`, failing validation the instant a creator renamed away from the template default; and several Workspace states re-rendered by appending instead of replacing (direct self-recursive calls skipped the dispatcher's own `innerHTML` clear), causing duplicate DOM fields whose edits silently landed on the wrong Layer. All four are fixed in `templates.js`/`projectModel.js`/`worldBuilderApp.js` and documented in new canonical `docs/FIRST_OFFICIAL_WORLD_REPORT.md`, alongside every contract enhancement, capability added, and the remaining honestly-named technical debt (no `theme.editor` block authoring, no `supportedFrames`/per-Representation `supportedCreationTypes` authoring, no `category`/`tags`/`bestFor`/`notRecommendedFor` editing yet — none of which block a World from validating, building, publishing, or importing correctly). Museum Gallery's Theme Project source (`official-worlds/MuseumGallery/`) and compiled package (`themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme`) were regenerated from a mechanical dump of the Builder's own in-memory output (verified checksum-identical to a fresh Build) — the only non-UI-driven step, disclosed as such, since a browser tool has no publish backend to place a file in the repository on its own. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: all 6 starter templates still generate contract-valid projects after the schema fixes; `goldenBuild.js`'s pre-existing 30 assertions still pass unchanged; a new 23-assertion suite exercises Frames/Layer Packs/Assets/Validation/Build/Publish including real file uploads and a real triggered download; and — the sprint's own acceptance bar — importing the Builder-produced `MuseumGallery.vtheme` into a clean Runtime shows zero `museum-gallery` anywhere before import, registers it immediately after with `source:'imported'` (no privileged flag), is discovered on Creation Flow Screen 2 with zero Runtime code changes, renders a Preview carousel of exactly the 3 authored Representations, resolves all 7 Frame Variations/5 Layer Pack entries/3 Representations through `ThemeEngine.getTheme()`, applies the correct authored Layout on Start Creating, and reaches `PublishStudio.open` through the ordinary Publish path with no special case.)
- Builder Stabilization (Sprint B2.0.1 — usability-only fixes to the now-frozen Builder from Sprint B2.0; explicitly no new screens, no new Workspace states, no architecture change, no Museum Gallery special-casing. **Toolbar**: Preview/Settings/Save/three-dot menu were all present but non-functional — Preview now packages the current Project through `builder.js`'s own `packageTheme()`/`buildManifest()`/`buildTheme()` (bare global identifiers, since `services/builder.js` exports only a lexical `const builder`, not `window.builder` — the same classic-script gotcha rediscovered from Sprint B1.0) and renders it in a real modal via the actual `renderer/slideRenderer.js` `SlideRenderer.init()`/`.render()` — the same engine Runtime uses, fed a synthetic slide object directly rather than going through `ThemeEngine` (already `typeof`-guarded for exactly this); Settings jumps to Overview; Save performs a real `ProjectStore.save()` with visible "✓ Saved" feedback; the three-dot menu's Duplicate/Delete call real, new `ProjectStore.duplicate()`/`ProjectStore.remove()` functions. **Overview representation-selection bug fixed**: Overview's Live Preview never actually read `currentRepresentationId` (Sprint B1.1's `AAF_STATES` set only covered Representations/Layouts/Frames), so clicking a Representation chip in Overview silently did nothing to the Preview despite correctly updating the shared state and re-highlighting the chip; fixed with one new predicate, `_showsRepresentationPreview()`, extending Preview rendering to Overview when Representations exist — no second selection variable introduced, per the ticket's explicit "do not duplicate selection logic" instruction. **Assets page**: every slot row now shows Purpose/Recommended Dimensions/Aspect Ratio/Recommended Formats/Maximum File Size, all read directly off `assetSpec.js` slot objects (`js/assetSpec.js` gained `aspectRatio`/`maxFileSizeMB` on every slot, mirrored into `docs/WORLD_ASSET_SPEC.md`'s per-slot schema) — zero values duplicated into the UI layer. **Builder guidance**: every one of the 9 Workspace states now opens with a concise "What is this? Why is it needed? What should I do here? What happens next?" intro box (`_stateIntro`), and advanced fields (Anchor, Z-Index, Default Frame, Layout, Representation, Layer Target, Aspect, Composition) gained one-line inline help text. **Validation UX**: error/warning rows now include a "Why" explanation and, where the failure is structurally attributable (unknown Layout/Frame reference, missing required field, duplicate id, missing folder/asset), a "→ Fix Now" button that navigates straight into the offending Workspace state — matching the ticket's literal before/after example. **Build UX**: a successful Build now shows "✓ World Package Built" with Package Name/Package Size/Build Timestamp and a "Continue to Publish →" action. **Publish rework**: "Official World" (previously identical to Export Package) is renamed "Publish to Official Themes" and now does something functionally distinct — it operates only on `project.lastBuild` (never `project.files`, preserving the Builder-owns-Projects/Runtime-owns-Packages split) and calls the real, unmodified `window.ThemeRegistry.importPackage(pkg, {onDuplicate:'replace'})`, loaded into the Builder's own page; because World Builder and the main app share an origin, this writes to the exact `localStorage` key the main app already reads at boot, giving genuine automatic Runtime discovery and version-replacement with zero Runtime code changes and zero duplicated import logic — the same honest same-origin-localStorage reasoning `FIRST_OFFICIAL_WORLD_REPORT.md` disclosed as the real constraint of a client-side tool with no literal filesystem access to `official-worlds/`/`themes/`; Export Package is unchanged, Community World remains Coming Soon. `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained sections documenting all three toolbar/publish/selection mechanisms. Verified via a new 39-assertion Playwright suite plus full regression (`verify_b20.js` 23/23 after updating one stale assertion for the intentional Publish rename, `verify_all_templates.js` all 6 templates clean, `goldenBuild.js` 30/30, `verify_runtime_parity.js` all 8 phases) and 3 screenshots (Preview modal, Overview with an active Representation preview, Assets spec grid) — zero dead buttons/thumbnails/ambiguous controls remain in the Builder Workspace.)
- Museum Gallery Authoring Feedback (Sprint B2.0.2 — usability fixes drawn from real-world feedback authoring the first Official World through the Builder; no new screens/states, no architecture change, no Museum Gallery special-casing. **Overview**: World Id is now read-only (`_readOnlyField` — auto-generated once at Project creation via `templates.js`'s `_slug(name) + '-' + _uid()`, never editable again, so nothing that already references it can break); the free-text Icon field is removed outright rather than reinterpreted (a future Icon, if any, comes from Category or an uploaded Asset, never free text). **Representations**: the Layer Pack field's help text now explains *why* every new World starts with a Layer Pack named "Basic" instead of only naming what a Layer Pack is. **Layouts**: gained a "Current Representation" banner reusing the existing shared `currentRepresentationId` (no new selection model) since a Layout is shared/reusable across Representations and creators had no way to know whose context they were editing in — deliberately not a stricter ownership model, since that question (see A-005 below) isn't settled yet. **Center Preview**: the Preview modal's synthetic slide was silently resolving to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s own Story-runtime fallbacks — an empty `handle` string falls through to the renderer's hardcoded `'@vihuplanet'` placeholder branding text (`_drawHandle`), and a null `themeOptions` resolved to `FALLBACK_OPTIONS` (`bookTitleVisibility:'show'`, `pageNumber:'bottom-right'`), so every World's Preview showed a stray `@vihuplanet` watermark, a footer named after the World itself masquerading as a book title, and an unrelated page number — three pieces of invented Story-runtime furniture that don't belong to the World being authored. Fixed by passing an explicit `themeOptions` object with `bookTitleVisibility:'hide'`/`pageNumber:'hidden'`/`handleVisibility:'hide'`, so Preview shows only what the World itself defines (Frame/Layout/Layer Pack) — a genuinely generic sample page. The modal's CSS was also restructured (new `.wb-preview-canvas-wrap` flex child, `.wb-preview-modal-box` at a fixed `88vh`) so the canvas always scales to fit the viewport with `overflow:hidden` guaranteeing no scrollbar ever appears, on any screen height. Two authoring findings are recorded as deliberately open in `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md` rather than resolved on one data point: **A-005** (should Layout become owned by a single Representation, or stay independent/reusable as today) and **A-006** (should "Portrait," currently a Representation, instead be modeled as a Layout) — both need more Official Worlds authored before deciding. A future **Visual Theme Composer** (interactive page anatomy, click-to-edit page layers) is noted as an explicit non-goal for any B2.x sprint. Verified via a new 15-assertion Playwright suite plus full regression (`verify_b201.js` 39/39, `verify_b20.js` 23/23, all 6 templates clean, `goldenBuild.js` 30/30, `verify_runtime_parity.js` all 8 phases).)
- Working View + Runtime Preview (Sprint B2.0.3 — transforms the Builder from a configuration tool into a true visual authoring tool; no new Builder screens, no Runtime/World contract changes, Museum Gallery authoring stays paused. Replaces the illustrative DOM-mockup Live Preview and the Sprint B2.0.1 on-demand Preview modal/button with two permanently-visible surfaces sharing the exact same `SlideRenderer.render()` call (never a second, Builder-owned rendering implementation): **Working View** (center, context-aware — the real render plus Builder-only guide overlays, Overview's own identity card the sole exception since World identity isn't a rendered page) and **Runtime Preview** (top of the right column, always clean, answering "what will the reader see?"). Making every edit re-render with no Save/Build/Validate step required a new lightweight, synchronous live-theme resolver — `_collectFolderLight`/`_buildLiveManifest`/`_buildLiveTheme` in `worldBuilderApp.js` — mirroring `builder.js`'s own `collectFolder()`/`buildManifest()`/`buildTheme()` merge rules exactly but reading `project.files` directly instead of round-tripping through the Blob/FileReader-based `ProjectCompiler` pipeline Validate/Build still correctly use for their one-shot compile. A cached generic Sample Artwork image plus generic sample metadata (title/artist/age/date/caption/quote/attribution) now feed every render, so editing always has something to show. **Layout Live Reflection**: Composition/Caption Position/Padding/Spacing/Alignment all now visibly update — Composition (a real Runtime contract field) genuinely changes both surfaces; Caption Position/Padding/Alignment (fields the Runtime never actually reads — a real gap this sprint's authoring surfaced, not a Working View bug) drive new Working-View-only guide overlays (Holder Boundary, Caption Area, Safe Margin, Padding inset, Alignment line, a caption-position-aware sample caption placeholder) honestly distinct from Runtime Preview's unchanged output. **Layout Guidance**: Aspect and Composition now auto-sync (Aspect=Quote forces and locks Composition=Quote; leaving Quote resets it) so the old "Must be Quote..." warning about a reachable invalid state was deleted rather than reworded — the combination is simply unreachable now. **Layout Library** gained "Used By," listing every Representation pointing at each Layout. New `docs/AUTHORING_FINDINGS.md` splits what real authoring surfaces into Builder Issues (fixed this sprint) and Future Product Insights (documented only, not implemented) — most notably that Layout's Padding/Spacing/Alignment/Caption Position have no Runtime effect today, and that Composition's "Below" vs "Right" only visibly differ once a caption-drawing Layer actually exists (every template ships an empty default Layer Pack). Verified via a new 35-assertion Playwright suite plus full regression across every prior sprint's suite (`verify_b201.js` 39/39 after 2 assertions updated for the removed modal, `verify_b20.js` 23/23 after 1 assertion updated for the real-canvas Working View, `verify_b202.js` 12/12 after 2 sections updated for the same, all 6 templates clean, `goldenBuild.js` 30/30, `verify_runtime_parity.js` all 8 phases) — Museum Gallery authoring intentionally not restarted, per this sprint's own closing instruction.)
- Workspace Ergonomics (Sprint B2.0.4 — layout-only sprint: no Builder logic, rendering logic, contracts, Project model, Runtime, Validation, Build, or Publish changes. Real authoring under Sprint B2.0.3 immediately exposed the problem: Runtime Preview shared a column with the Inspector, so as more Builder options were added the Inspector — where a creator actually spends their editing time — became cramped and required excessive scrolling. `.wb-workspace-body` becomes one CSS Grid (`nav`/`working`/`runtime`/`inspector` named areas) instead of nested flex columns: Navigation spans both rows (fixed, never scrolls); the top row splits Working View (center) and Runtime Preview (right, its own grid cell now instead of sharing one with the Inspector below it); the bottom row is the Inspector alone, spanning the full width beneath both — substantially more usable space than the old ~340px shared column, and now the only region of the Workspace allowed to scroll at all. Working View and Runtime Preview switch their canvases from width-first to height-first fitting (`height:100%; max-width:100%; aspect-ratio:...`, the same fit-to-viewport technique the Sprint B2.0.2 Preview modal used) so neither ever scrolls now that each is a fixed percentage of the Workspace's height rather than sized to its own content; this surfaced a guide-label clipping bug (Sprint B2.0.3's guide labels floated above their box, fine when Working View owned a whole column's height, clipped once it didn't) fixed by moving every label inside its box's own edge instead. A new `_fieldRow()`/`_buildFieldGroup()` pair finally wires up the previously-unused Sprint B1.1 `.wb-field-row` CSS class to pair short, related fields side by side: Layouts (Aspect|Composition, Padding|Spacing, Caption Position|Alignment), Frames (Thickness|Padding, Inset|Corner Radius, Border Color|Wall Tone, Shadow|Default Margin), Representations (Default Layout|Default Frame), Overview (Publisher|Version, Purpose|Mood). `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained "The Workspace is one CSS Grid" documenting the mechanics; `docs/AUTHORING_FINDINGS.md` gained a Sprint B2.0.4 Builder Issues section. Verified via a new 25-assertion Playwright suite (grid geometry, no-scroll assertions on Working View/Runtime Preview, guide-label-not-clipped, every field pairing present, end-to-end edit still updates both surfaces) plus full regression across every prior sprint's suite, all passing unchanged.)
- Builder Workspace Polish (Sprint B2.0.5 — visual-polish sprint on top of Sprint B2.0.4's grid: no new screens, no Workspace states, no architecture, contract, or rendering-pipeline change; Header/Navigation/Working View/Runtime Preview/Inspector regions stay frozen in position and role. Fixes two real, measured CSS defects rather than merely retuning numbers: (1) the `#wb-root` ancestor-padding bug — `#wb-root`'s `max-width:1080px; margin:0 auto; padding:48px 32px 96px;`, meant only for Screens 1–2's reading-column layout, was inherited by the always-`100vh` Workspace too, whose viewport-relative height doesn't shrink for an ancestor's padding — so the Workspace's true footprint overflowed the viewport by exactly that padding while also losing width; the single largest contributor to "excessive whitespace." Fixed by moving that padding/max-width onto `.wb-screen-welcome, .wb-screen-templates` specifically, leaving `#wb-root` as bare `min-height:100%` — the Workspace now measures exactly the full viewport rect. (2) A `flex:1` + `aspect-ratio` + `max-width:100%`-on-one-element distortion bug in Working View's and Runtime Preview's canvas wraps — flex-grow resolves a definite height before `max-width` later clamps width, and the browser never retroactively shrinks the already-resolved height to match, producing real, measured stretching (Runtime Preview's canvas measured ratio 1.573 against a correct 1.25). Fixed with the same outer-sizing/inner-aspect-locked two-layer split the Sprint B2.0.2 Preview modal already used: a new `.wb-working-canvas-inner`/`.wb-runtime-preview-canvas-inner` element alone carries `aspect-ratio`+`max-width`+`max-height`, wrapped inside the pre-existing plain-flex outer wrap; `index.html` gained the matching wrapper `<div>`s, canvas element ids unchanged so no JS changed. `.wb-workspace-body`'s grid moved from Sprint B2.0.4's split to explicit `170px 1fr 380px` columns / `64% 36%` rows — Navigation shrinks to only what icon+label+comfortable padding need, and the reclaimed width/height goes to Working View and Runtime Preview per the ticket's explicit P0 priority (not split evenly); Inspector's row-height share shrank in the trade but its architecture — full-width, beneath both, independently scrollable — is unchanged and it remains fully usable since it was already the one region allowed to scroll. Padding/gap tightened by a few px throughout Nav/Working View/Runtime Preview/Inspector as the "reduce gutters" P0 item; no component was stretched to fill space — Working View's own column is now the widest, most prominent region on screen (satisfying "largest visual region"), while the empty margin around its smaller portrait-oriented page is the same relationship Figma's canvas has to a smaller artboard, not a defect, since stretching or cropping to eliminate it is explicitly prohibited. Adds basic Draft Management to the Welcome screen (the sprint's other P1 requirement): every project card gains Rename/Duplicate/Delete controls, each reusing an existing, already-real function rather than new persistence — `ProjectModel.setIdentity(project, {name})` (the same call Overview's own World Name field already makes) for Rename, `ProjectStore.duplicate()`/`ProjectStore.remove()` (shipped in Sprint B2.0.1 for the Workspace header's overflow menu, never exposed here before) for Duplicate/Delete, `window.prompt()`/`window.confirm()` matching the header's own existing Delete confirmation pattern; Delete is architecturally incapable of touching a published Official Theme or exported `.vtheme` since `ProjectStore`'s `localStorage` key is a wholly separate persistence layer from `ThemeRegistry`'s imported-themes key or the `official-worlds/`/`themes/` folders — never wired together, so the ticket's "must never be deleted automatically" constraint holds by construction. The project card changed from a `<button>` to a `role="button"` `<div>` with its own `keydown` handler (Enter/Space), since a native button cannot legally contain the three new nested action buttons — the same pattern already used for Frame/Layout list rows, whose own controls likewise call `e.stopPropagation()`. Widening the card grid's `minmax()` floor from 220px to 320px was a companion fix, not a stylistic choice: the original value had no button-shaped content to make room for, and once Draft Management's controls were added the name column visibly collapsed and overlapped them — verified via before/after screenshot. `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a "Workspace Polish" section documenting both CSS bugs and the space reallocation; `docs/AUTHORING_FINDINGS.md` gained a Sprint B2.0.5 Builder Issues section. Verified via a new 20-assertion Playwright suite — edge-to-edge Workspace geometry, both canvases holding exact 1080:1350 ratio at their new larger sizes, reduced Nav width, and full Rename/Duplicate/Delete/no-accidental-open coverage — plus full regression across every prior sprint's suite and `goldenBuild.js`, all passing unchanged.)
- Builder Workspace Maturity (Sprint B2.0.6 — the Workspace's final maturity pass before it freezes: no new screens, no new Workspace states, no architecture/contract/rendering-pipeline change; Header/Navigation/Working View/Runtime Preview/Inspector regions stay exactly where Sprint B2.0.4/B2.0.5 put them. **Property Editor grouping**: every state's field order was re-paired into a genuine property grid using the existing `_fieldRow()`/`_buildFieldGroup()` machinery — Overview (World Name|Tagline, Publisher|Version, Purpose|Mood, Thumbnail|Hero Image as upload cards, Description last since it's the only multiline field), Representations (Name|Default Layout, Default Frame|Layer Pack, Supported Actions, Description), Layouts (Layout Name|Aspect, Composition|Caption Position, Padding|Spacing, Alignment|Used By — "Used By" is a new compact readout surfacing the same Layout-reuse data the list above already showed per row), Frames (Frame Name|Wall Tone, Border|Corner Radius, Shadow|Inset, Padding|Margin, Thickness alone, Description last), and the Layer Packs Selected Layer form (Type|Target Container, Anchor|Position, Offset X|Offset Y — Visibility/Lock were already inline icon buttons on each Layer List row, not stacked fields). The ticket's own illustrative Overview example named a "Category | Visibility" pair that doesn't exist anywhere in the World Project Contract or `ProjectModel`; rather than fabricate two new unused fields to match it, Overview's real pairing uses only fields Validation/Build/Runtime already read — a deliberate, disclosed judgment call, not an oversight. **Assets** moved from stacked full-width rows to a real `.wb-asset-card-grid` (`_assetSlotRow` rebuilt from a horizontal row into a vertical card); **Build**'s two info boxes and **Publish**'s three options both moved from stacked elements to compact card grids via a new shared `_statCardGrid()`/`.wb-publish-grid`. **Builder Information Density**: the Sprint B2.0.1 What/Why/Do/Next guidance block is now a native `<details>`/`<summary>` (`_stateIntro()`), collapsed by default, one click away — no JS toggle logic needed; short single-purpose status banners ("Previewing:", "Current Representation:") moved to a separate always-visible `.wb-info-banner` class so they're never mistaken for collapsible guidance. **Editing Confidence**: the static "Draft Saved" label is replaced by a real 🟠 Unsaved Changes / 🟢 All Changes Saved indicator (`_setSaveState()`); the underlying `ProjectStore.save()` write stays synchronous and immediate inside `_persist()` (never debounced, so navigating away right after an edit can never lose it) — only the *visible* return to "saved" debounces 600ms, so continuous typing shows one steady "Unsaved Changes" instead of flickering every keystroke; a synchronous save has no real "Saving…" moment to show, so that sub-state was deliberately not fabricated. The Header Save button gained a `wb-save-btn-dirty` ring so the button itself communicates state, not just the badge. **Workspace Customisation**: three new sash-style resize handles (`#wb-resize-nav`/`#wb-resize-runtime`/`#wb-resize-inspector`) are real CSS Grid tracks (`.wb-workspace-body` gained `navsash`/`rtsash`/`tbsash` — same nav/working/runtime/inspector region names, now with sash tracks threaded through), so a handle can never drift out of sync with the boundary it drags; each writes exactly one CSS custom property (`--wb-nav-w` clamped [180,280]px, `--wb-runtime-w` clamped to [25%,65%] of the combined Working+Runtime width, `--wb-inspector-h` clamped to [220px, 65vh]) via one shared `_wireResizeHandle()` mouse-drag driver. The chosen sizes persist to one Builder-wide `localStorage` key (`vihustudio.worldBuilder.workspaceLayout` — deliberately a creator preference, not per-Project World data) and reapply automatically via `_applyWorkspaceLayout()` every time a Workspace opens; a new "Reset Workspace Layout" item in the header's three-dot menu clears that key and restores the shipped defaults with no reload. `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full "Property Editor grouping, Editing Confidence, and Workspace Customisation" section; `docs/AUTHORING_FINDINGS.md` gained a Sprint B2.0.6 section recording both the synchronous-save/no-fake-"Saving"-state decision and the not-fabricating-Category/Visibility decision as Builder Issues, plus an open Future Product Insight on whether workspace layout should ever become per-Project. Verified via a new 34-assertion Playwright suite (every field pairing, the collapsed/expandable guidance panel, the full dirty→saved cycle including a `localStorage` check proving the debounce never risks data loss, all three resize handles' drag direction/clamping/cross-reopen persistence, Reset Workspace Layout, the Assets/Build/Publish grids, and that Sprint B2.0.5's Draft Management is unaffected) plus full regression across every prior sprint's suite and `goldenBuild.js`, all passing unchanged.)
- Builder V2 — Slice 1: Global Navigation, Scenes Library, Scene Configuration (implements `docs/BUILDER_V2_VISION.md` — the first vertical slice of `tools/world-builder`'s reset onto Engine V2's object model per `docs/ENGINE_V2_CANON.md`/`docs/BUILDER_V2_BLUEPRINT.md`/`docs/BUILDER_V2_UX_PACKAGE.md`; not a redesign, an implementation of documents already frozen. **Global Navigation** moves to a real top bar (`#wb-global-nav`, World/Scenes/Validation/Build/Publish) structurally outside the workspace grid, replacing the old left Builder Navigation sidebar (Overview/Representations/Layouts/Frames/Layer Packs/Assets/Validation/Build/Publish) — the corresponding CSS Grid nav column/sash retired along with it (`.wb-workspace-body` is now a 2-column grid, Working View + Runtime Preview, with only the Runtime and Inspector sashes remaining). "Overview" is renamed "World" (label only, Vision §1 — same fields, same screen). **New Engine V2 data model**: `js/services/engineSchema.js` defines the fixed Aspect Ratio vocabulary (portrait/landscape/square/wide/full-bleed/quote, each with a derived pixel Size and a Safe Area label — Blueprint §7's "Size is derived, never typed") and the 7 Engine Scene Templates (Single Holder/Dual Holder/Quote/Cover/Timeline/Comic/Gallery, Engine Canon §10) with their starting fractional Holder layouts; `js/projectModel.js` gained full Scene CRUD (`scenes`/`findScene`/`addScene`/`renameScene`/`duplicateScene`/`deleteScene`/`moveScene`/`setSceneAspect`) storing each Scene at `scenes/<id>.json` with a `sceneOrder` array, mirroring the existing Frame-ordering pattern. **Scenes — the Library** (Blueprint §5): a real grid of Scene cards (thumbnail, name, Rename/Duplicate/Delete) plus an Add-a-Scene card opening the Engine Scene Template picker — a Scene is never created from a blank Canvas (Engine Invariant 4). **The Scene Editor**: a new Scene Header strip (`#wb-scene-header`, hidden except while a Scene is open) shows the breadcrumb and a Scene Configuration glance (📄 Aspect · 📐 Safe Area · 📦 pixel Size, the Vision §2 worked example verbatim); clicking the glance selects Scene Configuration the same way any object is selected (Vision §2) and populates Context Inspector with an Aspect Ratio picker — Working View does not switch activity for this, since Scene Configuration has no page object to draw guides around. The three Creative Activities (Place/Decorations/Text, Vision §3) appear as a real switcher beneath Working View; Place/Decorations/Text themselves are an honest "Coming in the next sprint" stub this slice (matching the Builder's own established stub precedent, Sprint B1.1) since Blueprint §8-§10 are a following slice's scope. Working View and Runtime Preview for a Scene are a small, self-contained canvas draw routine (`_drawSceneCanvas`) — generic Holder placeholder chrome plus, in Working View only, a felt Safe Area guide — deliberately **not** routed through `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, because no Engine V2 render pipeline exists for Scene/Canvas/Holder/Layer/Element in any frozen document; reusing the Engine V1 renderer for a shape it has no concept of would have been exactly the kind of silent architecture workaround this phase's brief prohibits. **A genuine, disclosed architectural gap, not silently bridged**: Validation/Build/Publish (`js/services/validator.js`/`builder.js`, `js/projectCompiler.js`) are completely unchanged this slice and still compile only `representations/`/`layouts/`/`frames/`/`layer-packs/` — Scenes are new, additive authoring data with no compiled-package representation yet, because Engine V2 Canon defines an object model with no corresponding Engine V2 `.vtheme` format or Runtime support in any canon document. Every World template except Blank World now also seeds exactly one starter Scene (Blank World seeds none, matching its own "no assumptions" intent and exercising Blueprint §5's zero-Scene empty state). Representations/Layouts/Frames/Layer Packs' render functions are retained in `worldBuilderApp.js`, deliberately unreachable rather than deleted — Frame selection returns inside the Place activity per Blueprint §8 once that activity is built, and that logic will be needed again shortly. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: create World → Scenes shows the seeded starter Scene → open it → Scene Header glance shows Portrait/Instagram Safe Area/1080×1350 → selecting it populates Context Inspector with Aspect Ratio → changing to Landscape live-updates the glance, the Working View canvas, and the Runtime Preview canvas to 1350×1080 → the activity switcher shows the honest Coming-in-the-next-sprint stub → "back to Scenes" returns to the Library → Add a Scene opens the 7-template picker and opens the new Scene → World/Validation/Build/Publish remain fully reachable and functionally unchanged from before this slice, with zero console errors throughout.)
- Builder V2 — Slice 2: Place activity, real Holder authoring (implements Blueprint §8, the second vertical slice of the Builder V2 reset — Place is no longer a stub. Selection is exactly Blueprint §6.1's rule: clicking a Holder in Working View selects it, switches the activity indicator to Place regardless of what was active a moment before, and populates Context Inspector — a single `mousedown`/`mousemove`/`mouseup` driver wired once at module init (`worldBuilderApp.js`), reading `currentNav`/`currentSceneId`/`currentActivity` live rather than rebinding per render. **Position/Size** are draggable directly on the canvas (drag the Holder body to move, drag its bottom-right resize handle) and mirrored as Position X/Y % and Width/Height % sliders in Context Inspector — both paths write the same fractional `holder.position`/`holder.size` and redraw live via a new `_redrawSceneCanvases()`, clamped so a Holder can never drag or resize past the Canvas edge. **Shape** (Rectangle/Rounded/Circle) and **Fit** (Fit/Fill/Original, Engine Canon §6's vocabulary) are real dropdowns (`js/services/engineSchema.js` gained `HOLDER_SHAPES`/`HOLDER_FITS`); Shape actually clips the canvas draw (`_drawHolderShapePath`, arc/rounded-rect/rect). **Padding** is a real, persisted field, disclosed honestly as cosmetically minor until a real photo replaces the placeholder. **Frame** — confirmed living in Place, not Decorations, per Engine Canon §9's "Frame Element placed inside a Holder Layer" rule (Blueprint §8) — is a card-grid picker of the World's existing `frames/*.json` (None + every Frame, swatched by `borderColor`); choosing one now visibly changes the Holder's rendered border colour/thickness on both Working View and Runtime Preview. A "Manage Theme Assets (Frames) →" link reintroduces the Frames screen exactly where Slice 1's own report said it would return — reachable only from here, not Global Navigation (Vision §1) — and the Frames screen gained a "← Back to Scene" link (shown only when a Scene is open behind it) so the round trip never strands the Theme Author; `currentSceneId` is deliberately preserved across that visit rather than cleared. **Add/Remove Holder**: `js/projectModel.js` gained `findHolder`/`updateHolder`/`addHolder`/`deleteHolder` (`_ensureHolderDefaults` retrofits `permissions`/`shape`/`padding`/`fit` onto Holders authored before this slice, the same read-time-reconciliation pattern `_ordered` already used for stale ids) — the Engine places no upper bound on a Scene's Holder count (Canon §2), so a Gallery Scene can grow past its Template's starting arrangement, matching Scenes' own Add/Remove pattern. **The Holder-variant permission block** (Blueprint §6.2) is a real, collapsed-by-default `<details>` — skips "can the Story Author populate this" (not a permission, the Holder's entire reason for existing, Engine Invariant 10) and asks only the three real questions: move / change (its Frame, once populated) / see. Decorations and Text remain the honest Coming-in-the-next-sprint stub. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: click-to-select a Holder switches Place active and shows its panel; dragging the Holder body updates its persisted position; the Shape/Fit dropdowns and Padding slider persist and redraw; picking a Frame updates `holder.frame` and the canvas border colour; "Manage Theme Assets (Frames) →" opens Frames with a working "← Back to Scene" round trip that preserves the open Scene; the permission block's summary/checkboxes read and write correctly; Add a Holder/Remove this Holder both round-trip through `localStorage` correctly — zero console errors throughout.)
- Builder V2 — Slice 3: Decorations activity, the Scene Stack made real (implements Blueprint §9, the third vertical slice of the Builder V2 reset. Introduces the genuine Scene Stack Engine Canon §5 describes — "Canvas owns the Scene Stack...
