Scene Layers and Holders together, bottom to top" — as `scene.stack`, an ordered array of `{type:'holder'|'layer', id}` entries, reconciled lazily on read (`js/projectModel.js`'s `_ensureStack`, the same pattern `_ordered` already used for frameOrder/sceneOrder) so a Scene authored in Slices 1-2 before `stack` existed never crashes. **Background**: Blueprint §9's "set the background" is deliberately *not* a special `scene.background` field — Engine Canon §4/Invariant 8 forbid a second way to do something Elements-in-Layers already do — so it reuses or creates an ordinary full-bleed fill Scene Layer pinned to stack position 0 (`setSceneBackground`/`getSceneBackgroundColor`); a colour-picker in Decorations' Context Inspector edits it directly. **Decorations**: a small built-in emoji palette (real Theme Decoration Pack browsing, Engine Canon §9, is disclosed as not yet built — that is Theme Assets consolidation, out of this slice's scope) placed as ordinary Scene Layers (`addSceneLayer`/`updateSceneLayer`/`deleteSceneLayer`), draggable exactly like a Holder via the same generic fractional-rect hit test (`_pointInHolder`, unchanged, since it only ever read `.position`/`.size`) — selection, drag-to-move, and a Size % slider, but deliberately no resize handle (Blueprint §9 gives Decorations only "reposition," never resize). **"Bring Forward"/"Send Backward"** (`moveInStack`) is the one Builder verb Blueprint §9 names in place of a Layer Stack panel — swaps adjacent `scene.stack` entries, immediately visible since decorations can now render above or below a Holder they overlap. **Selection now spans the whole Stack**: the shared `mousedown` handler (Slice 2) hit-tests every stack entry topmost-first, selecting a Holder → Place or a decoration → Decorations, exactly matching Blueprint §6.1's "selection drives the activity" rule for both object kinds through one code path. `_drawSceneCanvas` was refactored from a Holder-only loop into a Scene Stack walk (`_drawHolderEntry`/`_drawLayerEntry`), gating render only on `visible` — never `moveable`/`editable` — per Engine Invariant 22. **The Decoration-variant permission block** (Blueprint §6.2) adds the one line beyond the standard three that Blueprint names explicitly: "Let the Story Author add their own decorations here too" — saying yes is the entire Decoration Slot mechanism (Engine Canon §7); there is no separate "mark as Slot" control anywhere, exactly as Blueprint specifies. Text remains the honest Coming-in-the-next-sprint stub. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: background colour change persists as a bottom-of-stack fill layer; adding a decoration appends it to the stack and top; dragging repositions it; Bring Forward/Send Backward reorder the stack; the 4-checkbox permission block (including Decoration Slot) reads and writes correctly; Remove Decoration round-trips through `localStorage`; and — the regression check this slice's own refactor most needed — clicking a Holder on the same canvas still correctly selects it and switches to Place, proving the combined Stack hit-testing didn't break Slice 2's own behaviour. Zero console errors throughout.)
- Builder V2 — Slice 4: Text activity, the Scene Editor complete (implements Blueprint §10, the fourth vertical slice of the Builder V2 reset — every one of Place/Decorations/Text is now real, closing out Blueprint §6-§10 in full. Text is a third `kind` of Scene Layer (`fill`/`decoration`/`text`, `js/projectModel.js`'s `addSceneLayer`/`_ensureSceneLayerDefaults` extended, not duplicated) — reusing the exact same Scene Stack, selection, and drag-to-move machinery Decorations already built, since a text Element is positioned and selected identically to a decoration, just never resized via a handle and never sourced from a Theme Asset shelf (Blueprint §2's own resolved contradiction: "a Theme Author may freely add a new Text Element, with no Theme Asset constraining what's available"). Selection routing (`worldBuilderApp.js`'s shared `mousedown` handler) now reads a hit Scene Layer's own `kind` to decide Decorations vs. Text, and skips full-bleed Background fills entirely — Background is edited only through Decorations' colour picker, never a clickable canvas object (Blueprint §9's own "set the background," not "select the background," phrasing). **Write directly, then style** (Blueprint §10's own two-step framing): a Words textarea, Font (5 fixed families) and Alignment dropdowns, a Size slider, and a Colour picker, all live-redrawing both Working View and Runtime Preview identically via a new top-down `_drawTextBlock` (deliberately separate from the pre-existing `_wrapText`, which vertically centers the Scenes-Library empty-state message and would have been wrong for a text box that should start at its own top edge). **The Text-variant permission block** (Blueprint §10) drops the Decoration Slot line (that mechanism is Decorations-specific, Engine Canon §7) and folds wording-change and restyling into one `editable` question, exactly as Blueprint §10 specifies. Add Text is unconstrained — no shelf, no template picker, just a default text box ready to type into. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: adding text creates a real Scene Layer and appends it to the stack; editing Words/Font/Alignment/Size/Colour all persist and redraw both canvases identically; the 3-checkbox permission block (no Decoration Slot line) reads and writes correctly; Remove Text round-trips through `localStorage`; and clicking a Holder afterward still correctly selects it and switches to Place, confirming the shared selection/hit-test code introduced across Slices 2-4 still routes all three activities correctly through one path. Zero console errors throughout.)
- Builder V2 — Slice 5: Scenes Library polish, reorder + live thumbnails (closes two gaps against Blueprint §5's own literal spec, discovered only once real Scene content existed to notice them against. **Reorder**: `ProjectModel.moveScene` existed since Slice 1 but had no Scene Library control ever wired to it; Scene cards now carry ↑/↓ buttons (`.wb-row-controls`, the same pattern Frame rows already used for `moveFrame`) — Blueprint §5's own "Rename, duplicate, delete, reorder a Scene" is now fully implemented, not three-quarters of it. **Live thumbnails**: Blueprint §5 asks for "a live-updating thumbnail of [each Scene's] actual composition," which the static per-aspect-ratio icon from Slice 1 never was; `_sceneCardThumb` now mounts a real `<canvas>` per card and calls the same `_drawSceneCanvas` the Scene Editor itself uses (`{guides:false, interactive:false}` — a Library card isn't an editing surface, so no Safe Area guide and no selection outline), so a Scene's Holders/Decorations/Text all actually appear in its card the instant they're authored, with zero second rendering implementation. Zero console errors.)
- Builder V2 — Workspace Alignment: the frozen three-pane layout, for real (`docs/BUILDER_V2_VISION.md` §4 specifies three permanent, full-height regions side by side — Working View | Runtime Preview | Context Inspector — but Slices 1-5 shipped Global Navigation's top-bar move without ever completing the matching Workspace reflow: the Inspector stayed the Engine-V1-era full-width row beneath Working View + Runtime Preview, a real implementation omission rather than a design choice, caught during an architecture-alignment review. `tools/world-builder/css/world-builder.css`'s `.wb-workspace-body` grid changes from two rows (`working rtsash runtime` / `tbsash tbsash tbsash` / `inspector inspector inspector`) to one row of five tracks (`working rtsash runtime inspsash inspector`) — Context Inspector is now its own full-height column, sized generously (420px default) rather than as a naive equal third, per Vision §4's own explicit warning. Both resize sashes are now vertical (col-resize): `#wb-resize-runtime` (Working View ↔ Runtime Preview, unchanged in role) and `#wb-resize-inspector` (repurposed from a horizontal height-sash to a vertical width-sash between Runtime Preview and Context Inspector — same element, same persisted-preference mechanism, `--wb-inspector-h` renamed `--wb-inspector-w`). Context Inspector gained its own heading bar (🔍 Context Inspector / "Properties for whatever is selected") matching Working View's and Runtime Preview's existing chrome, so all three read as peer panes; its content (every existing per-state renderer — World/Scenes/Validation/Build/Publish, and every Scene Editor state) is completely unchanged, only its container's geometry moved. A narrow-viewport (`<900px`) fallback keeps the old below-the-fold Inspector shape as a disclosed, ordinary responsive concession — the frozen 3-pane layout is the primary desktop authoring shape Vision §4 specifies; both resize sashes hide at that width since there's no longer room to drag them meaningfully. Verified via Playwright: Working View/Runtime Preview/Context Inspector share the same top and height (a real full-height 3-column layout, not an illusion) across every Global Navigation destination (World/Scenes/Validation/Build/Publish); dragging both sashes resizes and persists correctly (`localStorage`'s `vihustudio.worldBuilder.workspaceLayout` now stores `{runtimeW, inspectorW}`); Reset Workspace Layout restores the shipped defaults; selecting a Scene object still populates Context Inspector exactly as before. Zero console errors.)
- Engine V2 — the native Runtime, first real implementation (`docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` §5/LOCK V2-04's architectural decision — Validation/Runtime/Build/Publish operate directly on the canonical Scene Model, no translation layer — now has code behind it. New `tools/world-builder/js/services/engineRuntime.js` (`window.EngineV2Runtime`) is a small, generic module reading only a canonical Scene object (`scenes/<id>.json`'s exact shape, Scene Model §2/§3) plus one injected `resolveFrame` callback for the model's one cross-reference (a Holder's Frame Theme Asset id) — it never touches `window.ProjectModel`, `currentProject`, or any other Builder-only global, so it is callable from Working View, Runtime Preview, a Scene Library thumbnail, or a future non-Builder host with zero code change. `load(scene, resolveFrame)` performs Engine Canon §5 pipeline steps 1-3 (resolve the Canvas frame's pixel Size via `EngineSchema.aspectInfo`, walk `scene.stack` into an ordered, paint-ready graph); `render(ctx, graph)` performs step 4 (paint the Scene Stack bottom to top — Holder placeholder chrome + Frame border, Decoration fill/glyph, Text word-wrap — gating only on `visible`, per Engine Invariant 22, exactly as Engine Canon §5 step 5 specifies a published render must). `tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_drawSceneCanvas` — previously a Builder-only canvas routine, explicitly disclosed in Slice 1's own report as deliberately *not* a Runtime — now delegates its actual painting to `EngineV2Runtime.load`/`.render`, keeping only genuinely Builder-only authoring chrome as a thin wrapper on top (the felt Safe Area guide, selection outlines, the Holder resize handle — none of which a published render would ever show, Engine Canon §5 step 5). This means Working View and Runtime Preview, Builder V2's own two rendering surfaces, are now proof this Runtime is real rather than theoretical: every Scene a Theme Author authors already renders through it today. `docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` §7's open item on Holder Layers/Content Layer remains exactly as open as before — this Runtime renders a Holder's placeholder chrome only, since Builder V2 still authors no independent Holder Layer stack to render instead. Verified via Playwright: a hand-built Scene object fed directly to `EngineV2Runtime.load`/`.render` with no Builder involvement paints correctly (a fill Layer's colour reads back from `getImageData`); every existing Working View/Runtime Preview interaction (drag a Holder, add a Decoration/Text, pick a Frame, change Aspect Ratio) still renders pixel-identically through the new path; zero console errors.)
- Builder V2 — Workspace column reorder (explicit product amendment): the permanent three-column order changes from Working View | Runtime Preview | Context Inspector to **Working View | Context Inspector | Runtime Preview** — Context Inspector now sits beside Working View since editing the current selection is the higher-frequency action, Runtime Preview moves to the smallest, rightmost column reflecting its lower-frequency "what will the reader see" role. This reorders `docs/BUILDER_V2_VISION.md` §4's own diagram (v1.1) and `docs/BUILDER_V2_UX_PACKAGE.md`'s matching Part 5/shared-shell diagram — both frozen documents amended in place, with the change disclosed via an inline "Amended" callout and each document's own Change History, rather than silently diverging code from stale documentation. `tools/world-builder/css/world-builder.css`'s grid/area order and both resize sashes' drag math swap accordingly (`--wb-inspector-w` now the Working↔Inspector boundary, `--wb-runtime-w` the Inspector↔Runtime boundary); default widths keep the same relative sizing (Working largest, Inspector 420px medium, Runtime 340px smallest) — only position changed. Fixing this surfaced a real, unrelated regression from the same session's Engine V2 Runtime slice: a freshly-created Scene has no persisted `stack` field until `ProjectModel.sceneStack()`'s lazy reconciliation runs once, and the new `EngineV2Runtime.load` (deliberately pure, no Builder-global dependency) doesn't trigger that reconciliation the way the old inline drawing code incidentally did — `_drawSceneCanvas` now calls `ProjectModel.sceneStack(currentProject, scene.id)` once for its reconciling side effect before handing the Scene to the Runtime, fixing Holders silently failing to render on a Scene opened for the first time without an intervening canvas click. **Engine V2 Validation**, closing out this arc: new `tools/world-builder/js/services/engineValidator.js` (`window.EngineV2Validator`) checks every Scene against Scene Model §5's four named constraints — Canvas required + valid Aspect Ratio; every Stack entry resolves to a real Holder/Layer id with no duplicates/staleness (reported as a warning when reconciliation was needed, never silently fixed, mirroring `_ensureStack`'s logic without mutating); every Holder's `frame` resolves to a real Frame id; every fractional position/size stays in `[0,1]` with a fully-outside object an error and a partially-overflowing one only a warning. Deliberately a separate, synchronous engine from `js/services/validator.js` (Engine V1, which round-trips through the `projectLoader` Blob singleton) — no translation layer, per LOCK V2-04 — its own "Scenes (Engine V2)" report renders in the Validation Context Inspector alongside, never merged into, the existing "World Contract (Engine V1)" category list. **Build metadata restored**: `tools/world-builder/build-info.json`/`js/buildInfo.js` gain `phase`/`milestone`/`slice` fields (falling back to the older `sprint`/`task` naming) so the Workspace footer reflects the current Engine V2 slice; following this repository's own established `chore(build): pin build-info to Sprint X commit` convention (a small follow-up commit referencing the real just-made commit SHA, since a commit cannot self-reference its own hash in the same commit), this becomes the standard per-slice closing step going forward. Verified via Playwright: the three panes' new left-to-right order/relative sizing, both sashes' new drag directions and persistence, the Holder-render regression fix (pixel read-back confirms paint), and the Validation panel showing both engines' reports distinctly — zero console errors throughout.)
- Engine V2 — Build and Publish (compiling and sharing the canonical Scene Model, per `docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` §5/LOCK V2-02/V2-04). New `tools/world-builder/js/services/engineBuilder.js` (`window.EngineV2Builder`) is a pure function from a validated World's Scene Model to a package — requires `EngineV2Validator` to report zero errors first (mirroring Engine V1's own established Build-requires-Validation convention), then produces a flat JSON envelope (`{format:'engine-v2-world-package', formatVersion, manifest, metadata, theme, scenes, frames, builtAt}`) — World identity fields unchanged in shape from Engine V1 (Scene Model §2), every Scene exactly as authored, every Frame a Holder might reference (the model's one cross-reference). Deliberately not named or shaped like `.vtheme` (`<id>.v2world.json` instead) since Engine V1's and Engine V2's compiled formats are not interchangeable and sharing a name would misleadingly suggest otherwise (LOCK V2-04). No `assets/` folder — every Frame field is an enum resolved to a drawn canvas routine today, not a raster image, the same reasoning Museum Gallery's own Engine V1 package used. The Build screen gained a "Scenes (Engine V2)" section (its own stat cards, its own "🎬 Build Scene Package" button, storing the result as `project.lastSceneBuild` — a dataURL, matching Engine V1's own `project.lastBuild` shape so `_downloadDataURL` works identically for both) ahead of the existing, untouched "World Package (Engine V1)" section. The Publish screen gained a matching "Scenes (Engine V2)" section offering only **Export Scene Package** — deliberately just a download, since no Engine V2 Runtime exists outside this Builder yet for an "Official Themes"-style install to target (LOCK V2-04's native Runtime is implemented as Working View/Runtime Preview's own rendering path, not yet as a standalone reader-facing consumer); this is a disclosed gap, not an oversight, and matches Scene Model §5's own "sharing mechanics are unchanged in *kind*" framing — Export exists in both engines' Publish, Official/Community do not yet in Engine V2's. Both new sections read/write only `project.lastSceneBuild`, never `project.files` directly, matching Engine V1 Publish's own "never read the editable Project" discipline (Sprint B2.0.1). Verified via Playwright: Build produces a real, well-shaped package (`format`/`formatVersion`/scene count/frame count all correct); Publish's Export button triggers a real file download with the correct filename; the Engine V1 Build/Publish sections remain fully functional and unaffected; zero console errors throughout. With this, all six items Engine V2 needed — Workspace alignment, Runtime, Renderer, Validation, Build, Publish — are implemented against the canonical Scene Model with no translation layer and no parallel architecture, per LOCK V2-04.)
- Authoring Validation AV-001 — Working View/Runtime Preview adopt the Scene's own Aspect Ratio (a real authoring bug found while beginning to author the official Museum Theme in Builder V2, not an Engine/Runtime issue — Engine Canon §4 already correctly ties Canvas geometry to the Scene's Aspect Ratio, and `EngineV2Runtime`/`_drawSceneCanvas` already correctly resized the canvas's own pixel buffer, `canvasEl.width`/`.height`, per Scene — see Sprint "Engine V2: the native Runtime"). The bug was purely a CSS/layout omission: `.wb-working-canvas-inner`/`.wb-runtime-preview-canvas-inner` (the canvas's own parent box, which the canvas fills via `width:100%;height:100%`) carried a hardcoded `aspect-ratio: 1080 / 1350`, so a Landscape/Square/Quote Scene's correctly-sized bitmap was silently stretched to fill a portrait-shaped box — Working View and Runtime Preview looked permanently portrait no matter what Aspect Ratio was selected, while the underlying Holder/Layer geometry was already correct. Fixed with one line in `_drawSceneCanvas` (`canvasEl.parentElement.style.aspectRatio = graph.width + ' / ' + graph.height`), set from the same `EngineV2Runtime.load` graph already used to size the canvas buffer — the stylesheet's `1080/1350` value is now only a before-first-render fallback, overridden inline on every real draw. No Engine V2/Scene Model/architecture change of any kind; a one-line authoring-surface correctness fix. Verified via Playwright: switching Portrait → Landscape → Square → Quote → Portrait each produces a Working View/Runtime Preview box whose on-screen aspect ratio matches the Scene's own (0.8 / 1.25 / 1.0 / 0.8), Safe Area guide recalculates correctly for each, and Holder click-select + drag-to-move continue working correctly under a non-portrait Aspect Ratio. Zero console errors.)
- Authoring Validation AV-002 — the Scene becomes a first-class selectable object (a real selection/navigation gap found in the same authoring session as AV-001, again not an Engine/Runtime/architecture issue — Scene was always a real Context Inspector state, `currentInspectorTarget === 'sceneConfig'`, reachable via the Scene Header's own glance; the gap was that Working View itself had no path to it). Two call sites fixed, both in `tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`: (1) `_openScene` (fired both when a brand-new Scene is created and when reopening one from the Scenes Library) now defaults `currentInspectorTarget` to `'sceneConfig'` instead of `null` — configuring the Scene's own shape is the first authoring action a Theme Author sees, not an immediately-selected Holder; (2) the shared `mousedown` handler's "nothing hit" branch — previously it only cleared an existing Holder/Layer selection back to `null` when one was active, otherwise doing nothing — now unconditionally selects Scene Configuration, making the empty Canvas area the natural, always-available hit target for the Scene itself, mirroring exactly how clicking a Holder/Decoration/Text selects that object (Blueprint §6.1). No Scene Settings button or new UI added — the existing Scene Configuration Context Inspector state (Vision §2) is simply now reachable from within Working View, not only from the Scene Header strip above it. Verified via Playwright: opening a freshly-created Scene shows Scene Configuration (not a Holder list); clicking empty Canvas from any state (Holder selected, Decoration selected, Text selected) returns to Scene Configuration; clicking a Holder/Decoration/Text still correctly selects that object; Runtime Preview and canvas pixel dimensions unaffected. Zero console errors, no Engine V2 changes.)
- Authoring Validation AV-003 — the complete Holder presentation pipeline (Frame's full field set, plus Fit and Padding) actually renders (real Builder-side bugs found authoring the official Museum Theme's White Museum Frame — not an Engine/Scene-Model/architecture issue; every property persisted correctly all along). **Root cause 1 — Frame silently never applied:** `EngineV2Runtime`'s `_paintHolder` (`js/services/engineRuntime.js`) calls its injected resolver as `graph.resolveFrame(holder.frame)` — passing the Frame *id* — but `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_holderFrameFields` (the function wired in as that resolver) was written to accept a *Holder object* and read `.frame` off it; called with a plain id string, `arg.frame` is always `undefined`, so the resolver returned `null` for every Holder regardless of which Frame was picked. Fixed by changing `_holderFrameFields`'s parameter to the id it's actually called with — the Runtime's own call site was correct all along. **Root cause 2 — Fit and Padding never triggered a redraw:** unlike every other Holder field in `_renderHolderPanel`, the Fit `<select>` and Padding `<input type=range>` handlers called `updateHolder`+`_persist()` but never `_redrawSceneCanvases()`. Fixed by adding the same call already present on every sibling field. **Root cause 3 — the deeper, systemic one, found only after a direct follow-up question ("verify every Frame property end to end; find the common point, not the individual symptoms"):** `_paintHolder` had only ever consumed 2 of the 8 fields the Frames screen actually authors (`borderColor`, `frameThickness`) — `wallTone`, `cornerRadius`, `shadow`, `inset`, `matWidth`, and `defaultMargin` all persisted correctly via `ProjectModel.setFrameFieldValue` but had no code path into either rendering surface at all, redraw bugs aside. `_paintHolder` is that common point, not any one field's own handler. Rewrote it as a set of concentric filled bands, outside in — wall margin (`defaultMargin`+`inset`, filled `wallTone`) → frame border (`frameThickness`, `borderColor`) → mat (`matWidth`, a fixed neutral tone) → content (the Holder's own `padding`, Engine Canon §6) — each via one shared `_band(insetPx, color)` helper that also shrinks `cornerRadius` by the running inset so every band's outer edge meets the previous band's inner edge exactly, with no gap and no overlap (an earlier centered-stroke version of the border band left a visible unstyled gap before the mat; replacing the stroke with a filled band removed the half-thickness bookkeeping that bug came from). `shadow` (`none`/`soft`/`floating`/`gallery`) is applied once, only to the outermost band, via real `ctx.shadowColor`/`shadowBlur`/`shadowOffsetY` presets. **Fit's visual meaning implemented for the first time**, matching the three-way vocabulary Engine Canon §6 already names (`fit`/`fill`/`original`), applied to the placeholder glyph since no Primary Element/Content Layer is separately authored yet (Scene Model §7 open item 1, unchanged). Verified via Playwright: Frame None→Classic White changes the rendered border colour immediately in both Working View and Runtime Preview, identical in both; every one of the 8 Frame fields (wallTone, defaultMargin, inset, cornerRadius, shadow, matWidth, frameThickness, borderColor) set to a distinct extreme value produces its own correctly-ordered, correctly-bounded band, sampled pixel-by-pixel across the transition from the Holder's outer edge inward with no gaps; Fit fit→fill→original all persist and visibly resize the placeholder; Padding small→large visibly insets the placeholder; Holder/Scene selection (AV-002) and Aspect Ratio switching (AV-001) both still work unaffected; zero console errors; no Engine V2/Scene Model changes.)
- Authoring Validation AV-004 — Working View becomes an adaptive construction workspace instead of a duplicate of Runtime Preview (a Builder UX finding, not an Engine/rendering issue — Runtime Preview was already correct and unaffected; Working View simply carried zero authoring-specific affordances beyond the pre-existing Safe Area guide and selection outline, so it read as a second, redundant "what the reader sees" surface rather than a construction tool). **Product principle established**: Runtime Preview is frozen — always exactly the published reader output, selection-independent; Working View is allowed to adapt to whatever is currently selected, showing Builder-only guides that never serialize, never publish, never affect exports, and never touch Engine V2 rendering. **Implementation, entirely inside the existing frozen architecture**: `engineRuntime.js`'s `_paintHolder` already computed a Holder's Frame band geometry (wall margin → border → mat → content, AV-003) inline; that geometry was extracted into one shared, read-only function, `_holderInsets(holder, fields, graph)`, so the paint routine and any future geometry query are guaranteed to agree — a guide computed from separately-reimplemented math could otherwise silently drift out of sync with what's actually drawn. A new public query, `EngineV2Runtime.holderBands(holder, graph)`, reuses `_holderInsets` to return the same band rectangles (`outer`/`border`/`mat`/`content`) as plain data, with no drawing side effect — added to the module's existing `{load, render, rectFor}` export as `holderBands`, still a pure function of the canonical Scene Model plus the injected Frame resolver, nothing new for `EngineV2Runtime` to know about Builder UI. `worldBuilderApp.js` gained `_drawHolderConstructionGuides(ctx, holder, graph, canvasWidth)`, called only from `_drawSceneCanvas`'s pre-existing `opts.interactive` branch (Working View only, never Runtime Preview) when a Holder is selected — it calls `EngineV2Runtime.holderBands()` and draws dashed, labelled boundary lines ("Wall → Frame", "Frame → Mat" or "Frame → Artwork" when there's no mat, "Artwork") directly on top of the identical `EngineV2Runtime.render()` output already painted by both surfaces, deduplicating adjacent bands that share identical bounds (e.g. zero-width mat) so a redundant line is never drawn. Scene selection's own construction context (composition/safe area) was already served by the pre-existing Safe Area guide from AV-001/Slice 1 and needed no new code. This is deliberately scoped to visual, non-interactive guide lines — not drag-to-edit handles on the guide boundaries themselves — since the ticket's own "exact affordances are a Builder decision" left room to choose the lower-risk option for this slice; a future slice could make these boundaries draggable without changing this slice's architecture. Verified via Playwright: selecting a Holder shows correctly-labelled dashed band-boundary guides in Working View only; deselecting back to Scene Configuration (AV-002) removes them; a pixel-level comparison of Runtime Preview's canvas (`getImageData` sampled across a 20×20 grid) is byte-identical before and after Holder selection, proving the guides never bleed into the reader-facing surface; full regression across AV-001/AV-002/AV-003/Slice/Validation/Build/Reorder test suites all pass unchanged; zero console errors; no Engine V2/Scene Model/Runtime Preview rendering changes.)
- Authoring Validation AV-005 — Runtime Preview stays project-scoped instead of switching to a reusable-asset editor's own specimen (a Builder product bug found authoring the Museum Theme's Frames, not an Engine/rendering issue — correcting, not walking back, AV-004's own "Runtime Preview is frozen/project-scoped, Working View is editor-scoped" contract, which `_renderPreview()`/`_redrawSceneCanvases` hadn't actually honoured for every Builder screen). **Root cause**: `_renderPreview()` (`worldBuilderApp.js`) picked one rendering mode for *both* Working View and Runtime Preview based solely on `currentNav` — for every nav other than `'scenes'` (Frames/Layouts/Representations/Layer Packs/etc.) it built a synthetic specimen slide via `_buildPreviewSlide`/`SlideRenderer.render()` and painted it into both canvases, so entering "Manage Frames" (Slice 2's own "manage the full shelf" bridge, which deliberately keeps `currentSceneId` set so "← Back to Scene" can return) replaced Runtime Preview's Museum Scene render with a standalone Frame specimen — Working View becoming the specimen editor was correct, Runtime Preview following it along was the bug. Compounding it, `_redrawSceneCanvases(sceneId)` unconditionally early-returned whenever `currentNav !== 'scenes'`, so even a manual redraw request while a Scene was open behind another editor was silently dropped. **Fix, entirely inside frozen architecture, no second renderer**: a new `_activeSceneForRuntimePreview()` reads `currentSceneId` independent of `currentNav`; `_renderPreview()` now paints Runtime Preview via the existing `_drawSceneCanvas(runtimePreviewCanvas, activeScene, {guides:false, interactive:false})` — the exact same Engine V2 pipeline Scenes nav already uses — whenever a Scene is active, regardless of which nav/editor Working View shows instead, and only falls back to the legacy `SlideRenderer` specimen for Runtime Preview when no Scene is open at all (Overview/Representations/etc. on a project with zero Scenes, unchanged prior behaviour); Working View's own per-nav specimen/identity-card logic is completely untouched, since AV-004's "Working View is editor-scoped" half of the contract was never wrong. `_redrawSceneCanvases` now redraws Runtime Preview whenever `currentSceneId` matches, and additionally redraws Working View's own Scene-editor canvas only when `currentNav === 'scenes'` — same split. **A second, related bug surfaced and fixed in the same pass**: `_renderFramesPanel`'s field handlers only called `_renderPreview()` after 3 of its 8 Frame fields (Wall Tone, Border Color, Frame Thickness) — Corner Radius/Shadow/Inset/Padding(Mat Width)/Default Margin persisted via `setFrameFieldValue` but never triggered a repaint of either canvas, the identical "missing redraw call" class of bug AV-003 found and fixed for the Holder panel's Fit/Padding fields; added the same `_renderPreview()` call to all 5 missing handlers so every Frame property updates both the Working View specimen and the live Runtime Preview Scene immediately, per this ticket's own acceptance criteria. `EngineV2Runtime`/`engineRuntime.js` and the Scene Model are completely unchanged — the fix lives entirely in which canvas `worldBuilderApp.js` chooses to paint and when, reusing the same `_drawSceneCanvas`/`EngineV2Runtime.load`/`.render()` calls Scenes nav already made. Verified via Playwright: selecting a Holder, assigning it a Frame, then opening Manage Frames shows Working View switch to the Frame specimen editor while Runtime Preview's canvas stays pixel-identical (still the Museum Scene, framed Holder and all); editing Border Color and — critically — Corner Radius (previously silently dead) both now visibly update Runtime Preview's rendered Scene live; full regression across AV-001/AV-002/AV-003/AV-004/Slice/Validation/Build/Reorder suites all pass unchanged; zero console errors; no Engine V2/Scene Model changes, no serialization/export changes.)
- Builder Authoring Polish — AP-001/AP-002/AV-006 (a Builder-usability-only pass, no architecture/Engine V2/Scene Model change; all three items found or requested while continuing Museum Theme authoring after AV-005). **AP-001 — developer language removed from Builder UI copy**: every Context Inspector panel string that leaked internal terminology to the author is rewritten in plain product language — the Decorations "Add a Decoration" help text (`Engine Canon §9... a future slice, not yet built here` → `Choose a decoration to place in your scene`, the ticket's own literal example), the `scenes` STATE_GUIDANCE entry (`Engine V2 Canon §0`/`arrive in a following slice` → plain wording matching that Place/Decorations/Text are already real, not upcoming), Scene Configuration's heading/help text (`Engine V2 Canon §4`/`Vision §2`/`Blueprint §7` → plain wording), the Place panel heading (`Blueprint §6.2, §8` → plain wording), and — the largest offender, found by grepping every `textContent`/`innerHTML` UI string rather than stopping at the ticket's one example — the Validation/Build/Publish panels' own permanent section headings literally read `Scenes (Engine V2)` / `World Contract (Engine V1)` / `World Package (Engine V1)` verbatim in the rendered UI, plus a Publish note disclosing `no Engine V2 Runtime exists outside this Builder yet to install it into` (an implementation-status admission the ticket explicitly forbids); all renamed to plain `Scenes` / `World Contract` / `World Package` (the two package kinds stay distinguishable by name alone, since one produces a Scene Package and the other a World Package) and the Publish note reworded to `Download the built Scene Package to your computer to back it up or share it`. The permanent dev build-info footer (`World Builder 2.2.x-EV2 | Authoring Validation — AV-00x | ...`) is deliberately left untouched — it's a separately-and-explicitly-instructed dev/QA indicator (see the Sprint 11.0 "Studio Arrival Experience" build-info footer decision), not Builder authoring-panel copy, so it's outside this ticket's "Builder should present itself as a finished creative product" scope. **AP-002 — emoji panel-title headings replaced with inline SVG icons**: `assets/icons/{navigation,actions,status}/` were confirmed to be empty placeholder folders (Product Asset System sprint reservations, no actual icon files), and emoji is genuinely the Builder's own consistent, pervasive icon language elsewhere (Global Nav, Activity switcher, row-control buttons, stub panels, Publish cards) — so rather than fabricate a full replacement icon set unilaterally (a real design decision the ticket's own example didn't fully specify), this narrowed to the specific large panel-title emoji the ticket's example pointed at: a new `ICONS` lookup (`worldBuilderApp.js`) with three small inline `<svg>` glyphs (picture/sparkle/pencil, `currentColor` stroke, no binary assets) for Place/Decorations/Text, `_heading()` gained an optional third `iconSvg` parameter, and the three permanent pane headings (Working View/Context Inspector/Runtime Preview, hardcoded in `index.html`) got matching inline SVGs (frame/magnifying-glass/eye) — Nav bar, Activity switcher, and row-control glyphs are unchanged emoji, a disclosed scope decision, not an oversight. **AV-006 — text drag movement had an invisible barrier, root cause found and fixed**: a text Scene Layer's declared `position`/`size` box (Scene Model §3's generic fractional-rect vocabulary, shared with Holder/Decoration) is, for text specifically, only ever a wrap-width and a creation-time placeholder height (`size:{w:0.7,h:0.15}` by default) — completely decoupled from the layer's actual rendered extent, which depends on real word count and line-wrapping (`engineRuntime.js`'s `_paintLayer`/`_drawWrappedText`, top-down from the box's own top edge, never clipped to or centered within `size.h`). The Builder's drag-clamp (`Math.min(1 - obj.size.h, ...)`), hit-test (`_pointInHolder`), and selection-outline drawing all clamped/tested against that declared box, so a short line of text sitting in the default 15%-tall box could never be dragged closer than 85% down the Canvas, stopping visibly short of the actual Safe Area with an unstyled gap below the true glyphs — exactly Blueprint's own "invisible movement barrier" framing. Fixed entirely inside the frozen architecture, matching AV-004's established pattern of adding a pure, read-only geometry query rather than a second implementation: `engineRuntime.js`'s wrap-loop was extracted into a shared `_wrapLines(ctx, text, maxWidth)` used by both `_drawWrappedText` (paint, unchanged output) and a new exported `textFootprint(ctx, layer, graph)` (query only, no drawing) that measures the real rendered line count/height and returns the *actual* footprint rect — added to the module's existing `{load, render, rectFor, holderBands}` export. `worldBuilderApp.js` gained `_effectiveObjectRect(obj, kind, canvasEl)`, returning that measured footprint for text Layers and `null` otherwise (Holders/Decorations completely unaffected, since their declared rect already *is* what's drawn); `_pointInHolder` now accepts the object's kind + canvas element and hit-tests against the footprint when it's text, the drag-clamp's `Math.min(1 - obj.size.h, ...)` now clamps against the measured footprint's fractional height for text specifically, and the selected-Layer outline (`_drawSceneCanvas`'s interactive branch) traces the same footprint rather than the stale declared box. Verified via Playwright: dragging a short "New text" element toward the Canvas bottom now reaches y≈0.956 (previously hard-clamped at 0.85), landing flush with the true bottom edge in both Working View (selection outline hugging the actual glyph, no gap) and Runtime Preview identically; full regression across AV-001 through AV-005/AP-001/AP-002/Slice/Validation/Build/Reorder suites all pass unchanged; zero console errors; no Engine V2 rendering change (`render()`/`_paintLayer`'s pixel output is byte-for-byte the same — only a new, additive, non-drawing query function was added) and no Scene Model change.)
- Project Card Representation — Welcome screen shows the authored World thumbnail (a Builder usability fix found authoring the Museum Theme; no Engine V2/navigation/architecture change). `_projectCard`'s `.wb-project-thumb` (`tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`, the "My World Projects" list on Screen 1) unconditionally rendered `project.icon || '🌎'` as plain text — it never checked whether the World had an authored `thumbnail.png` asset, even though the exact same `getAsset(project,'thumbnail.png')`-with-`<img>`-fallback pattern already existed one screen away in the Overview identity card (`_renderIdentityCard`), and the CSS (`.wb-project-thumb img{...}`, `overflow:hidden`) was already in place anticipating an image the JS never actually inserted. Fixed by reusing that identical pattern in `_projectCard`: when `ProjectModel.getAsset(project,'thumbnail.png')` returns a value, an `<img>` fills the thumb; otherwise the icon glyph placeholder renders exactly as before. Verified via Playwright: a World with an uploaded thumbnail shows the real image on its Welcome-screen card; a World with no thumbnail continues showing its emoji placeholder; full regression across every prior AV/AP/Slice/Validation/Build/Reorder suite passes unchanged; zero console errors; no Engine V2, Scene Model, export, or navigation changes.)
- Authoring Validation AV-007 / Builder Evolution EV-002 — Holder Fit/Fill made visually meaningful via a Theme's own representative artwork (real Builder authoring findings, not Engine V2/Scene Model issues; investigated before assuming a cause, per the ticket's own instruction). **Root cause (AV-007)**: two compounding bugs in `_paintHolder`'s placeholder rendering (`engineRuntime.js`), not one. (1) `fill`'s glyph size was `Math.min(cw,chgt) * 0.55` — always *smaller* than the content rect, so it could never overflow/crop against anything, reading as barely different from `fit`'s `0.3`. (2) Even fixed, an emoji glyph is a poor demonstration of crop behaviour — a single small icon centred in a box can't show "cover vs. contain" the way a real photo does, since there's no edge-to-edge detail to visibly clip. **Fix**: `_paintHolder`'s content band is now clipped to its own content rect (previously only the outer Holder-shape clip existed, so a naively-enlarged glyph or image could spill onto the mat/border bands), and draws `graph.representativeImage` — a real `Image`, when available — via a new `_drawImageWithFit(ctx, img, rect, fit)` using genuine `object-fit` math (`fit`=contain, `fill`=cover-and-crop, `original`=native size), the same vocabulary the Engine V1 image viewer already uses for a real photo. The glyph fallback (no artwork authored at all) keeps working exactly as before except `fill`'s multiplier is corrected to `1.4` (genuinely larger than the content rect, so it now visibly clips at the corners too). **EV-002's resolution**: rather than fabricate a second "sample artwork" concept (the ticket's own explicit instruction — `_sampleArtworkImage`, the generic gradient stand-in the legacy Engine V1 specimen path already uses, is untouched and unrelated), `worldBuilderApp.js` gained `_representativeArtworkImage(project, sceneId)`, which resolves the World's own authored Hero Image (`preview.png`, the higher-resolution source Overview's own "Hero Image" field uploads to) and falls back to Thumbnail (`thumbnail.png`) only if no Hero Image exists yet — matching the ticket's own "prefer its original high-resolution source" instruction exactly; no technical constraint was hit, so no new asset concept was needed. Cached by data-URL (invalidates automatically on re-upload) and loaded asynchronously via a real `Image`, redrawing the Scene once decoded. `EngineV2Runtime.load(scene, resolveFrame, representativeImage)` gained one new optional third parameter, threaded onto the returned graph exactly like `resolveFrame` — the Scene Model schema, the 4-step pipeline, and `render()`'s own signature are unchanged. Verified via Playwright: with a Theme's own Hero Image authored and no Frame assigned, `fit` shows the image letterboxed inside the Holder (background visible at all four content-rect corners, identical in Working View and Runtime Preview) while `fill` shows the image covering the Holder edge-to-edge with the overflow cropped (all four corners and centre pixel-match the image exactly) — an unambiguous, easily-authored difference; full regression across every prior AV/AP/Slice/Validation/Build/Reorder/Project-Card suite passes unchanged; zero console errors; no Engine V2/Scene Model/export changes.)
- Authoring Validation AV-008 — a real Builder workspace/navigation model, not an Engine or rendering issue (four findings from prolonged Museum Theme authoring). **(1) Resume last editing context**: `openWorkspace(project)` previously always reset to World/no-Scene; it now restores the author's last meaningful context (Global Nav tab, active Scene, `currentActivity`, `currentInspectorTarget`, and any open Frame — covering Scene→Holder→Frame, Scene→Text, Scene→Decorations chains) via a new `_loadEditingContext`/`_saveEditingContext` pair, hooked into the one function (`_renderWorkspace()`) every nav/selection change already calls, so no call site needed individual instrumentation. No architectural constraint blocked this — the same `ProjectModel` lookups Working View already uses to render each state are enough to validate a remembered Scene/Holder/Layer/Frame still exists, falling back cleanly to World/no-Scene if one was deleted since. Deliberately stored under its own `vihu-world-builder-editing-context` localStorage key, never touching `project.updatedAt`/`ProjectStore.save` — see (4). **(2) Explicit inactive states**: `_renderPreview()` previously always built a legacy Engine V1 specimen (from whichever Representation/Layout/Frame happened to be selected) into Working View and, when no Scene was active, into Runtime Preview too — a pseudo-preview of World metadata Museum Theme authoring doesn't use. New `_renderInactiveWorkspace()` replaces both with an honest message whenever `!_activeSceneForRuntimePreview()` (nav-independent, matching AV-005's own "project-scoped" Runtime Preview rule) and nav isn't `'scenes'` (which already had its own equivalent Scene-Library empty state): Working View shows "No Scene yet. Create your first Scene to begin authoring." + a **+ Create Scene** button that jumps straight to the Scenes template picker when the World truly has zero Scenes (Blank World template, or before this session's ProjectModel.scenes() check returns empty), or the milder "No Scene open. Select a Scene to begin authoring." + **Go to Scenes** when Scenes exist but none is open (the common case, since every non-Blank template seeds one starter Scene — so even a "brand-new" World already has a Scene, just not one currently selected); Runtime Preview shows the matching "Runtime Preview becomes available once a Scene has been created/is open." A real DOM bug surfaced building this: mounting the panel inside `.wb-working-canvas-inner` (the aspect-ratio-locked box) left it invisible, since that box collapses to near-zero size once its only normally-sized content — the canvas — is hidden; fixed by mounting on the outer `.wb-working-canvas-wrap` instead (a real flex:1 box, sized independent of canvas state) and explicitly hiding/showing the inner box alongside every other Working View state transition (identity card, Scene editor, Scene Library). **(3) Obvious route back to the Gallery**: a working `#wb-workspace-home` button already existed, but as a bare 🏠 glyph with no visible text it was easy to mistake for a decorative brand mark rather than a navigation control (a real, disclosed UX gap, not a missing mechanism) — it now reads "🏠 My Worlds" with a bordered button treatment matching the header's other controls. **(4) Project Activity investigation**: extensive testing (immediate edits, drag-completions, full page reloads, multi-project scenarios) found `_persist()`/`ProjectStore.save()` and `renderMyWorlds()`'s fresh `ProjectStore.list()` read on every `showWelcome()` call both already work correctly — no reproducible stale-timestamp bug was found in the current build. The one real risk this ticket's own "open time vs. edit time" hypothesis correctly anticipated is (1)'s new session-resume feature itself: had "remember where I was" been implemented by calling `ProjectStore.save()` on every navigation/selection change, merely *browsing* a World would have bumped `updatedAt` and made "Edited X ago" lie. Built defensively from the start via the separate `EDITING_CONTEXT_KEY` store instead, so navigation memory can never be mistaken for a content edit, now or in any future extension of it. Verified via Playwright: a brand-new Blank World shows the exact "No Scene yet…"/"+ Create Scene" copy and the CTA opens the Scene Template picker directly; a template that seeds a starter Scene shows "No Scene open…"/"Go to Scenes" instead; reopening a World resumes exactly on Manage Frames with the same Holder/Frame selected, and separately resumes on the same Text layer selected; deleting the remembered Scene and reopening falls back gracefully to World with zero console errors; the home button is clearly labelled; `updatedAt` still updates correctly on every save and survives reload. Full regression across every prior AV/AP/Slice/Validation/Build/Reorder/Project-Card suite passes unchanged; no Engine V2/Scene Model/rendering changes.)
- Authoring Validation AV-009 — Hero Image silently failed to persist, root cause traced (not assumed) to a swallowed localStorage quota failure, not an Engine issue. **Root cause**: a realistic camera-resolution photo's data URL routinely runs several megabytes; `ProjectStore._writeAll` wrapped its `localStorage.setItem` in a bare `try{}catch(e){}` that discarded a thrown `QuotaExceededError` with no signal anywhere — `_persist()` still showed "All Changes Saved," so the failure was invisible until the very next reload, when the stale pre-upload project (the last write that *did* fit) silently loaded back. Confirmed empirically: uploading a 5.7MB test image threw `QuotaExceededError` on `setItem`, and `preview.png` was absent from `localStorage` immediately after the "successful" save. **Fix, two parts**: (1) large image uploads are now downscaled/re-compressed client-side (`_downscaleImageDataURL` in `worldBuilderApp.js`, wired into the one shared `_fileInputUpload` every asset-upload control already uses — Thumbnail, Hero Image, and the Assets screen's per-slot uploader all get the fix uniformly) — only files whose data URL exceeds 1.5MB are touched, resized to a 1600px longest edge and re-encoded as JPEG at 0.85 quality, falling back to the original bytes if the shrunk version somehow isn't smaller; anything already small (icons, small graphics) passes through byte-for-byte untouched. (2) `ProjectStore.save()`/`_writeAll` no longer lie: `_writeAll` now returns `{ok, error}` instead of swallowing the exception, `save()` returns `{project, ok, error}` (no existing caller read the old return value, so widening it broke nothing), and `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_persist()`/manual Save button now show a real, non-auto-dismissing 🔴 "Save Failed — try a smaller image" state instead of "All Changes Saved" whenever a write doesn't actually reach localStorage — a defensive backstop for any future asset that still doesn't fit, so a silent lie can never recur. Neither change touches Engine V2, the Scene Model, or any rendering path — this is entirely `js/projectStore.js` and the Builder's own upload plumbing. Verified via Playwright end-to-end: upload a 5.7MB test photo as Hero Image → `localStorage` write succeeds (down from ~7.7MB base64 to ~1.8MB) with zero `setItem` errors → explicit Save → full page reload → reopen the World → Hero Image field shows the restored image → Project card (with a Thumbnail also uploaded) continues showing it → the empty Holder in a Scene renders the actual restored photo (pixel-sampled, not the generic placeholder colour) identically in Working View and Runtime Preview → Theme representation preview still renders. Full regression across every prior AV/AP/Slice/Validation/Build/Reorder/Project-Card suite passes unchanged; zero console errors; no Engine V2/Scene Model/rendering changes.)
- Authoring Validation AV-010 — text editable bounds now auto-size to rendered width, not just height (a direct extension of AV-006, found continuing Museum Theme authoring: "New text" → "Big Tree" rendered correctly but the selection/drag box stayed at the full declared wrap-width). **Root cause**: AV-006's `textFootprint(ctx, layer, graph)` only ever measured height (line count × line height); it still returned the declared `rect.w`/`rect.x` untouched, so a short line of text kept the old, much-wider invisible box regardless of content. **Fix**: `textFootprint` now also measures the widest wrapped line via `ctx.measureText` and returns that as `w` (capped at the declared wrap width, since wrapping still can't render wider than its own container), with `x` offset per `align` exactly as `_paintLayer` computes `tx` (`left`→`rect.x`, `center`→centred within `rect.w`, `right`→flush with `rect.x+rect.w`) — reusing the same `_wrapLines` call so it can never drift from the real paint, matching AV-006's own one-source-of-truth pattern. `worldBuilderApp.js`'s drag-clamp now clamps `position.x` too (previously only `position.y`): since the footprint's x-offset from the declared box's own left edge is content/alignment-dependent but position-independent, it's computed once from the object's current position and reused to convert the footprint clamp back into a `position.x` clamp, correct for left/center/right alignment alike. Hit-testing and the selection outline already read `textFootprint` directly (AV-006), so both automatically inherit the width fix with no separate change. Only an explicit fixed-width text container (a capability this Builder hasn't built) would need to keep the declared box's width — by default every text Layer now auto-sizes to its content, per this ticket's own product principle. Verified via Playwright: "Big Tree" (short, left-aligned) measures a footprint ~0.155 of canvas width vs. the declared 0.7 — over 4× narrower, matching the selection outline visibly hugging the glyphs; dragging the object now reaches x≈0.845 toward the right edge (previously capped near 0.3 by the old wide box). One prior AV-006 test needed its own click-target x-coordinate corrected (it assumed the old, incorrectly-wide hit area) — not a regression, the exact intended consequence of this fix; re-verified AV-006's own original height-based scenario still passes unchanged. Full regression across every prior suite passes unchanged; zero console errors; Runtime rendering (`render()`/`_paintLayer`) byte-for-byte unchanged — only an additive, non-drawing query function was extended, no Engine V2/Scene Model change.)
- Authoring Validation AV-011 — rich text emoji authoring, via the existing EmojiPicker rather than a second picker (Museum Theme authoring needed decorative inline symbols — "The Big Tree 🌳," "By Vihaan 🧒" — with no convenient way to insert them). **Investigation**: `js/emojiPicker.js` already exists and is already wired onto every Text Element field in the main Studio app (Sprint 9.6) — a small, self-contained module (`EmojiPicker.wrap(el)`) that wraps an existing `<input>`/`<textarea>` with a toggle button + emoji grid, inserting at the cursor and dispatching a real `input` event on the same element so it persists through whatever save path the field already had, with zero knowledge of the caller's own state. This is exactly "the simplest solution that provides a smooth authoring experience" the ticket asked for, so no new picker was built. **Implementation**: World Builder's `index.html` now loads `js/emojiPicker.js` alongside the other reused Studio Runtime scripts; `world-builder.css` gained the same `.emoji-picker-*` rules the main app's `css/style.css` already has, ported to Builder's own `--wb-*` variables (`--wb-border`/`--wb-cream`/`--wb-gold`/`--wb-paper`/`--wb-shadow`/`--wb-sand`) so the toggle/panel match Builder's theme rather than the main app's; `worldBuilderApp.js`'s Text Layer panel wraps its existing "Words" `_textarea(...)` with `EmojiPicker.wrap(...)` before mounting it in the field group — no change to the textarea's own `input` handler, since EmojiPicker drives it through the identical event path a real keystroke would. Canvas `fillText` already renders emoji glyphs natively (a font/rendering-engine concern, not something Engine V2 needed to do anything for), so Working View and Runtime Preview show them identically with no renderer change. Verified via Playwright end-to-end: the 😊 toggle appears on the Words field, opens a 40-emoji grid, inserting one appends it into the textarea and immediately persists to the Scene Layer's `text`; both canvases render it identically; a full page reload and Scene reopen (AV-008's resume-context) shows the emoji-bearing text intact; a built Scene Package (Engine V2 Build) contains the emoji correctly UTF-8-encoded in its JSON. Full regression across every prior suite passes unchanged; zero console errors; no Engine V2/Scene Model/rendering changes — the module is a Builder-only UI affordance reused as-is.)
- Builder V3 Experience Studio — Milestone 1: Foundation terminology, Holder renamed to Place (per `docs/BUILDER_V3_EXPERIENCE_STUDIO.md`'s frozen Canon Decisions and the "Foundation (Final)" implementation-kickoff instruction: Foundation is `World → Scene → Place(s)`, a Builder authoring-language change only, explicitly not a new Engine ownership tier — "internally, Engine V2 may continue using the existing Holder implementation if appropriate"). Scoped precisely to Engine V2's Scene Editor Place activity in `tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`/`js/projectModel.js`: every Builder-facing string a Theme Author sees (`_renderPlacePanel`'s heading/intro/empty-state/Add button, `_renderHolderPanel`'s "Place Name" field/Padding help text/Remove-and-back buttons, the Scene Header's Place count, the Place Boundary construction guide label) now says Place; the two data-level default names a new Holder is seeded with (`_holdersFor` for a fresh Scene Template, `addHolder` for one added later) changed from `'Holder'`/`'Holder N'` to `'Place'`/`'Place N'`, since those defaults are themselves user-visible text until a Theme Author renames one. Internal identifiers — `holder`, `findHolder`/`updateHolder`/`addHolder`/`deleteHolder`, `scene.holders`, `holder.frame`/`.position`/`.size` — are deliberately unchanged, exactly as the instruction permits, since renaming them would be pure internal churn with no Theme-Author-visible benefit and higher regression risk across a 4700-line file. The legacy Engine V1 Layouts/Layer-Packs screens' own, unrelated "Holder Area"/"Holder" strings (`_renderLayoutsPanel`'s static diagram, Layer Pack's Layer Target vocabulary) are deliberately left untouched — a different, older concept (Engine V1's Representation/Layout/Frame/Layer-Pack pipeline, `docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` §6's "remains legacy, unmodified"), not Engine V2's Place. Verified via Playwright: the Place activity's empty-state, Add-a-Place, selected-Place panel (including a freshly-template-seeded Place and a newly-added one), and the Scene Header's Place count all show zero occurrences of the word "Holder"; full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and the AV-001/AV-003/AV-006/runtime/validation/build/reorder suites all pass unchanged, confirming the rename is copy-only with no behavioral or rendering change. First of several incremental, independently-verified milestones toward the full Experience Studio — Experience data model, Nursery/Gallery, Experience Home navigation, the Inspector, and the Graduation workflow follow in subsequent commits, per the implementation brief's own "many small validated commits over one large rewrite" instruction.)
- Builder V3 Experience Studio — Milestone 2: Experience Foundation + Experience Home (Parts 1-5 of `docs/BUILDER_V3_EXPERIENCE_STUDIO.md`'s implementation kickoff; explicitly architectural — establishes the foundation every later milestone builds on, not a finished authoring experience). **Part 1 — data model**: new `js/services/experienceSchema.js` holds a Builder-only, open `EXPERIENCE_TYPES` vocabulary (Frame/Decoration/Atmosphere/Lighting/Text Style) deliberately separate from `engineSchema.js`, since Experience is explicitly not an Engine V2 Canon concept; `js/projectModel.js` gained `experiences`/`findExperience`/`setExperience`/`addExperience`/`updateExperience`/`deleteExperience`/`validateExperiences`, persisted as `experiences/<id>.json` + a lazily-reconciled `experienceOrder` following the exact `_ordered` pattern `frameOrder`/`sceneOrder` already use, plus a `_ensureExperienceDefaults` read-time migration hook so a project saved before Experiences existed never crashes. Every Experience is created Nurturing; `deleteExperience` refuses anything else (Canon Decision #9 — Delete exists only for Nurturing Experiences), enforced at this one choke point rather than left to the UI. `validateExperiences` is a plain, standalone hook — not yet wired into the Validation screen (Milestone 3's own "Validation UX changes" scope) — that skips Nurturing Experiences entirely, since they aren't part of the Theme yet. **Part 2 — Global Navigation**: `Experiences` (🌟) becomes a permanent destination between Scenes and Validation. **Part 3 — Experience Home**: a new `_renderExperiencesPanel` with two creative spaces, both reusing the proven `.wb-scene-library-grid`/`.wb-scene-card` visual language rather than inventing a second card system — **The Gallery** ("what can I use today?", Theme Experiences only) and **The Nursery** ("what am I still growing?", Nurturing ideas only, never mixed with the Gallery per Canon Decisions #4/#5); Working View shows the same generic World-identity card already used for an empty Overview, since Experience Home has no single rendered page of its own to show there. **Part 4 — Experience Cards**: domain-sensitive — a Gallery card shows preview/name/description/type/attachment/ownership(lifecycle)/usage/tags; a Nursery card deliberately omits ownership and usage, since neither concept exists yet for an unpromoted idea (usage is hardcoded to "Used by 0 Hosts" in the Gallery this milestone, since nothing can attach until Milestone 3). **Part 5 — placeholder creation**: a minimal inline form (Name/Type/Intended Attachment/Description) reachable only from the Nursery's "+ New Experience," saving via `addExperience` and always landing Nurturing — no Inspector, no Graduation, no attach-to-Place/Scene, no Reuse Existing, no Usage Explorer, all explicitly out of this milestone's scope per its own brief. Verified via Playwright end-to-end: the Gallery's honest empty state (with a direct "Go to the Nursery" bridge, never a dead end) and the Nursery's own empty state; creating "Wax Seal" (Decoration, Free) and seeing it appear immediately with the correct Nursery-omitted fields; a full page reload and Scene-list reopen showing the Experience intact; Delete removing it correctly. Full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and the AV-001/AV-003/AV-006/runtime/validation/build/reorder/place-rename suites all pass unchanged; zero unexpected console errors; no Engine V2/Runtime/rendering change — this milestone is entirely new, additive Builder data and UI, with Frame/Decoration/Text's existing authoring paths completely untouched.)
- Builder V3 Experience Studio — Milestone 3: Experience Authoring (completes the Creative Journey from `docs/BUILDER_V3_EXPERIENCE_STUDIO.md`: Inspector, Graduation, Ownership, Attachment, Contextual Authoring, Usage Explorer, Reuse Existing, and Validation integration, all built and Playwright-verified together). **Terminology review**: Milestone 1/2's own retrospective found "draft" still describing World Projects while Experiences already said Nurturing — `js/projectStore.js`'s two status-assignment sites now write `'growing'`, with a defensive read-time fallback in `worldBuilderApp.js` so an already-saved `'draft'` project displays correctly with no migration write; `templates.js`'s unrelated "Drafts"/"draft" tags on the Sketchbook template (describing the *kind* of artwork, not Builder's own lifecycle concept) are deliberately left alone. **Data model** (`js/projectModel.js`): `graduateToPersonal(project, id, sceneId)`/`graduateToPublic(project, id)` implement the frozen fork — Nurturing goes directly to Personal (recording which Scene) or straight to Public; Personal may later choose Public; there is no reverse path, enforced at the model layer, not just the UI. Milestone 2's placeholder singular `host` field is replaced by a real `attachments` array (a Public Experience may attach to many Hosts at once) — a safe, lossless migration since Milestone 2 shipped no attachment workflow at all, so every existing `host` was already null. `attachExperience`/`detachExperience` enforce real ownership rules (Nurturing can never attach; Personal may only attach within its own `scopeSceneId`) and validate the target Scene/Place actually exists; `usageOf` resolves every attachment to real Scene/Place names for the Usage Explorer. **The mirroring bridge** (`_syncExperienceAttachments`) is a compatibility shortcut into Engine V2's existing, unmodified rendering mechanisms — never a change to `engineRuntime.js` or the Scene Model. Investigation found only two real projection targets exist today: a Place's single Frame slot (Engine Canon §9) and a Scene's Layer array (Engine Canon §7) — there is no Holder Layer mechanism yet for anything else to attach to a Place (Scene Model §7, still an open question, not resolved here). This is disclosed honestly rather than papered over: `js/services/experienceSchema.js`'s `EXPERIENCE_TYPES` now carries a `renders: {attached, free}` flag per type — Frame mirrors into the Place's `frame` field when Attached; Decoration/Text mirror into a Scene Layer (tagged with a new, additive `sourceExperienceId` back-reference) when Free; Atmosphere/Lighting/Text Style record real attachments (Usage still works) but paint nothing yet, since Engine V2 has no rendering concept for them at any granularity — the Inspector shows an honest inline note whenever a chosen type+attachment combination has no render path. Also found and corrected: the approved Experience Types vocabulary (Frame/Decoration/Atmosphere/Lighting/Text Style) had no type for actual text *content* (only "Text Style," which is styling-only) — Museum Theme's real Museum Caption need requires one, so a "Text" type was added, additively, alongside Text Style rather than overloading it. `validateExperiences` extended: every attachment must reference a real Scene/Place; a Personal Experience's attachments must stay within its own `scopeSceneId`. **Experience Inspector**: clicking any card (Gallery or Nursery) selects it and replaces the grid with its Inspector, exactly like selecting a Place already does — no dedicated Experience workspace (Blueprint §6.1's philosophy, restated). Properties render per Type, mirroring the exact field shape the existing Frame/Decoration/Text authoring surfaces already use, so editing here and editing the old surface never disagree about what a field means; every edit re-syncs any live attachment immediately. Ownership renders the frozen fork (Graduate to Personal/Public side by side while Nurturing; only Make Public while Personal; neither while Public) with no reverse-path action anywhere in the UI. Usage Explorer lists every real attachment, each entry doubling as one-click Detach; the Attach control is the same one mechanism for "attach somewhere new" and "Reuse Existing" browsed from the Gallery. **Contextual authoring** (Place's Frame picker, Decorations'/Text's no-selection states): an "Experiences" block offers "+ Add Experience" (creates Nurturing, then immediately graduates to Personal scoped to this Scene and attaches in one motion — a disclosed convenience, since a Theme Author clicking this wants it here, now, not a trip to the Nursery) and "Reuse Existing Experience" (browses already-Public, type-compatible Experiences and attaches directly); once attached, the block shows "Attached: `<name>`" with a one-click "Open in Experience Home →" — the old Frame/Decoration/Text authoring stays fully functional alongside this (no destructive migration), giving both paths side by side while Experience-first authoring becomes preferred. **Validation**: a new "Experiences" section mirrors the existing "Scenes (Engine V2)" pattern exactly — its own separate report, run alongside the other two, Nursery items excluded entirely. Verified end-to-end via Playwright across every piece: Nurturing cannot attach; graduation requires and records a Scene for Personal; attaching a Frame Experience sets the Place's real frame reference and creates a correctly-synced mirrored Frame record, visible immediately in both Working View and Runtime Preview; a Personal Experience is correctly refused attachment outside its own Scene; a Decoration/Text Experience attach creates a correctly-tagged mirrored Scene Layer; a full Museum Theme walkthrough (a Frame Experience reused across two Places in a "Gallery Wall," a Text Experience for a Museum Caption, a Decoration Experience for a Wax Seal, all created via contextual authoring) produces a clean Validation report with zero console errors; a Milestone-2-era project record (pre-`attachments`, `host: null`) loads and migrates correctly with no crash, confirming existing projects keep working. Full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and every prior AV/runtime/validation/build/reorder/place-rename/experience-home suite passes unchanged. No Engine V2/Runtime/Story Studio change; no Builder navigation redesign; no new product concepts beyond what the frozen design already specified.)
- Builder V3 Experience Studio — Canon Alignment Sprint / Product Model Purification (a deliberate pause on Experience feature work, run immediately after Milestone 3, to align implementation with the approved paper design rather than add capability — "the objective is not more capability, the objective is conceptual clarity," per the sprint's own closing instruction; produced `docs/BUILDER_V3_CANON_ALIGNMENT_REPORT.md`, the permanent four-section checkpoint (Confirmed Product Concepts / Engine Adapter Concepts / Resolved Inconsistencies / Open Questions) this entry summarizes). **Hosted By replaces Attachment**: the binary Attached/Free axis (`js/services/experienceSchema.js`'s `EXPERIENCE_ATTACHMENTS`, `js/projectModel.js`'s `exp.attachment`) is replaced by the frozen three-way product model — Place / Scene / Free (`EXPERIENCE_HOSTS`, `exp.hostedBy`) — because Milestone 3's binary model had no way to express "fills the whole Scene" (e.g. a full-bleed background), a real product-model gap surfaced by implementation, not a bug; the migration is lossless (`_ensureExperienceDefaults`: old `'attached'` → `'place'`, everything else → `'free'`). "Hosted by Scene" is wired to the pre-existing full-bleed background fill mechanism (`setSceneBackground`) rather than any new Engine capability — `decoration` is the one Experience Type whose `renders` map gained a real `scene: true`, since its existing `color` property is exactly what that fill needs. Every author-facing string was updated to match (Card meta line via a new shared `_hostedByLabel` helper, Inspector heading, the renamed Host/Reuse picker — "Attach"/"Attach Here" → "Host Here" — the contextual "Attached: `<name>`" note → "Hosting: `<name>`", and the Nursery quick-create form's "Intended Attachment" field → "Hosted By"); the internal `exp.attachments` array (real usage/placement records) was deliberately left unrenamed, since it's never shown to an author as a raw field name and renaming it would be pure internal churn the sprint's own "remove leakage, not capability" framing argues against. **Engine Adapter boundary made explicit** (Objective 5's "Experience ↓ Frame ↓ Scene Layer ↓ Runtime" chain): `projectModel.js`'s `_syncExperienceAttachments` is now doc-comment-labeled as *the* Engine Adapter — the one function allowed to know a Place-hosted Frame projects onto a Place's `frame` slot, a Scene-hosted Experience onto the background fill Layer, and a Free-hosted Decoration/Text onto a tagged Scene Layer; nothing else in the Inspector/Card/picker code touches this translation. `experienceSchema.js`'s `renders` map (now `{place, scene, free}` per Type, renamed from `rendersWhenAttached` to `rendersWhenHosted`) is documented as Engine Adapter *metadata riding on* a product field — it discloses what the current adapter can paint, but Hosted By itself stays a pure product choice regardless. Two literal author-facing "Engine V2" wording leaks (the Inspector's two disclosure notes in `_renderExperienceProperties`) were found via a full audit and rewritten in plain product language ("doesn't appear on the page yet — that's coming in a future Builder release"); every other "Engine V2" occurrence in the codebase was confirmed to be a code comment, never rendered UI text, and left alone, since the mandate was about what an author sees. **Type field reviewed, not restructured** (Objective 3): confirmed the field currently serves two purposes at once — a legitimate creative decision (which Properties fields the Inspector shows) and an Engine Adapter dispatch key (which mirror routine runs) — documented as an Open Question rather than split into two fields, since doing so would be new data-model capability, out of this sprint's paused scope. **Experience → Objects deferred** (Objective 4): confirmed today's one-implicit-shape-per-Type design is not a prohibited "specialized subclass," but is also not yet the frozen model's `objects[]` array; building that this sprint would have been new capability, so it's recorded as an Open Question instead. Atmosphere/Lighting/Text Style (zero adapter, zero Museum Theme usage) were kept per "do not remove capabilities" and disclosed honestly as reserved vocabulary, also an Open Question. `docs/BUILDER_V3_EXPERIENCE_STUDIO.md` gained a new Part 2.1 (Canon Alignment Addendum) with a translation table for reading every earlier Part's "Attachment" language as "Hosted By," plus a v1.2 Change History entry — chosen deliberately over silently rewriting all 19 "Attachment" occurrences scattered through the document's prose, so the terminology change is traceable rather than silently reinterpreted. Verified via Playwright: Place/Scene/Free hosting all round-trip correctly (a Place-hosted Frame still sets the real `holder.frame` reference; a Scene-hosted Decoration correctly sets the Scene's background color; a Free-hosted Text still mirrors to a tagged Scene Layer); the Inspector and Gallery/Nursery cards show zero "Attached"/"Attachment" wording and correct "Hosted by X" copy throughout; a Milestone-2-era legacy record (`attachment: 'free'`) migrates correctly to `hostedBy: 'free'` with no crash; full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and every prior Milestone 2/3/AV/AP/runtime/validation/build/reorder/place-rename suite passes unchanged (one test script, `wb_m3_inspector_test.js`, was itself updated for the intentional `'attached'` → `'place'` enum rename — not a product regression). No Engine V2/Scene Model/Runtime change; no new Experience capability added, per this sprint's own "pause feature development" instruction.)
- Builder V3 MEP — Experience Builder Foundation (the first Builder MEP implementation milestone, explicitly scoped down twice during planning to stay additive: no Experience persistence redesign, no Parts array, no data migration, no Type field removal, no new Builder concepts such as Recipes — "reuse the existing implementation wherever possible," per the approved plan's own governing rule, "can the Museum Theme be authored more naturally after this change?"). **Host-aware Bounds** (new Builder Canon rule — the Host determines the bounds): the Experience Inspector gained a "Bounds" section, inserted right after Properties — Hosted by Scene shows a static "Inherited from Scene (read-only)" note, Hosted by Place shows "Inherited from Place (read-only)," and only Hosted by Free shows real, editable X %/Y %/Width %/Height % sliders; those Free sliders read and write the *same* mirrored Scene Layer's existing `position`/`size` that Working View has always dragged (AV-006/AV-010) — a second, synced entry point onto data that already existed, never a duplicate store. `js/projectModel.js` gained exactly one small, additive export, `findMirroredSceneLayer` (exposing the pre-existing private `_findMirroredLayer` lookup rather than duplicating it), and a new `_experienceFreeLayer(exp)` helper in `worldBuilderApp.js` resolves an Experience's first Free usage entry to its real mirrored Layer via that export + the existing `findSceneLayer` (for defaults reconciliation). **Decoration Image**: an optional `image` property (a data URI) sits alongside Decoration's existing `glyph`/`color` in the same flat `properties` bag — per explicit instruction, Image and Glyph are deliberately *not* mutually exclusive in the underlying model (both are simply optional properties, "permissive for future evolution"), only in which one the Runtime prefers when painting. The Experience Properties panel's Decoration branch gained one field reusing `_assetUploadRow`/`_fileInputUpload` verbatim — the exact same controls Overview's Thumbnail/Hero Image fields already use — no new upload infrastructure of any kind. **Runtime** (`js/services/engineRuntime.js`): `_paintLayer`'s decoration branch is extended, not rewritten — it now checks for a loaded Image first, via a new optional `resolveLayerImage` callback threaded onto `load()`'s 4th parameter (mirroring the existing `resolveFrame`/`representativeImage` "caller resolves, this module only draws" pattern exactly, so the module stays pure and synchronous), and falls back to the pre-existing glyph `fillText` when none is available or not yet decoded. `worldBuilderApp.js` gained a small, generic image cache (`_resolveLayerImage`/`_layerImageCache`), the identical async-decode-then-redraw shape EV-002's `_representativeArtworkImage` already established for the one Holder-artwork slot, now generalized to any Scene Layer's `image` field. Type is deliberately unchanged and unremoved throughout — every Experience still carries a `type`, still read internally by the Engine Adapter for dispatch, exactly as before this milestone; "Parts" (Color/Border/Image/Text) stayed a conceptual label only, never a stored array. Verified via Playwright: Place-hosted and Scene-hosted Experiences show the correct read-only Bounds note with zero editable fields; a Free-hosted Text Experience shows all four editable bounds fields and a Width % drag correctly writes the real mirrored Layer's `size.w` (confirmed via direct model inspection); a Decoration Experience's Image field uploads correctly, sets `properties.image` without clearing `properties.glyph`, and the Runtime visibly prefers the uploaded Image over the glyph in both Working View and Runtime Preview (pixel-sampled against the exact known decoded color of the test fixture); full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and every prior Milestone/Canon-Alignment/AV/AP/runtime/validation/build/reorder/place-rename suite passes unchanged; zero console errors. No Engine V2/Scene Model redesign; no Parts persistence; no migration; no Type removal; no new Builder concepts.)
- Builder V3 MEP — Museum Authoring Complete (the second Builder MEP implementation milestone, driven by a hands-on authoring pass — building the actual Museum Theme through the Builder exactly as a Theme Author would, rather than a feature-by-feature review — per the milestone's own "does this help an author build the Museum Theme?" test.
