Every fix below is additive/corrective; no new Builder concepts, no architecture change. **(1) Starter Scene name/shape mismatch**: the Artwork Gallery template's seeded Scene was named "Showcase" ("big and bold, the classic gallery look") but defaulted to Portrait, since its Engine Scene Template (`single-holder`) always does; `TEMPLATE_STARTER_SCENE` gained an optional `aspect` override applied via the existing `setSceneAspect` right after seeding — Showcase now seeds Landscape. **(2) Legacy Frame picker/Usage desync — a real correctness bug**: the Place panel's pre-Experience "FRAME" picker (kept functional since Milestone 3's "both paths side by side" decision) wrote `holder.frame` directly via `updateHolder`, bypassing `attachExperience`/`detachExperience` — switching or clearing a Place's Frame through that picker left a hosting Experience's `attachments` record stale, so Usage/Gallery bookkeeping silently lied about where an Experience was actually hosted. Fixed by making `_setHolderFrame` Experience-aware: detaches any currently-hosting Frame Experience properly before applying a new selection, attaches through the real mechanism when the newly-picked Frame is itself Experience-backed. **(3) Decorations list leaked Text layers**: `_renderDecorationsPanel`'s existing-items filter was `kind !== 'fill'` instead of `kind === 'decoration'`, so Text layers appeared misfiled inside the Decorations activity; fixed, and the card icon now shows an uploaded Image (Prompt 1's Decoration Image support) instead of only ever reading `.glyph`. **(4) New Decorations/Text spawned dead-center**: `addSceneLayer`'s default `position` was `{0.4, 0.4}` — directly on top of a Scene's usual Place — so a freshly-created Free Experience was often invisible or accidentally selected instead of the artwork right after creation; moved to `{0.38, 0.82}` (clear of a typical Place, still exactly as draggable), fixed at both call sites (the default itself, and the standalone "Add a Decoration" glyph-picker's hardcoded duplicate) — this also serendipitously improved the Experience-based Text creation path's default position to better match a real Museum Caption's actual below-the-photo placement. **(5) Inspector field grouping**: the Experience Properties panel was the one Inspector still stacking every field full-width; paired via the existing `_fieldRow`/`_buildFieldGroup` convention Frames/Layouts/Overview already use (Mat Width|Frame Thickness, Border Colour|Wall Tone for Frame; Glyph|Colour for Decoration; Font|Alignment, Font Size|Colour for Text/Text Style). **(6) Usage completeness**: nothing told an author that editing a reused Public Experience silently changes every place it's hosted; `_renderExperienceProperties` now shows "Editing this updates everywhere it's hosted — N places right now" whenever real usage exceeds one, reading the same `usageOf` data "Used In" already lists. **(7) Gallery card previews**: every card showed the same generic Type icon regardless of content, so several Frame variations or Decorations were indistinguishable at a glance; a Frame card now shows its real border-colour swatch (same style the legacy Frame picker uses) and a Decoration card shows its real Image or Glyph. **Considered and deliberately declined**: fast-pathing "Hosted by Scene" creation from the Decorations panel's contextual quick-create — the panel's own pre-existing dedicated Background colour field already fully covers the real per-Scene wall-colour need with zero ceremony, and Scene-hosted Experiences remain reachable via the Nursery's full form plus Reuse for the rarer cross-Scene-consistency case; adding a Hosted-By selector to the fast quick-create form would cut against "smooth creation flow" for no Museum-Theme-blocking gain. Verified via a new consolidated Playwright regression covering all seven fixes plus a full end-to-end Museum Theme authoring pass (Scene → Place → Frame Experience → Text Experience → Decoration Experience → cross-scene reuse → Usage Explorer → Gallery → Validation → Build → Publish, with a 900-sample pixel-parity check confirming zero difference between Working View and Runtime Preview); full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and every prior Milestone/Canon-Alignment/MEP/AV/AP/runtime/validation/build/reorder/place-rename suite passes unchanged (one test's own hardcoded pixel-sample coordinates needed updating for the intentional spawn-position fix — not a regression; one pre-existing timing-flaky test confirmed flaky on the unmodified baseline too via `git stash`, unrelated to this milestone). No Engine V2/Scene Model/Runtime redesign; every fix reuses existing mechanisms.)
- Builder V3 MEP Freeze — Release Candidate Audit (the closing MEP milestone: "treat Builder V3 as if it is shipping tomorrow." Five audits, not another feature pass. **Audit 1 (fresh authoring pass) surfaced this milestone's most significant finding**: a systemic data-loss bug across all three Experience-backed legacy editing surfaces kept intentionally functional since Milestone 3 ("both paths side by side") — the Text Layer panel, the Decoration Layer panel's Name field, and the "Manage Frames" screen all wrote directly to the mirrored Layer/Frame record (`updateSceneLayer`/`setFrameField`/`setFrameFieldValue`), bypassing the owning Experience's own `properties` entirely; since the Engine Adapter (`_mirrorSceneLayer`/`_mirrorFrame`) unconditionally re-derives the mirror from `properties` on every sync, the next unrelated Experience-Inspector edit silently discarded whatever had just been typed or changed through the legacy surface — reproduced with real data (a typed Museum Caption's words vanishing after an unrelated Colour edit; a Manage-Frames Wall Tone change reverting after an unrelated Shadow edit). Fixed identically in all three places, mirroring the exact adapter-routing pattern the previous milestone already established for the legacy Frame picker: when Experience-backed, field writes route through `updateExperience`/`updateExperienceProperty` instead of the mirror directly. A related bug found in the same investigation: `_mirrorSceneLayer`'s `text`-branch sync omitted `color` entirely, so a Text Experience's Colour field persisted but silently never rendered — fixed by adding it to the synced set. **Audit 2 (consistency sweep)** found the Canon Alignment Sprint's Attachment→Hosted-By rename had missed one button ("Create & Attach" → "Create & Host"), and normalized the Experience Inspector's delete button to "Delete this Experience" (matching Place/Decoration/Text's "Remove this X" convention while keeping the deliberately stronger "Delete" verb — Canon Decision #9's one real, permanent deletion); confirmed zero "Engine V1"/"Engine V2"/"Scene Layer" in any literal UI string, and confirmed the one remaining "Holder" occurrence (`_renderLayoutsPanel`'s "Holder Area" diagram) is unreachable from any UI control in Builder V3 (no Global Navigation entry or bridge link since Slice 1) — left as the pre-existing, already-documented dead code it is. **Audit 3 (Working View vs. Runtime pixel-level review)**: a full-canvas diff (not sampled) on a fully-authored Scene with nothing selected found 12,240 differing pixels out of 1,458,000, traced to a thin border-shaped pattern spanning 976 of 1,080 rows — matching exactly the known, always-on Safe Area guide (Blueprint §7, Working-View-only by design), not any accidental content difference; confirmed intentional, left unchanged. **Audit 4 (Experience System workflow completeness)** verified creation/editing/hosting/reuse/graduation/deletion/validation/publishing all function correctly via the fixes above plus full regression. **Audit 5 (regression)**: full existing suite plus a new end-to-end proof — authored a complete 3-Scene Museum Theme (Showcase/Portrait/Quote) with a Public Frame Experience reused across two Scenes, a Text Experience Museum Caption, a Decoration Experience Wax Seal, and a Scene-hosted Quote background — reaching a clean Validation (0 errors, 0 warnings, every category), a successful Scene Package Build, a successful World Package Build, and a fully functional Publish screen. Full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and every prior Milestone/Canon-Alignment/MEP/AV/AP/runtime/validation/build/reorder/place-rename suite passes unchanged. No Engine V2/Scene Model/Runtime redesign; no new Builder concepts; every fix reuses the exact adapter-routing pattern already established for the legacy Frame picker. Builder V3 MEP is frozen as of this milestone — see the Final Deliverable report for the full MEP Status checklist, remaining-issues statement, deferred-ideas list, and release recommendation.)
- Builder V3.1 — Universal Experience Authoring (removes the biggest remaining source of Museum Theme authoring friction found across the MEP milestones: the Experience Type picker, which forced an author to choose an implementation category — Frame/Decoration/Text/Atmosphere/Lighting/Text Style — before a creative idea even existed. **Type selector removed**: the Nursery's "+ New Experience" form no longer shows a Type field; every new Experience internally defaults to the existing Decoration implementation (`js/services/experienceSchema.js`'s `DEFAULT_EXPERIENCE_TYPE`) — an Engine Adapter detail the author never sees; the Experience Card and Inspector header both dropped their Type label to match. **Universal content**: every Experience — new or pre-existing — now exposes the same four content sections in its Inspector, each with its own Properties and Transform (Move/Resize): 📝 Text (Content/Font/Size/Weight/Alignment/Colour/Opacity), 🖼 Image (Upload/Replace/Remove/Preview/Fit/Opacity), 🎭 Graphics (a reusable SVG/PNG visual asset, no Fit control), and 🎨 Colour (Colour Picker/Opacity/Transparent checkbox, so an Experience can be pure Text/Image/Graphics with no fill at all). Implemented additively — `js/services/experienceSchema.js` gained `defaultUniversalContent()`, a set of entirely new namespaced property keys (`textContent`/`textFont`/`textSize`/`textWeight`/`textAlign`/`textColor`/`textOpacity`/`textX/Y/W/H`, the equivalent `image*`/`graphic*` sets, `colorValue`/`colorOpacity`/`colorTransparent`) merged into every type's `defaultProperties()`, deliberately distinct from every legacy field name so a pre-existing Frame's mat/border/wallTone/shadow fields and a pre-existing Decoration's/Text's legacy fields are never touched; `js/projectModel.js`'s `_ensureExperienceDefaults` gained a read-time `_ensureUniversalContentDefaults` migration (one-time per Experience) that seeds the new fields and copies a legacy Decoration's `image`→`imageSrc` / legacy Text's `text`/`font`/`fontSize`/`align`/`color`→`textContent`/`textFont`/`textSize`/`textAlign`/`textColor` — a legacy Decoration's `color`→`colorValue` is copied but `colorTransparent` deliberately stays at its fresh default (`true`) rather than flipping to visible, since `color` was already inert on a Decoration Layer and flipping it live would have been an undisclosed visual regression, not a migration. **Engine Adapter extended, not replaced**: Scene-/Free-hosted Experiences now sync through a new `_syncUniversalContent` (Place-hosting stays Frame-only, a disclosed gap — no Holder Layer stack exists yet for anything else to project onto) that mirrors up to four tagged Scene Layers per Experience, one per populated Text/Image/Graphics/Colour section, reusing the exact unmodified Layer kinds Engine V2 already renders (`fill` for Colour, `text` for Text, `decoration` with `.image` set for both Image and Graphics — the same mechanism Builder V3 MEP's Decoration Image support already proved out); an empty section mirrors nothing. Colour has no Transform of its own — its rect is the live bounding box of whichever Text/Image/Graphics is currently populated, recomputed on every sync. A pre-existing Experience's single untagged mirrored Layer is *claimed* in place (same position, re-tagged) the first time it's touched under the new model rather than orphaned while a duplicate is created at a default rect — verified directly. The Free-hosted "Bounds" editor from Builder V3 MEP is superseded by each section's own Transform; the Inspector's Bounds section is now purely informational for all three Hosted-By values. `js/services/engineRuntime.js`'s `_paintLayer` gained a generic `layer.opacity` read (`ctx.globalAlpha`, defaulting to 1 so every pre-existing Layer renders byte-identically) and an `imageFit`-aware `layer.fit` read (defaulting to 'fit', matching prior hardcoded behaviour) — both apply uniformly across Layer kinds, not as per-content-type special cases. **P0 image upload bug, root-caused not patched**: instrumented the full pipeline (upload → Asset → Experience property → Engine Adapter mirror → Working View → Runtime Preview) and found all six links already worked correctly; the actual defect was the Inspector's own upload row never re-rendering after a successful upload, so it visibly stayed on "Upload" with no thumbnail even though the upload had already fully succeeded everywhere else — exactly what reads as "the button doesn't work" to an author watching the one place they're looking. Fixed with a narrowly-scoped `onUploadProp(key)` (used only by Image/Graphics upload rows, not every Properties field) that re-renders the panel after persisting; `_assetUploadRow` also gained a Remove action, a side effect also reaching Overview's pre-existing Thumbnail/Hero Image rows. Gallery/Nursery cards now prefer whichever universal section is populated (Image, then Graphics, then a non-transparent Colour) over the old Type-icon fallback for their thumbnail. Verified via Playwright end to end: no Type field anywhere in creation; all four sections present with working Transform for every Experience regardless of legacy type (a legacy Frame Experience keeps its own dedicated fields too, unchanged); an Image upload's row updates immediately and the uploaded pixels render identically in Working View and Runtime Preview; a Colour fill renders correctly at the live content footprint once positioned clear of the Place; Graphics Opacity blends visibly; a hand-constructed pre-V3.1 legacy Decoration Experience migrates correctly on read, keeps rendering from its original untouched Layer until first touched, then claims that same Layer in place with no duplication; a full Museum Theme authoring pass (Frame Experience, Text → Museum Caption via the universal Text section, Decoration → Wax Seal) reaches a clean Validation, successful Scene and World Package Builds, and a functional Publish screen. `goldenBuild.js` passes 30/30 unchanged; zero console errors. No Engine V2/Scene Model/Runtime redesign beyond the two small, generic `_paintLayer` additions; no persistence redesign; the Engine Adapter boundary remains the one place a Builder-facing Experience is projected onto Engine V2's own, otherwise-unmodified rendering mechanisms.)
- Working View Experience Studio (restores the Builder's original two-view philosophy — Runtime Preview is always the Reader's complete published Scene, Working View is the Author's own isolated workspace — which Universal Experience Authoring had inadvertently left broken: `_workingViewIsIdentityCard()` returned `true` for the entire Experiences nav unconditionally, so selecting any Experience from the Gallery or Nursery still showed the plain World identity card in Working View, never the Experience itself, while Runtime Preview correctly kept showing the active Scene throughout. **Root cause**: `_experienceCard`'s click handler and the Inspector's "← Back"/"Delete this Experience" buttons all only ever called `_renderContextPanel()` (repaints the Context Inspector alone) instead of `_renderWorkspace()` (which also calls `_renderPreview()`) — Working View was structurally unreachable from Experience selection no matter how the isolated Studio itself was built; fixed at that exact source. **The isolated Studio**: a new `_renderExperienceStudio(exp)` crops Working View to just the selected Experience's own populated content — `js/projectModel.js` exports the same rect math the Engine Adapter already uses for a Free-hosted Colour fill's footprint (`experienceContentFootprint`), padded 18% and normalized to a ~900px canvas, independent of the rest of the Scene (a Nurturing Experience with no Scene at all renders identically). Colour fills the whole isolated canvas or shows a real checkerboard when Transparent; Image, Graphics, and Text all paint via one new export, `EngineV2Runtime.paintLayer` — the exact `_paintLayer` function `render()` already uses internally, reused directly rather than reimplemented. Each populated section gets a selection outline + resize handle (reusing the Scene editor's own `_drawSelectionOutline`) — Move and Resize for Text/Image/Graphics alike, a deliberately expanded affordance specific to this new isolated Studio (the Scene editor's own Working View and its reposition-only Decorations/Text convention are untouched). **Move/Resize dragging** is a second click-to-drag driver (`_experienceStudioDragState`), separate from the Scene editor's own `_holderDragState`, writing the dragged section's X/Y or W/H directly via `updateExperienceProperty` on every mousemove tick (verified live-syncing Runtime Preview — a moved image's pixels appear at their new location mid-drag, before mouseup) while redrawing the Studio against the same frozen stage/canvas size the gesture started with, never recomputing a fresh crop mid-drag (which would otherwise chase its own tail, since the very rect being dragged is part of what decides the crop) — the stage only re-settles to a fresh fit on mouseup, mirroring the Scene editor's own established freeze/mutate/persist shape exactly. Verified end to end via Playwright: selecting an Experience shows a small, correctly-cropped isolated canvas distinct from the full Scene's own dimensions while Runtime Preview keeps showing the complete Scene unchanged; Colour Transparent shows a real checkerboard; Image/Graphics uploads render immediately; dragging an uploaded Image moves it with Runtime Preview reflecting the new position mid-drag; "← Back" correctly restores the identity card; the Scene editor's own Working View is completely unaffected. Full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and every V3.1 verification script passes unchanged; zero console errors. No Engine V2/Scene Model/Runtime redesign; no new product concepts; Working View is the permanent Experience authoring workspace going forward.)
- Authoring Convergence Sprint (a pause-on-features, converge-toward-one-pipeline sprint — the Builder had two enrichment authoring systems, legacy Place/Decoration/Text → Scene Layer → Runtime and Experience → Engine Adapter → Runtime, and this sprint began closing that gap rather than widening it. **The two concrete parallel-creation paths converged**: the Decorations panel's glyph-picker grid and the Text panel's "➕ Add Text" button both used to call `addSceneLayer` directly, producing a plain Scene Layer with no Experience behind it. Both now call the same `addExperience` → `graduateToPersonal` → `attachExperience` sequence "+ Add Experience" already uses, landing on the new Experience's own Inspector immediately — a picked glyph is rasterized into a small PNG (`_rasterizeGlyphToDataURL`) stored as the Experience's Graphics section content (the Universal content model has no bare glyph concept of its own); "Add Text" seeds the Text section's `textContent` directly. **Runtime consistency**: a new `_experienceHostingStatus(exp)` compares an Experience's real Usage against the currently open Scene and shows a plain banner in the isolated Experience Studio whenever Working View and Runtime Preview would otherwise silently disagree ("Not yet hosted anywhere…" / "Hosted in `<Scene>` — open that Scene to see it in Runtime Preview"), nothing when they already match — a synchronization-status readout over existing `usageOf` data, not a new renderer. **Host Here redundancy fixed**: a Personal Experience scoped to one Scene and already hosted there now shows "Already hosted in `<Scene>` — nothing more to host here" instead of a redundant picker; otherwise the "Host Here" button recomputes live as the Scene/Place dropdowns change, reading "✓ Already Hosted Here" (disabled) once the selection matches a real Usage entry. **A disclosed, deliberately-deferred exception**: Frame's dual identity (a reusable Theme Asset shelf in its own right, and something an Experience can front-end) was investigated and left untouched — the sprint's own scope names only Decoration/Text as legacy entry points to converge, and Frame's Manage-Frames reorder/duplicate/delete identity is a materially bigger question; recorded as an open item in the new `docs/BUILDER_V3_CONVERGENCE_REPORT.md`. Verified via Playwright: clicking a Decoration glyph and "Add Text" both produce a real, correctly-attached Experience with zero orphan Scene Layers; the hosting-status banner and Host Here button/note both react correctly across hosted-here/hosted-elsewhere/never-hosted states; a full Museum Theme authoring pass using only the converged creation paths reaches a clean Validation and successful Scene/World Package Builds. Full regression across `goldenBuild.js` (30/30) and every prior Builder V3/V3.1/Working-View-Experience-Studio suite passes unchanged; zero console errors. No Engine V2/Scene Model/Runtime redesign; no second rendering implementation; no new Builder concepts.)

- Platform Integration Sprint — Builder → Studio (a proof sprint, not a feature sprint, per its own explicit "the objective is not to build more, the objective is to prove the platform" instruction — zero application code changed. Verified, end to end in one continuous Playwright session (one browser, two pages sharing one origin's `localStorage`, exactly how a real person would use two tabs — no mocks, no manual file copying, no `storageState()` serialization shortcut), the complete real handoff the platform has always intended: a Theme authored in World Builder (real Overview identity, two genuinely-content-bearing uploaded images, a real Frame Experience named "Emerald Frame" with a distinct border colour, created through Scene → Place → "+ Add Experience") passes Validation with 0 errors/warnings, Builds into a real 21.84 KB `.vtheme`, and Publishes via "Publish to Official Themes" straight into the shared `localStorage['vihu.themeRegistry.imported.v1']` key — the same key, same file, same origin Studio's own boot sequence already reads (`js/themeRegistry.js`'s `_loadImported()`), a mechanism implemented and documented in a much earlier sprint and now exercised for real rather than only asserted from code inspection. Opening Studio in a second page of the same browser context showed the theme already present among 9 registered themes with zero explicit import step; Studio's Creation Flow (Screen 1 "Showcase My Artwork" → Screen 2's Vihu Worlds row → the theme's own real Showcase/Portrait/Quote Representation carousel) found and used it exactly as any Official World would be found; a real second image (distinct from the Builder's own Hero Image) was uploaded into the new Story via the ordinary Upload Images → Picture Studio → Apply path; Studio's own five-stage Publish Studio (Read My Story → Almost Ready → Choose Story Destination → Publishing → Celebration, destination Story Carousel, format Instagram Portrait) produced a real, downloaded, inspected ZIP (`..._carousel_portrait.zip`, 228,521 bytes) whose `page-02.png` shows the uploaded artwork rendered at full Instagram Portrait resolution with the theme's own page background/footer/page-number — genuine Reader-facing output. Zero console errors on either page throughout. Two discovered, non-blocking findings are disclosed rather than fixed, per the sprint's own explicit "no Builder polish beyond issues that block the integration pipeline" scope: (1) the Artwork Gallery template's default Representations don't set `actions:['editCaption']`, so Studio's Context Panel showed no Title/Artist/Age/Date fields for this specific authored theme — a content-authoring completeness gap in `tools/world-builder/js/templates.js`'s starter data, already named as open technical debt in the Sprint B2.0 report, unrelated to this sprint's integration-pipeline scope; (2) a single-file image upload always creates a new page rather than filling an existing Representation page's placeholder in place — pre-existing, disclosed Sprint 10.0 behaviour, not an integration defect. Full report: `docs/PLATFORM_INTEGRATION_REPORT.md`.)

- AV-012 — Representation/Holder Frame Reference Integrity (a P0 correctness fix, found publishing the real Museum Theme: Validation correctly blocked Publish with "Representation 'showcase'/'portrait' — defaultFrame classic-white — Frame no longer exists." **Root cause traced, not assumed**: every Artwork-type World template seeds a starter Frame (Museum Gallery's `classic-white`, `templates.js`) and hardcodes it as the seeded Representations' `defaultFrame` at generation time; `addRepresentation()` (`js/projectModel.js`) does the same with `frames(project)[0].id` for any Representation added later. `deleteFrame()` — the only place a Frame record is ever removed (Manage Frames' 🗑) — deleted the Frame file and cleaned up the Builder-only `frameOrder` display list, but never scanned for or cleared anything that *referenced* the deleted id: a Representation's `defaultFrame`, or a Scene Holder's `frame` (the same class of dangling reference `EngineV2Validator` already separately checks for Holders). Once "Classic White" was replaced by a newly authored Frame during real Museum Theme authoring, both Representations kept silently pointing at the now-deleted id — a bug in `deleteFrame`, not in Validation, which was correctly reporting exactly the broken state Builder had created. **Fix, at the source**: `deleteFrame()` now clears (`null`, never a fabricated substitute id) any Representation `defaultFrame` or Scene Holder `frame` that pointed at the deleted Frame in the same operation that removes it, so no *new* dangling reference can ever be created going forward. **Automatic repair for Themes already carrying a legacy stale reference** (the real Museum Theme's actual state): a new `ProjectModel.reconcileFrameReferences(project)` — the same silent reconcile-on-read discipline `_ordered`/`_ensureHolderDefaults` already use elsewhere in this file — scans every Representation and every Scene Holder for a `defaultFrame`/`frame` that no longer resolves to a real Frame and clears it; `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `openWorkspace()` runs it the moment any Project is opened and persists immediately if anything needed repair, so an author never has to inspect internal ids or manually edit anything — Representations has no reachable Builder screen of its own to fix this by hand in the first place. Deliberately never "picks a replacement Frame" (that would be exactly the fabricated-substitute-id shortcut the fix rejects) — `null` is the schema's own pre-existing "no Frame chosen" state, identical to what a Representation with zero Frames already gets. Verified end to end via Playwright, reproducing the reported bug two ways rather than one: (1) creating a real Artwork Gallery project and deleting its seeded Frame the ordinary way confirms no dangling `defaultFrame` is ever created; (2) a hand-corrupted legacy-shaped project (a dangling `defaultFrame` *and* a dangling Holder `frame`, reproducing the exact reported state) is auto-repaired the instant it's reopened, then Validates with 0 errors, Builds a real package, and Publishes successfully into the shared ThemeRegistry — all on the pre-existing, already-authored Project, never a newly created test Theme. `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged, including its own negative fixture that intentionally ships a broken `defaultFrame` and must still fail Validation — this fix repairs a live Builder Project's own data, it never weakens or bypasses the validator itself.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint (a contract-hardening pass, not a feature sprint — Builder feature development stayed paused; "no new Builder capabilities, no new Studio capabilities, no redesigns, no speculative improvements, no Theme versioning" per its own Working Rules. Continued directly from the Platform Integration Sprint, auditing the complete Builder → Publish → Studio pipeline against the Museum Theme as reference, and produced the new canonical `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` — a field-by-field parity ledger between what World Builder produces in a compiled `.vtheme` and what Studio's `ThemeRegistry`/`ThemeEngine`/`renderer/slideRenderer.js` actually consume, deliberately *not* duplicating `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`/`docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md`'s own schema documentation. Three real contract gaps were found, each reproduced against the actual defect before being fixed at the root cause: **(1) Frame Variations missing `background`/`frame`/`paper`** — World Builder's Frames screen never exposed the three enum fields `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_artworkBorder()` needs to select anything but its own `'none'` fallback for mat fill and frame ornament, so every Builder-authored Frame rendered in real Studio with no mat and no frame design at all, regardless of matWidth/frameThickness/borderColor; fixed via a new `ProjectModel._ensureFrameFieldDefaults()`, called from the `frames()` read accessor (the same reconcile-on-read discipline `_ordered`/`_ensureHolderDefaults` already use), seeding Museum Gallery's own "Classic White" values (`background:'white'`, `frame:'white-mat'`, `paper:'smooth'`) for any Frame missing them — repairs both new and already-authored Frames, no new Builder UI. **(2) Layer `target:"element"` validated but never rendered** — `element` is one of the four containership scopes `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §7/§11 explicitly names, and World Builder's own Layer Pack editor already offers it, but `renderer/slideRenderer.js` only ever called `_renderLayers()` for `slide`/`frame`/`holder`; fixed with one additional call site reusing the Holder's own content rect (Holder and Element are geometrically identical with today's one-Holder-per-page Layouts, so no new geometry was invented). **(3) The compiled `assets` map vanished on import** — `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `importPackage()`/`_setImported()` only ever kept `manifest`/`theme` on a registered theme record, silently discarding `pkg.assets` even though `builder.js` compiled it correctly and `validatePackage()` accepted it — meaning any relative-path asset reference (a Representation thumbnail, a Frame ornament image) became permanently unresolvable the instant a package was published; fixed by storing `assets` alongside `manifest`/`theme` (surviving `_persistImported`/`_loadImported`'s `localStorage` round-trip too) and adding `ThemeRegistry.getAsset(id, relativePath)`, wired into `js/creationFlow.js`'s Representation-thumbnail rendering — the one concrete, reachable consumer today. **Two gaps investigated and deliberately left disclosed, not fixed**, per the sprint's own no-redesign rule: `fields.cornerRadius`/`inset`/`defaultMargin` are real Builder-authored, Builder-preview-rendered fields with no home in `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §6's canonical Frame field list and no established override mechanism in the real renderer (which derives corner radius only from its fixed frame-design enum table) — extending the renderer to honor them would be a contract redesign, not a hardening fix, so they're documented as Builder-preview-only with zero effect on a published Theme; `theme.supportedCreationTypes` still has no Builder authoring surface, a pre-existing gap named in `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §8/§13 and out of scope for a "no new Builder capabilities" sprint. Verified via Playwright: hand-corrupting a Frame to the pre-fix shape and reopening it confirms automatic repair; importing a synthetic theme with a `target:"element"` Layer and rendering a real slide confirms the Layer now actually paints; importing a synthetic package with a real asset entry confirms `getAsset()` round-trips it correctly including through a `localStorage` persistence cycle. `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged, including its own negative fixtures. No Builder or Studio capability changes beyond the three root-cause fixes; no Theme versioning; `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` is now the one place this parity information lives going forward.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint — Repository Architecture Transition, Phase 1 (a deliberate architecture pivot, explicitly authorized by product direction: Builder produces a complete in-memory Theme, not a package; Publish (install into a repository) and Export (produce a portable `.vtheme` for outside transport) become two distinct operations, with Export explicitly deferred to a future sprint; Official Themes become repository-native instead of in-code/file entries Studio special-cases; Supabase becomes the platform's first persistent repository backend, scoped narrowly to the Official + Personal Theme Repositories only — not a Builder backend, not a Studio backend, not a session store; `ThemeRegistry` is to become a repository abstraction (discover/list/load/resolve-assets) rather than a `localStorage` wrapper, so Studio eventually consumes every repository identically with no per-source branching. This phase is foundation only — per its own explicit "do not redesign Builder or Studio" scope, **zero existing files changed**: `js/themeRegistry.js`, `js/themeEngine.js`, `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, World Builder's Publish flow, and `localStorage`-based persistence are all completely untouched and still the only things Studio/Builder actually use today. New `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` is the canonical design doc (deliberately not duplicating `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md`'s field-parity ledger or `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`/`docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md`'s schema docs), defining: the canonical `themes` table shape (`repository`/`owner_id`/`theme_id` composite uniqueness, with an empty-string owner-id sentinel for Official rows since Postgres treats every `NULL` as distinct and would otherwise silently defeat that constraint); the decision that assets live as raw objects in Supabase Storage rather than embedded base64 (directly answering the file-size question the sprint grew out of, resolved as a repository-storage question rather than the file-transport/zip question explored earlier and explicitly deferred) — a Theme's resolved `assets` map is populated with Storage URLs instead of data URIs, which is not a breaking change since every existing consumer already just uses whatever string is in that map directly as an image `src`; and the identity mechanism for the Personal Theme Repository — Supabase's own Anonymous Sign-In (`signInAnonymously()`), a real, invisible-to-the-author session giving Postgres a server-verified `auth.uid()` for Row Level Security, deliberately chosen over a hand-rolled `localStorage` random id (which a client could trivially spoof against Supabase directly, making any ownership check unenforceable) — disclosed honestly as a "no accounts yet" limitation with a real, native upgrade path (anonymous-to-permanent conversion) rather than a permanent ceiling. New `js/themeRepositoryClient.js` implements the 4-function Repository interface (`discover`/`list`/`load`/`publish`) against Supabase — loaded via its official ESM CDN build (no `package.json`, no bundler, matching this repo's zero-build-step convention throughout), reading connection config from a new gitignored `supabase-config.json` (templated by committed `supabase-config.example.json`) the same resilient fetch-with-graceful-fallback way `js/buildInfo.js` already reads `build-info.json` — "not configured" is a normal, handled state (`isConfigured()` resolves `false`, `discover()` returns Official only), never a crash. Asset resolution lists Storage objects under a Theme's own prefix directly (mirroring how `js/themeEngine.js`'s existing zip-import path already scans a zip's `assets/` folder wholesale rather than cross-referencing a separately-declared list) rather than requiring a redundant manifest of what was uploaded. New `supabase/schema.sql` is a disclosed, unexecuted draft (no real Supabase project exists to run it against yet) — `themes` table + RLS policies + a `theme-assets` Storage bucket, with Personal rows fully self-service via `auth.uid()` and Official rows deliberately given **no** anon-writable policy at all this phase, since "who may publish an Official Theme" has no authorization model yet and is an open Phase 2 question, not something to invent here. Nothing in this phase is wired into any real call site — `js/themeRepositoryClient.js` is new, additive, uncalled code, proven correct only on its own terms (its graceful "not configured" path verified via Playwright with zero console errors; `goldenBuild.js` still 30/30 unchanged, confirming the addition touches nothing existing). Phases 2–5 (replacing Publish, refactoring `ThemeRegistry`, updating Studio's consumption, and full happy-flow validation with Museum Gallery v2.1 as reference) remain explicitly future work — this phase's own deliverable is the foundation they build on, not a working end-to-end repository yet, since that requires a real Supabase project's credentials that only a human can create.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint — Repository Architecture Transition, Phases 2–4 (Supabase MEP continuation — completes the Publish/Registry/Studio wiring the Phase 1 foundation deliberately left unbuilt, per this continuation's own explicit instruction: "Do not redesign Builder. Do not redesign Studio. Replace only the storage layer." **Schema trimmed to the minimum this sprint needs** (`supabase/schema.sql`): removed the Phase 1 draft's denormalized `name`/`version` columns (every real reader already has the full `manifest` JSONB and derives them from it — `list()` selects `theme_id, manifest` only), the `updated_at` column + trigger (a plain upsert plus `created_at` is enough provenance for now), and speculative extra indexes — all premature for "a few themes." **One thing was added, not removed**: Official rows are now writable by the anon role (`themes_official_write`/`_update` + matching Storage policies), a disclosed, deliberate gap — this sprint's own happy-flow ("Builder → Publish Official Theme → Supabase → Studio discovers it") is impossible with Phase 1's original select-only Official policy, and with no accounts/authorization model yet, anyone holding the public anon key can currently publish or overwrite any Official Theme row; resolving real Official-publish authorization is disclosed future work, not invented here. **Builder wiring** (`tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`): `_renderPublishPanel()` gained a shared `_publishToRepository(repositoryId, label)` used by both the pre-existing "Publish to Official Themes" card and a new "Publish to My Themes" card — checks `ThemeRepositoryClient.isConfigured()`, reads `project.lastBuild` (never `project.files`, preserving the Builder-owns-Projects/Runtime-owns-Packages split), calls `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`, and shows a plain success/failure message; no other Publish-screen UI changed. **Registry wiring** (`js/themeRegistry.js`): new `refreshFromRepository()` discovers every repository, lists/loads/validates each theme (`validatePackage()`, the same check a local import already runs), and registers valid ones via the existing `_setImported()` — the identical path a drag-and-drop file import already uses — deliberately never calling `_persistImported()`, so Supabase-sourced themes are never written to `localStorage` and are refetched fresh every boot, keeping the old file-import path and the new repository path from ever fighting over which one wins; a theme that fails to load/validate is silently skipped, never blocking the rest. Both Official- and Personal-repository themes register with `source:'imported'` — the same tag a local file import already uses — so they appear in Studio's existing World Library row with zero new UI, a disclosed trade-off (Official vs. Personal vs. locally-imported are visually indistinguishable there today). **Boot wiring** (`js/app.js`): `_startCreationFlow()` now awaits `ThemeRegistry.refreshFromRepository()` racing a 4-second timeout before calling `CreationFlow.start()` — the only boot-sequence change, no new reactive re-render machinery added to `CreationFlow` itself. **A real cross-cutting bug found and fixed while verifying the Builder's new Publish cards**: `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`'s config path was a bare relative string (`'supabase-config.json'`), which resolves against the *page's* URL — correct for Studio's root `index.html`, silently 404ing for `tools/world-builder/index.html` (two folders deeper), making a correctly-configured project look "not configured" from Builder alone; fixed by resolving the path relative to the script's own `<script src>` location instead. Verified via Playwright against a real (but sandbox-network-blocked) `supabase-config.json`: Studio boots to Creation Flow in ~1.1s with `isConfigured()` true and zero page errors; the Builder's Publish screen renders all 4 cards (Export Package/Community World/Publish to Official Themes/Publish to My Themes) and both new buttons fail gracefully with a clear, disclosed error rather than hanging or throwing, confirming the config-path fix actually mattered (before the fix, Builder's own Publish reported "not configured" even with real credentials present; after the fix, it correctly attempts the network call and fails only because this sandbox's egress policy blocks `supabase.co`/`esm.sh`). `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged. Full live verification against a real Supabase project (Phase 5) is explicitly deferred to the project owner's own local browser, since this environment cannot reach Supabase — see the sprint's own manual verification checklist for the exact SQL/Storage/config steps and expected results.)

- Platform Hardening Sprint — Asset Repository Transition (Sprint 2 — completes the Publish pipeline's remaining externalization gap: a published Theme's `manifest`/`theme` must carry repository asset *references*, never embedded base64, identically whether the repository is Cloud (Supabase) or a future Local extracted package. Per this sprint's own explicit instruction, every embedding site was traced before any fix was written: `assets/*` files, and every Layout/Frame/Layer/Representation image field `tools/world-builder/js/services/validator.js`'s `findAssetPaths()` recognizes, were *already* reference-based — the compiled `assets` map was never stored in `supabase/schema.sql`'s `themes` table to begin with (no `assets` column exists), so `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`/`load()` already treated it as a generic upload/sign target requiring no change. The **only two real embedding sites** were `tools/world-builder/js/services/builder.js`'s `buildManifest()` and `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_buildPackageFromZipFiles()` (the local zip-import producer) — both overwrote the placeholder path (`"thumbnail.png"`/`"preview.png"`) with a literal embedded data URI at Build/Import time, so even though Publish itself was already correct, the `themes` table's `manifest` JSONB column still carried embedded image bytes for these two fields forever. **Fixed at the source, in both producers**: `packageTheme()`/`buildManifest()` and `_buildPackageFromZipFiles()` now merge `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png`'s real bytes into the *same* `assets` map every other asset already uses, leaving `manifest.thumbnail`/`.previewImage` as the plain relative-path reference they were always meant to be — giving the sprint's own Cloud/Local parity requirement real teeth, since both producers now emit the identical shape. **One new, small, shared consumer-side helper**: `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef(id, value)` — factored out of `js/creationFlow.js`'s pre-existing `_repThumbnail`, which had already independently discovered this exact "already a usable src vs. a bare reference needing `getAsset()`" rule for Representation thumbnails — is now the one place every manifest-level image reference resolves through (`js/themeEngine.js`'s `_renderThemeCard()`, `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_themePreview()`), so a legacy embedded package, a local import's data URI, and a Supabase repository's signed URL all resolve identically with zero rendering-code redesign. Verified via `tools/world-builder/verify/goldenBuild.js` (still 30/30, now also asserting `manifest.thumbnail === 'thumbnail.png'` — not a `data:` URI — with the real bytes in `pkg.assets`, plus a round-trip proving `resolveAssetRef()` resolves a freshly-imported reference back to real bytes) and a full Playwright pass: built a real Theme end-to-end through World Builder's own UI (upload → Build) confirming the compiled package carries references only; separately registered a theme with its `assets` map holding **signed-URL-shaped strings** (the literal shape a real Supabase `load()` produces) and confirmed the World Library card's actual `<img src>` in the live DOM resolved to that signed URL, proving Studio's existing card-rendering code needed zero changes to consume a repository-sourced Theme correctly. `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` §8.4, `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` §10, `docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md`, and `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` all updated to state the reference contract as canonical, replacing the prior "embedded as a real data URI" language throughout. No Builder/Studio capability changes beyond this externalization fix; no Marketplace/Community/Export/Import/Versioning work, per the sprint's own Out of Scope list.)

- Platform Hardening Closure Sprint — Publish Contract Alignment & MEP Finalization (a terminology/UI/documentation alignment sprint only — no new capabilities, no Builder/Studio redesign, no Marketplace/Community/Versioning/new repository features. Locks the following as canonical MEP decisions, verified against the actual implementation rather than merely asserted: **Asset Ownership** — each Theme owns all assets required to render itself (decorations/layouts/frames/images/thumbnails/preview images/fonts/future types), with no cross-theme sharing, deduplication, hashing, reference counting, or garbage collection — a Theme that stops referencing an asset leaves it orphaned in Storage rather than deleting it, a locked simplicity choice, not a bug. **Publish Behavior** — publishing replaces the previously published Theme atomically (`ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`'s existing `upsert(...,{onConflict:'repository,owner_id,theme_id'})` already did this correctly; no code change needed); there is exactly one published copy per `(repository,owner_id,theme_id)`, no repository version history, no internal version management. **Determinism, verified not asserted**: two consecutive Builds of an unmodified Builder Project were compared byte-for-byte and found identical, confirming Publish (which sends exactly what Build produced) is deterministic. **Signed URLs never persisted** — confirmed unchanged since the Asset Repository Transition sprint: the stored `manifest`/`theme` never contains a signed URL, only plain relative-path references; repositories generate signed URLs only transiently while loading. **Repository Independence** — Official, Personal, and any future Local repository must expose exactly the same published Theme representation, differing only in where bytes are stored; already true, verified. **Publish vs. Export, made explicit everywhere**: Publish installs a Theme into a Repository and never creates a package; Export creates a portable `.vtheme` and never installs into a Repository — previously both lived under one ambiguous "World Package" heading with no structural separation. `tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_renderPublishPanel()` now renders two clearly separate, individually-headed sections — **Publish** (Official Repository card, Personal Repository card) and **Export** (one card, retitled "Export .vtheme Package") — replacing the old flat 4-card grid. "World Package" is removed as a compound term from both the Build and Publish screens (Build button → "🎁 Build Theme", success state → "✓ Theme Built", the Scenes-section divider on both screens → "Theme"); "My Themes" is renamed to "Personal Themes" throughout (UI copy, internal function names `publishToMyThemes`→`publishToPersonalRepository`, and `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md`'s own prose). The **Community World card is removed outright** from the Publish screen — not left as a disabled placeholder — since Community is out of MEP scope and this screen now only exposes completed workflows (the separate, pre-existing "Community Worlds — Coming soon" card on the Welcome screen's Explore section is untouched, a different and long-standing Builder feature area). `docs/WORLD_BUILDER_ARCHITECTURE.md`'s LOCK 02 diagram is corrected from the stale two-hop `Project → World Package → Runtime` to the canonical three-model `Builder Project → Published Theme → Studio` this sprint locks in; `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full §11 documenting every MEP decision above plus a locked UI-terminology table (Builder Project / Published Theme / Official Repository / Personal Repository / Export Package — never "My Themes"/a bare "Package"/"Publish" when the concepts differ). Frozen historical documents (`docs/PLATFORM_INTEGRATION_REPORT.md`, `docs/BUILDER_V3_CONVERGENCE_REPORT.md`, `docs/BUILDER_V3_EXPERIENCE_STUDIO.md`, `docs/BUILDER_V2_UX_PACKAGE.md`) were deliberately left untouched — they're point-in-time records of what was built/tested/drawn at the time, not living specs, and rewriting their old "World Package" mentions would misrepresent the actual history. Verified end to end via Playwright: the Publish screen shows exactly 3 cards (Publish to Official Themes, Publish to Personal Themes, Export .vtheme Package — Community absent, not disabled) under two headed sections; the screen contains zero occurrences of "World Package" or "My Themes"; both repository Publish buttons still produce a real, graceful failure message under this sandbox's standing network restriction (unchanged from before this sprint); `goldenBuild.js` still passes 30/30 unchanged, confirming this sprint touched only UI copy, internal naming, and documentation — no Build/Publish/Validation behavior changed.)

- Platform Status & Repository Reset (a new Platform Hardening developer utility — explicitly not a Builder or Studio feature, no product styling, reached only by opening `tools/platform-status/index.html` directly. Answers "is everything connected? what exists? what is published? can I safely start over?" without opening Supabase's own dashboard. **Platform Status** shows 🟢/🟡/🔴 Platform Health for Builder/Build Pipeline/Repository Connection/Official Repository/Personal Repository/Theme Registry/Studio Discovery; a Builder section reading this tool's own `build-info.json` plus (read-only) the most-recently-edited World Builder Project from `localStorage`'s existing `vihu-world-builder-projects` key; Official/Personal Repository Theme+Asset counts via a new `ThemeRepositoryClient.getStats(repositoryId)`; a Theme Registry section showing how many repository Themes would actually register cleanly, computed by mirroring `refreshFromRepository()`'s own list→load→`validatePackage()` steps directly rather than calling that function itself — calling it would have silently mixed in this browser's unrelated hardcoded built-in Official themes and any locally-imported Themes sitting in the same origin's `localStorage`, discovered and disclosed during design rather than after the fact; and a plain-text Platform Summary. **Repository Reset** adds one destructive action behind an explicit confirmation modal (Cancel / Reset Repositories, the sprint's own exact copy) implemented entirely through the repository abstraction — a new `ThemeRepositoryClient.reset(repositoryId)` that lists a repository's Theme rows, recursively deletes every Storage object under each one's prefix, then deletes the theme rows themselves (assets before rows, so a mid-failure can't leave either side orphaned in the worse order) — the UI never touches Supabase directly, so a future Local Repository implements the identical contract with no UI change. Reset deletes only published Theme rows and uploaded assets in both repositories; Builder Projects, current Builder state, Settings/Preferences, `supabase-config.json`, authentication, database schema, and Storage buckets themselves are never touched — enforced structurally, since `ThemeRepositoryClient` has no code path that reads or writes `ProjectStore`'s entirely separate `localStorage` key at all. **A real, pre-existing bug found and fixed while building the recursive Storage walker this needed**: `_resolveAssets()` (used by every repository `load()`) only ever listed one Storage folder level, so a nested asset like the golden fixture's own `assets/textures/linen.png` would have silently failed to resolve from a real repository — fixed by extracting a proper recursive `_listAllObjectPaths()` and reusing it in `_resolveAssets()`, `getStats()`, and `reset()` alike, so all three now agree on what "the assets under this Theme" actually means. Required a new, disclosed schema addition: `supabase/schema.sql` gained `themes_official_delete`/`themes_personal_delete` and matching `storage.objects` delete policies — the one capability every earlier draft deliberately left out ("not part of the Publish → Discover happy flow") — carrying the same disclosed Official-authorization gap `themes_official_write`/`_update` already do. Verified against a real local PostgreSQL 16 instance (fresh + idempotent re-run, both clean) and functionally as a non-superuser role: Official deletes for any caller, Personal deletes only for its own owner, and a Personal row/asset belonging to a *different* `auth.uid()` is correctly left untouched — confirmed by querying as superuser afterward, not merely by the delete reporting zero rows affected (which alone wouldn't distinguish "blocked" from "already invisible under RLS"). The page itself was verified via Playwright against this sandbox's real (but network-blocked) `supabase-config.json`: all 7 Health indicators render, the Reset confirmation modal opens/closes correctly, and confirming Reset produces the same class of graceful, disclosed failure message every other Supabase-touching feature already shows under this sandbox's standing network restriction — zero console errors. `goldenBuild.js` still passes unchanged, since it exercises only the local-import path and never touches `ThemeRepositoryClient` at all.)

- Builder Convergence Sprint — Unify Build → Publish → Export into One Canonical Theme Pipeline (a purely architectural convergence sprint, per its own explicit brief — no Builder/Studio/Repository redesign, no new features, no Engine V3, no Versioning/Marketplace/Community/Reader work. Closes the gap the earlier Scene-background pipeline trace found: Engine V1 (`builder.js` → `project.lastBuild` → Publish → Repository → Studio) and Engine V2 (`engineBuilder.js` → `project.lastSceneBuild` → Export Scene Package only) were two independent, parallel build artifacts — Scene/Experience content reached the second one but Publish/Repository/Studio only ever consumed the first, so a Scene's background/image/decoration/text never reached a real reader. **The canonical choice, made explicitly before any code changed, per the sprint's own closing instruction**: Engine V1's `{manifest,theme,assets}` becomes the one canonical Published Theme — not because it's older, but because it's the only shape `renderer/slideRenderer.js`/`js/themeEngine.js`/`js/themeRegistry.js` actually understand; inventing a native Engine V2 Runtime for Studio (Engine V3, effectively) or bolting Engine V2 onto Publish were both explicitly rejected, matching the brief's own "promote one canonical pipeline and migrate the other into it, not merge two architectures" instruction. **`tools/world-builder/js/services/builder.js`'s `packageTheme()`** gained one additive step, `convergeScenes()`/`convergeScene()`/`convergeSceneLayer()`/`externalizeSceneImage()`, running after its four pre-existing `collectFolder()` calls: it walks every `scenes/*.json` file and appends each Scene's converged content onto the exact same `layouts`/`representations`/`layerPack`/`assets` collections those calls already populate — a project with no Scenes appends nothing, so the compiled package is byte-identical to before this sprint (confirmed via `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite, unchanged). One Scene converges into one Layout (`id:'scene-<id>'`, `aspect` taken directly from `scene.canvas.aspectRatio` — already the same vocabulary as `LAYOUT_ASPECTS`, no translation needed) and one Representation (same id, `layout` pointing at it, `defaultFrame` taken from the Scene's first Place's `frame` reference — Place and Frame already share the Engine V1 Frame id space too); every Scene Layer (background fill / image Decoration / Text, in Scene Stack order so z-ordering survives) converges into one Layer Pack entry each, `scope:'scene-<id>'` restricting it to that one Layout so multiple converged Scenes in one theme never cross-contaminate (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_activeLayerPack(s)` gained the scope filter — absent `scope`, every layer authored before this sprint, means global, unchanged). Since Experience content already mirrors onto ordinary Scene Layers before Build runs (`_syncExperienceAttachments`/`_syncUniversalContent`, built in earlier sprints), Experience convergence needed zero additional code — it rides the same Scene Layer conversion for free. **Two additive, backward-compatible renderer extensions were required, discovered only once real Scene content was rendered and checked pixel-by-pixel, not assumed**: (1) `js/layerEngine.js`'s `render()` gained an optional fractional `rect:{x,y,w,h}` field on a Layer entry (a free-form absolute position, alternative to the existing anchor/offset scheme) — absent `rect` (every pre-existing Layer), positioning is unchanged; `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawDecoration` gained two new `decoration.kind` values, `"fill"` (a solid-colour rect) and `"image"` (a real image drawn via the same per-src cache/`onload`-redraw pattern `_ensureStickerImage` already established, resolved through `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef()` — the same mechanism every other asset reference already resolves through). (2) A genuine rendering-order bug found by actually sampling pixels, not by inspection: converging a Scene's foreground content (an image, a caption) onto the existing `target:"slide"` scope rendered it correctly *behind* the Frame/Panel, which then painted over it — `slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element` all render at one fixed point *inside* the Frame/Panel pipeline (three of them gated on a resolved Picture Border existing at all), the wrong place for content meant to sit unconditionally on top. Fixed by adding a fifth containership scope, `target:"overlay"` (`docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §7), painted last in `render(s)`, on top of literally everything (frame/image/decorations/footer/page number/legacy Scene elements/stickers) — a true full-bleed fill (a Scene Background) still converges onto the pre-existing `"slide"` scope (correct wall-level behaviour, unchanged); everything else converges onto `"overlay"`. No hand-authored theme uses `overlay` directly — it exists purely as the Scene converger's own target. `project.lastSceneBuild` is retired as a concept: World Builder's Build screen shows exactly one Build action ("🎁 Build Theme," Scenes shown only as an informational stat) and Publish shows exactly one Theme's worth of options — the "🎬 Build Scene Package"/"💾 Export Scene Package" UI and their `EngineV2Builder`/`project.lastSceneBuild` plumbing are removed from `worldBuilderApp.js` entirely; Engine V2 Scene *Validation* (`EngineV2Validator`, a Scene Model consistency check, unrelated to compilation) is untouched and still shows its own separate report. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` gained a full "Builder Convergence Sprint — Scene Convergence" section (the exact field mapping) plus `scope`/`rect`/`overlay`/`fill`/`image` documentation in §7; `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` §6 gained a row for the new `overlay` target; `docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` gained inline "Amended" callouts on §5/§6 plus a v1.5 Change History entry, disclosing this as a deliberate reversal of that document's original "the two pipelines do not merge" position for the *published-artifact* question only — the canonical Scene Model and the native authoring-time Runtime (Working View/Runtime Preview) are completely unchanged; only the compiled/published representation now converges into Engine V1's. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: a Scene authored with a full-bleed colour background, an image Decoration, and Text converges correctly into `theme.layouts`/`representations`/`layerPack`/`assets` (the image externalized to a plain relative-path reference, resolving back to real bytes); the compiled package imports into the real Studio runtime with zero console errors; rendering a real slide against the Scene-derived Representation actually paints the background colour and the Decoration image (pixel-sampled to confirm, not merely inspected) and holds space for the Text; Museum Gallery (a theme with no Scenes) still imports/applies/renders with zero behaviour change and its 5 pre-existing Layer Pack entries all render correctly; `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged throughout.)

- Repository Reset false-success fix (a small, real bug found operating the platform for real: `ThemeRepositoryClient.reset()` reported its `deletedThemes` count from the pre-delete `SELECT`, not from what the `DELETE` actually removed — so a delete silently blocked by RLS, exactly what happens when a live Supabase project hasn't had `supabase/schema.sql`'s delete policies applied yet, still showed "N Theme(s) removed" even though nothing was deleted. Fixed by chaining `.select()` after `.delete()` so Supabase returns the real deleted rows (`Prefer: return=representation`); Platform Status now distinguishes "found some, deleted none" from a real success and points at the likely cause. No architecture change; `goldenBuild.js` unaffected.)

- Happy Flow Completion Sprint — Representation Ordering fix; Export confirmed already correct (closes the Builder → Repository → Studio Happy Flow the Builder Convergence Sprint opened but didn't fully complete, per this sprint's own explicit "instrument first, no speculative fixes" brief. **Root cause, traced live rather than assumed**: a real authored Theme (a World Builder template's legacy, unfilled Representations — e.g. Artwork Gallery's "Showcase"/"Portrait"/"Quote," pointing at empty template Layouts with no relationship to any Scene — plus one hand-authored Scene with a background/scene image/decoration/text) was built, registered, and opened in a simulated Studio session; Theme Discovery and Theme Application both worked correctly (`ThemeEngine.applyArtworkTheme()` activated the right Theme, confirmed via `getActiveArtworkThemeId()`), but the rendered page showed none of the authored content — reading exactly like "the default placeholder experience." Traced to `js/creationFlow.js`'s Screen 2: the Representation carousel always starts at index 0, and "Start Creating" applies `reps[currentIndex]` with no swipe required to reach index 0 — since the Builder Convergence Sprint's `convergeScenes()` *appended* each Scene's converged Representation after the legacy, `collectFolder('representations')`-sourced ones, a Theme Author's own real content always landed last, and a naive "Start Creating" click applied an empty legacy Representation instead. **Fixed at the source**: `tools/world-builder/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScenes()` now collects every Scene's converged Representation separately and prepends them ahead of the legacy ones (`convergeScene()` returns the Representation object instead of pushing it directly, so ordering is decided once, after the loop) — real, authored content takes priority over untouched template scaffolding; legacy Representations are preserved, not removed, just reordered. Zero Studio changes were needed — Creation Flow already faithfully reads `theme.representations` in array order; only the compile-time order was wrong. **Export was investigated in the same pass and found to already satisfy the platform's own established contract, confirmed by direct comparison rather than assumption**: World Builder's Export button (`_downloadDataURL(project.lastBuild.dataURL, ...)`) and Publish's `_lastBuiltPackage()` (`fetch(project.lastBuild.dataURL)`) read the textually identical object — there is no second serialization path for Export to converge onto Publish's. The reported "embedded `data:image/...` base64" is real but confined to the `assets` side-map (verified via recursive scan: zero embedded data URIs anywhere in `manifest`/`theme` fields, which hold only plain relative-path references, exactly as the Asset Repository Transition sprint established) — and that is required, not a defect, since Export's whole purpose is a self-contained, portable `.vtheme` file that must not depend on a reachable Repository/Storage bucket to open later; Publish externalizes those same bytes into Storage only because *its* destination is a Repository. No Export code was changed. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` gained a "Happy Flow Completion Sprint — Representation Ordering" section (the full trace, fix, and Export finding); `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` gained a matching §8.5. Verified end-to-end via a new 15-assertion Playwright suite (Build → Representation ordering → asset/reference cleanliness → simulated Publish, since live Supabase is unreachable from this sandboxed environment — asset externalization to Storage-URL-shaped strings, the exact transform `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`+`load()` perform → Studio Theme Selection → Theme Application → Renderer, confirming a naive "Start Creating" now selects the authored Scene Representation and the Renderer actually paints its background colour, pixel-sampled → Export/Publish source identity → re-import → re-publish, both idempotent with zero state drift) plus `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion regression suite, unchanged throughout; zero console errors.)

- WEP Scope Freeze — Import Deferred, Promote to Official Repository (a deliberate product decision, not a technical limitation: the WEP proves exactly one complete authoring workflow — `Builder Project → Build Theme → Publish to Personal Repository → Author/Test/Iterate → Promote to Official Repository → Studio Consumption` — before any additional entry point is introduced. **Repository Model, locked**: Personal Repository is the author's own working environment and the *normal* authoring workflow, not an offline mode — every Theme is published there first; Official Repository is the curated, released environment a Theme is promoted into once it's tested and ready. **Publish vs. Promote, a real mechanical distinction, not just friendlier wording**: Publish (`ThemeRepositoryClient.publish()`) reads whatever Build just produced and installs it — the only way new Build output ever reaches a repository, and the only way a Theme reaches Personal. The new `ThemeRepositoryClient.promote(themeId)` creates nothing new: it copies whatever is *already* published to Personal — the Theme row and every Storage asset, via Supabase Storage's own `copy()` (no client-side download/re-upload) — into Official; promoting a Theme with no Personal row yet fails with a distinguishable reason (`not_published_to_personal`) rather than silently building one, and promoting again atomically replaces the previous Official copy (assets cleared and re-copied, then the row upserted), matching Publish's own established "replaces, no version history" convention. `tools/world-builder/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s Publish screen now shows three ordered sections — **Publish** (Personal Repository only, the primary first step), **Promote** (Official Repository, a later dependent step, requiring Personal already published), **Export** (reframed as portability/backup, explicitly not part of the primary workflow) — replacing the old flat "Publish to Official Themes"/"Publish to Personal Themes" pair. No repository schema change was needed — the existing storage RLS policies (Personal-owner-scoped read, Official write, from the Closure Sprint) already cover `copy()`'s source-read + destination-write requirements. **Import — deferred, not removed**: every Import code path (`js/themeEngine.js`'s `importThemeFile`, `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `importPackage`, `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_wireImportButton`/`_importInput`) is completely unmodified and fully functional; only its UI reachability changed. `js/creationFlow.js` gained one module constant, `IMPORT_ENABLED=false`, gating Screen 2's header-level "⊕ Add New World" button and the World Library row's own "Add New World" card — both simply aren't created while the flag is false, with an honest "No worlds published yet — publish one from World Builder to see it here" message replacing what would otherwise be a dead-end empty row. `index.html`'s original Theme Library modal's own "+ Import Theme" button (`#importThemeBtn`, a separate, older Import entry point reachable from inside the editor, distinct from Creation Flow's) is hidden via `style="display:none"` rather than deleted, so `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_wireImportButton()` still finds and wires it correctly the moment it's ever un-hidden. World Builder itself has no Import UI to hide — it has never imported Theme packages, only Published/Promoted/Exported them. Re-enabling Import in a future milestone (`.vtheme` sharing, Marketplace, Community exchange, local repository sync, backup/restore — all explicitly out of WEP scope) is a one-line flip of `IMPORT_ENABLED` plus un-hiding `#importThemeBtn`, since nothing was removed. `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full §13 documenting the two-repository model, the Publish/Promote distinction, the Import-deferred rationale, and Export's non-primary status. Verified via Playwright: Creation Flow Screen 2 renders zero "Add New World" affordances anywhere; the old Theme Library modal's Import button still exists in the DOM (not deleted) but is visually hidden while `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile` remains a real, callable function; World Builder's Publish screen shows the exact new button labels/copy/wiring (`_promoteToOfficial()` calling `ThemeRepositoryClient.promote()`, never `publish()` again); `ThemeRepositoryClient.promote` is exposed and callable; `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite and the Happy Flow Completion Sprint's own 15-assertion suite both pass unchanged — this sprint touched UI visibility, one new repository-to-repository copy function, and documentation only, no rendering/Build/Validation behavior changed.)

- Builder & Studio Alignment Sprint — Author-Owned Representations (a platform-alignment pass, per its own explicit brief — no Builder/Studio/Repository redesign, no new capabilities, Import stays deferred, the Personal → Official promotion workflow unchanged. Locks the **Platform Representation Contract**: a Theme **MUST** contain at least one valid Representation (the only structural requirement); a Theme **SHOULD** contain multiple Representations when they improve the storytelling experience (guidance only); a Theme **CAN** use any Representation names at all — the platform never reserves a name, and Museum Gallery's own `showcase`/`portrait`/`quote` (Sprint 10.2) are one Theme's own authorial choice, not platform vocabulary. **A real, systemic bug found while auditing, not assumed**: every World Builder template except Blank World already seeds one starter Scene that converges into one Representation at Build time (the Builder Convergence Sprint) — but every template *also* still carried a static legacy `representations/*.json` array from before Scenes existed (`templates.js`), so every non-blank template actually compiled 2-4 Representations, never the single baseline the platform intends (Artwork Gallery alone carried the flagged Showcase/Portrait/Quote trio). Fixed by removing every template's static `representations` array entirely — the starter Scene's own converged Representation is now each template's sole default, verified via a real Build (not just Project inspection) to produce exactly one Representation per non-blank template. Artwork Gallery's starter Scene is renamed from "Showcase" (one of the three explicitly flagged names) to "Story," the sprint's own suggested neutral default; Storybook/Quotes/Sketchbook/Greeting Cards' starter names (Cover/Quote/Sketch/Card) were never part of that flagged set and already read as ordinary, template-appropriate authorial choices, so they're unchanged. The now-fully-unused `_representation()` factory in `templates.js` was deleted as genuine dead code (distinct from WEP Scope Freeze's deliberately-preserved, merely UI-hidden Import functions — this had zero remaining call sites and no future re-enablement reason to keep). **Validation gained the one rule the contract actually requires**: `tools/world-builder/js/services/validator.js`'s `validateRepresentations()` previously enforced nothing at all (a Theme with zero Representations from any source validated cleanly); it now errors when both `representations/` and `scenes/` are empty (since either alone converges into ≥1 Representation at Build time), never checking for a specific name or a minimum greater than one. **Studio required zero code changes**, confirmed by direct source audit: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_representationsForTheme`/`paintPreview`/`_finish` and `js/contextPanel.js`'s `_activeRepresentations` already read `theme.representations` generically with no hardcoded name/id/count branching anywhere (a discipline already established since Sprint 10.1/11.2) — one Representation already shows a single-slide carousel needing no swipe before Start Creating; several already show exactly those, in the Theme's own declared order. **Backward compatibility verified, not assumed**: Museum Gallery's compiled `.vtheme` still carries its original `showcase`/`portrait`/`quote` ids/names completely untouched — no migration, no automatic rename, no compatibility shim. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §8 gained the explicit MUST/SHOULD/CAN contract text (its own example JSON swapped from "Showcase" to the neutral "Story") plus a new "Builder & Studio Alignment Sprint" history section. Verified end-to-end via a new 15-assertion Playwright suite: all six templates compile to exactly one Representation (Blank World to zero, its own deliberate baseline); Artwork Gallery's sole Representation is "Story," never "Showcase"; a custom 3-Representation Theme (Adventure/Puzzle/Ending) compiles with exactly those three, in that exact order; Museum Gallery's original three Representations are confirmed unchanged; Representation structure (id/name/order) is byte-identical between a simulated Personal copy and a simulated Official promotion, with zero mutation relative to the original Build output; `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite, the Happy Flow Completion Sprint's 15-assertion suite, and the WEP Scope Freeze sprint's own suite all pass unchanged.)

- World Builder V2 — Builder Project Cloud Backup, Save Button Removed (a deliberate, disclosed extension of Supabase's scope in `tools/world-builder-v2/`, the parallel Builder redesign kept alongside `tools/world-builder/` for comparison — every earlier Repository Architecture sprint scoped Supabase to "the Official + Personal Theme Repositories only," and this decision crosses that boundary on purpose rather than silently. Until now the editable World Builder Project itself (Scenes/Places/Experiences/Frames, everything authored before a Build ever runs) lived only in `localStorage` (`js/projectStore.js`) with no backup anywhere — a cleared browser, a different device, or a quota failure could silently lose in-progress authoring. A new Supabase table, `builder_projects` (`supabase/schema.sql`), holds one owner-scoped row per Project (`jsonb data`, the exact shape `ProjectStore` already persists) via the same `auth.uid()` RLS pattern the Personal Theme Repository already established — deliberately separate from `themes`, since a Builder Project isn't a portable, shared, referenced-file bundle the way a compiled Theme is. New `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/projectSync.js` (`ProjectSync.isAvailable()`/`.push(project)`) reuses `ThemeRepositoryClient.getClient()`/`.getSession()` (two small additions to that module's exported API) rather than a second sign-in or config fetch — same one Supabase project, same one anonymous session. **Local-primary, cloud backup, confirmed explicitly before building**: `localStorage` stays the only source of truth the Workspace reads from/renders immediately; the Supabase copy is a best-effort background push, debounced 2s off the trailing edge of edits, never a second read path — authoring works exactly as before if Supabase is unreachable. **The identity caveat is disclosed, not hidden**: the anonymous session is itself a `localStorage` token, so clearing all browser data loses that identity too — this does not fully solve "my work survives anything," only real narrower problems (quota failures, accidental local-only loss, resuming later on the same browser); a real account system would close the remaining gap and doesn't exist yet. Shipped anyway per explicit product direction (single-user product today). A second, honest header badge (`#wb-cloud-sync`) reports the background copy's own state (unavailable/pending/synced/error) completely independently of the pre-existing 🟢/🟠/🔴 local-save badge, which is unchanged. **The Save button was removed outright, not demoted**: `_persist()` already saved synchronously on every edit and the local badge already reported that truth immediately — the button only ever re-ran the identical write "as an explicit, user-visible confirmation," per its own pre-existing code comment, and added nothing real now that the cloud badge reports the one thing that wasn't already visible. `index.html`/`worldBuilderApp.js`/`world-builder.css` all had their Save-button-specific markup/wiring/CSS removed together; the local-save badge's CSS was generalized from id-scoped selectors to shared `.wb-save-dot-glyph`/`.wb-save-text` classes so the new cloud badge reuses the identical dirty/saved/error styling with no duplication. `docs/THEME_REPOSITORY_ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a full §14 documenting the decision, the caveat, and the implementation. Verified via Playwright: the Save button no longer exists in the DOM; the local save badge continues working completely independently of the cloud one; against this sandbox's own real (but network-blocked) `supabase-config.json`, the cloud badge correctly distinguishes "configured but unreachable" (a real attempted push that fails, reported honestly) from what "not configured at all" would show, never silently lying about success; `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged.
