Live end-to-end verification against a real, reachable Supabase project is explicitly deferred to the project owner's own local browser, matching every other Supabase-touching feature's own disclosed verification limits in this sandboxed environment.)

- Decoration Shapes — real vector primitives with fill, outline, resize, and rotation (`tools/world-builder-v2/` only — the parallel `tools/world-builder/` Builder was left untouched apart from a matching Artwork Gallery starter-scene rename already in progress. Studio's own Sticker Studio has always had a disconnected "Shapes" category of fixed-colour emoji glyphs, but World Builder's Decorations authoring had no shape concept at all until an author asked for one with real fill/outline/resize/rotation control — a genuinely new capability, not a quick fix, since rotation didn't exist anywhere in Engine V2 before this. Implemented entirely inside the existing Universal Experience Content model (Builder V3.1) rather than a parallel mechanism: `js/services/experienceSchema.js`'s `defaultUniversalContent()` gained five new namespaced Graphics-section fields (`graphicShape`, `graphicFillColor`, `graphicStrokeColor`, `graphicStrokeWidth`, `graphicRotation`) plus a `SHAPE_KINDS` vocabulary (Circle/Star/Arrow/Speech Bubble/Banner) — a Shape is mutually exclusive with an uploaded Graphics image on the same Layer/slot (picking one clears the other, enforced in the UI layer, not the Engine Adapter). The Decorations quick-picker gained a parallel "Add a Shape" tile grid alongside the existing emoji-glyph grid, creating a real Experience with `graphicShape` set directly rather than rasterizing a fixed-colour PNG the way the glyph picker does — the whole point of a Shape being that its own colours stay editable afterward. `js/projectModel.js`'s `_syncUniversalContent` folds Shape handling into the same Image/Graphics mirroring loop that already handles uploaded images (one Layer, one set of position/size bookkeeping, only the styling fields differ) rather than a second implementation. `js/services/engineRuntime.js`'s `_paintLayer` gained a generic `layer.rotation` read (applied around the Layer's own rect centre, so it works for an uploaded Graphics image too, not just Shapes) and a new `_drawShape` function drawing each of the five kinds as a real filled+stroked canvas path. Reaching Studio required one more step, found and closed in the same pass: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s Scene-convergence pipeline (the Builder Convergence Sprint) only ever converted a Decoration Layer's `.image` into a compiled `decoration:{kind:'image'}` entry or fell back to `decoration:{kind:'sticker'}` for a bare glyph — a Shape Layer has neither, so it would have silently rendered as a stray ✨ sticker in a real Studio-published Theme; fixed by converging `layer.shape` into a new `decoration:{kind:'shape', shape, fillColor, strokeColor, strokeWidth, rotation}` entry, and by extending `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawDecoration` with the matching `kind==='shape'` branch — the exact same five-path drawing routine reimplemented in that file's own coordinate/context style, since the real Reader-facing renderer has no dependency on any World Builder module and the two must be kept in lockstep by hand. Card/thumbnail preview sites (the Scene Stack sidebar row, the Experience Library tab, Gallery/Nursery cards) all gained a shape-aware swatch (the shape's own fill colour plus its icon) instead of falling through to the generic ✨ placeholder. Verified end-to-end via Playwright driving the real UI (not just model calls): clicking a Star tile creates a real Personal-lifecycle Experience with `contentKind:'graphics'`/`graphicShape:'star'`; the Inspector's real Fill Colour/Outline Colour/Outline Thickness/Rotation range and colour inputs persist to the Experience and its mirrored Scene Layer; Working View and Runtime Preview both paint the shape (Runtime Preview's sampled pixel matched the fill colour exactly); uploading an image correctly clears `graphicShape`, and the mirrored Layer itself — not just the Experience property — updates from a shape decoration to an image decoration with zero orphaned data; and a real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` through the unmodified `validator.js`/`builder.js` compiled a `decoration:{kind:'shape', shape:'star', strokeWidth:6, ...}` Layer Pack entry targeting the `overlay` scope, confirming the fix reaches an actual published Theme, not only the Builder's own preview. `tools/world-builder-v2/verify/goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. No Engine V2 Scene Model/architecture change; Frame's existing "Holder clip/mask Shape" concept (Rectangle/Rounded/Circle, an unrelated pre-existing vocabulary) was deliberately left alone and not reused or renamed into.)

- Decoration Shapes — basic-geometry vocabulary + independent fill/outline transparency (a direct, immediate follow-up on the Decoration Shapes sprint above, per explicit feedback that the original 5-shape set — mostly decorative — should include the standard drawing-tool primitives, and that fill and outline each need their own transparency, not just the whole shape's overall Opacity slider. `SHAPE_KINDS` grew from 5 to 14: Rectangle/Triangle/Diamond/Pentagon/Hexagon/Octagon/Cross/Trapezoid/Parallelogram joined the original Circle/Star/Arrow/Speech Bubble/Banner. `engineRuntime.js` gained a shared `_regularPolygonPath` helper (one N-sided-polygon routine reused for Triangle/Pentagon/Hexagon/Octagon rather than four near-duplicate hand-plotted paths) plus straightforward path geometry for Rectangle/Diamond/Cross/Trapezoid/Parallelogram; `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawShape` got the identical geometry added by hand, in lockstep, since it has no dependency on any Builder module. **Transparency**: two new namespaced fields, `graphicFillOpacity`/`graphicStrokeOpacity` (each 0..1, defaulting to 1 so every pre-existing Shape renders exactly as before), ride alongside the existing `graphicFillColor`/`graphicStrokeColor` through the same mirrored-Layer/Engine-Adapter/Build-convergence pipeline the original sprint built (`shapeFillOpacity`/`shapeStrokeOpacity` on the mirrored Layer, `fillOpacity`/`strokeOpacity` on the compiled `decoration:{kind:'shape',...}` entry) — no second pipeline. `_drawShape` composes (multiplies) each against the Layer's own overall `opacity` rather than replacing it, so a half-opacity Shape with a half-opacity fill reads as one authoring decision layered on another; fill and outline are painted as two separate `fill()`/`stroke()` calls each with their own `ctx.globalAlpha`, restored afterward. The Inspector gained "Fill Opacity" and "Outline Opacity" sliders (0-100%) paired beside their respective Colour pickers via the existing `_fieldRow` convention, and the isolated Experience Studio preview's shape-field passthrough was updated to match. Verified end-to-end via Playwright: all 14 `SHAPE_KINDS` entries have exactly one real, distinct Add-a-Shape tile; a Hexagon Experience's Fill/Outline Opacity sliders persist to both the Experience and its mirrored Layer independently; a real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` compiles the correct `fillOpacity`/`strokeOpacity` values into the published Theme's Layer Pack; and a pixel-sampled before/after (Fill Opacity 30% vs. 100%, same background) shows a real, visibly different rendered colour — genuine transparency, not a cosmetic no-op. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. No Engine V2 Scene Model change; Frame's unrelated Holder clip/mask Shape vocabulary untouched.)

- Dev Footer Size Fix (a Studio-page fix, not World Builder — reported as "the build info strip is too big." Root cause traced, not guessed: `js/buildInfo.js`'s footer text builder concatenated the entire long-form `sprint`+`task` changelog prose from `build-info.json` — this project's own established multi-hundred-word commit-message style — directly into the on-screen badge, producing a 1000+ character string that rendered as a 1388×60px, 3-line banner spanning almost the full viewport width. Fixed at the source: the footer now only ever shows version/build/commit/environment; `sprint`/`task` are dropped from the visible badge entirely (still present in the fetched `build-info.json` for anyone opening the file directly — nothing was deleted from the record, only from the DOM). `css/style.css`'s `.dev-footer` also shrunk to match its own original intent (a small, unobtrusive fixed corner badge, `pointer-events:none`) — font-size 11px→9px, padding 6px 10px→3px 7px, corner offset 12px→8px, opacity 0.85→0.7. Verified via Playwright: 1388×60px → 215×18px, single line, correct badge text.)

- Decoration Shapes — Rounded Rectangle + "Draw Your Own" freehand shape (a second direct follow-up on the Decoration Shapes work: one more preset shape, plus a genuinely new authoring capability — a creator-drawn outline, not another preset. **Rounded Rectangle**: `SHAPE_KINDS` gained one entry reusing `engineRuntime.js`'s existing `_roundedRectPath` helper (`renderer/slideRenderer.js` got the identical arcTo geometry added by hand, in lockstep, same discipline as every other shape) at a fixed `min(w,h)*0.2` corner radius — no new control surface, since the request was for the shape option itself. **"Draw Your Own"**: a new `graphicCustomPath` field (`experienceSchema.js`'s `defaultUniversalContent()`) holds an array of `{x,y}` points, each 0..1 fractional within the pad the creator sketched on — deliberately the same fractional-rect vocabulary every Shape/Holder/Layer Transform already uses, so a drawn shape resizes/moves/rotates/fills/outlines through the exact existing machinery with zero new plumbing; picking a fixed drawing-canvas-plus-Transform split (rather than drawing directly at final placement) keeps "what the shape looks like" decoupled from "where it sits," matching this codebase's own established Properties-vs-Transform separation throughout the whole Experience system. A new `_shapeDrawPad` (`worldBuilderApp.js`) is a small freehand sketch pad — real `pointerdown`/`pointermove`/`pointerup` handlers capture a stroke, normalize it to fractional coordinates on release (not on every frame — one model write per completed stroke, not per pixel moved), and redraw a live preview using the same Fill/Outline styling already chosen; a Clear button resets to `null`. Both `engineRuntime.js`'s `_drawShape` and `slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawShape` gained a `kind === 'custom'` branch mapping the stored fractional points onto the target rect (identical placement math to every other shape) and closing the path — falling back to a plain circle placeholder when nothing's been drawn yet, so the Experience is never invisible the instant the tile is picked, matching every other shape's own default-visible convention. `builder.js`'s Scene-convergence pipeline carries `customPath` through into the compiled `decoration:{kind:'shape',...}` Layer Pack entry alongside the existing fill/stroke/opacity/rotation fields, so a hand-drawn shape reaches a real published Studio Theme, not just Builder's own preview. Verified end-to-end via Playwright driving real pointer events (not synthetic model calls): Rounded Rectangle renders the correct fill colour at the expected pixel; drawing a real freehand triangle-ish stroke on the pad persists a ≥3-point fractional path to both the Experience and its mirrored Scene Layer; a real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` compiles a `decoration:{kind:'shape', shape:'custom', customPath:[...]}` entry — confirming the drawn shape survives the full Build pipeline. A real test-harness bug was found and fixed during verification, not a product bug: the Draw pad rendered below the Inspector's scrollable fold when opened from an already-tall Experience panel, so raw OS-level pointer events landed outside the viewport until the test called `scrollIntoViewIfNeeded()` first — an ordinary Playwright interaction-visibility gotcha, unrelated to the app's own real, working scroll behaviour. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. No Engine V2 Scene Model change.)

- Creator UI Convergence Sprint (a presentation/interaction polish sprint across the whole Studio Creator UI — Screen 1, Screen 2, Workspace, a brand-new Object Strip, Publish, and a language pass — explicitly not a capability, architecture, or Runtime change; every existing selection model, autosave path, Theme Contract, and Builder compatibility guarantee is untouched, verified via Playwright with zero console errors throughout. **Screen 1**: card/typography/spacing polish only (circular icon badges, warmer shadows/hover states) — the Story Meadow background architecture stays exactly as Sprint 11.0 built it, a deliberate scope decision favouring low-risk, real visual improvement over a literal split-panel rebuild that risked the hand-tuned atmosphere. **Screen 2**: sources-panel/world-card/preview-container/carousel/CTA all restyled warmer (22px radii, gold-tinted shadows, a pill-shaped active dot, a gradient Start Creating button) with zero DOM/JS changes — the carousel's own scroll-IS-selection model (Sprint 11.1) is completely unchanged, confirmed via a real arrow-click scroll-position check. **Workspace — the sprint's primary focus**: the Header gained a Home button (reuses `CreationFlow.start()` as-is — no new capability, just a new entry point) and a read-only "🏛️ Museum Gallery · Showcase" orientation readout (`js/app.js`'s new `_updateHeaderContext()`, reusing the exact `ThemeEngine`/`ThemeRegistry` lookups `contextPanel.js` already made for its own Page Style row) alongside softer pill buttons and a warmer Publish gradient; the Page Strip stays exactly where and how it always worked — vertical, in the left sidebar, full drag-reorder/⋮-menu/Cover-End-anchoring functionality untouched — only visually polished, correcting an initial mis-scoped attempt to relocate it horizontally before re-reading the brief's own explicit "Page Strip scrolls vertically" instruction. A **real, pre-existing latent bug was found and fixed** in the process: `renderList()`/`renderTimeline()`'s async thumbnail-generation completion handlers could each independently kick off their own `ThumbnailEngine.generate()` call when two renders raced before a slide's thumbnail was set, and both completions would insert their own `<img>` — invisible in the old cramped vertical grid layout, but immediately obvious once the strip was restyled; fixed by moving the stale-image check to right before insertion (inside the `onload` callback, not before it) so whichever completion wins the race is the only one left. Also fixed a second real, unrelated, pre-existing bug found in the same pass: Publish Studio's close button was missing `!important` on its `width:38px`, so the codebase's own global `button{width:100%}` rule silently stretched it into a bizarre full-width pill spanning the header — a one-line fix. **The NEW Object Strip** (`js/objectStrip.js`, mounted beneath the canvas where the mis-scoped Page Strip relocation attempt had briefly sat): a horizontally-scrolling, child-friendly readout of every object on the current page — Background and, for Story-role pages, Artwork (both synthetic entries reusing the exact `image-holder` selection id `js/app.js`'s own canvas-click handler already established for Context Panel routing on pages with no real SceneEngine element) — plus every `SceneEngine.listElements()` object (Cover/Hook/End role Frame/Text/Sticker/Decoration, sticker names/glyphs resolved via `StickerLibrary.getById`) and every `SlideRenderer.getTextElements()` text object (Story Text plus the World's own Handle/Footer/Page Number chrome) — each card showing a thumbnail/icon, friendly name, and 🟢 Editable / 🔒 Part of this World status (mapped from the pre-existing Sprint 8.3 `locked` flag, not a fabricated new concept). Deliberately not a Layer Panel: no drag handle, no reorder control, objects show in the page's own existing render order only. Selection is genuinely bidirectional — tapping a card calls the identical `window.setSelectedSceneElement`/new `window.setSelectedTextElement` entry points the canvas's own click handlers already call, so a canvas click and an Object Strip tap are indistinguishable to every downstream listener (Context Panel, Card Designer section routing), verified end-to-end via Playwright (tapping "Handle" selects it, shows the gold canvas outline, and routes Card Designer to its Typography controls, exactly as clicking it on the canvas would). **Publish flow**: presentation-only polish (header brand colour, the close-button bug above); the deeper stages (the Read-My-Story CTA, the confetti/rise-animation Celebration screen) were already well-crafted from Sprint 9.0 and needed no further investment. **Language review**: a real grep-driven audit, not a guess — found and fixed genuine leaks of the brief's forbidden vocabulary (Theme/Representation/Holder/Layer) in previously-shipped, real UI surfaces that had accumulated across many prior sprints: the sidebar's "THEME" section header → "WORLD"; the in-editor Theme Picker modal's full text (heading, intro paragraph, "Story Themes"/"Artwork Themes"/"Official Themes"/"Imported Themes" section headings, the empty-state message, the Import Conflict modal) → World language throughout; the World Designer tab label and "Current Theme"/"Reset to Theme" banner and buttons (4×) → World language; Card Designer's "Picture Holder" (5 occurrences across the Frame section title/selected-label/empty-state/hint/reset-button) → "Picture Frame"; the z-order "Layer" row label (3 occurrences, Bring-Forward/Send-Backward controls for stickers and frames) → "Order"; Context Panel's "🔄 Change Representation" button → "🔄 Change Look"; three "Theme Default"/"Theme default" font-dropdown option labels (Card Designer ×2, Theme Engine ×1) → "World Default"/"World default". **Builder↔Creator mapping review**: confirmed Frame Variations, Representation actions (editCaption/editQuote), and Museum Caption fields are already correctly surfaced in Creator via Card Designer's Frame section and Context Panel's Caption/Quote field groups; identified one real, disclosed gap rather than attempting a blind fix — Layer-Pack-declared decorative content (Museum Caption text, Wax Seal, Gallery Spotlight, and Handle/Page-Number position overrides) has no individual Object Strip entry today, since `renderer/slideRenderer.js` exposes no public enumeration of the active Layer Pack and this sandboxed environment has no way to verify field shapes against a real Museum Gallery theme (Supabase/the Repository are network-blocked here, same standing limitation disclosed throughout every earlier Repository-touching sprint) — recorded as real future work rather than guessed at with unverifiable risk. Verified end-to-end via Playwright throughout every stage: Screen 1/2 visual checks, full Workspace functional regression (add/select/duplicate page, dark-mode toggle, Home button return-to-Screen-1, all via the real sidebar Page Strip), Object Strip selection sync in both directions, Publish Studio stage rendering, and a final combined visual QA pass across all four surfaces — zero console errors anywhere, zero regressions in any pre-existing capability.)

- Creator V2 — Ground-Up UI Rebuild (a full visual rebuild of Creator per an approved wireframe board — "CREATOR: A Child's Journey from Imagination to Celebration" — explicitly not an incremental polish pass on top of the Creator UI Convergence Sprint above; that sprint's own presentation was itself treated as disposable per the rebuild's governing instruction: "preserve behaviour, discard presentation," modeled explicitly on how Builder V3 replaced its own dashboard UI while keeping every compile/validate engine underneath untouched. Runtime/Theme Engine/Theme Contract/Repository/Publish Engine/Workspace behaviour/Selection model/Autosave/Theme loading/Project model/file format are all completely unchanged — every edit in this sprint is CSS, DOM structure, or small additive JS wiring into existing entry points, never new architecture. Illustration strategy was an explicit decision point, resolved by asking rather than assuming: elevate the existing CSS/emoji Story Meadow technique (denser detail, gentle motion, refined styling) rather than pull in `vihuplanet/`'s own separate hand-illustrated asset library — no new binary asset dependency, no cross-product coupling. **Screen 1**: grid restructured 4-up → a 3-column 6-card layout, each card's icon badge recoloured per a new `accent` field (sand/amber/sky/rose/lilac) instead of one flat tint; added a "?" help affordance top-right; subtitle reworded to "Every idea has a world."; the Story Meadow scene gained a new "children reading under a tree" illustration group (`.creation-scene-reading-circle`, three child/animal emoji with a `creation-breathe` idle animation) and a third drifting butterfly. **Screen 2**: split the World's own constant identity (icon badge + name + new description line, sourced from `_themePreview()`'s existing manifest lookup) from the Begin-With Representation carousel below it, adding a "🌿 Begin With 🌿" label between them — Sprint 11.1's scroll-is-selection carousel mechanic is completely unchanged, confirmed via a real scroll-position assertion, only the surrounding layout was restructured. **Workspace header**: the World/Page-Style readout (Creator UI Convergence Sprint's own `_updateHeaderContext()`) gained a chevron and became a second, real entry point into `ThemeEngine.openThemePicker()` — the same picker the left World card already opens; a new "+ Add Page" button above the sidebar Page Strip reuses `PageOps.addAfter(AppState.currentSlide)` verbatim, the identical function the page ⋮ menu's own "Add Blank Page After" already calls. An editable project-name field the wireframe shows in the header was deliberately **not** implemented — it directly conflicts with the separately Locked Product Decision #1 (Workspace Simplification: "Hide Project Title, Author and editable Book Name from the editor"), and this sprint's own scope was a visual rebuild, not authorization to reverse an already-locked decision; disclosed rather than silently resolved either way. **Context Panel** (`js/contextPanel.js`): every selection state — previously a bare hand-off straight into the raw CardDesigner accordion section with no state-specific chrome beyond the pre-existing "Your Picture" actions row — now opens with a small, consistent identity banner (a 38px icon-circle + friendly label: 🖼️ Your Picture, 📝 Your Text, ✨ Your Sticker, 🎀 Your Decoration) via a new shared `_renderSelectionHeading()`, and the default "Nothing Selected" view gained a "👆 Tap anything on the page to edit it" hint pill at the top — all purely presentational additions above the exact same underlying CardDesigner sections (Frame stays folded into Picture, per the pre-existing, still-accurate Sprint 10.0 rationale that a Story-role page has no separate Frame/Holder hit-target). Building this surfaced and fixed a real, pre-existing CSS bug: `.text-empty` (the "Click any text on the canvas to edit it." hint) had a `.hidden` class toggled onto it by `_refreshText()` on every selection, but no `.text-empty.hidden{display:none}` rule existed anywhere in the stylesheet (only `.text-editor.hidden` did) — so the hint stayed visibly stacked above the real editor controls for every single text selection since the feature shipped, invisible enough inside the old permanent tab bar to go unnoticed until the new banner made the redundancy obvious. Fixed with the one missing CSS rule. **Object Strip** (`js/objectStrip.js`): gained a static legend row above the card list ("Shows everything in this page. Tap any object to select it." + 🟢 You can edit / 🔒 Part of the world keys), and each card's own badge text was reworded to match that legend exactly (previously "🟢 Editable"/"🔒 Part of this World", inconsistent phrasing between the two) — the underlying bidirectional selection sync (`window.setSelectedSceneElement`/`setSelectedTextElement`) is completely unchanged. **Publish stages**: `.publish-studio`'s flat two-stop grey gradient gained a third, warm stop (`color-mix(in srgb, var(--panel) 88%, #ffcb45 12%)`) so every stage now resolves to a soft gold wash at the bottom, matching Screen 1/2/Workspace's own warmer palette instead of reading as a separate, colder surface — verified deliberately with `color-mix` rather than a low-alpha `rgba` stop, since a first attempt using `rgba(255,203,69,0.08)` as the terminal stop made the gradient partially transparent and let the modal's own dark backdrop (`rgba(8,10,16,0.86)`) bleed through as an ugly dark band at the bottom, a real rendering bug caught via screenshot before shipping. The Almost Ready stage gained a 64px circular icon badge (🎉 when the book is ready, 💡 when there are nudges) above its headline, extracted out of the headline's own previously-inline emoji into a proper visual element (`_almostBadge`, matching the Context Panel banner's icon-circle language) — Read My Story, Choose Story Destination, Publishing, and Celebration were reviewed and found to already carry the celebratory, card-based visual language this rebuild calls for from earlier sprints, so they were left unchanged rather than rebuilt without cause. Verified end-to-end via Playwright across every surface, in both light and dark mode: Screen 1/2 render correctly with the new grid/carousel layout; the header World-picker shortcut and "+ Add Page" both work; all four Context Panel selection states show the correct banner with zero duplicate hint text; the Object Strip legend renders without disrupting the horizontal-scroll card row or selection sync; every Publish stage (Read/Almost Ready/Destination) renders the corrected warm gradient with no dark-backdrop artifact in either theme; the full pre-existing regression suite (page add/duplicate/select, dark mode toggle, Home button, Object Strip bidirectional sync) passes unchanged — zero console errors anywhere throughout.)

- Creator V2 — Wireframe Precision Pass (a direct follow-up once the actual wireframe board image became viewable in full detail, rather than only a text description of it — closes two real gaps the text description had glossed over. **Frame Variations now render as colour swatch tiles**, matching the wireframe's "FRAME SELECTED" panel exactly: `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s new `_buildSwatchRow()` reuses the exact `.icon-row`/`.icon-card`/`.icon-preview`/`.icon-label`/`.active` classes Frame Look's own preset row already established (zero new visual language), showing each Frame Variation's `fields.borderColor` as a small colour circle plus a "Default" reset tile; the `frameVariation` control in `CONTROL_CATALOG` now calls this instead of the generic `_buildSelectRow` dropdown. **A real, pre-existing Object Strip sizing bug, found and fixed**: comparing rendered card dimensions against the wireframe's own proportions surfaced that every Object Strip card was being silently crushed to exactly 40px tall (a 44px thumbnail rendering at ~4px) — traced to `.object-card` being a `<button>` element with no explicit `height`/`width`/`margin` of its own, so the codebase's own global `button{height:var(--button-height)}` (40px) and `button:not(.tab-btn)...{width:100%;margin-bottom:12px}` reset rules (both pre-dating this session, confirmed via `git show` against the part-1 commit) silently won the cascade and flex-shrank every card's contents into a fixed 40px box — the identical class of bug the Creator UI Convergence Sprint already found and fixed once for the Publish Studio close button. Fixed the same proven way: explicit `!important` overrides on `.object-card` (`width:78px`, `height:auto`, `margin:0`) plus `flex-shrink:0` on both `.object-card` and `.object-card-thumb` so a future container-level squeeze can't reintroduce it. Also added the small pencil-icon overlay (`.object-card-edit-badge`) the wireframe shows on every editable object's thumbnail, positioned inside the thumb's own bounds (not overlapping its edge, since `.object-card-thumb{overflow:hidden}` would otherwise clip it). Verified via Playwright: Frame Variation swatches render and sync correctly against synthetic theme data (5 tiles, click-to-select, active-state ring); Object Strip cards measure their full intended 78×91px with a genuine 44×44px thumbnail; full regression (page ops, dark mode, Context Panel routing, selection sync) passes unchanged with zero console errors.)

- Creator V2 — No-Scroll Screens, Real Screen 2 Visual Fallback, Branding Removal (four concrete, user-reported fixes, none of them presentation-only — two real bugs and one deliberate scope decision. **(1) Screen 1 and Screen 2 no longer scroll on ordinary laptop viewports**: both were verified to overflow their `.creation-flow-overlay` container at common heights (Screen 1 at ≤720px, Screen 2 at ≤800px — reproduced directly by measuring `scrollHeight` vs `clientHeight` at 640/700/720/800/900px, not guessed). Fixed by converting the overlay's padding and every major vertical space-consumer (Screen 1's question/subtitle/card padding/icon size; Screen 2's preview-panel padding, badge, heading, carousel slide `min-height`, and carousel art `height`) from fixed pixel values to `clamp()` expressions anchored on `vh` units — content now compresses gracefully as the viewport shrinks instead of overflowing; `overflow-y:auto` stays on the overlay only as a safety net for genuinely extreme cases, never triggered at any realistic laptop height (verified fitting with zero scroll at 640/700/720/800/900px). **(2) Screen 2's Preview carousel now shows a real visual even when a Representation has no `thumbnail` of its own**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_repThumbnail()` used to fall back to a hardcoded generic 🎭 mask emoji for every World's every under-authored Representation, regardless of what that World actually is — a real "no real visual" gap, not a styling choice. Fixed by falling back to the World's own preview image/icon (`_themePreview()`, the exact fields `ThemeEngine`'s own Theme Library card already reads) before ever reaching a generic glyph — verified with a synthetic theme whose Representations declare no `thumbnail` field: the carousel now shows the World's own hero image instead of a mask. **(3) Removed every hardcoded `'@vihuplanet'`/`'by Vihu'` branding fallback from the render pipeline** — a real, confirmed bug, not a style preference: `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_drawHandle()` drew the literal string `'@vihuplanet'` at full render weight whenever a slide's Handle was empty (i.e., on every page a creator hadn't explicitly typed a social handle into, which is nearly all of them), and `buildPayload()`'s own `defaultHandle` fallback did the same; `js/sceneEngine.js`'s `resolveTextSource('handle')` was the most severe instance — its own doc comment says "Returns '' if absent" but the implementation contradicted that specifically for `'handle'`, returning `'@vihuplanet'` as if it were real creator content and bypassing the Text Holder's own 50%-opacity "unfilled placeholder" dimming entirely; two Scene Blueprint defaults (`_textHolder('handle-holder',...,'@vihuplanet',...)` on both Hook and End role pages, and `_textHolder('author-holder',...,'by Vihu',...)` on Cover pages) baked the same fabricated content into every fresh Hook/End/Cover page's starting Handle/Author fields. All four fixed at the source: an empty Handle now renders nothing (matching the pre-existing, correct `_drawFooter` convention of `if(!bookTitle) return null`), and the Author placeholder became the generic, non-branded `'by You'` (matching the file's own existing convention of neutral placeholders like `'Your Title'`/`'Subtitle'`). Verified via Playwright, in both the Workspace canvas and the Publish Studio's Read-My-Story render: the fabricated `'@vihuplanet'` watermark is gone from every unedited page, while the book title and page number — genuine project data (the creator's own title, the real page count), never fabricated content — are correctly unaffected and keep rendering exactly as before, since visibility defaults for those two were deliberately left untouched pending explicit confirmation (a scope decision disclosed, not silently made). Full regression (page ops, dark mode, Object Strip sync — now correctly showing 3 objects instead of 4, since an empty Handle has nothing to select — Frame Variations swatches) passes unchanged with zero console errors.)

- Book Title / Page Number Turned Off By Default (explicit product direction, a direct follow-up to the branding-removal fix above — after the fake `@vihuplanet` watermark was removed, the real project title and real page number were still showing on every page by default, and the instruction was to hide both "for now," reversibly, until reactivated. Traced to two separate hardcoded sources, not one: `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_defaultOptionsFor()` (`pageNumber:'bottom-right'`, `bookTitleVisibility:'show'`) and `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s matching `FALLBACK_OPTIONS` were the first — flipped to `'hidden'`/`'hide'`. The real, deeper source was `js/state.js`'s `AppState.project.themeOptions`, which pre-seeds every project (new and default) with its own literal `pageNumber:'bottom-right'`/`bookTitleVisibility:'show'` — since `ThemeEngine.getOptions()`'s `Object.assign({},base,stored)` always lets a project's *stored* `themeOptions` win over the computed base defaults, the `_defaultOptionsFor()` change alone was silently shadowed for every real project. Fixed at all three sources together. Each edit is commented as an explicitly reversible default — flipping the two values back to `'bottom-right'`/`'show'` in all three places restores the prior always-on behaviour with no other code change, per the "if needed we will reactivate that" instruction. `handleVisibility` stays `'show'`, unaffected — with the branding fix above, an unset Handle already renders nothing, so `'show'` now correctly means "show it if the creator or theme actually provided one." Verified via Playwright: the Workspace canvas and the Publish Studio's cover render both show only the artwork/frame with no title or page number by default; the Object Strip correctly lists only Background as a selectable object (Footer/Page Number have nothing to select once hidden). Full regression passes unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Object Strip / Canvas Selection Now Respects Builder-Authored Layer Pack Content (answers a direct product question — "the object strip was to show all the objects used in building the scene in builder, i don't think creator is respecting the theme created by builder" — with a real, confirmed gap, not a misunderstanding: a Builder-authored theme's Layer Pack (`theme.layerPack` — Museum Gallery's Museum Caption/Wax Seal/Gallery Spotlight, or anything a future World declares) has always drawn correctly to the canvas via `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_renderLayers`/`LayerEngine.render` pipeline — the theme's look genuinely was being respected pixel-for-pixel — but the three draw functions behind it (`_layerDrawText`/`_drawMuseumCaption`, `_layerDrawSticker`, `_layerDrawDecoration`) only ever painted to canvas and returned nothing, so no bbox for that content was ever recorded anywhere. Since `_lastTextElements`/`_lastSceneElements` (populated during `render()`) are the *only* source both the Object Strip and real canvas click hit-testing/selection-outline drawing read from, this meant Layer Pack content was invisible to the Object Strip, unclickable on the canvas, and could never show a selection outline — present in the picture, absent from the product. Fixed at the source: all three draw functions (plus `_drawMuseumCaption`, which `_layerDrawText` delegates to for the `museumCaption` text source) now return a `{bx,by,bw,bh}` geometry box describing what they actually drew (or `null` when nothing was drawn — an empty Museum Caption with no title/artist/age/date, for instance). `_renderLayers`'s three callbacks wrap each call through a new `_pushLayerObject(layer,type,box)`, producing the exact same shape `_sceneBbox()`/`_stickerBbox()` already use (`{id,type,label,bx,by,bw,bh,visible,locked:true}` — always `locked:true`, since Layer Pack content is theme-owned, not creator-editable) into a new accumulator, `_layerObjectBboxes`. That accumulator can't be pushed directly into `_lastSceneElements` at each `_renderLayers` call site, because `render()` has a real ordering hazard: `_lastSceneElements=[]` resets *after* the 'slide'/'frame'/'holder'/'element'-scoped `_renderLayers` calls but *before* the final 'overlay'-scoped one (Builder Convergence Sprint's own 5th target) — so anything pushed early would be silently wiped by that later reset. Fixed by concatenating the whole accumulator into `_lastSceneElements` exactly once, right after the 'overlay' call and before the drag-guide/selection-outline code that reads it. A label falls back through `layer.label` (if the theme declared one) or a new `_humanizeLayerId(id)` helper (`'wax-seal'` → `'Wax Seal'`) — no theme needs to add a `label` field for this to work correctly. `js/objectStrip.js` gained one new loop, after the existing SceneEngine.listElements()/getStickers() loops, iterating `SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()` and skipping any id already shown by those (tracked via a `shownSceneIds` set, so a blueprint element or a user-placed sticker is never double-listed) — every remaining entry is, by construction, Layer Pack content, shown via the exact same `FRIENDLY_TYPE` fallback table (`text`/`sticker`/`decoration`) every other Object Strip card already uses, always as 🔒 "Part of the world" (never 🟢 editable). Selection and Context Panel routing needed zero changes: `js/contextPanel.js`'s `TYPE_TO_SECTIONS` already maps `text`/`sticker`/`decoration` to the correct Card Designer section, and `locked:true` already correctly suppresses resize handles (`_supportsResize`) the same way it does for any other locked object — clicking a Layer Pack object routes to the right section and shows it as non-editable there, matching what it actually is. Verified via Playwright with a synthetic Museum-Gallery-shaped theme carrying a 3-entry Layer Pack (a 'slide'-scoped Decoration, a 'frame'-scoped Sticker, and a 'holder'-scoped `museumCaption` Text): before a picture is added, only the 'slide'-scoped entry renders/selects (matching the pre-existing, correct "Frame/Holder/Element layers only draw once there's a picture" gating in `render()` — not a bug); once a picture is set, all three appear correctly in both `SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()` and the Object Strip with the right labels and 🔒 badges, and clicking each one selects it and routes Card Designer to the right section. Full regression (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`) passes unchanged with zero console errors; two pre-existing test failures (`objstrip_check.js`, `ctx_states2.js`, both expecting a "Handle" card at a fixed index) were confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified codebase — a stale expectation left over from the earlier Book Title/Page Number default-hide fix, not a regression from this change.)

- Theme → Creator Map (`docs/THEME_TO_CREATOR_MAP.md`) — a documentation-only addition answering a direct product question: for every field a `.vtheme` package can carry, where does it actually surface in Creator — shown, editable, and reflected — not just "does Studio's code consume it" (that parity question is `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md`'s own job, and this document deliberately doesn't restate it). Built by tracing real call sites, not by re-deriving from memory: `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s `CONTROL_CATALOG` (every dynamic control's storage location), the exact `WorkspaceBuilder.layout()` call sites in `js/cardDesigner.js`/`js/pageDesigner.js` (panelId → actual Creator section), `index.html`'s World Designer tab markup (`data-section` groups → control ids → `themeOptions.*` keys), and `js/contextPanel.js`'s Representation `actions` gating. Covers ten field groups (Manifest/Identity, core rendering fields, Presentation Presets, Layouts, Frame Variations, Layer Pack, Representations, the Editor block's full control-to-storage table, Assets, and a closing "reaches nowhere in Creator" list) plus a repeatable four-question method (Consumed? / Shown? / Editable? / Reflected?) for adding a new row when a future theme field ships. Cross-references, rather than duplicates, `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md`/`docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`/`docs/VTHEME_PACKAGE_SPEC.md` — this is the one new thing none of those three answer: the Creator-facing "where does a person actually touch this" index.

- Creator Reconciliation Sprint — Phase 1: The Render Tree Becomes Creator's Object Model (implements the user's own architectural directive — "Builder becomes the single source of truth for both presentation and interaction... Creator should never reconstruct any of this independently... The render tree becomes Creator's object model" — as a narrow, additive, backward-compatible first phase, arrived at only after three parallel investigation passes plus a dedicated Plan-agent validation pass, per the user's own explicit "investigate first, find the narrowest point" instruction. **The core finding**: World Builder already had the exact mechanism this sprint needed, fully authored, sitting unused. `tools/world-builder-v2/js/projectModel.js` has stored `holder.permissions`/`layer.permissions = {moveable, editable, visible}` (default all `true`) with real authoring UI since Builder V2/V3 (`_render{Holder,Layer,Text}PermissionBlock` in `worldBuilderApp.js`) — but `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer()` (the function that turns a Builder Scene Layer into a compiled `theme.layerPack[]` entry) only ever read `layer.permissions.visible` onto the compiled package; `moveable`/`editable` were silently dropped at Build time. Completing that one half-finished wire, not inventing a new one, is this phase's entire mechanism. **Render tree becomes uniform**: a new shared `_sceneObject(raw, owner)` normalizer in `renderer/slideRenderer.js` gives every pushed entry into `_lastSceneElements` — whether it started as a Cover/Hook/End blueprint element (`_sceneBbox`), a Story-Author-placed sticker (`_stickerBbox`), or a theme-authored Layer Pack entry (`_pushLayerObject`) — the same uniform shape: `{id,type,label,bx,by,bw,bh,visible,owner,moveable,editable,locked}`. `owner` is `'world'` (Layer Pack) or `'story'` (blueprint/sticker — exactly today's existing Sprint 8.3 Universal Object Consistency behaviour, now named explicitly instead of re-derived from `!locked` at five different call sites); `moveable`/`editable` default to `!locked` when not supplied, so nothing changes for any object type this sprint didn't give real Builder-sourced values to. `convergeSceneLayer()` gains two lines mirroring the exact, already-proven `visible` pattern (`!(layer.permissions && layer.permissions.X===false)`) — a real gap found in review is resolved by this same arithmetic, not a separate fix: `_ensureSceneLayerDefaults` (Builder's own reconciler stamping `{moveable:true,editable:true,visible:true}`) only runs on-demand via `findSceneLayer`, never at Build time, so a Scene Layer positioned once and never reopened could reach `convergeSceneLayer` with `permissions` still `undefined` — the mirrored pattern already resolves `undefined` to `true` for all three fields, identical to what the reconciler would have stamped, verified directly (`node -e` against the literal expression) before relying on it. Hand-authored `layer-packs/*.json` entries (the Builder's other, separate `layerPack` source, via `collectFolder('layer-packs')`, which never passes through `convergeSceneLayer`) simply never gain these keys — `!!undefined` in `_pushLayerObject` resolves to conservative `false`, exactly matching every pre-sprint theme's existing always-locked behaviour (Museum Gallery, unchanged). **Object Strip becomes a pure render-tree reader**: `js/objectStrip.js`'s `refresh()` stopped calling `SceneEngine.listElements()`/`getStickers()` directly for blueprint elements and stickers — a real architectural gap the investigation surfaced, since those two categories were being reconstructed from SceneEngine rather than read back from what actually rendered, while only Layer Pack objects went through the render tree, stitched together with a manually-maintained `shownSceneIds` de-dup Set. Now there is exactly one source (`SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()`+`getTextElements()`), the de-dup hack is gone by construction, and user-placed stickers appear in Object Strip for the first time (a pre-existing gap closed as a natural consequence of unification, not a separate feature). Background and Artwork remain the two disclosed synthetic entries (genuinely page-level concepts with no independent render-tree bbox today — Background is the canvas itself, Artwork has no SceneEngine element on Story-role pages). The ownership badge is now driven by the entry's own `owner`/`editable` fields, and gained a third distinction the investigation found conflated before: `editable:false` used to always read "🔒 Part of the world" even for a Story-owned object the child individually locked themselves — now `owner==='story'` reads "🔒 Locked" instead, `owner==='world'` keeps "🔒 Part of the world". `_lastTextElements`' four Story-Theme-furniture entries (Story Text/Handle/Footer/Page Number) are deliberately untouched — fixed Story Theme chrome, not Builder-authored variable content, out of this phase's scope. **Context Panel asks the selected object, not a type table**: a real, verified misleading-UX bug, not a harmless dead end, was the trigger for this — selecting a Layer Pack object routed through the same `TYPE_TO_SECTIONS` a real blueprint element uses, opening a section (e.g. the decoration case in `cardDesigner.js`) that reads `slide.metadata.elementOverrides` without ever checking whether the selected id resolves to anything real; a child could select "Wax Seal" and land in a fully live-looking editor that doesn't target it at all. Fixed by a new `_findSceneObject(sceneId,sceneType)` (reading the identical render tree Object Strip already reads) checked before type-routing in `refresh()`: a selected object with `owner==='world'` never opens the generic section — instead `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure(sceneObj)` shows an honest banner, worded from the object's own `editable` flag ("This is part of the World, but you may adjust it. That kind of edit isn't available in Creator yet." vs. plain "This is part of the World.") — never a fabricated editor for content Creator has no real controls for yet. Every Story-owned object (blueprint/sticker/text) is completely unaffected — verified directly: adding a real sticker via Sticker Studio and selecting it still opens its real, correctly-targeted section exactly as before. **Investigated and deliberately not done**: `js/contextPanel.js`'s `TYPE_TO_SECTIONS` and `js/app.js`'s `SCENE_TYPE_TO_SECTION` looked like a textbook duplicate-logic case worth consolidating (both 5-entry type→section tables) — direct comparison found they are **not** interchangeable: `'image-holder'` maps to `['image']` in one and `'frame'` in the other, for genuinely different, documented reasons (Context Panel's Story-role-specific override vs. Card Designer's Universal Object Selection `focusSection()` on Cover/Hook/End pages) — merging them without a full behaviour audit on Cover/Hook/End page selection risked a real regression the "preserve backward compatibility" constraint rules out, so this was disclosed as a finding rather than forced through. **Explicitly deferred, named not silently dropped**: Phase 2 (actually persisting a drag when a `moveable:true` Layer Pack object is moved — needs one new small override bag mirroring `slide.metadata.elementOverrides`; a real generic Modify surface for Builder-owned editable content); Phase 3+ (Holder/Frame-level permissions as their own Object Strip row — Frame Variation is already a separate, working, creator-editable control per `docs/THEME_TO_CREATOR_MAP.md` §5/§8, not a render-tree object today; a `removable`/delete capability — Builder's schema has none today, and nothing about Layer Pack objects is Creator-deletable today, correctly, so nothing changes here). `tools/world-builder/` (v1) is deliberately untouched throughout, per this codebase's own recent, explicit precedent (the Decoration Shapes sprint). No new rendering engine, no Theme Contract redesign, no second object model — every change is an additive field or a read-path consolidation onto structures that already existed. Docs updated: `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §7 (new `moveable`/`editable` Layer fields), `docs/THEME_CONTRACT.md` (new §6.1), `docs/THEME_TO_CREATOR_MAP.md` §6 (corrected from "No, by design — `locked:true` always" to the real capability-gated behaviour), `docs/ENGINE_V2_SCENE_MODEL.md` (a precisely-scoped v1.6 Change History entry — its own "never a published render" claim stays exactly true for Engine V2's own native Runtime paint step, unmodified; what's new is a second, separate consumer, Studio itself, reading the same authored data through the already-open Scene-convergence path). Verified via a synthetic-theme Playwright harness test simulating real `convergeSceneLayer` output (three Layer Pack entries: real `moveable:true,editable:true`, explicit `false`, and legacy-shaped with neither field) confirming the render tree, Object Strip badges, and Context Panel disclosure wording all match exactly; a second test confirming a real Sticker-Studio-placed sticker still gets `owner:'story'` and still opens its real, correctly-targeted section; full existing Creator Playwright regression suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, etc.) passing unchanged with zero console errors; `tools/world-builder-v2/verify/goldenBuild.js` passing unchanged (36/36) confirming the two-line `convergeSceneLayer` addition broke nothing in the existing compile/validate/import pipeline; a direct `node -e` algebraic check confirming the absent-permissions-resolves-to-true reasoning before relying on it in the actual code.)

- Engine V2 Promotion Strategy (`docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`) — an investigation-and-strategy-only deliverable, no code changes, answering a direct architectural question: can Engine V2 (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/engineRuntime.js`, World Builder's own native preview runtime) be promoted into a shared platform runtime for Builder Preview/Creator Canvas/Publish/eventually Reader, replacing Engine V1 (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) incrementally, with Builder's authoring architecture held frozen. Three parallel Explore investigations (Engine V2's real capability surface, Engine V1's full feature inventory, and exact consumer/Theme-Contract boundary mapping) converged on one confirmed, load-bearing blocker: `engineRuntime.js` has **zero** consumption of any compiled `.vtheme` field (`layouts`/`frameVariations`/`layerPack`/`representations`/`slide`/`holder`/`frame`/`panel`/`storyText`/`footerText`/`watermark` — confirmed by grep, not inferred) — it only ever renders a *live Builder authoring session's* in-memory Scene objects, resolving Frame references through Builder's own global `ProjectModel`, never a compiled Theme. `convergeSceneLayer`/`convergeScene` (Builder Convergence Sprint) is confirmed strictly one-way (Scene Model → Engine V1 shape); no reverse path exists. The verdict: **Engine V2 cannot be promoted as-is** — doing so is a parity-building program, not a swap. Engine V2 is standalone/pure and is genuinely *ahead* of Engine V1 in two respects (real word-wrap for Scene text, where V1's Scene text draw calls never wrap at all; a 13-kind vector Shape system richer than V1's hand-mirrored 5-kind subset) — but lacks, with no Engine V2 equivalent found anywhere: Layer Pack's 5-scope declarative containership system, Artwork Themes as an independent theme-layering dimension, Frame Variations' 7-preset ornament pipeline (storybook/polaroid/ribbon/wooden/magic/vintage/tape/cloud), Layout `composition` variants (especially Quote's entirely different no-Frame draw path), Presentation Presets' three-tier resolution, page furniture (Handle/Footer/PageNumber/decorative glyphs) with position enums, the full per-image adjustment stack (crop/focal/straighten/brightness/contrast/highlights/shadows/warmth/saturation/sharpness/vignette), the Cover/Hook/End blueprint dual-pipeline, and the DPR-aware `init(canvas,{dpr})` WYSIWYE mechanism itself (Engine V2 uses a genuinely different canvas model — variable per-aspect pixel dimensions vs. Engine V1's always-fixed 1080×1350 logical canvas). No live "Reader" surface exists anywhere in the codebase today (confirmed via repo-wide grep — only `FileReader` API hits and doc prose using "reader" to mean the end consumer of a downloaded export), confirming the request's own "eventually Reader" framing is correctly forward-looking, not a near-term target. The proposed strategy: build one new, additive, Studio-side adapter (`js/engineV2Adapter.js`, proposed not built) translating a resolved compiled theme into Engine V2's Scene Model shape — the missing reverse direction of `convergeSceneLayer`'s existing one-way translation — then migrate **consumer by consumer, never feature by feature** (the Decoration Shapes sprint's own "kept in lockstep by hand" duplication is cited as a live demonstration of what a feature-split produces at scale): Phase 0 builds and pixel-verifies the adapter against Museum Gallery with zero call sites wired to any real UI; Phase 1 migrates the lowest-stakes one-shot consumer (Card Designer's Frame swatch or `ThumbnailEngine.generate()`); Phase 2 moves the real export engine (`js/storyDestinations.js`, where page-furniture/Quote-composition parity actually has to close, not stay deferred); Phase 3 moves the live editor canvas only after full-fidelity parity is proven; Phase 4 retires Engine V1 only once every consumer has migrated and a full regression pass shows zero behaviour change; Phase 5 (Reader) is named as a future consumer of the same runtime, explicitly out of this document's own scope. Builder's Scene/Holder/Layer authoring model, the compiled `.vtheme` shape, `convergeSceneLayer`'s existing one-way translation, and every already-published Theme are explicitly named as staying completely frozen throughout — every proposed change is new Studio-side code (plus disclosed, scoped Engine V2 capability extensions for the ornament-preset/page-furniture gap, an explicit open question, not resolved by this document) reading from structures that already exist, never a change to how a Theme Author authors anything. Three real open risks are disclosed rather than glossed over: ornament-preset fidelity is sized as "the largest single fidelity gap" with no proposed solution yet; whether to extend `engineRuntime.js` with the missing drawing routines vs. keep a small permanent Engine-V1-only hybrid for page furniture is flagged as a real product decision needing explicit sign-off before Phase 2; and Engine V2's per-object drawing performance at editor-interaction frequency (every drag-move frame) was never measured and is flagged as needing a real performance pass before Phase 3, not assumed safe. No code was written — this is a strategy proposal only; per the standing "architecture changes require explicit approval" rule, even Phase 0's isolated, zero-call-site adapter would need its own sign-off before implementation begins.

- Scene Adapter Architecture Analysis (`docs/SCENE_ADAPTER_ARCHITECTURE_ANALYSIS.md`) — an investigation-only companion to `docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`, no code changes, answering five questions about a proposed `Builder → Publish Theme → Standalone Scene Adapter → Canonical Scene → Shared Runtime → Creator/Publish/Reader` pipeline with Builder held frozen. **Q1 (remaining Creator work)**: the Adapter by itself retires almost none of the hard remaining work — Object Strip/Selection are already Mostly Complete (Creator Reconciliation Sprint Phase 1 did this without any Adapter), but Rendering/Publish (gated entirely on the Shared Runtime reaching feature parity with Engine V1 — see the Promotion Strategy doc's own gap list) and Context Panel/Editing/Save-Reload (all gated on redesigning Creator's override-bag key space from blueprint-element-ids/fixed-bag-keys to canonical Scene Object ids) all Require Significant Work regardless of whether the Adapter exists, because an Adapter reshapes data, it doesn't paint pixels or invent generic editing UI. One genuinely good finding, verified by reading `js/projectManager.js`'s `serialize()` directly: Creator's save format already stores Story-Author deltas plus a bare theme-id reference, never a resolved Theme snapshot — the right shape for a re-derived-canonical-Scene architecture already, with re-keying as the only real gap. **Q2 (does the Adapter isolate Creator from Builder evolution)**: only partially, and the partition is precisely bounded by this session's own Phase 1 precedent — additive changes (a new Scene property, a new capability flag, a new named preset within an existing closed vocabulary) cost only Adapter+Runtime changes, proven directly by how cheaply `layer.permissions.moveable/editable` shipped; structural changes (new object types, new Frame systems that don't fit the flat-band model, and — not hypothetical, already on this project's own Roadmap as item 6 — Audio, plus Animation/Perspective/Lighting) require changes all the way into Creator, because no Adapter can invent Runtime drawing capability or Creator interaction affordances that don't exist yet. **Q3 (permanent boundary, temporary layer, or unnecessary)**: temporary migration layer — the key insight being that the proposed pipeline places the Adapter *after* Publish (consumption-time), while the codebase already has a Build-time translation step doing conceptually the same job (`convergeSceneLayer`), and every "Convergence Sprint" in this project's history has consistently preferred extending one existing pipeline over standing up a parallel one. The architecturally clean end-state is retargeting Build-time convergence to emit the canonical Scene shape directly (so Publish *is* the canonical Scene, no runtime-time Adapter needed) — explicitly out of reach under "Builder frozen" as a near-term constraint, but named as the Adapter's own correct retirement condition, not a competing alternative. **Q4 (risk)**: short-term (bounded, expected to resolve) — fidelity gaps during transition, dual-engine maintenance, unmeasured interactive-frequency performance, and doubled translation-drift risk while both `convergeSceneLayer` and the new Adapter exist simultaneously; long-term (only real if the Adapter is kept permanent) — institutionalized double translation contradicting "minimal future duplication," unbounded Adapter complexity growth (the same kind-by-kind branching pattern `convergeSceneLayer` already shows, risking a second full rendering-semantics implementation), information loss (a concrete, already-observable risk — `_resolveArtworkFields` already discards a chosen Frame Variation's authored *name*, keeping only resolved values, and Object Strip's Layer Pack labels already depend on Builder having authored an explicit `.label` field), a larger blast radius once multiple consumers share one Runtime with no existing compatibility-versioning practice in this codebase, and the risk of stakeholders over-trusting the Adapter as general Builder-evolution insulation when Q2 shows it's bounded to the additive case only. **Q5 (recommendation)**: Option A, conditionally — build the Adapter exactly as `docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s Phase 0-3 already proposed, but govern it explicitly as temporary scaffolding with a named retirement condition (a new Phase 4.5 this document adds: once Runtime fidelity parity and the canonical Scene shape are proven, retarget Build-time convergence to emit it directly and retire the runtime-time Adapter) rather than treating it as the platform's permanent boundary — reasoned against plain Option B (real progress, proven this session, but has a hard ceiling: never reaches one shared Runtime, leaves the Decoration-Shapes-style hand-synced duplication permanent rather than temporary) and against unconditional Option A (institutionalizes exactly the double-translation duplication the investigation's own stated optimization goals rule out). No code was written; this is the second of two paired strategy documents, both explicitly gated behind the standing "architecture changes require explicit approval" rule before any implementation begins.

- Creator Runtime Pass Sprint — Promote the Center Pane into the Page Runtime (`docs/CREATOR_PAGE_RUNTIME.md`; implements the user's own directive to formally promote Creator's existing center pane into a named "Page Runtime" — the single source of truth for the active page, its rendered objects, and its selection — with every surrounding panel becoming a pure consumer/projection of it, never independently reconstructing state; explicitly a **promotion, not a rewrite**, per the brief's own closing instruction: "reuse the existing implementation wherever possible... this sprint changes ownership of state, not rendering technology." Investigation (following directly from the Creator Reconciliation Sprint's own render-tree work) found most of the "Page Runtime" concept already existed in Creator, scattered across `js/app.js` with no single name and two divergent notify sequences — five concrete, verified findings, not speculative: (1) `draw()` called directly from ~10 drag-handler sites, bypassing `window.redrawPreview()`; (2) two different, overlapping "notify everyone" tails — the selection setters' 4-call sequence vs. `showSlide`'s own 6-call sequence; (3) **a confirmed real bug** — `showSlide()` never cleared `_selectedSceneElement`/`_selectedTextElement`, so a selection from page N could open editing controls on page N+1 that don't correspond to anything real there, and `js/contextPanel.js`'s scene-element branch only checked whether the selected object still existed *after* deciding to open a section (only to pick disclosure wording), never to gate opening the section at all; (4) `PageOps.reorderPage`/`moveToEnd` duplicated or short-circuited the otherwise-uniform `_afterMutation` pipeline instead of going through it consistently; (5) "Start Creating" triggered three independent, redundant re-render sequences on one click. Save (`js/projectManager.js`'s `serialize()`) and Publish (`js/storyDestinations.js`/`js/publishStudio.js`/`js/pdfWriter.js`, confirmed rendering through the identical `SlideRenderer.buildPayload()`+`.render()` pair as the editor canvas on the same live slide reference, zero bypasses) were investigated and found to already satisfy the sprint's own requirements — explicitly left unchanged, stated rather than re-implemented for its own sake. **The fix**: new `js/pageRuntime.js` (`window.PageRuntime`) is a thin ownership/dispatch layer — not a new rendering system — wrapping the exact existing `js/app.js` functions via the same `configure({...})` host-binding pattern `js/objectStrip.js`/`js/contextPanel.js` already used. Read accessors: `getActivePage()` (→ `AppState.slides[AppState.currentSlide]`, now the one source every panel's `getCurrentSlide` host binding points at — `CardDesigner`/`PageDesigner`/`StickerStudio`/`ContextPanel`/`ObjectStrip` alike), `getRenderedObjects()` (→ `{scene, text}`, naming the Creator Reconciliation Sprint's own render-tree contract as the Runtime's object-discovery API, no new shape), `getSelection()` (→ `{sceneId, sceneType, textId}`), `selectionIsValid()` (does the current selection still resolve to something actually rendered on the active page right now — `'image-holder'` always valid as the disclosed synthetic exception, everything else checked against the render tree). Mutation entry points: `openPage(index)` (delegates to `showSlide`), `clearSelection()`, and **two** explicit selection functions — `selectSceneObject(id,type)` / `selectTextObject(id)` — deliberately not one `selectObject(id,type)` dispatching on `type==='text'`, because a Scene Object can itself legitimately carry `type:'text'` (a Layer Pack text entry like a Museum Caption) which is a completely different selection channel from Story Theme text furniture (Story Text/Handle/Footer/Page Number); an earlier single-function draft silently rerouted a selected Museum-Caption-shaped Scene Object into the wrong channel, caught by the sprint's own Playwright verification (clicking Museum Caption after Wax Seal left the Context Panel showing Wax Seal's stale banner) and fixed by the two-function split before shipping — a real bug found and fixed via testing, not a hypothetical. `notify()` is the one dispatch function (`redrawPreview()` + `CardDesigner.refresh()` + `ContextPanel.refresh()` + `ObjectStrip.refresh()`) both selection setters and `showSlide` now end with, replacing their two divergent tails. The selection-teardown fix for finding (3) lives inside `showSlide` itself, not only inside `PageRuntime.openPage()` — since `showSlide` is the one real choke point every page-change path already funnels through (thumbnail clicks, `PageOps._refreshSelection`, session restore, `CreationFlow`, `PublishStudio`'s "Fix in Editor", `ThemeEngine`'s theme-apply path all call it directly, confirmed by grep, zero bypasses), putting the fix there means every one of those callers gets it for free. `js/contextPanel.js`'s scene-element branch now checks `PageRuntime`-backed object existence **before** opening any section, not only before choosing disclosure wording — a selection left over from a different page now falls through to the default view instead of a live-looking but id-blind editor. `js/pageOps.js`'s `reorderPage` and `moveToEnd` now always route through `_afterMutation` (the "not selected" branch's hand-duplicated pipeline collapsed into `_afterMutation(idx!==-1?idx:AppState.currentSlide)`, reusing the exact same object-identity-lookup logic instead of a separate inline copy). `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_finish` now calls `PageRuntime.openPage(AppState.currentSlide)` once instead of three independent re-render sequences. Deliberately **not** folded into `notify()`: the ~10 direct `draw()` calls inside continuous mousemove drag-tick handlers (resize/scene/text drag, image pan) — a correct, pre-existing 60fps performance decision the code's own comments already call out, not an oversight; their `mouseup` drag-end handlers already run the full refresh sequence once the gesture completes, so routing every mousemove tick through `notify()` would have been a real, unrequested performance regression. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright Runtime Pass test plus full regression across the existing Creator suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`) — all pass unchanged, zero console errors; two pre-existing, already-stale failures (`objstrip_check.js`, `ctx_states2.js`, confirmed via `git stash` in the preceding sprint to fail identically on the unmodified codebase) carried forward unresolved, not new regressions. `docs/CREATOR_PAGE_RUNTIME.md` is the new canonical doc for runtime ownership, the Active Page lifecycle, object discovery, the selection lifecycle, the Runtime Pass, `PageRuntime`'s public API, and a full per-consumer before/after table. No Builder redesign, no Theme contract redesign, no rendering-engine redesign, no second page model, no second runtime — the existing center pane was promoted into the canonical Page Runtime, exactly as scoped.)

- Creator Acceptance Sprint — Theme Fidelity Pass (Museum Gallery) (`docs/CREATOR_THEME_FIDELITY.md`; a P0 product-convergence sprint, explicitly not a feature or architecture sprint, judged by one acceptance test: a Builder-authored page must open in Creator exactly as Builder's own Runtime Preview shows it, before any Story Author content exists — "Creator does not recreate the page. Creator does not reinterpret the Theme." Investigation (three parallel code-verified traces: the compiled Museum Gallery package + Builder's Runtime Preview semantics via `engineRuntime.js`'s `_paintHolder`, Creator's actual image-less render/panel behaviour, and whether any placeholder mechanism already existed to reuse) found one root cause, not several unrelated bugs: `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveBorder(s)` resolved an Artwork Theme's Frame only `if(hasImage)` (a deliberate Sprint 9.3 decision, "if a page contains no artwork, Artwork Theme has no effect," now reversed specifically for the Frame chrome). Because the Frame/mat/ornament/stroke/caption draw block and every Frame/Holder-scoped Layer Pack entry (Wax Seal, Gallery Spotlight, Museum Caption) only run when that resolved border is non-null, the entire World disappeared behind one boolean — wall tone was already correctly image-independent (`_resolveWallTone`, Sprint 9.7), and every function the frame block calls (`_artworkBorder`/`_resolveArtworkFields`/`_drawPictureFrameFill`/`_drawArtworkPresentation`/`_drawArtworkCaption`) was *already* purely theme/card-override-driven with zero `s.image` dependency, so lifting the one gate closed the entire visual gap with no further drawing-code changes; only `_drawImage` itself correctly still requires a real image. `_artworkTheme(s)` returning `null` whenever no Artwork Theme is active scopes the fix to Artwork Theme pages only (zero effect on plain Story Theme pages), and Quote composition's own pre-existing `if(_composition==='quote'){...}else if(_border){...}` short-circuit keeps Museum Gallery's frame-less Quote layout frame-less regardless. New `_drawArtworkPlaceholder(panelRect,border,chromeColor)` mirrors Cover/Hook/End's own existing `_drawSceneImageHolder` "Add an image" dashed-placeholder pattern (Sprint 6.2) for the one shape that never had an equivalent — a Story-role page's artwork content rect, since `SceneEngine.getRenderData` returns `null` for Story role by design — but takes an explicit `chromeColor` (the same wall-tone luminance check already used for Handle/Page Number text) instead of the original's hardcoded white, since a light Frame Variation's wall (Museum Gallery's own "Classic White") would make a white dashed line invisible; wired into `render()` right after the existing image-draw call, using `_holderRectFor` so it sits exactly where the real picture will land. `js/objectStrip.js`'s Artwork card — previously hard-gated on `slide.image` truthy, the reason "Tap Artwork Place → Replace Artwork" was unreachable before an image existed — now always shows once there's no Scene blueprint, worded "Artwork Place" before a picture exists and "Artwork" once it does. **A second, deeper bug found while verifying this exact fix, not assumed**: the card's original gate was `slide.pageType==='story'`, but a freshly Creation-Flow-created page's `pageType` never gets promoted away from `'blank'` — grepped every `pageType=` assignment site and confirmed nothing in `js/creationFlow.js`/`js/pageOps.js` ever sets it to `'story'` for that path (only the sidebar's separate bulk "Upload Images" importer does, on pages *it* creates); this would have left the Artwork card permanently absent for the actual primary onboarding path even after every other fix in this sprint. Fixed by matching the exact criterion `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s own `_hasScene` gate already uses (`SceneEngine.getRenderData(slide)!==null`) instead of a hardcoded pageType string — correctly covers `'story'` and `'blank'` alike (and any future non-scene pageType), since the renderer already treats them identically. `js/contextPanel.js`'s default view gained a "Welcome to `<World Icon> <World Name>`" heading (new `_worldIdentity()`, reusing the exact `ThemeEngine.getActiveArtworkThemeId`/`ThemeRegistry.get` lookup `js/app.js`'s own header readout already makes) plus a two-line ownership legend ("✏️ Objects marked editable can be changed." / "🌍 Objects marked World belong to the World."), above the pre-existing, completely unchanged Page Style/Caption/Background/Add Sticker controls — real Story-Author capability, not removed to match the acceptance spec's own illustrative minimal mockup. `_renderArtworkActions()` now reads "🖼️ Add Artwork" before any picture exists, "🖼️ Replace Artwork" after, and hides "✂️ Crop / Rotate" until there's something to crop (it already silently no-oped with nothing selected — hiding it removes a dead button, not new capability). Object Strip's World-owned badge glyph changed from 🔒 to 🌍 to match the acceptance checklist's own explicit vocabulary and the 🌍 icon Context Panel's World-object disclosure banner already used — text/glyph only, the editable/owner gating logic (already correctly distinguishing editable, locked-World, and locked-Story) is unchanged. **Checked directly against the acceptance checklist and found already correct, no change made**: Sticker Studio (already CSS-hidden until "Add a Sticker" is clicked, never a default panel), the sidebar's "Upload Images" button (a separate, pre-existing bulk multi-page importer, never part of Context Panel's default view), `CardDesigner`'s image section (already gracefully disables its controls with no image), and Publish (`js/storyDestinations.js`/`js/publishStudio.js` render through the identical `buildPayload`+`render` pair as the editor canvas, so the fix reaches Publish for free — verified directly by opening Publish Studio on an image-less page and confirming it renders without error, not merely asserted). **Two findings investigated and deliberately left disclosed, not fixed, per the sprint's own "do not redesign the Theme contract / do not build new capability" constraints**: `representation.defaultFrame` is authored in the compiled package but never consumed anywhere in the Creator runtime (Builder-authoring-time-only today) — zero visible effect for Museum Gallery specifically since both real representations point at `classic-white`, whose fields are deliberately empty and already delegate to the `gallery` Presentation Preset's own System Defaults, so wiring it would render identically for this theme; flagged as real follow-up work for a future theme whose representations pick a non-default Frame Variation. The Museum Gallery `handle` Layer Pack entry's default-to-`'spotlight'` decoration kind (when a layer has no `decoration` payload) was investigated as a possible bug but found genuinely ambiguous — `gallery-spotlight`, a different, clearly intentional entry, relies on the exact same default for its own glow, so "fixing" it risks silently removing a real, intentional effect and second-guessing Builder's own authored intent, which the sprint's own Golden Rule explicitly forbids; left untouched. Verified via a new Playwright test (`museum_fidelity_test.js`, scratch-only) driving a Museum-Gallery-shaped synthetic fixture (frameVariations + a full layerPack) through the real acceptance journey: before any picture, the canvas already paints wall tone + a mat/frame/placeholder (pixel-sampled non-blank), Object Strip lists Background/Artwork Place/Wax Seal/Gallery Spotlight (Museum Caption correctly absent — an empty caption with no title still draws nothing, matching pre-existing correct behaviour), Context Panel's default view shows the Welcome heading + legend, and selecting Artwork Place shows only "Add Artwork"; after a real picture is set, the placeholder is gone (sampled pixel matches the uploaded image), the card renames to "Artwork," and selecting it shows "Replace Artwork" + "Crop / Rotate"; Publish Studio opens and renders without error on the image-less page. Full regression across the existing Creator suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`) passes unchanged, zero console errors throughout. No Builder redesign, no Theme contract redesign, no new object model, no new editing capability — every change either lifts a single overly-strict gate or makes an already-correct capability reachable at the right moment.)

- Museum Gallery Fidelity Trace — real `.vtheme`, not a fixture, surfaces two silent crashes (a direct follow-up to the Theme Fidelity Pass above, requested explicitly to re-run the same acceptance journey against the real, compiled `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` file loaded through the real production import path — `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile()` → `ThemeRegistry.importPackage()` — rather than the hand-written, Museum-Gallery-*shaped* synthetic fixture every earlier test in that sprint had used. This surfaced two real, previously-invisible bugs no synthetic fixture had ever exercised. **Bug 1 — a real crash, silently swallowed everywhere**: tracing the real file produced a fully blank canvas (`getImageData`→`[0,0,0,0]`), empty `SlideRenderer.getSceneElements()`/`getTextElements()`, and Object Strip's "Nothing on this page yet." Manually re-invoking `showSlide()`/`SlideRenderer.render()` outside the app's own defensive `try{...}catch(e){}` wrappers surfaced the real exception: `TypeError: Cannot read properties of null (reading 'variants')` at `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_defaultOptionsFor`, called via `getOptions()`→`resolveTheme()`→`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `buildPayload()`. Root cause: Museum Gallery's `supportedCreationTypes` has no `'story'` entry, so `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_finish()` only ever calls `applyArtworkTheme()` for it, never `applyTheme()` — on a genuinely fresh project whose only chosen World is a pure Artwork Theme, the Story Theme (`ThemeEngine.getActiveTheme()`) never gets set. This is not hypothetical: `js/themeRegistry.js`'s own comments disclose that Studio ships with **zero built-in themes today** (`OFFICIAL_THEMES` deliberately commented out, `storybook-classic` "deliberately left unresolved rather than rewired... exists only until reintroduced by import/publish") — a null active Story Theme is an accepted, normal state in this Repository-only architecture, not something to paper over with a fallback registration. The real bug was that nothing downstream *handled* that accepted null state: `_defaultOptionsFor(theme)` dereferenced `theme.variants`/`.slide`/`.holder` assuming a real object; `resolveTheme()` dereferenced `base.id`/`base.frame.color`/etc. the same way; and `buildPayload()` called `ThemeEngine.resolveTheme()`/`getOptions()` **directly, with no try/catch**, bypassing the exact safety net `_theme(s)`/`_options(s)` already established elsewhere in the same file (both already fall back to `FALLBACK_THEME`/`FALLBACK_OPTIONS` on any thrown exception) — and because `creationFlow.js`'s `_finish()` and `app.js`'s `showSlide()` both wrap their own calls in `try{...}catch(e){}` by design (so one bad refresh doesn't wedge the UI), the exception was caught and silently discarded at every call site, never surfacing as a console error.
