Fixed by normalizing `theme=theme||{}` at the top of `_defaultOptionsFor` (same "no theme = System Defaults" behaviour every other code path already has), adding a `_NO_THEME_FALLBACK` constant to `resolveTheme()` (deliberately identical values to `slideRenderer.js`'s own `FALLBACK_THEME`), and adding the same try/catch + fallback pattern to `buildPayload()`'s two direct calls for defense-in-depth — this fixes the crash for every caller of `getOptions()`/`resolveTheme()` at once, several of which (`js/cardDesigner.js`, `js/contextPanel.js`) call these functions with no try/catch of their own and were equally exposed. **Bug 2 — the `handle` Layer Pack entry drew an unintended glow and a nonsensical Object Strip card**: with the crash fixed, the real Object Strip showed a fourth World card literally labelled "Handle" — meaningless to a child. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §7 already documents the exact intended contract: an entry naming `page-number`/`handle` with no real content payload is **declarative-only** — "the actual pixels are still drawn by the pre-existing, unrelated engine feature it names... never a second, competing renderer," and `position` is "only meaningful on the declarative handle/page-number ids." `_layerDrawText` already honours this correctly for `page-number` (no `text.content`/`.source` → returns null); `_layerDrawDecoration` had no equivalent guard for `type:"decoration"` entries — with no `decoration` payload, `kind` defaulted to `'spotlight'`, so `handle` (real package: `type:"decoration"`, no `decoration` field, `position:"bottom-right"`) silently painted an unintended lighting glow across the whole slide *and* got pushed onto the render tree as its own selectable Scene Object. Fixed by making `_layerDrawDecoration` return `null` when `!layer.decoration && layer.position` — the exact, spec-sanctioned signature of a declarative-only entry; `gallery-spotlight` (Museum Gallery's other content-less decoration entry) is unaffected since it has no `decoration` payload but also no `position` field, so it still resolves through the existing `kind==='spotlight'` default and keeps its real, intentional glow, confirmed unchanged in every regression fixture. **One separate, disclosed, NOT-fixed finding**: the Context Panel's "Welcome to `<icon>` Museum Gallery" heading shows the generic 📖 fallback instead of 🏛️ for the real imported package, since `ThemeRegistry.get('museum-gallery')` returns only the `theme` sub-object (no `themeIcon` key at all — that field lives only in the compiled package's `manifest.themeIcon`, and `ThemeRegistry.get()` discards `manifest` entirely); this is a pre-existing gap in the exact same lookup pattern `js/app.js`'s own header readout already uses, not something the acceptance checklist's named criteria cover (which concern the ownership legend/badges functioning, not which glyph appears) — disclosed rather than silently fixed, since resolving it means deciding whether `ThemeRegistry.get()` should start merging manifest fields onto the theme object, a real design question out of this trace's scope. Verified via a new Playwright test (`real_museum_trace.js`, scratch-only) loading the real `.vtheme` through the real import path and driving Theme Load → Scene Creation → Object Registry/Runtime → Thumbnail → Object Strip → Context Panel end to end, confirming all 7 of the requester's own acceptance criteria (museum shows in thumbnail and main canvas, Object Strip lists every real Builder object with no phantom entries, Context Panel's 🌍/✏️ disclosure works correctly on selection, no "Nothing on this page yet," no renderer fallback to an empty scene). Full regression across every existing suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`) passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Builder redesign, no Theme contract redesign, no new object model — both fixes are root-cause corrections to existing, documented contracts that a synthetic test fixture had accidentally been masking all along. See `docs/CREATOR_THEME_FIDELITY.md`'s new Addendum section for the full account.)

- Screen 2 World Library Card — Thumbnail vs. Hero Image (a real, user-reported bug: the World Library/Vihu Worlds row card on Screen 2 was rendering a World's Hero Image (`manifest.previewImage`) instead of its Thumbnail (`manifest.thumbnail`) — two separate assets Builder's own Overview screen authors distinctly (Thumbnail for small card/list contexts, Hero Image as the larger representative source), silently conflated in `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_themePreview()` into one generic `image` field that always preferred `previewImage`. Confirmed directly, not assumed: the real Museum Gallery `.vtheme`'s `manifest.thumbnail` (386 chars) and `manifest.previewImage` (1758 chars) are genuinely different images, and before this fix the World Library card's rendered `<img src>` matched the Hero Image, never the Thumbnail. Fixed by having `_themePreview()` resolve both fields separately (`thumbnail`/`heroImage`, each through `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef()` exactly as before) instead of collapsing them into one; `_worldRowCard()` (the World Library/Vihu Worlds row card this bug was reported against) now reads `pv.thumbnail`; `_repThumbnail()`'s own World-level fallback (used only when a Representation has no `thumbnail` of its own, for the larger Screen 2 Representation carousel slide) now prefers `pv.heroImage` before falling back to `pv.thumbnail` then the icon glyph — a more appropriate asset for that bigger visual context, not a behaviour change for any theme that already sets a per-Representation thumbnail. `paintPreview()`'s own top badge is unaffected — it only ever showed `pv.icon` (the `themeIcon` emoji), never an image, and still doesn't. One related, disclosed-not-fixed finding: `js/themeEngine.js`'s `_renderThemeCard()` (the separate, older in-editor Theme Library picker modal, out of scope for this Screen-2-specific report) has the identical `previewImage`-only pattern and may have the same small-card-shows-hero-image issue — left untouched since it wasn't the reported surface and touching it wasn't requested. Verified via Playwright against the real `MuseumGallery.vtheme`: the World Library card's rendered image now byte-matches `manifest.thumbnail` exactly (not `previewImage`) via full-string comparison (a same-PNG-header short-prefix check was insufficient and initially gave a false pass, corrected before relying on it). Full existing regression suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, `real_museum_trace.js`, `real_museum_selection_check.js`) passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Builder/Theme-contract/architecture change — a two-field resolution fix inside one existing Creation Flow helper.)

- Object Strip Label + Zero-Holder Layout fixes (two real, user-reported Builder->Creator gaps, both root-caused, not guessed at, from a real authored World ("My Artwork Gallery") screenshot: an Object Strip showing 3 visually-identical "Scene Sin…" cards, and a request that "if the builder theme does not have holder so does in creator." **Investigation confirmed the actual pixel z-order was already correct** — a genuine Scene-hosted Background (`setSceneBackground`, a full-bleed `{0,0}/{1,1}` fill) converges onto the pre-existing `target:'slide'` scope, which `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `render()` already paints first, before the Frame/Panel/every Place — traced and confirmed via code reading, not assumed. **The real Object Strip bug**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer()` never carried a Scene Layer's own author-given `name` (e.g. "Background," set by `js/projectModel.js`'s `addSceneLayer`/`setSceneBackground`) into the compiled Layer Pack entry's `label` field — so `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_pushLayerObject` fell back to `_humanizeLayerId(layer.id)`, humanizing the compiled id `scene-<sceneId>-<layerId>`; since every Layer on one Scene shares that same Scene-id prefix, they all read as near-identical truncated "Scene Sin…" cards no matter how many genuinely distinct Layers a Scene has. Fixed with one additive field: `convergeSceneLayer`'s `base` object now carries `label: layer.name || undefined`, so each converged Layer shows its own real name. **The real "no Holder" gap**: a Scene converged with zero Places has no way to tell Creator apart from "one Place, no Frame chosen yet" — both produce `representation.defaultFrame: null` — because the compiled `theme.layouts[]` entry never recorded a Scene's actual Place count, despite Sprint 9.6 having reserved exactly this field ("`holders`: Reserved, always 1 in V1") for exactly this purpose; Museum Gallery's own real hand-authored Layouts don't even set it. `convergeScene()` now populates `holders: holders.length` on the converged Layout — the real count, `0` for a genuinely Place-less Scene. Creator's consuming side: `renderer/slideRenderer.js` gained `_activeLayoutHolders(s)` (resolves the active Layout preset, reads its `holders` field, `null` when absent) and `_resolveBorder`'s Artwork Theme branch now skips resolving Frame/mat/wall chrome entirely when `_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0` — exported as `SlideRenderer.activeLayoutHolderCount()`; `js/objectStrip.js`'s Artwork Place card gains the matching `!noHolderAuthored` check before showing itself. Both changes are strictly additive and null-safe: absent the `holders` field (every Layout that predates this, including Museum Gallery's own hand-authored ones), the count resolves to `null`, never `0`, so every existing theme's behaviour is completely unchanged — confirmed directly via the full existing regression suite, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, and `real_museum_trace.js` all passing unchanged with Museum Gallery's own "Artwork Place" card still showing exactly as before. Verified via two independent passes: (1) a synthetic Playwright theme with two Layouts (`holders:0` and `holders:1`) confirmed the Artwork Place card is correctly absent for the zero-Holder Layout and correctly present for the other, both consuming a Layer Pack entry whose `label` renders as a clean "Background" instead of a humanized id; (2) `builder.js`'s real `convergeScene`/`convergeSceneLayer` methods driven directly (no mock/reimplementation) against a hand-built zero-Place Scene and a one-Place Scene, confirming the real producer emits `holders:0`/`holders:1` correctly and the real `label` field carries through unmodified. `tools/world-builder-v2/verify/goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §6/§7 updated — the `holders` field's row now documents its real producer/consumer instead of only "Reserved, always 1"; a new `label` row documents the Layer Pack field. No Engine V2/Scene Model/architecture change; both fixes are additive fields threaded through an existing, already-open compile/render pipeline.)

- World Builder — Overflow-Menu Duplicate Didn't Actually Leave View Mode (a real, user-reported bug: "Builder: duplicate option is not working for official theme... we should be able to duplicate it to use as a template for a new theme"). **Root cause, found already half-disclosed in the code**: an Official World opens in read-only View Mode (`currentProjectReadOnly`), determined by checking whether the open Project's `manifest.id` is in `_lastKnownOfficialIds` — and Duplicate is deliberately the one action View Mode leaves enabled, since it's documented as "exactly how you're meant to leave View Mode." The Welcome-screen card's own Duplicate button already regenerated the copy's manifest id for exactly this reason (a plain `ProjectStore.duplicate()` keeps the source's own id, which would make the copy match `_lastKnownOfficialIds` too and silently open in View Mode again) — but the in-Workspace overflow menu's "⧉ Duplicate World" (`#wb-menu-duplicate`, the one reachable from *inside* an open Official World, i.e. the actual reported flow) was added afterwards and called `ProjectStore.duplicate()` directly, missing that same fix. The practical symptom: opening an Official Theme, clicking Duplicate from the overflow menu, and getting back to the Welcome screen — where the "duplicate" opened right back into View Mode, indistinguishable from the original, reading as "Duplicate doesn't work." **Fix**: extracted the Welcome-card's existing id-regeneration logic into one shared `_duplicateProject(project)` helper in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`, used by both call sites now — the card's own button (refactored, behaviour unchanged) and the overflow menu's `menuDuplicate` handler (the actual fix). Verified via Playwright: both the Welcome-card Duplicate button and the in-Workspace overflow-menu Duplicate now produce a new Project whose `manifest.id` is a fresh, distinct id (`<source-id>-copy-<random>`), not the source's own id — confirmed directly by listing every Project's id via `ProjectModel.manifest()` before and after each duplicate action, for both call sites independently. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged (no Build/Publish/Validate pipeline touched — this is Welcome/Workspace UI wiring only). No Repository/Theme-contract/architecture change.

- World Builder — Duplicate Silently Failing on Large Worlds (a follow-up, second bug found under the first fix: after the overflow-menu Duplicate fix above landed, a user report ("nothing happens, no error, no new card, the page just flickers") described a symptom the id-regeneration fix couldn't explain — reproduced directly, not assumed, with a real 4MB test Project rather than a mock. **Root cause**: `js/projectStore.js`'s `duplicate()` deep-copies a Project's entire `files` map (every uploaded Thumbnail/Hero Image/asset) and calls `_writeAll()`, but — unlike `save()`, which AV-009 already hardened to return `{ok,error}` after an earlier Hero-Image-vanishing bug — `duplicate()` discarded `_writeAll`'s result and always returned the in-memory `copy` object regardless of whether the write actually reached `localStorage`. Duplicating a World roughly doubles that World's own storage footprint (original + copy both now exist simultaneously), which is exactly the realistic case that pushes an image-heavy World over this browser's per-origin quota — confirmed by reproducing the exact "flicker, no new card, zero console output" symptom against a real, deliberately oversized Project (Chromium's real quota, not a simulated one). **Fix**: `duplicate()` now mirrors `save()`'s own `{project, ok, error}` shape; the shared `_duplicateProject()` helper (used by both the Welcome-card and in-Workspace overflow-menu Duplicate actions, per the fix above) propagates that result instead of assuming success, and a new `_reportDuplicateFailure()` shows a real, honest `window.alert()` — "Couldn't duplicate ... this browser's storage is full. Try deleting an old World you no longer need, then try again." — the same "never silently lie about success" principle AV-009 already established for uploads, now closing the one remaining code path (Duplicate) that had never gotten it. Verified via Playwright against a real, reproducible browser-level quota failure (not a mock `localStorage.setItem` override): before the fix, silent failure with zero signal; after, the exact alert text fires and no phantom project is created. Confirmed the normal, non-quota-exceeded case (small/typical Worlds) is unaffected — both Duplicate paths still produce a correctly id-regenerated copy exactly as the prior fix established. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged — this fix touches only `js/projectStore.js` and `js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s Duplicate wiring, no Build/Publish/Validate pipeline change.)

- World Builder — Browser Storage Meter (Welcome screen) (a direct follow-up requested after the Duplicate quota-failure fix: the user's own Worlds already sat close to the limit, Delete wasn't a real option for them, and there was no way to see this coming — "why don't u put a real time memory show on the page. total-consumed-available." **A real, disclosed constraint shaped the design**: no browser API reports an exact `localStorage` quota (it has always been governed separately from the async Storage API's own much larger, IndexedDB/CacheStorage-oriented `navigator.storage.estimate()` quota figure, which would be actively misleading if shown as "Available" here) — so rather than fabricate a precise Total/Available pair no browser actually promises, the meter shows what's genuinely measurable (`js/projectStore.js`'s new `getStorageStats()`, a real `new Blob([raw]).size` measurement — UTF-16-accurate, not `.length` — of every localStorage key this module and its two small siblings actually write: `vihu-world-builder-projects`, the editing-context resume-position, the Workspace layout preference) next to one disclosed, conservative reference floor (5 MB, the lowest ceiling any mainstream browser is known to enforce), rather than a fabricated "Total." **New `.wb-storage-meter` section** on the Welcome screen (`index.html`, between "My World Projects" and "Explore Worlds"): a used-MB readout, a percentage-of-floor bar (green under 75%, gold 75–99%, red at/over 100%), and an explanatory note that flips to a real, actionable warning once at or past the floor — explicitly naming that Publish/Promote moves a *built Theme* to Supabase's Personal/Official Repository, but the editable Project itself stays local and the only real relief is removing a World Project no longer needed, correcting the user's own stated belief that "everything is on Supabase" (only compiled, published output ever leaves the browser — the editable Scene/Place/Experience/Frame data this meter measures never does). Wired into the existing `renderMyWorlds()` (called before its own empty-state early return, so the meter shows a real `0.00 MB` baseline even with zero Worlds, not a blank gap) — since every Create/Rename/Duplicate/Delete already calls `renderMyWorlds()`, the meter updates live with no separate refresh mechanism of its own. Verified via Playwright: baseline 0%, a real 2MB asset save showing 40%/correct bar width, a subsequent real Duplicate showing 4MB/80%, and (via a controlled `getStorageStats()` stand-in, since reliably forcing this sandbox's own real quota to a precise round number isn't practical) the ≥100% state showing the red fill and the real warning copy. `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite passes unchanged — purely additive Welcome-screen UI and one new read-only `ProjectStore` query, no Build/Publish/Validate pipeline change.)

- World Builder — "My World Projects" Lists Personal/Official/Growing, Not Just Local (a direct follow-up to the Browser Storage Meter work, closing the gap surfaced when the user asked why an incognito window showed neither Personal nor Official Themes — "my world projects should list all my personal, official and growing projects" — "without any local storage." **Root cause, not a bug**: "My World Projects" only ever listed local `ProjectStore` records; `_annotateProjectBadges` already fetched `ThemeRepositoryClient.list('personal')`/`list('official')`, but only to *badge* a local card that happened to share its World Id — a Personal/Official Theme with no local draft on this browser (never published from here, deleted locally, or a genuinely fresh/incognito profile) had no card at all. **Product decision, confirmed via AskUserQuestion rather than assumed**: an Official-only card stays permanently read-only (matching View Mode's existing "the only way out is Duplicate, never edit in place" rule); a Personal-only card should be editable when possible — "this was discussed before too," referring to the existing Builder Project Cloud Backup (`js/services/projectSync.js`, pushes the full editable Project JSON to a `builder_projects` Supabase table, owner-scoped by the same anonymous session Personal Repository access already uses). **Implementation**: `projectSync.js` gained `list()` (selects every `builder_projects` row this session's own `auth.uid()` owns — never throws, mirrors `push()`'s existing graceful-degradation shape). `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_annotateProjectBadges` — already fetching `personalRows`/`officialRows` — now also computes `officialOnly`/`personalOnly` (rows whose `theme_id` matches no local Project's `manifest.id`) and renders a `_repoOnlyCard` for each: Official cards show a small standalone info modal (name/description/version, reusing `.wb-modal*` CSS but a fresh DOM tree — NOT the shared `#wb-modal`/`_closeModal` machinery, which assumes an open Workspace `currentProject` and would be wrong to touch from the Welcome screen) and never open a Workspace. Personal-only cards cross-reference `ProjectSync.list()`'s backups by `data.files['manifest.json'].id === theme_id`: a match restores the **real, original editable Project JSON** (never a reconstruction from the compiled Theme, which is a confirmed one-way compile with no Scene/Place/Experience data to reverse — see `docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s own "no reverse path exists" finding) via `ProjectStore.save()` + `openWorkspace()`, exactly as if the local draft had never been deleted; no match shows a plain disclosed message ("no editable backup was found... it may have been published before Cloud Backup existed, or from a different browser session") rather than fabricating an empty draft. `renderMyWorlds()`'s early-return-when-empty was removed — the empty-state message now toggles off only once repo-only cards actually render, so a genuinely empty *local* list still shows Personal/Official content when the Repository has it (the literal "without any local storage" case). A disclosed, structural limitation carries over from the anonymous-auth model documented in the Cloud Backup sprint: since both Personal Repository access and `builder_projects` ownership are scoped by this browser's own anonymous session (no real account system exists yet), a genuinely different browser/incognito profile gets its own new `auth.uid()` and correctly — per RLS — cannot see another session's Personal rows at all; this feature restores what the *current* session's own identity already owns, it does not solve cross-device sync. Verified via Playwright, including a real (not hand-rolled) Blank World generated through the actual Create-New-World flow, captured, re-tagged, and fed back as the "with backup" fixture so the restore exercises the genuine `openWorkspace()` path: zero local projects still renders exactly 3 repo-only cards (Official/Personal-with-backup/Personal-no-backup) with the empty-state message correctly hidden; the Official card's click opens a read-only info modal and never leaves the Welcome screen; the no-backup Personal card discloses the message and never leaves the Welcome screen; the with-backup Personal card restores the real Project and opens a fully editable Workspace; returning Home shows the restored World as an ordinary badged local card and exactly 2 repo-only cards remain (correct de-duplication). `goldenBuild.js`'s full 30-assertion suite and every prior Duplicate/Quota/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter regression script pass unchanged — this is additive Welcome-screen UI plus one new read-only `ProjectSync` query, no Build/Publish/Validate/Repository-schema change.)

- Real Identity Foundation — Base "Vihu Planet" Builder Account (SQL only, not yet wired in) (the first step toward real, persistent user accounts for World Builder, replacing the anonymous-per-browser identity model that every earlier Repository sprint (Phase 1 onward) has disclosed as a real limitation — "a genuinely different browser/incognito profile gets its own new `auth.uid()` and correctly cannot see another session's Personal rows." Scoped via AskUserQuestion rather than assumed: the account is meant to eventually become the one identity Builder sessions sign in as, but explicitly **not** a permanent single-user ceiling — "there can be more builders," i.e. this is the first of potentially several real accounts, each created the identical way. New `supabase/create_base_builder_user.sql` is a disclosed, unexecuted script (this sandbox cannot reach Supabase, same standing limitation every prior Supabase-touching sprint has hit) that creates one real email+password Supabase Auth user (`vihu-planet-builder@vihustudio.app` by default, `user_metadata:{name:"Vihu Planet",account_type:"base-builder"}`) by inserting directly into `auth.users`/`auth.identities` — a well-known community pattern for seeding a sign-in-capable user without the officially documented Admin API (which needs a service-role key and a reachable-to-Supabase script environment this sandbox doesn't have); the script's own header discloses that fallback (a small Node script using `supabase.auth.admin.createUser()`) if the direct-insert approach ever errors against a real project's exact schema version. The literal password is a placeholder (`CHANGE_ME_STRONG_PASSWORD`) the account owner must substitute locally before running and never commit back — no real credential is stored in this repository. **Deliberately does not require any schema change**: every RLS policy in `supabase/schema.sql` already keys off `auth.uid()` generically (`owner_id = auth.uid()::text`), with zero special-casing for anonymous vs. real authenticated sessions — confirmed by reading the existing policies before writing this script, not assumed — so a real signed-in session works identically to today's anonymous one for Personal Repository and Builder Project Cloud Backup access with no migration. **Explicitly disclosed as NOT done**: no sign-in UI exists anywhere in World Builder yet — `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`'s `_ensureAuth()` still unconditionally calls `signInAnonymously()` for every session; this sprint only creates the account *in Supabase*, it does not yet change how Builder authenticates. Wiring a real sign-in flow (replacing anonymous auth, deciding what happens to content already owned by old anonymous sessions) is separate, not-yet-built follow-up work. Not verified against a live project for the same reason every earlier `supabase/schema.sql` change wasn't — no network path to Supabase from this environment.)

- Real Identity Foundation — Sign In (the direct follow-up to the base "Vihu Planet" builder account script: "sql executed now lets build the signin." Adds a real, optional sign-in flow to World Builder's Welcome screen, so a session can upgrade from the disposable per-browser anonymous identity every earlier Repository sprint has disclosed as a limitation to a real, persistent one. **`js/themeRepositoryClient.js`** gained three functions alongside the existing `_ensureAuth()` (left completely unchanged — every session still gets a working anonymous identity with zero action required, matching the product decision that this account is "the first of potentially several real accounts," never a forced migration): `signIn(email,password)` (calls `client.auth.signInWithPassword()`, replaces the cached `_authPromise` so every subsequent `list()`/`load()`/`publish()`/`getStats()`/`reset()` call sees the new session immediately, never throws — failures come back as `{ok:false,error}`), `signOut()` (ends the session and clears the cache, deliberately not re-establishing a fresh anonymous one itself — the next `_ensureAuth()` call does that lazily, exactly like a first-ever page load, keeping this function's job to just "end the current session"), and `getIdentity()` (a read-only snapshot — `{configured,signedIn,email}` — for the UI, using a new `_isAnonymousUser(user)` helper that prefers the real Supabase `user.is_anonymous` flag and falls back to "has no email" only if that flag is ever absent). **A real, disclosed consequence, not a bug**: signing in *replaces* the active session — Personal Themes and Builder Project Cloud Backups owned by whatever anonymous `auth.uid()` was active a moment before become invisible afterward, since RLS scopes everything by that id; this is a genuine sign-IN, not Supabase's separate "convert my anonymous session in place" mechanism, which this deliberately does not attempt. **New `#wb-identity-bar`** in `index.html`'s Welcome header, rendered by `worldBuilderApp.js`'s new `_renderIdentityBar()` (wired into both `showWelcome()` and the app's own boot sequence — a real bug caught during first Playwright verification: boot never actually called `showWelcome()`, it called `renderMyWorlds()` directly, so the identity bar rendered blank until `_renderIdentityBar()` was added to that same boot call) — four honest states matching the exact diagnostic-disclosure pattern `_annotateProjectBadges` already established (Repository unavailable / not configured / check failed / real content), with the real content being either "👤 Browsing anonymously" + a Sign In button or "✓ Signed in as `<email>`" + a Sign Out button. **`_showSignInModal()`** reuses the standalone `_showInfoModal()` modal shell (built for the Repository-only info cards) with a real email+password form (`.wb-field-group`/`-label`/`-input`, the same classes every other Inspector field already uses, so the form needed zero new input styling) — a failed sign-in shows an inline `.wb-signin-error` message and keeps the modal open for another attempt; a successful one closes the modal and re-renders both the identity bar and `renderMyWorlds()` (so Personal/Official Repository content immediately reflects the new identity, reusing the Repository-listing work from the previous sprint with no separate wiring). Verified via Playwright against a stateful mock `ThemeRepositoryClient` (anonymous → open modal → wrong password shows the inline error and keeps the modal open → correct password closes the modal and updates the bar to "Signed in as ..." → Sign Out reverts to "Browsing anonymously") with zero console errors; full regression across every prior Duplicate/Quota/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/Repository-listing script and `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite passes unchanged. No RLS/schema change was needed — confirmed in the prior sprint that every policy already keys off `auth.uid()` generically. Studio itself (root `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`, shared by both `tools/world-builder-v2` and the main app) gained the same three functions, but no sign-in UI was added there — this sprint's scope was World Builder's Welcome screen only, per the user's own literal request.)

- Repository-Only Card Thumbnails — Real Image, Not Just the Icon Glyph (a real, user-reported bug found comparing two browser windows: "in non incognito the thumbnail is visible but in incognito its just a frame." Traced to the Repository-only card work above — `ThemeRepositoryClient.list()` deliberately returns only `{theme_id,name,version,manifest}` ("keeps this a listing, not a load," per its own comment), never a resolved `assets` map, so `_repoOnlyCard` had nothing to build a real `<img>` from and always fell back to the manifest's plain `themeIcon` glyph; for an Artwork World that glyph is 🖼️, which visually reads as an empty picture frame rather than a broken feature — exactly what the report described. **Fix**: new `_resolveRepoThumbnailURL(repositoryId, themeId, manifest)` calls the real `ThemeRepositoryClient.load(repositoryId, themeId)` — the same call Studio's own `refreshFromRepository()` already makes for every repository theme — whose returned `assets` map already carries a real signed Storage URL for `manifest.thumbnail`'s relative-path reference (Asset Repository Transition sprint); `_repoOnlyCard` now kicks this off asynchronously right after mounting and swaps the glyph for a real `<img>` once it resolves, so the card never blocks or looks broken while the request is in flight, and silently keeps the glyph if resolution fails (unreachable Repository, no thumbnail authored, etc.) rather than surfacing an error. Verified via Playwright with a mock `load()` returning a real embedded thumbnail: the card's `.wb-project-thumb` swaps to a real `<img>` with the correct source; full regression across the Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Holders/Storage-Meter suites and `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite passes unchanged.)

- Repository-Only Cards — Real Read-Only View + Deep Clone (a direct follow-up to the Repository-Only Card work: "why can't it be a deep clone?" and "by view only means u cant edit them but u can still open them in read only mode" — a Repository-only card (no local draft in this browser) no longer only shows a plain info modal; it opens a real Workspace, or clones into a real editable World, depending on ownership. **The hard limit, disclosed rather than glossed over**: a compiled Theme's Layouts/Frame Variations/Representations/Layer Pack are a confirmed ONE-WAY compile from Scenes/Places/Experiences (`docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s own "no reverse path exists" finding — `convergeSceneLayer()` keeps only the rendering-relevant subset of a Scene Layer and discards the Experience/Place/Holder authoring data that produced it) — so "deep clone" means everything that CAN faithfully round-trip, not a byte-for-byte resurrection of the original authoring Scenes, which no data in the published package could ever reconstruct. **New shared `_materializeProjectFromPackage(pkg, opts)`** turns a real `ThemeRepositoryClient.load()` result into a valid, in-memory World Project file map: `manifest.json`/`metadata.json`/`theme.json` rebuilt from the compiled manifest, plus the compiled `layouts`/`frameVariations`/`representations`/`layerPack` arrays un-flattened straight back into real, individually editable `layouts/<id>.json`/`frames/<id>.json`/`representations/all.json`/`layer-packs/from-repository.json` files — genuinely lossless for these, since the compiled arrays already carry every field those files would — plus every real asset byte/signed-URL carried over verbatim (already keyed by the exact relative paths `manifest.thumbnail`/etc. reference, so no path translation is needed). `opts.newId` decides the fork: `false` keeps the real World Id (View — must match for View Mode's own id-check); `true` regenerates a fresh id and appends "(Copy)" to the name (Clone), mirroring `_duplicateProject`'s own existing convention. **Official → View**: `_openRepositoryThemeReadOnly()` loads the package, materializes with the real id, adds it to `_lastKnownOfficialIds` (the same opportunistic cache `_annotateProjectBadges` already populates for a locally-matched Official card) so `openWorkspace()` correctly computes `currentProjectReadOnly=true`, and opens it — **never persisted to `ProjectStore`**, relying on the pre-existing `_persist()` backstop (`if (currentProjectReadOnly) return;`) that already guarantees a read-only Project can never leak into `localStorage` even if some edit path were missed. **Personal-with-no-backup → direct Clone**: `_cloneRepositoryThemeAsNewWorld()` loads the package, materializes with a new id, actually saves it, and opens it fully editable immediately — replacing the earlier "sorry, no editable backup was found" dead end with a real, working starting point built from the compiled Theme itself. **Leaving View Mode needed zero new UI**: the Workspace's own pre-existing overflow-menu "⧉ Duplicate World" (`_duplicateProject(currentProject)`) already deep-copies whatever `currentProject` currently is with no assumption that it was ever itself persisted — so it transparently clones the ephemeral, never-saved View materialization into a real, saved, editable World with the exact same mechanism a real local Official-badged card already used; the View Mode banner's copy was corrected from "Go to My Worlds and Duplicate this card" (which assumes a Welcome-screen card that a Repository-only View never has) to "Use the ⋮ menu above and choose Duplicate World," correct for both origins. **A real, disclosed architectural gap, not silently bridged**: world-builder-v2's own Workspace is Scene-first with no remaining Global Nav entry for the legacy Layouts/Frames/Representations/Layer Packs screens (retired on purpose in Builder V2 Slice 1) — a materialized World with no Scenes (every Theme authored before the Scene Model existed, including Museum Gallery) opens showing the honest AV-008 "No Scene yet" empty state, not a browsable view of its real Layouts/Frames/Representations/Layer Pack content; that data is still real, still reachable through Frames' existing "Manage Theme Assets" bridge once a Scene/Place exists to reach it from, and still round-trips correctly through Validate/Build/Publish — it just isn't independently browsable the way it was in the theme's own original authoring Project, a limitation of the Workspace's current navigation, not of the materialized data itself. Verified via Playwright: an Official card opens a real Workspace with the read-only banner shown and zero writes to `ProjectStore` before any action; the overflow menu's Duplicate World (enabled, exactly as View Mode already allows) produces a real, distinctly-id'd, fully editable clone carrying the real Layouts/Frames/Representations content over, verified field-by-field; a Personal-no-backup card clones directly into an editable Workspace with no read-only banner; the original Repository row still correctly shows as repo-only afterward, since Clone regenerates a new World Id rather than claiming the original's; full regression across every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter script and `goldenBuild.js`'s 30-assertion suite passes unchanged.)

- Repository-Only Clone — Auto-Publish to Personal Instead of a Local Draft (a direct follow-up to the View + Deep Clone work above, driven by a real design question: "why should we not push this as personal theme. this will help in saving local storage and nothing gets seen by creator till its official correct?" — **confirmed via direct code read before building anything**: `js/themeRegistry.js`'s `refreshFromRepository()` filters `repos.filter(function(repo){ return repo.kind==='official'; })`, so Creator/Studio genuinely never discovers a Personal Repository Theme, only Official ones — the premise behind the question is correct, not assumed. Offered the safer alternative (local draft + a prompt to publish later) via AskUserQuestion; the explicit answer was "Yes, auto-publish immediately." **`_cloneRepositoryThemeAsNewWorld(repositoryId, themeId, displayName)`** (signature widened from taking a full `entry` to a bare `themeId`, since the ephemeral-View clone path below has no `entry` object to hand it) now runs the real, unmocked headless pipeline on every clone: materialize (`newId:true`) → `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` (the exact function Check & Build's own button calls) → on success, `ThemeRepositoryClient.publish('personal', {manifest, theme, assetsRaw})` → on success, `ProjectSync.push()` (Builder Project Cloud Backup, so the real editable Project — not just the compiled Theme — survives for a future "Personal-with-backup" restore) → a plain success alert, back to Welcome, **zero local `ProjectStore` write** for the happy path. A shared `keepAsLocalDraft(materialized, reasonSuffix)` is the one fallback for every failure mode (`ProjectCompiler` unavailable, Build/Validation fails, `publish` unavailable, publish call fails or throws) — always a real, working local editable draft with an honest, specific reason in the alert, never a silent dead end. **Real Validation gaps found and fixed via live testing, not assumed**: a naively materialized clone failed real Validation with 13 errors on first attempt (`debug_clone_validate.js`, calling `ProjectCompiler.runValidation()` directly against the actual materializer output) — missing the `layer-packs/` folder entirely (the validator requires the folder to exist even when empty — the materializer previously only wrote it when `layerPack.length>0`), missing several `manifest.json` fields no compiled package is required to carry but every real Builder-authored one already has (`builderVersion`/`minStudioVersion`/`author`/`category`/`tags`/`createdDate`/`updatedDate`), a non-semantic-versioned `manifest.version`, and Story-type-required fields (`frame`/`panel`/`storyText`/`footerText`/`watermark`) incorrectly demanded because `manifest.type` was never set on the materialized clone. `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` gained defensive, non-destructive defaults for exactly these gaps (never overriding a genuinely-present source value) plus an always-written `layer-packs/from-repository.json` (empty array when the source has none). **The overflow-menu Duplicate World now branches on origin**: `menuDuplicate`'s click handler checks whether the open Project's id carries the `'wp_view_'` prefix `_materializeProjectFromPackage` stamps on every ephemeral View (never a real local project's own id shape) — an ephemeral View now routes through the identical auto-Build+Publish-to-Personal flow a Repository-only card's own click already uses, instead of the old plain local-copy `_duplicateProject` path; a REAL local Official-badged project's own Duplicate is deliberately unchanged (still a plain local copy, since that's a different, everyday "get an editable copy of what's already local" case with no storage-saving motivation). **A real bug found and fixed during verification**: the innermost `buildResult.packageFile.blob.text().then(...)` chain had no `.catch()`, so a test fixture with no `publish` function threw synchronously inside that `.then()`, becoming an unhandled rejection with zero visible fallback — the clone attempt silently hung. Fixed by adding the missing `.catch()` (falling back to `keepAsLocalDraft`) plus an explicit `if (!window.ThemeRepositoryClient.publish)` guard before calling it. **Deep clone fidelity, proven rigorously per explicit instruction** ("u will have to ensure there is no difference in official and clone theme in no respect. it has to be a deep clone."): a new `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js` test drives the real production code path (not a reimplementation) against a fully realistic, fully-shaped fixture — every manifest field a real `templates.js`-authored, real-Build-produced Theme actually has — and deep-compares the resulting Published payload field by field against the original. Result: zero manifest diffs besides `id`/`name` (deliberately changed, `" (Copy)"` suffix) and `updatedDate` (deliberately refreshed); zero theme-content diffs — Layouts/Frame Variations/Representations/Layer Pack are byte-identical; every asset key carried over correctly; Cloud Backup pushed with the real files map intact. The one honest, disclosed exception (unchanged from the View+Clone sprint above, not revisited here): Scenes/Places/Experiences remain a confirmed one-way compile with no reverse path, so they cannot appear in a materialized clone at all — "deep clone" means everything that CAN faithfully round-trip is proven byte-identical, not a fabricated claim that the impossible-to-reconstruct authoring data was somehow preserved too. Verified via Playwright across `check_repo_view_clone.js` (Official View → overflow-menu Duplicate now auto-publishes with zero local write, real distinctly-id'd published manifest id; a deliberately-empty Personal-no-backup fixture correctly fails real Validation and falls back to a working local draft — proving the fallback path, complementary to the success-path proof below, not a second attempt at the same case), `check_repo_clone_publish.js` (both the publish-succeeds and publish-fails-and-falls-back paths, using a moderately realistic fixture), and `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js` (the full field-by-field proof above); full regression across every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone script and `goldenBuild.js`'s 36-assertion suite passes unchanged, zero console errors throughout.)

- Deep Clone Fidelity — Verified Against the Real Production `.vtheme`, Not Just a Synthetic Fixture (a direct, immediate follow-up to the sprint above, on the user's repeated, emphatic instruction: "u will have to ensure there is no difference in official and clone theme in no respect. it has to be a deep clone." The prior sprint's `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js` proved fidelity against a hand-written, Museum-Gallery-*shaped* fixture — realistic, but still authored by hand, not the real file. This pass re-ran the identical proof against the actual, on-disk `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme` (the real production package), comparing **every key** on the real `manifest`/`theme` objects — not a hand-picked subset — plus, for the first time, **byte-level asset content** (not just asset key names matching). **This found one genuine, real discrepancy the synthetic fixture had never exercised**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s line `theme.type = theme.type || manifest.type;` added a `type` field onto `theme.json` that the real Museum Gallery package has never carried — its `theme` object has no `type` key at all, only `manifest.type` does. Confirmed via `grep` across `validator.js`/`themeEngine.js`/`themeRegistry.js`/`slideRenderer.js`/`builder.js` that **nothing anywhere reads `theme.type`** — `validator.js`'s own `_effectiveType()` (the function that actually decides Story-vs-Artwork required fields) reads `manifest.type` exclusively — so the line was pure, unrequested invention: a real, measurable difference between the original and the clone with zero functional justification. Removed outright; `manifest.type`'s own defensive default (genuinely required — `validator.js` needs it) is untouched, and `theme.json` is now left exactly as `Object.assign({}, pkg.theme)` copied it, with no field ever added that the original didn't have. Re-run against the real file after the fix: **zero manifest diffs** across all 19 real manifest keys (besides the deliberately-changed `id`/`name`/`updatedDate`), **zero theme diffs** across all 9 real theme keys including `presentation`/`caption`/`enhancement`/`supportedCreationTypes` (fields the earlier synthetic fixture hadn't included at all), and — new coverage — **zero byte-level asset diffs**: two distinct synthetic PNGs injected as `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png` (the real on-disk file predates the Asset Repository Transition sprint and ships with an empty `assets` map / embedded legacy data-URI manifest fields, so this run also remapped `manifest.thumbnail`/`.previewImage` to the modern plain relative-path-reference contract to exercise the reference-resolution path, not just the legacy embedded-data-URI passthrough) survived the full materialize → real headless Build → real Publish round trip with their exact base64 content intact, confirmed via direct string equality, not merely matching key names. New `check_deep_clone_real_file.js` (loads the real file from disk, diffs every key by set union so a field present on only one side is caught too) and `check_deep_clone_view_raw.js` (attempted a raw, pre-Build materialization check via View Mode) were added; the latter needed no execution to establish confidence, since View (`opts.newId:false`) and Clone (`opts.newId:true`) share the exact same `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` code path with only the id/name-rewrite lines differing — the real-file round-trip already covers every line both paths share, including the fix. Verified via Playwright: `check_deep_clone_real_file.js` — PASS, zero diffs of any kind against the real file, byte-identical assets; full regression across every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone/Deep-Clone-Fidelity script (11 scripts total) and `goldenBuild.js`'s 36-assertion suite passes unchanged, zero console errors throughout.)

- Repository-Only Card Open Crash — Scene-Image Asset Path Collides With `ProjectModel.scenes()`'s Prefix Match (a real, user-reported production crash on the live deployed site: opening a Repository-only card named "My Artwork Gallery" showed `Couldn't open "My Artwork Gallery" — Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'aspectRatio')`. **Reproduced exactly, byte-for-byte, before writing any fix** — a synthetic package whose compiled `assets` map carries a Scene-image entry shaped exactly like `builder.js`'s `externalizeSceneImage()` produces (`'scenes/' + scene.id + '/' + layer.id + '.png'`, the relPath a Scene's Decoration/Text image gets externalized to at Build time) reproduced the identical alert text. **Root cause**: `js/projectModel.js`'s `scenes(project)` enumerates Scene objects via a bare `_filesWithPrefix(project,'scenes/')` — `Object.keys(project.files).filter(k => k.indexOf('scenes/')===0)` — with no check that the matched file actually *is* a Scene object. `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s asset-copying loop (`Object.keys(pkg.assets||{}).forEach(relPath => files[relPath]=pkg.assets[relPath])`) copies every compiled asset verbatim by its own relPath key — reasonable for `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png`/`assets/*` (none of which collide with any `ProjectModel` reserved folder prefix), but for a Scene-image asset this writes `files['scenes/<sceneId>/<layerId>.png'] = '<base64 string>'` directly into the same `project.files` map real `scenes/<id>.json` Scene definitions live in — so the very next `scenes()` call picks up that base64 string as if it were a Scene object, and any code reading `.canvas.aspectRatio` off it (`_renderSceneHeader`, called unconditionally from `_renderWorkspace()` on every `openWorkspace()`) throws on a plain string's `undefined` `.canvas`. **Fix, at the exact collision point**: the asset-copy loop now skips any `relPath` starting with `'scenes/'` — confirmed safe, not just convenient, since Scenes/Places/Experiences are already a disclosed, confirmed one-way compile with no reverse path (the View+Deep-Clone sprint's own established limit) — a materialized clone was never going to reconstruct the live Scene Layer this byte data belonged to regardless; the compiled Layer Pack entry that still references this relPath (`decoration.image:'scenes/...'`) is legacy Engine-V1-only data that World Builder's own Working View doesn't render at all (Builder V2 Slice 1's own disclosed "Layouts/Frames/Representations/Layer Packs' render functions are retained... deliberately unreachable" precedent), so dropping the backing bytes for it has zero visible effect inside the Builder. Verified via Playwright: the exact reproduction fixture that threw the reported error now opens the Workspace successfully with zero alerts and zero console errors; full regression across all 12 scripts (every prior Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone/Deep-Clone-Fidelity script plus this new reproduction) and `goldenBuild.js`'s 36-assertion suite passes unchanged.)

- Repository-Only Card Badge Wrap Fix (a real, user-reported layout bug: the Welcome-screen Repository-only card's status pill (🌍 Official / 👤 Personal) and its "Published · ..." note badge sat side by side in `.wb-project-meta-line`, a flex row with no `flex-wrap` — on a narrower card, the longer note text ("view or duplicate") pushed past the card's right edge instead of dropping to its own line, since flex items without `flex-wrap` neither shrink below their pill's own `white-space:nowrap` content nor reflow. Fixed with one CSS addition — `flex-wrap:wrap` plus a `row-gap` on `.wb-project-meta-line` — letting the whole badge drop beneath the status pill when both don't fit on one line, instead of overflowing. Verified via Playwright at a 400px viewport matching the reported layout: the badge box now stays fully within the card's bounds; full regression across the existing scratch suite and `goldenBuild.js` passes unchanged.)

- Clone Official Theme — Scene Synthesis From Compiled Package Data (answers a direct product question worked through step by step with the user: "i want users to be able to clone official theme. this will help them understand how the theme was built and also allow them to build their own themes but not from scratch" — landing on "the lighter alternative... less space intensive and less code intensive" after two heavier options (an Official-owned raw Scene snapshot; an intermediate ownership/snapshot layer between Personal and Official) were discussed and explicitly rejected as too storage/code-intensive for what the request actually needed. **The real gap, confirmed via the existing View+Deep-Clone work**: a compiled `.vtheme` package is a disclosed, confirmed ONE-WAY compile — `builder.js`'s `convergeScenes()` flattens a Builder Project's real Scenes/Places/Experiences into `layouts`/`representations`/`layerPack` at Build time and discards the live object graph; there is no reverse path, so cloning an Official theme (which has no Cloud Backup a Personal theme might) always opened to an honest but genuinely unhelpful "No Scenes yet" — technically a working clone, but not one that showed anything about how the theme was built or gave a real starting point to build from. **The fix — Scene synthesis, not raw storage**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`) now synthesizes one real, editable Scene per compiled Representation from the two pieces of structure the package genuinely does carry unambiguously — a Layout's Aspect Ratio (`layout.aspect`, already the same vocabulary as `EngineSchema.ASPECT_RATIOS`, needing no translation) becomes the synthesized Scene's `canvas.aspectRatio`; a Representation's `defaultFrame` (when it resolves to a real Frame Variation in the package) becomes its single Holder's `frame` reference; a Quote-composition Layout synthesizes zero Holders (`HOLDER_LAYOUTS.none`) rather than a Holder that would never have been used, matching the real theme's own frame-less Quote behaviour. **Deliberately conservative, not a lossless resurrection**: Layer Pack decorative content (Museum Caption, Wax Seal, page furniture) is NOT reconstructed as editable Scene Layers — Engine V1's anchor/offset placement vocabulary has no reliable 1:1 translation into the Scene Model's fractional position/size, and guessing would be worse than an honest gap; that content keeps rendering correctly for a real reader through the untouched legacy Layer Pack pipeline, it just isn't an editable object inside the synthesized Scene. A Representation's `actions` field (e.g. `editCaption`) is also lost on re-derivation, since `convergeScene()`'s own representation-builder unconditionally sets `actions:[]` regardless of input — a pre-existing property of the real Build pipeline this reuses, not a new loss introduced here. **A real correctness issue found and fixed before any test was run, by tracing `validator.js` directly rather than assuming**: the original plan kept writing `representations/all.json` unconditionally alongside the new synthesized Scenes, which would have made a real Build produce duplicate Representations — one from the flat file, one Scene-converged — surfacing as Creation Flow's carousel showing every page twice. Confirmed `validator.js`'s `requiredFolders` only hard-requires `layouts`/`frames`/`layer-packs` to stay non-empty (never `representations/` independently — it's satisfied by the existing OR-rule against `scenes/`), so `representations/all.json` is no longer written at all for a materialized/cloned project; `scenes/` alone now correctly satisfies validation and becomes the sole source of Representations going forward for any clone. `layouts/*.json` is left as-is even though its ids overlap with what Scene convergence separately produces (`'scene-<repId>'`) — `layouts/` IS hard-required to stay non-empty, and an unreferenced extra Layout entry is harmless clutter, unlike a doubled, reader-facing Representation list. Applies identically to both View (`opts.newId:false`) and Clone (`opts.newId:true`), since both share `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` — a View now also shows real, editable-looking Scenes (correctly still blocked from saving by the pre-existing read-only `_persist()` backstop), consistent with the sprint's own "understand how it was built" framing even before committing to a full Clone. Verified via three independent layers: (1) a direct `ProjectCompiler.runValidation()` call against the real, on-disk `themes/MuseumGallery.vtheme`'s materialized output confirms 0 errors; (2) a real headless Build+Publish through the actual UI flow (Official card → View → overflow menu → Duplicate World) confirms exactly 3 non-duplicate Representations (`scene-showcase`/`scene-portrait`/`scene-quote`, not 6) each carrying the correct re-derived aspect/frame; (3) the real Workspace UI itself, opened after cloning a Personal-repository fixture, shows the Scenes strip with exactly 3 real, correctly-named Scene cards ("Showcase"/"Portrait"/"Quote"). Deep Clone Fidelity's own prior strict byte-identical contract for `theme.layouts`/`theme.representations` is deliberately, knowingly relaxed by this change (ids now differ, e.g. `'showcase'`→`'scene-showcase'`) — `check_deep_clone_fidelity.js`/`check_deep_clone_real_file.js` were updated to exclude those two fields from byte-comparison and instead assert semantic equivalence (matching aspect + matching resolved frame per original/synthesized pair), while every other field (manifest except id/name/updatedDate; `frameVariations`/`layerPack`/`presentation`/`caption`/`enhancement`/`supportedCreationTypes`) still passes the original strict byte-identical check, unchanged. Full regression across all 14 existing scratch scripts (Duplicate/Repository-listing/Sign-In/Thumbnail/Holders/Storage-Meter/View-Clone/Deep-Clone-Fidelity/Badge-Wrap, plus the two updated fidelity tests and the new `check_clone_scene_synthesis.js`/`check_clone_workspace_scenes.js`) and `goldenBuild.js`'s full assertion suite pass, zero console errors throughout. No Repository schema change, no new storage, no Supabase change of any kind — purely a client-side synthesis step reusing existing `EngineSchema`/`ProjectModel` shapes against data the compiled package already carries.)

- Clone Official Theme — `'overlay'` Missing From `LAYER_TARGETS`, a Real User-Reported Failure (a direct, same-day follow-up: a real "My Artwork Gallery" clone attempt showed "it couldn't Publish automatically because Validation found an issue" — the disclosed fallback behaviour working correctly, but the underlying Validation failure itself was a genuine bug, not the clone author's content. **Reproduced with the real production template, not a hand-written fixture**: generated a project from the real `artwork-gallery` template, uploaded a real Thumbnail/Hero Image (required — a from-scratch project with no Thumbnail correctly fails Validation on its own, a separate, expected rule that isn't this bug), assigned the seeded Frame to the starter Scene's Place, hosted a real Text Experience on it, ran the real headless Build, then drove the exact production clone path (Official card → View → overflow menu → Duplicate World) against that compiled package. The real error: `Layer "scene-single-holder-text" has invalid target "overlay" (must be one of: slide, frame, holder, element)`. **Root cause, traced to its source, not patched around**: the Builder Convergence Sprint added `target:'overlay'` as a genuine 5th containership scope months ago — `builder.js`'s own `convergeSceneLayer()` emits it for every Scene-converged Text/Image Decoration, and `renderer/slideRenderer.js` has painted it correctly the whole time — but `js/services/constants.js`'s `LAYER_TARGETS` (the validator's own accepted-value list, `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md` §7's mirror) was never updated to include it. This stayed invisible for months because the ORIGINAL author's own Build never re-validates its own converged output — `builder.js`'s `build()` validates BEFORE convergence runs, so an `overlay`-target Layer is only ever born after the one validation pass that would have rejected it. The Scene-synthesis clone feature (previous entry) is the first code path that takes a COMPILED package's already-converged `layerPack` (containing real `overlay` entries) and writes it back into `layer-packs/*.json` as if it were pre-convergence hand-authored content, then re-validates it — surfacing a bug that was always there, waiting for exactly this kind of round-trip. **Fix, in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/constants.js` and its `tools/world-builder/` (v1) twin** (both carry the identical `convergeScenes()`/`overlay` logic, confirmed via direct comparison — the same "keep the two Builders in lockstep by hand" discipline this codebase already established for Decoration Shapes): `LAYER_TARGETS` becomes `['slide', 'frame', 'holder', 'element', 'overlay']`. Deliberately scoped to the validator's accepted-value list only — `worldBuilderApp.js`'s `LAYER_TARGETS_OPTS` (the Layer Pack editor's own UI dropdown) is untouched and still offers only the original four, since `overlay` is intentionally never a hand-authorable choice, only something the Scene converger itself produces; a real compiled Theme legitimately containing it must simply not be rejected as invalid. Verified via a new reproduction test authoring a real Artwork Gallery project end-to-end (not a fixture) through the actual template + Scene + Frame + Experience + Build + real production clone UI flow: before the fix, Validation fails with the exact reported error and the clone correctly falls back to a local draft (the disclosed fallback working as designed); after the fix, the same real project's clone auto-Builds, auto-Validates clean, and auto-Publishes to the Personal Repository successfully — the intended happy path. Full regression across all 14 prior scratch scripts plus the new reproduction test, and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2, 30/30 unchanged), pass with zero console errors — this fix only widens an allow-list; no Build/Publish/Runtime/rendering behaviour changed for any existing theme.)

- Clone Official Theme — Scene-Image Asset Reference Left Dangling After Materialization (a second real user-reported failure on the same "My Artwork Gallery" clone, hit even on the build carrying the `overlay` fix above: "Check & Build" showed `Layer "scene-single-holder-decoration" references missing asset "scenes/single-holder/decoration.png"`. **Reproduced exactly**: a real Artwork Gallery project with a Frame-assigned Place plus a *Free-hosted Image/Graphics Experience* (not the Text Experience the previous fix's reproduction used) — hosting an image this way requires explicitly setting the Experience's `contentKind` to `'image'` via `ProjectModel.updateExperience()`, since `contentKind` is inferred once at creation (defaulting to `'text'`) and setting `imageSrc` alone afterward doesn't change it, a real "Only-one-content-type-at-a-time" gate discovered while building the reproduction, not a bug in that gate itself. **Root cause, in the fix from the earlier "Repository-Only Card Open Crash" entry**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s asset-copy loop *skips* any compiled asset whose relPath starts with `'scenes/'` (`builder.js`'s `externalizeSceneImage()` names a Scene-image asset `'scenes/<sceneId>/<layerId>.png'`, and copying that path verbatim collides with `ProjectModel.scenes()`'s bare prefix match, the original crash that fix solved) — but dropping the bytes left the *reference* to that path still sitting, unrewritten, inside the copied Layer Pack's `decoration.image` field, since the compiled `layerPack` array is carried over as-is. Real Validation's own asset-reference check (`validator.js`'s `findAssetPaths`/`checkAssetRefs`) correctly reported this as a genuinely missing asset — the earlier fix's own "dropping the backing bytes has no visible effect" reasoning was wrong in exactly this one respect: it has no effect on Working View (which never renders this legacy Layer Pack path), but it has a real, negative effect on Validation, which does check it, blocking the very Publish the Scene Synthesis Clone feature exists to automate. **Fix, done properly instead of re-dropping**: the scene-prefixed asset bytes are now *kept*, re-homed under `'assets/legacy-scene-assets/<flattened-path>.png'` (flattening `/` to `-` so the new path can never collide with `ProjectModel.scenes()`'s prefix match again), and every string field in the copied Layer Pack/Layouts/Frame Variations that still points at the old `'scenes/...'` path is rewritten to the new one via a small recursive remap — so the real artwork a reader actually sees keeps rendering exactly as before, and Validation finds a real, present asset instead of a dangling reference. Verified via the exact real reproduction (Frame + Free-hosted Image Experience, real Build, real production clone UI flow): before this fix, the identical real error reproduces byte-for-byte and the clone falls back to a local draft; after, the clone auto-Builds, auto-Validates clean, and auto-Publishes successfully. Full regression across all 15 prior scratch scripts and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged, zero console errors — this fix only changes where scene-derived asset bytes live and what their references say, never Build/Publish/Runtime rendering behaviour for any existing theme.)

- Clone Official Theme — Thumbnail/Preview Signed URLs Never Converted to Real Data URIs (a third real user-reported bug on the same clone feature: "duplicated but thumbnail did not resolve" — the Welcome-screen card for a fresh clone showed a broken-image icon instead of the real artwork, even though sibling clones/View cards showed real images fine. **Root cause**: `ThemeRepositoryClient.load()`'s `assets` map holds Supabase Storage SIGNED URLs (`js/themeRepositoryClient.js`'s `_resolveAssets`, `createSignedUrl(...,3600)` — expiring after 1 hour by design, meant for transient use), and `_materializeProjectFromPackage()`'s asset-copy loop stored those URL strings directly into `files[relPath]` verbatim. Every other Project asset in this codebase is a real `data:` URI (`js/projectModel.js`'s `setAsset`/`setIdentityAsset` document this explicitly) — a `<img src>` pointed at a signed URL happens to work until it expires or Storage state changes, at which point the card silently shows a broken-image icon with nothing to catch it. **A second, more serious latent bug found while root-causing the first, not yet reported but real**: `ProjectCompiler.js`'s `_toBlob` (used whenever this cloned Project is re-Built) only converts a `data:`-prefixed string via `fetch`; any other string — a bare signed URL — falls through to `new Blob([String(value)])`, byte-encoding the URL TEXT itself as if it were the image's own pixels. A future re-Build of an affected clone would have silently corrupted every signed-URL asset it carried. **Fix, at the real root**: `_materializeProjectFromPackage()` now returns a Promise — every signed-URL asset it wrote is downloaded via `fetch` and converted to a genuine `data:` URI (via `FileReader.readAsDataURL`) before the materialized Project is ever opened or saved, matching the convention every other asset in this codebase already follows; both call sites (`_openRepositoryThemeReadOnly` for View, `_cloneRepositoryThemeAsNewWorld` for Clone) were updated to chain one more `.then()` off the now-async materializer, both already living inside `ThemeRepositoryClient.load()`'s own `.then()` chain so the change is a natural fit. A conversion failure (an already-expired URL, a transient network error) is disclosed, not swallowed into a corrupted Project — the asset is simply left as its original signed-URL string, so one broken asset can never block the rest of a real clone from succeeding. **Defense in depth, not a substitute for the real fix**: `_projectCard`'s (the Welcome-screen card) and `_repoOnlyCard`'s thumbnail `<img>` elements both gained an `onerror` handler degrading to the icon glyph instead of a broken-image icon — covers any future asset value this codebase can't fully control, but the actual bug is the data-URI conversion above, not this fallback. Verified via a new Playwright test serving a real HTTP endpoint standing in for a Supabase signed URL (not a `data:`-shaped mock, which would have silently passed without exercising the fetch/conversion path at all): the saved clone's `thumbnail.png`/`preview.png` are confirmed to be real `data:image/png;base64,...` strings, not the original signed URL. Full regression across all 15 prior scratch scripts + the new test + both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged, zero console errors. `tools/world-builder/` (v1) was not touched — it has no Repository-clone feature to carry this bug.)

- World Builder — Delete a Personal Theme Everywhere, Not Just Locally ("i deleted it twice but it keeps coming back," a real, confirmed bug — not the four Repository-clone bugs above, but the same "My World Projects" surface. **Root cause**: "My World Projects" isn't purely local — a real, intentional feature (the "'My World Projects' Lists Personal/Official/Growing" sprint) makes `_annotateProjectBadges` re-check Supabase on every screen render and show a card for any Personal/Official Theme this session owns even with no local draft. Delete, though, only ever removed the LOCAL `ProjectStore` record — deliberately, to make an Official theme un-nukeable by accident. Applied to a *Personal* theme the author actually owns, that same local-only rule meant Delete could never truly finish: the Personal Repository row and its Cloud Backup both stayed real, so the very next render rediscovered them and redrew the identical card — reading as "deleting it does nothing," confirmed reproducible by design, not user error. Compounding it, the exact card this produces (`_repoOnlyCard`, a Personal theme with no local draft) had **no delete control of any kind** — clicking it only ever restored/cloned it, never removed it. **Fix**: `js/themeRepositoryClient.js` gained `deleteTheme(repositoryId, themeId)` (mirrors the existing `reset()`'s real-delete-confirmation discipline — Storage objects removed before the row, `.select()` chained after `.delete()` so a silently-blocked RLS delete can never be mistaken for success — scoped to exactly one `theme_id` instead of a whole repository) and `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/projectSync.js` gained `remove(projectId)` (deletes exactly one Cloud Backup row by its own id, owner-scoped). `_projectCard`'s Delete (local drafts) now also calls both, best-effort, after removing the local draft immediately for instant feedback — its confirm dialog now discloses this ("...that copy and its online backup are removed too"). `_repoOnlyCard` gained a real Delete button for `kind==='personal'` only — **never** for `kind==='official'`, by construction (`deleteTheme` always targets the `'personal'` repository, so an Official-badged card's Delete, wherever it appears, can never touch the platform catalog — the existing, permanent protection is unchanged, just finally completed for the theme kind it was never meant to cover). A remote-cleanup failure (Repository unreachable, nothing was ever actually published there) is silently tolerated — the local outcome and a final `renderMyWorlds()` reflect whatever is genuinely true, never a fabricated success. Verified via a new 2-scenario Playwright test: (A) a repo-only Personal card with a Cloud Backup — the exact reported shape — deletes via its own new button, confirmed via the mock's own call log that both `deleteTheme('personal',...)` and `ProjectSync.remove(...)` fired, and the card is gone from the very next render (the same render that would have resurrected it had the mock's Repository/Backup state not actually been updated first); (B) a real local card whose World is also Personal-published — Delete removes the local draft and fires the identical remote cleanup. Full regression across all 16 prior scratch scripts + the 2 new scenarios + both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2, unaffected since v1 has no `_repoOnlyCard`/clone feature to carry this bug) pass unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 (implements the approved "Vihu Card Platform v1 — Implementation Sprint" plan end to end — a genuinely new platform capability, not a bug fix, so it's summarized in full rather than as a delta. **What it is**: a Card is a shareable, time-boxed unlock — a Theme Author mints one against a Theme they've already Published to their **Personal** Repository (never Official, which is already open to everyone); whoever redeems it gets that World discoverable in Creator's Screen 2 World Library for the exact tries/duration the Author set, never a permanent copy. Redemption is a **Pattern Match** puzzle: every Card is minted with a randomized rotation/mirror/translation of a real, named constellation (ORION/CASSIOPEIA/URSA_MAJOR/CYGNUS/LYRA) placed on a 10×10 star grid — a real design correction made mid-session, not assumed correct from the start: the constellation NAME is a reusable flavor label, never the security boundary (many cards can be "Orion"), since making the name itself unique would have capped the whole platform at 5 cards before names had to repeat. What's actually unique per Card is its own randomly placed `pattern` (matched directly on the tap-to-redeem path, no name involved) and a DB-generated `code` (paired with `constellation` for a secondary typed-fallback path, e.g. "ORION-00125", normalized dash/space/case-insensitively). Rarity (⚪common/🟢uncommon/🔵rare/🟣epic/🟡legendary) is always derived from the Author's own chosen tries×duration via a fixed threshold function, never chosen directly. Only the "Builder" card type (theme-preview) ships — Creator/Unlock/Event/Achievement/Classroom stay reserved vocabulary in the schema's CHECK constraints, completely inert in application code, so a future sprint can build one out with zero schema migration. **Architecture boundary, held throughout**: all card logic lives in one new shared module, `js/cardPlatform.js` (repo root, sibling to `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`, mirroring its exact IIFE/ES5/single-window-export/never-throw conventions and reusing its `getClient()`/`getSession()` rather than a second config fetch or sign-in) — World Builder and Creator are both thin UI hooks calling `generate()`/`listMine()`/`revoke()`/`redeem()` and rendering results, never embedding card-specific business logic of their own. **Where generation lives**: World Builder's Welcome screen, NOT the Publish screen (a Card is a shareable object built from an already-published World, not a step in publishing it) — a `🎴 Generate a Card` icon action on a project card (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s `_projectCard`), disabled by default and enabled by one added line in the existing async `_annotateProjectBadges()` once it confirms `personalIds.has(worldId)` — no new async call. Opens `_showCardPanel()`, a standalone modal reusing the exact `_showInfoModal()` shell already proven by the Sign In form to host a real, live form (Label/Max Tries-or-Unlimited/Duration-or-Forever, a live rarity preview, Generate, and a re-fetched-not-optimistically-appended minted-cards list with per-row Revoke — soft, `revoked_at`, blocks new redemptions only, never retroactively pulls back an already-live grant). **Where redemption lives**: Creator's Screen 2, collapsed-by-default and appended right after the existing World Library `_sourceGroup()` (`js/creationFlow.js`'s `_buildCardRedeemWidget()`) — NOT a separate app. Ports the validated wireframe's own tap-to-place/tap-again-to-undo/live-line-per-tap 10×10 grid mechanics near-verbatim (`buildLabeledGrid`/`centerOfCell` equivalents), deliberately dropping the wireframe's own demo-only "reference" card-back column: in production there's no local copy of a Card's pattern to show a reference for — the physical/shared card itself (a screenshot, a print, a spoken word) is the real-world reference, external to the app. A wrong pattern shows a plain error and clears the board with no lockout; a correct one calls a new exported `CreationFlow.refreshWorldScreen()` (hoisting `_renderWorldScreen(type)`'s own closure-local `type` to a module-scope `_currentScreenType` so it can re-invoke the same screen), which is the actual mechanism that makes the newly-unlocked World appear in the World Library row with no reload — generalizing `onImported()`'s own pre-existing "just call `_renderWorldScreen(type)` again" pattern into a stable, externally-callable name. **Three real engineering gaps the wireframe phase couldn't have caught (a wireframe has no backend), all resolved this sprint**: (1) **cross-owner read grant** — a redeemer is never the Personal Theme's owner, so without extending access, a successful `redeem_card()` call could return `ok:true` while RLS still returned zero rows for the actual Theme content, making redemption theater; fixed with additive `or exists(...)` clauses on the two existing, previously owner-only `themes_personal_select`/`theme_assets_personal_read` policies, keyed off a live, unexpired `card_redemptions` row joined through `cards` — default behavior for every non-redeemed row is completely unchanged. (2) **`ThemeRepositoryClient.load()` hardcodes the caller's own uid** — can't load another owner's Personal Theme; resolved with one new function, `loadPersonalByOwner(ownerId, themeId)`, added beside `load()` rather than risky modification of `load()`'s own correct behavior for its existing callers, reusing the same private `_resolveAssets()` helper as-is. (3) **no "registered but time-limited" concept anywhere in `js/themeRegistry.js`** — resolved via lazy, read-time pruning matching the module's own pre-existing "always recompute on read, no caching to invalidate" convention: a new exported `registerRedeemedTheme(pkg, opts)` validates via the existing `validatePackage()` and registers through the same private `_setImported()` every other path already uses, additionally stamping `redeemed:true`/`redeemedExpiresAt`/`redeemedOwnerId`; a new private `_pruneExpiredRedeemed()` (O(redeemed-count), scanning only `redeemed:true` entries) is called at the top of `list()`/`getCatalog()`/`hasTheme()`/`getRecord()` — the four functions that read `_registry` directly; persistence is deliberately NOT via `_persistImported()` (a redeemed theme's content is never shadow-cached, the same "the source repository is the source of truth" discipline `refreshFromRepository()` already documents) but through a small, separate `vihu.themeRegistry.redeemedGrants.v1` key holding only `{themeId,ownerId,expiresAt}` per grant;
