boot-time rehydration (`_rehydrateRedeemed()`, called right after the existing `_loadImported()`) drops already-expired entries and re-fetches survivors fresh via `loadPersonalByOwner()`, mirroring `_loadImported()`'s own tolerant, swallow-one-failure pattern. **The platform's first RPC/SECURITY DEFINER function**: `redeem_card(p_pattern jsonb, p_typed_code text)` in `supabase/schema.sql` (a disclosed, unexecuted draft, per this project's standing convention — this sandbox cannot reach Supabase) — the only mechanism that can compare a caller's tapped pattern or typed code against the `cards` table's own secret `pattern`/`constellation`/`code`/`serial_no` columns without ever exposing them via a direct client SELECT (`cards` deliberately carries zero anon/public SELECT policy at all — that absence is the actual security mechanism); canonicalizes a tapped pattern via a small immutable `_card_platform_sort_pattern()` set-comparison helper (order-independent, since a redeemer's tap order need not match the Card's original mint order) and normalizes a typed code (`upper(regexp_replace(v,'[\s-]+','','g'))`) so "ORION-00125"/"orion 00125"/"Orion00125" all resolve identically; on match, atomically increments `tries_used`, inserts one `card_redemptions` row, and returns only `{ok,card_type,target_repository,target_theme_id,target_owner_id,label,rarity,expires_at,tries_remaining}` — **never `pattern`/`code`/`serial_no`/`constellation` on any branch**, verified mechanically this sprint (parsing the function's own `jsonb_build_object(...)` calls, not merely asserted) rather than only claimed; on failure, returns only a `reason` enum (`not_authenticated`/`no_input`/`no_match`/`exhausted`). `cards`' own INSERT policy `with check`s an `exists()` subquery proving the minting owner already owns a real Personal Theme matching `target_theme_id` in `themes` — the actual enforcement that a Card can't be minted for someone else's World. Verified via a new scratch Playwright suite (47 assertions, since a live Supabase call is unreachable from this sandbox — the same standing limitation every earlier Supabase-touching sprint in this codebase has disclosed): the Generate a Card gate (disabled → enabled once Personal-published, driven through the real `_annotateProjectBadges` code path, not a shortcut), rarity-boundary computation (Unlimited+Forever → legendary), the full generate→minted-list→Revoke round trip, the redeem widget's tap/undo/live-line mechanics, a wrong-pattern-clears-with-no-lockout-then-a-later-correct-attempt-still-succeeds sequence, the typed fallback, and the static leak-proof check against the real `redeem_card()` SQL body — all passing, zero console errors on either surface; both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged, confirming this sprint touched neither Builder's nor Studio's existing Build/Publish/Validate/rendering pipelines. See `docs/VIHU_CARD_PLATFORM.md` for the full canonical reference.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 — Card Art (front/back visual, download, print) ("the card is distributable so it should be downloadable, printable. in builder i should be able to see it front and back" — a real product gap, not a bug: the minted-card list showed only a text row, never an actual card artifact, which this codebase's own docs had already disclosed as deferred — "Print & Play card-back rendering... no schema change is needed later, pattern is already stored in full"). Implements it entirely from data this session already has: `card.pattern`/`constellation`/`code`/`rarity`/`label`/`createdAt` (from `CardPlatform.listMine()`) plus the World's own real `name`/`icon`/Hero-Image (`ProjectModel`) — never a fabricated illustration or a fictional "Creator" credit, since neither exists as real data anywhere in this codebase; a design reference board supplied mid-session (front: full-bleed art, type pill, title, bottom rarity+code bar; back: dark starfield with the card's own constellation connected star-to-star, the code, "Map the stars. Unlock the magic.") was followed directly wherever real data could support it, and deliberately simplified (a flat gradient + the World's icon glyph when no Hero Image exists; "Minted Xh ago" instead of an invented name; a simple Canvas-drawn corner accent instead of full gold filigree) wherever it couldn't, rather than inventing data. A new 🎴 **View Card** button on each minted-card row (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`) opens `_showCardArtPreview()`, reusing the same `_showInfoModal()` shell every other Card Platform panel already uses — two real `<canvas>` elements (`CARD_ART_W/H = 700×980`, a poker-card-ratio print-usable resolution — the same intrinsic pixels serve both the on-screen preview, scaled down via CSS, and the downloaded/printed PNG, so "what you see is what prints") drawn by `_drawCardFront()`/`_drawCardBack()` using only Canvas 2D primitives (`fillText`/`arcTo`/gradients/`shadowBlur`) per this codebase's own established "reach for Canvas rather than hand-authoring assets" convention — no image-generation dependency, no binary asset. `_drawCardFront()`: a full-bleed Hero-Image background (cover-fit crop) or, absent one, a rarity-tinted gradient with the World's icon glyph centered; a bottom scrim for text legibility; a "🏠 BUILDER CARD" type pill (the only type v1 ships) and rarity glyph top corners; the World's own name (auto-shrunk to fit via `_cardFitText()`) and the Card's own optional label; a bottom bar pairing a rarity-coloured pill (`CARD_RARITY_META` — grey/green/blue/purple/gold, matching the reference exactly) with the real `code`. `_drawCardBack()`: a dark radial-gradient starfield, simple gold corner accents, a "⭐ VihuCard" header, the Card's own real `pattern` coordinates plotted as glowing gold stars connected in tap order (the identical shape a redeemer would need to trace — verified via a real pixel-sample at one of the card's own seeded pattern coordinates, not merely "a grid exists"), the constellation name, the human-readable code (`ORION-00125`), and the tagline. **Download**: reuses the existing `_downloadDataURL()` helper (already used for Build/Export elsewhere in this file) against each canvas's own `toDataURL('image/png')` — genuine print-resolution files, `<code>-front.png`/`<code>-back.png`. **Print**: `_printCardArt()` builds a small, normally off-screen `.wb-card-print-sheet` (two `<img>` built from the same canvas PNG data) appended to `document.body`, calls `window.print()`, and removes it afterward (`afterprint` listener plus a 5s fallback timeout, since browser support/timing for that event varies) — a new `@media print` block hides everything else on the page and sizes each image to its real physical dimensions (2.5in × 3.5in) for the duration of the print. Verified via a new 12-assertion Playwright suite (View Card reachable from a minted row; both canvases render at real 700×980 resolution with genuine non-transparent painted pixels, not a blank canvas; a direct pixel sample at the card's own real pattern coordinate confirms the back matrix reflects *this* card, not a placeholder; Download Front/Back trigger real browser downloads with the correct `<constellation>-<serial>-front/back.png` filenames; Print mounts a real 2-image sheet with genuine PNG data-URI `<img src>`s and tears it down afterward) plus the full existing 47-assertion Card Platform suite (one assertion updated for the row's new second button — not a regression, the intended consequence of adding View Card; a revoked card correctly keeps its View Card button since its art is still real and viewable, only Revoke itself disappears) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged. No schema/RPC/`js/cardPlatform.js` change — this is purely additive World Builder UI drawing from data the platform already had.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 — Redeem Moved to Screen 1, Distinct Marking for Card-Unlocked Worlds (two real product findings from the same screenshot: "card imported themes should have some distinct marking" and "the redeem should be on 1st screen else you can import a wrong category theme in a wrong category." **Root cause of the second, more serious finding**: the Redeem widget originally lived on Screen 2, whose own World Library row is filtered to whichever single Creation Type is currently active (`_themesForType`) — a Card redeemed while on "Tell a Story," for a Theme whose `supportedCreationTypes` was `['artwork']` only, would register correctly but then vanish from that filtered view, reading as "nothing happened." **Fix**: the widget moved to Screen 1 (`_renderTypeScreen`), before any Creation Type is chosen — there is no category to get wrong yet. Since Screen 1 has no "current type" for a bare `refreshWorldScreen()`-style repaint to target, `_handleCardRedeemResult` was replaced with a real router, `_routeAfterRedeem(result, status)`: it reads the just-registered theme's own real `supportedCreationTypes` (already stamped by `ThemeRegistry.registerRedeemedTheme`, no new field) and matches it against `CREATION_TYPES`; exactly one match auto-navigates straight to that Creation Type's Screen 2 with the World pre-selected (landing there IS the confirmation); zero or several matches stays on Screen 1 and says so in the widget's own status line, naming the real matching type titles rather than guessing one — never a guessed/default destination. `refreshWorldScreen()` and its backing `_currentScreenType` are removed outright (zero remaining callers once Redeem left Screen 2 — "if unused, delete completely," not left as dead exported API). **Distinct marking, the first finding**: `ThemeRegistry.getRecord(id)` already stamped `redeemed`/`redeemedExpiresAt` on a Card-unlocked theme's own record (`registerRedeemedTheme`, Vihu Card Platform v1's own original work) — creationFlow.js simply hadn't read it yet. New `_redeemedInfo()`/`_redeemedTimeLeft()` helpers feed: a small 🎴 corner ribbon on the World Library thumbnail (`_worldRowCard`, opposite corner from the selected-state checkmark) plus a time-left caption under the name ("22h left" / "45m left" / a plain "Card" for a forever-unlocked one); and a matching "🎴 Unlocked with a Card — Xh left" note in the Selected World Preview panel (`paintPreview`), so the marking is visible both in the row and at the moment "Start Creating" is about to be pressed. Verified via an updated 54-assertion Playwright suite (the redeem-widget tests now run against Screen 1 before any type is chosen; new coverage for single-match auto-navigation with the 🎴 badge/time-left/preview-note all visibly present, multi-match staying on Screen 1 with the real type names in the status line, and Back correctly returning to Screen 1) plus the full existing 12-assertion Card Art suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged — this sprint touched only `js/creationFlow.js` and `css/style.css`, no schema/RPC/`js/cardPlatform.js` change. **Same-day follow-up — redeem board restyled to match the validated wireframe artifact**: the shipped widget had ported the wireframe's tap/undo/line-draw *mechanics* faithfully but not its dark "VihuCard" starfield *visual* language, instead using a plain light-paper board that read as a different, lesser product than the card art itself (`_drawCardBack`'s own dark radial-gradient starfield with gold-glow stars). `.creation-flow-card-board`/`-gridlabel`/`-cell`/`-lines`/`-line`/`-counter`/`-status`/`-redeem-btn` in `css/style.css` were restyled to the wireframe's own values — a `radial-gradient(circle at 30% 20%, #2A2140, #120E1E)` board with a gold (`#E8C766`) border, `SF Mono`/`Cascadia Code`/monospace grid labels and status text, gold-glow selected cells and connecting lines (`text-shadow`/`filter:drop-shadow`) — deliberately reusing the exact hex values already established in `_drawCardBack()`'s canvas drawing, so the printed card back and the live redemption board now read as the same object. The redeem button's label changed from "Redeem" to "✨ Redeem," matching the wireframe's exact text. The wireframe's own demo-only reference-card column stays deliberately unported (unchanged reasoning from the original build: in production there's no local pattern copy to show a reference for). Verified via the same 54-assertion Playwright suite (unchanged pass rate — this was a pure CSS/copy change, no DOM/JS structural change) plus the 12-assertion Card Art suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged; a fresh screenshot pair confirmed the restyled board visually matches the wireframe.)

- Creator Authoring Fidelity Check — Representation Frame Never Applied, World-Object Selection Left Stale Controls Visible (a real end-to-end authoring test requested directly — "lets get on with creator authoring test to see if builder themes show properly" — not a bug report, an open-ended investigation. Authored a real World through World Builder v2's real `ProjectModel`/`ProjectCompiler` APIs (an Artwork Gallery template, a landscape Scene, a Frame with distinct wall-tone/border-colour/thickness/mat values assigned to its Place, an Image Experience, a Text Experience "Caption," and a Shape Experience "Wax Seal"), ran a real headless Build, then imported the compiled package into a fresh Creator page through the real production path (`ThemeEngine.importThemeFile`) and drove Creation Flow → Workspace exactly as a Story Author would — finding two real, previously-undetected bugs, both fixed at the root. **Bug 1 — a Theme Author's chosen Frame Variation never reached the page**: `representation.defaultFrame` (the Frame a Theme Author assigns to a Scene's Place in World Builder) is compiled into every published package, but `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveArtworkFields` has only ever read a per-card override (`slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation`, written by Card Designer's own Frame Variation swatch picker) — nothing anywhere ever seeded that override from `representation.defaultFrame` when a page was first created. Confirmed by pixel-sampling a freshly-created page's canvas: the wall showed the System Default cream (`#F4F1EC`), not the custom blue (`#2255AA`) the Theme Author had actually chosen — a real, previously disclosed-but-unfixed gap named explicitly in the earlier "Creator Theme Fidelity Pass" sprint ("flagged as real follow-up work for a future theme whose representations pick a non-default Frame Variation") and now hit for real. Fixed with one new shared helper, `_seedDefaultFrameVariation(slide,representation,theme)` in `js/creationFlow.js`, called from both `_finish()` (Start Creating) and `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide()` (Change Representation) — seeds the override from `representation.defaultFrame` only when it resolves to a real `theme.frameVariations` entry AND the slide has no per-card choice of its own yet, so a Story Author's own hand-picked Frame Variation is never clobbered; reuses the exact override bag every manual Frame Variation pick already writes to, no second resolution mechanism. Verified: the same authored page now shows the correct wall tone (`rgb(34,85,170)`, an exact match for `#2255AA`) and frame border colour in both the editor canvas and Publish Studio's Cover render. **Bug 2 — selecting a World-owned object left the PREVIOUS selection's editing controls visible underneath the disclosure banner**: `js/contextPanel.js`'s `refresh()` calls `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure(sceneObj)` for a World-owned Scene Object (a Theme-authored Layer Pack entry) but never called `_hideAllTabs()` first — so if a Story Author had just been looking at, say, "Your Picture"'s Fit/Frame controls (`#card-tab.context-visible`, `[data-card-section="image"].context-active`, both CSS-driven to `display:block`), then tapped a World-owned Caption object, those stale controls stayed fully visible and interactive directly beneath the "This is part of the World" message — exactly the "live-looking but doesn't target what was clicked" problem this same file's own code comments already warn against, except surfacing for an unrelated, previously-selected object rather than the newly-selected one. Confirmed via direct DOM inspection (`#card-tab`'s `context-visible` class, `[data-card-section].context-active`) before and after the fix. Fixed with one added `_hideAllTabs()` call before `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure(sceneObj)`. Verified via Playwright: selecting Artwork Place then the World-owned Caption now correctly shows only the disclosure banner, with `#card-tab` confirmed hidden; full regression across the entire existing Creator suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, `real_museum_trace.js`, `real_museum_selection_check.js`) passes unchanged — `scene_object_test.js`'s own Museum Gallery Wax Seal selection independently confirms the same fix (`cardTabVisible:false`); both `goldenBuild.js` suites (v1 and v2) pass unchanged. **One suspected third bug was investigated and found to be a test-script artifact, not a product defect**: a Shape Experience ("Wax Seal," a green circle) initially failed to render or compile into the Layer Pack at all when authored via raw `ProjectModel` calls — traced to the raw calls omitting `updateExperience(project,id,{contentKind:'graphics'})` before setting `graphicShape`, a real, already-known, already-solved gate (`contentKind` is inferred once at creation and never re-inferred on a later property write, the identical class of gap the Repository-Only Card work had already found and disclosed for Image content) — confirmed the REAL "Add a Shape" quick-picker in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js` (line ~5931) already sets `contentKind:'graphics'` correctly before writing `graphicShape`, so real authors are unaffected; re-running the authoring test with the correct sequence confirmed the shape compiles correctly (`decoration:{kind:'shape',shape:'circle',...}`, `target:'overlay'`) and renders at the exact authored colour (`rgb(17,170,51)`, an exact match for `#11AA33`) in Creator. No Builder/Theme-contract/architecture change — both fixes are root-cause corrections inside `js/creationFlow.js` and `js/contextPanel.js`, reusing structures that already existed.)

- Vihu Card Platform v1 — Redeemed Theme Vanished On Every Hard Refresh (a real, user-reported bug found via live testing on the deployed site, not the sandboxed test suite — "the theme added through vihucard why does it goes away on every hard refresh." **Root cause, traced not guessed**: `registerRedeemedTheme` deliberately never caches a redeemed Theme's own content to `localStorage` (only its identifiers + expiry, via `_persistRedeemedGrants()`) — by design, the redeemed Theme is meant to be re-fetched fresh from its owner's Personal Repository on every boot via `_rehydrateRedeemed()`. But `_rehydrateRedeemed()` was called from inside `js/themeRegistry.js`'s own self-initializing top-level IIFE — and `index.html` loads `js/themeRegistry.js` BEFORE `js/themeRepositoryClient.js`, so at the exact moment that call ran, `window.ThemeRepositoryClient` was always `undefined`; the function's own defensive guard (`if (typeof window.ThemeRepositoryClient==='undefined') return;`) silently no-oped on literally every single boot, regardless of script order elsewhere or network reachability — the re-fetch never ran, ever, so a redeemed Theme (never cached, never re-fetched) simply vanished the instant the tab was closed or reloaded. **Fix**: `_rehydrateRedeemed` is exported from `ThemeRegistry`'s API (`rehydrateRedeemed`) instead of self-invoking, and is now triggered from `js/app.js`'s `_startCreationFlow()` — the exact same place, timed the exact same way, `refreshFromRepository()` (an analogous "needs `ThemeRepositoryClient`, must run after all scripts load" case) already runs from; by the time `app.js` executes, both scripts are guaranteed loaded regardless of tag order. **A second, real robustness gap found while writing the fix**: `_refreshRepositoryWithTimeout()`'s call to `ThemeRegistry.refreshFromRepository()` was never wrapped in try/catch — a synchronous throw from a partial/broken `ThemeRepositoryClient` (reproduced directly during verification: a test double missing one method) would escape before any Promise existed to attach `.catch()` to, aborting the rest of `_startCreationFlow()`'s own function body outright — including the new `rehydrateRedeemed()` call placed right after it. Fixed by wrapping `_refreshRepositoryWithTimeout()`'s body in try/catch, returning `Promise.resolve()` on a synchronous failure, so one broken repository call can never silently take a sibling boot step down with it. Verified via a new Playwright test reproducing the exact reported scenario end-to-end: seed the real `vihu.themeRegistry.redeemedGrants.v1` localStorage key (exactly what a real redemption writes), perform a real `page.reload()` (a genuine hard refresh, not a simulated one), and confirm the Theme is re-registered — failed exactly as reported before the fix (`hasTheme:false`, zero `loadPersonalByOwner` calls), passes after (`hasTheme:true`, `redeemed:true`, one correctly-addressed `loadPersonalByOwner` call). Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged. No schema/RPC/data-model change — both fixes are boot-sequence-ordering corrections in `js/themeRegistry.js` and `js/app.js`. **A deeper, disclosed limitation, raised directly and confirmed rather than papered over**: this fix guarantees `_rehydrateRedeemed()` actually RUNS on every boot — it does not, and cannot, guarantee the redeemer's own identity still resolves. Creator/Studio has no user-account system of any kind; the only "identity" a redemption is tied to is the redeemer's disposable Supabase anonymous session (`_ensureAuth()`), persisted by Supabase's own client library to its own `localStorage` key, separate from the small `vihu.themeRegistry.redeemedGrants.v1` grant list this fix rehydrates from. `card_redemptions.redeemer_id` is recorded against that anonymous `auth.uid()` at redemption time, and the Personal Repository's read policy checks it matches on every later fetch. `_ensureAuth()` correctly calls `getSession()` before ever calling `signInAnonymously()`, so an ordinary reload on the same browser reuses the same identity — confirmed via the Playwright test above, a genuine `page.reload()`. But if that anonymous session is ever lost — private/incognito browsing, the user clears site data, a different browser or device, or Supabase's own anonymous-session lifecycle expiring it — the grant becomes permanently unrecoverable through any refresh, since nothing maps "this person" to "their redeemed themes" beyond that one disposable token. Explicitly decided, when raised, to leave this as a disclosed limitation for now rather than build local content-caching or real account support — matching this codebase's own existing precedent for Personal Repository/Cloud Backup ("no accounts yet," a real native upgrade path later, not a permanent ceiling). Revisit if this becomes a real recurring complaint.)

- Creator Rendering Bug Fixes — Hosted-by-Scene Image Backgrounds, Change Look Modal Size (three real, user-reported bugs from a real "My Artwork Gallery" screenshot: a full-bleed decorative image sat on top of the picture Holder instead of behind it, a Scene authored with no Holder still appeared to show one, and the "Change Look" mid-edit screen took over the entire viewport. Two root-caused and fixed; one investigated and disclosed. **Bug 1 — Background renders on top of the Holder**: traced to `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer()` — only a true Colour fill (`kind:'fill'`) ever converged onto the `'slide'` compile target (rendered first, i.e. behind the Frame/Holder); an Image/Graphics/Text Experience the Theme Author explicitly set "Hosted by Scene" fell through to `'overlay'` (rendered last, on top of literally everything) regardless of that choice, because `js/projectModel.js`'s `_syncUniversalContent()` never carried "Hosted by Scene" onto the mirrored Scene Layer for anything but Colour — the capability existed in the Inspector's Hosted-By dropdown (all three hosts were always selectable for any content type) but silently did nothing for Image content until now. Fixed by stamping a new `hostedByScene` marker onto every mirrored Layer kind (not just the Colour fill path), and having `convergeSceneLayer()` honour it identically to `kind==='fill'` — "Hosted by Scene" now uniformly means wall-level/behind, matching what its own name promises, for any content kind. Confirmed via a real headless Build + Creator import: a full-bleed green image Hosted by Scene now compiles to `target:'slide'` and the Holder's own placeholder chrome renders correctly on top of it (pixel-sampled, not the green background bleeding through). A Theme Author with an already-authored, Free-hosted "Background" needs to switch its Hosted By to Scene in World Builder for this fix to take effect — the code change makes the capability work correctly, it doesn't retroactively re-host existing content. **Bug 2 — "Change Look" fills the entire screen**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `changeRepresentation()` (the Context Panel's mid-edit Page Style shortcut) reused the exact same `.creation-flow-overlay` element Screens 1/2 use for a brand-new project's first arrival — full-viewport, illustrated Story Meadow scene included — appropriate for onboarding, wildly oversized for a quick "pick a different look" action taken mid-edit. Fixed with a new `mode-change-look` CSS class (`css/style.css`) applied only for this reuse: the same overlay element and JS, but the decorative scene is hidden, the backdrop becomes a plain dimmed scrim (so the editor stays visibly present behind it, dimmed), and `.creation-flow-panel` becomes a compact ~560px centered modal card instead of an edge-to-edge panel. Verified: the panel's own bounding rect is 560×231px against a 1500×950 viewport, not full-viewport, confirmed via both a DOM measurement and a screenshot. **Bug 3 — investigated, not reproduced**: a Builder Scene authored with zero Places was reported to still show a Holder in Creator; a from-scratch reproduction (a real Build with a genuinely zero-Place Scene, imported through the real production path) showed the existing `holders:0` gating (from the earlier "Object Strip Label + Zero-Holder Layout fixes" sprint) already correctly hides the Artwork Place card and skips the Frame/Holder chrome entirely — the fix works as designed for a freshly-compiled package. The most likely explanation, disclosed rather than guessed further into, is that the user's live "My Artwork Gallery" World was built before that earlier fix shipped and hasn't been rebuilt/republished since; flagged for the user to confirm by rebuilding, rather than inventing a second, unverified code change for a symptom that couldn't be reproduced. Verified via a new 2-scenario Playwright reproduction (`three_bugs_check.js`, scratch-only — real headless Build via `ProjectCompiler`, real import through `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile`, real Creation Flow drive-through, pixel-sampled z-order check, DOM-measured modal size) plus full regression across every existing Creator/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model change — both fixes are additive completions of an already-existing "Hosted By" capability and a CSS-only variant of an already-existing overlay reuse.)

- Host-Aware Bounds, Actually Enforced — Scene-Hosted Content Self-Heals to Full Bleed (a direct, same-day follow-up: after Bug 1 above shipped, the user tested a fresh "Hosted by Scene" Background and still saw it render incorrectly. Investigated with a real World Builder screenshot rather than assumed — the Context Inspector's own "Bounds" section read "Inherited from Scene (read-only) — this Experience fills the whole Scene," but the Experience's actual Transform sliders showed `X:1% Y:29% Width:99% Height:40%` — a real, confirmed contradiction between what the UI claimed and what it actually let an author do. **Root cause**: `_contentTransformFields()` in `tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js` — the shared helper rendering each content section's (Text/Image/Graphics) X/Y/Width/Height sliders — has never been gated on `hostedBy` at all; it always rendered fully free, editable sliders regardless of whether the Experience was Hosted by Scene/Place/Free, silently contradicting the Bounds panel's own pre-existing copy (itself dated to Builder V3.1's original "Host-aware Bounds" design intent, which this function never actually implemented). Before Bug 1's fix, this mismatch was invisible — only a Colour fill could be Scene-hosted, and Colour has no Transform sliders at all — so the gap only became reachable once Image/Graphics/Text could meaningfully be Scene-hosted. **Fix**: `_contentTransformFields` now takes a `hostedBy` parameter (threaded through from all three call sites — Text/Image/Graphics); for `hostedBy==='scene'` or `'place'`, it renders a plain read-only note instead of sliders, and — critically — self-heals any already-drifted stored rect back to `{x:0,y:0,w:1,h:1}` the moment that Experience's Properties panel renders, the same read-time-reconciliation discipline this file already uses elsewhere (`_ensureHolderDefaults`, `_ordered`) so a Theme Author never has to manually drag sliders back or hunt for a "reset" control — simply opening/checking on the Experience (something they'd naturally do anyway) fixes it, and the next Build picks up the correction automatically. Verified end-to-end via a real Playwright reproduction of the user's own exact drifted values (`X:0.01 Y:0.29 W:0.99 H:0.40`, Hosted by Scene): confirmed the drifted rect is genuinely stored before any UI interaction, then drove the real Working View (open the Project → Scenes nav → open the Scene → click the Background Experience card) and confirmed the stored rect self-corrected to `{0,0,1,1}` purely from that click, with no slider interaction at all; a subsequent real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()` confirmed the compiled Layer Pack entry now carries `target:'slide'` with a full-bleed rect. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model change — this closes the last gap in Bug 1's own fix, making "Hosted by Scene" behave exactly as its own UI has always claimed it does.)

- Zero-Holder Scenes — the "no border, period" gate closed for the legacy fallback path too (a follow-up found while chasing a user-reported "the Builder says no Place, but Creator still shows a Holder box" report; the earlier "Object Strip Label + Zero-Holder Layout fixes" sprint's own stated intent was "`_resolveBorder`'s Artwork Theme branch skips resolving Frame/mat/wall chrome entirely when `_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0`," but the implementation only ever gated that one branch — the function still fell through to the older, artwork-independent Sprint 8.4.2 "Picture Holder defaults" (`themeOptions.holder`) fallback beneath it, which can resolve its own non-null border from a theme's generic cornerRadius/padding/shadow/fill defaults with no relationship to Places/Holders at all; once that fallback's border came back non-null, `render()`'s artwork-placeholder-box code (gated only on `_border` being truthy, not on holder count) still drew the "Tap to add your artwork" box for a Scene that genuinely has zero Places. Fixed by moving the `_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0` check to the very top of `_resolveBorder`, before either branch runs, so zero-Holder now means no border resolves at all — matching Builder's own Runtime Preview, which draws nothing for a Scene with no Places. The now-always-true inner check inside the Artwork Theme branch was simplified away as dead condition. Verified via a real Playwright A/B test (`git stash`-toggling the fix on a synthetic zero-Holder Scene, comparing full-panel-rect pixel diffs before/after) — for a freshly-authored World Builder theme with no `themeOptions.holder` defaults set, the legacy fallback branch was already returning null even pre-fix, so this specific reproduction shows the fix closes a real, disclosed gap without changing observable output for that particular case; the actual visible symptom the user reported is still being triaged separately (a second, still-present object in their real World, not yet root-caused) since it didn't reproduce against this synthetic fixture — this entry documents the `_resolveBorder` gap-closure on its own merits, not as a confirmed fix for that report. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including the earlier `three_bugs_check.js`'s own zero-Holder Object Strip assertion) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged.)

- Zero-Holder Scenes — the real white-box source found and fixed (a direct, confirmed follow-up to the previous entry, found by reproducing the user's actual live World rather than a synthetic guess: "My shapes › First" — a zero-Place Scene with a Scene-hosted dark Colour-fill background and a Free-hosted gold octagon Decoration Shape. The previous fix (closing `_resolveBorder`'s legacy-fallback gap) was real and necessary but insufficient — it correctly made `_border` resolve to `null` for a zero-Holder Scene, but `render()`'s own composition-selection code, `if(_composition==='quote'){...}else if(_border){...}else{ _drawPanel(t.panel.color,opts.panelStyle,_panelRect) }`, then routed into that `else` branch precisely because `_border` was null — and that branch unconditionally paints the classic pre-Artwork-Theme "story picture panel" rectangle (`t.panel.color`, in practice a near-white page colour) at the panel rect, with zero awareness of Holder count at all; it predates the whole Scene/Place/Holder system and exists for the case of a plain Story Theme with no Artwork Theme active, where painting that rectangle is correct (it's where the picture will go). For a zero-Holder Artwork Theme Scene, though, there is no picture area to paint a background for at all — Builder's own Working View/Runtime Preview show nothing there. Fixed with a third branch, `else if(_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0){ /* draw nothing */ }`, inserted between the Quote check and the `_border` check, so a Scene explicitly declaring zero Places now paints nothing beyond its own 'slide'-scoped Layer Pack content (background fill / decorations), matching Builder exactly. Verified with a real `git stash`-based A/B test reproducing the user's exact World shape end-to-end (real `ProjectCompiler.runBuild()`, real `ThemeEngine.importThemeFile`/`applyArtworkTheme`, real `SlideRenderer.render()`): pre-fix, the panel-rect center pixel reads pure white `(255,255,255,255)`; post-fix, the same pixel reads the theme's own cream page colour `(247,244,238,255)` — the exact "white box" signature confirmed present before this change and gone after it, on the same input, same commit tree, only this one code path toggled. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (Museum Gallery — a real Holder-bearing theme — still renders its Frame/mat/Wax Seal/placeholder exactly as before, confirming no regression for the non-zero-Holder case) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged.)

- Honour World-Owned Object Commitments + Accurate Object Strip Thumbnails (a design-sprint feature, requested directly after the user asked whether Creator actually honours the four checkboxes in World Builder's per-object permission block — the answer was "no, only `visible`" — and separately asked why the Object Strip showed generic icons instead of an object's real content. Investigated via three parallel Explore passes (Object Strip's card-building code and what the render tree already carries; existing Story-Author move/edit override patterns; the compiled Layer Pack shape and Decoration Slot's actual implementation state) before designing, then implemented per an approved plan. **A. Accurate thumbnails**: `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_pushLayerObject` (previously discarding `layer.decoration`/`.sticker`/`.text` after using them only to draw) now also computes a normalized `visual` descriptor (`_layerVisual`) forwarded onto every Scene Object — `{kind:'color',color}` for a fill, `{kind:'image',src}` (resolved via `ThemeRegistry.resolveAssetRef`, or a live Story-Author-uploaded data URI) for an image, `{kind:'shape',shape,fillColor,...}` for a vector shape, `{kind:'glyph',glyph}` for a sticker, `{kind:'text',content,snippet}` for a text Layer (`content` full for editing, `snippet` truncated for display) — reflecting any live Story-Author override, so an edited object's thumbnail stays in sync with what's actually drawn. New exported `SlideRenderer.drawObjectThumbnail(ctx,visual,size)` reuses `drawFrameSwatch`'s own context-swap technique to render a Shape thumbnail via the existing `_layerDrawShape`, no second drawing implementation. `js/objectStrip.js`'s `_card()` gained a `_renderThumb` branch per `visual.kind` — a real CSS background-colour swatch, a real `<img>`, a real `<canvas>` shape, the real glyph, or a truncated text snippet — falling through to the old generic icon when `visual` is absent (every pre-existing card shape, unchanged). **B. Honour "Can a Story Author move this?" (moveable)**: two structural gaps closed together — `_pushLayerObject` previously hardcoded `locked:true` regardless of the real `moveable` value (the one flag `js/app.js`'s existing drag machinery actually checks), now `locked:!layer.moveable`, so a `moveable:true` World object engages the *exact same* mousedown/mousemove/mouseup chain Cover/Hook/End elements already use — no new drag code; and since `js/app.js`'s existing non-sticker drag path already reads/writes `slide.metadata.elementOverrides[id].position` generically for *any* element id (confirmed by reading the code, not assumed — this made the plan's original "new sibling override bag" design unnecessary and simpler to just reuse the existing bag directly, since a Builder-generated Layer id never collides with SceneEngine's own fixed blueprint-element ids and `getRenderData()` only ever reads keys present in the current page's own blueprint), `_layerDrawDecoration`/`_layerDrawText`/`_layerDrawSticker` each gained one resolution step reading that same bag via a new shared `_layerOverride(s,layerId)` helper before falling back to the authored anchor/rect — a pure translation applied to whatever the Layer would have drawn naturally (computed from the natural bbox center for text, so the shift stays correct regardless of alignment), byte-identical to before this sprint when no override exists. **C. Honour "Can a Story Author change this?" (editable) — in-place content edit only, no delete/remove, confirmed directly with the user**: `js/sceneEngine.js` gained one generic `setContentOverride(slide,id,field,value)` (mirroring `setPosition`/`setRotation`'s own `_ensureEntry`/`_maybePrune` shape) for the `fillColor`/`content`/`image` fields a World-owned object's content can carry; `js/contextPanel.js`'s `_renderWorldObjectDisclosure` now renders one real, kind-specific control when `editable:true` and the object's `visual.kind` supports one — a colour input for `color`/`shape`, a Replace Image upload row for `image`, a Words textarea for `text` — writing through that same override bag and redrawing live (never calling the panel's own `refresh()`, which would rebuild the very input mid-edit); a bare `glyph` object keeps the original "that kind of edit isn't available in Creator yet" wording, a disclosed simplification since recolouring/replacing a glyph has no natural analog and wasn't one of the two examples the user named. **D. Decoration Slot, shipped in the same sprint per explicit direction, rather than deferred**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeSceneLayer` previously never copied World Builder's own `layer.decorationSlot` (the 4th permission-block checkbox) into the compiled package at all — dead data on both sides — now carried through as `decorationSlot` on the compiled entry. Creator reuses the *existing* Sticker Studio flow end to end (pick-from-library → place-on-canvas → `slide.metadata.stickers[]`) rather than inventing a second "Story Author adds content" mechanism: a selected `decorationSlot:true` object's disclosure gains a "✨ Add your own decoration here" button; `js/stickerStudio.js` gained a one-shot `setNextPlacementSeed(centerX,centerY)` (consumed and cleared by the very next insert only, so every other Add-a-Sticker flow keeps its ordinary centered default) seeding that one placement near the slot's own position instead of dead-center — the resulting sticker is a completely ordinary, fully Story-owned object with the same Select/Move/Resize/Rotate/Layer/Lock/Delete capabilities every other sticker already has. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright fixture (a synthetic World with a Scene-hosted Colour fill [moveable+editable], a Free-hosted Shape [moveable+editable+decorationSlot], a Free-hosted Image [editable, not moveable], and a Free-hosted Text layer [editable] — each compiled through the real `ProjectCompiler`, imported through the real `ThemeEngine`/`ThemeRegistry`, rendered through the real `SlideRenderer`): all four kinds show accurate, distinguishable Object Strip thumbnails; the moveable/non-moveable objects' `locked` flags resolve correctly; a real colour-input edit persists into `elementOverrides` and the Object Strip thumbnail reflects it live with zero panel rebuild; the Decoration Slot button appears only for the flagged object and is absent otherwise. One real bug found and fixed during fixture-building, unrelated to this sprint's own code: the test's Scene-hosted Colour Experience initially failed to compile at all, traced to a spelling mismatch (`contentKind:'color'` vs. the codebase's actual `'colour'` enum value in `_syncUniversalContent`) — not a defect, just confirms this convention is real and consistent. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (Museum Gallery's own Wax Seal — a glyph-kind, non-real-control object — still shows the original disclosure wording unchanged, confirming the new control only appears where a real one exists) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged.)

- Change Look Modal — Oversized Representation Thumbnails Blew Out the Panel (a direct, user-reported layout bug: "change look is very bad looking layout" — a screenshot showed a giant, cropped photo overflowing the "Change Look" mid-edit modal with visible scrollbars, distinct from the earlier "Change Look fills the entire screen" bug already fixed via the `mode-change-look` CSS class. **Root cause**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_repCard()` (the Page Style card builder used only by `_renderChangeRepresentationScreen`, the Context Panel's "Change Representation"/"Change Look" shortcut) renders `<img class="creation-flow-card-icon-image">` whenever a Representation's thumbnail resolves to a real image — which, per `_repThumbnail()`'s own fallback chain, means the World's own Hero Image whenever the Representation itself has no thumbnail of its own (the common case) — but `css/style.css` had zero rules for that class at all; the `<img>` rendered at its full intrinsic photo resolution (e.g. a real 900×1200 upload) with nothing constraining its size, blowing out its card, the grid, and the `mode-change-look` panel's own 560px/85vh box (confirmed via a real `git stash` A/B test: pre-fix, `panel.scrollWidth` 1211px against a 560px `clientWidth` — genuine horizontal overflow — with each `<img>` rendering at its full 900×1200 natural size; post-fix, both images constrain to 196×110 with zero overflow). **Fix**: added `.creation-flow-card-icon-image{width:100%;height:110px;object-fit:cover;border-radius:14px;box-shadow:inset 0 0 0 1px var(--cf-line);flex-shrink:0;}` right after `.creation-flow-card-icon`'s own rule — the same `width:100%`/fixed-height/`object-fit:cover` shape every other Creation Flow image thumbnail already uses (`.creation-flow-world-thumb img`, `.creation-flow-carousel-art img`), sized as a real photo preview rather than the small 56×56 emoji-badge circle `.creation-flow-card-icon` uses for a glyph. `_repCard` itself, `_renderChangeRepresentationScreen`, and the `mode-change-look` modal sizing from the earlier fix are all unchanged — this was purely a missing CSS rule for one image class. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`change_look_image_overflow.js`, scratch-only) driving the real `CreationFlow.changeRepresentation()` against a synthetic World whose Representation has no thumbnail of its own (forcing the Hero Image fallback, a realistic 900×1200 photo): post-fix, both Page Style cards' images measure 196×110 with the panel holding its 560px width and zero horizontal overflow; full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `frame_variation_test3.js`, `ws_check.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `lang_check.js`, `baseline3.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `museum_fidelity_test.js`, `real_museum_trace.js`, `real_museum_selection_check.js`, `three_bugs_check.js`, `commitments_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged — this fix touches only `css/style.css`, no JS/architecture change.)

- A New Sticker Sits Centered But Can't Be Dragged, Layer Order Buttons "Don't Work" (a real, user-reported bug from a real "My shapes" screenshot: an Apple sticker sat centered over a large World-owned Decoration Shape and could not be dragged on canvas. **Root cause, traced directly, not assumed**: the Honour World-Owned Object Commitments sprint's own `_pushLayerObject`/`_layerObjectBboxes` accumulator (introduced earlier, in the Creator Reconciliation Sprint) concatenates every World-owned Layer Pack object onto the very END of `_lastSceneElements` as one lump, regardless of which of the 5 containership scopes (`slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element`/`overlay`) actually drew it — but only `overlay`-scoped objects are genuinely drawn LAST, on top of everything (the Builder Convergence Sprint's own explicit design); `slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element`-scoped World objects are all drawn EARLIER in the same render pass, visually BEHIND every Scene element and Story-Author sticker. `js/app.js`'s `_hitTestSceneElement` reads `_lastSceneElements` topmost-first (last element in the array wins), so a `slide`-scoped World shape — visually sitting behind the sticker — was nonetheless always hit-tested as if it sat on top, silently intercepting every click/drag meant for an overlapping sticker (or any Scene element) drawn beneath it; since that World shape is typically `locked` (non-`moveable`), the drag machinery correctly refused to move it, reading as "the sticker can't be dragged." **Fix**: `_pushLayerObject` now records which `target` scope produced each entry (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`); at the single concatenation point, the accumulator splits into `overlay`-scoped objects (still appended after everything, unchanged) and every other scope (now spliced in BEFORE Scene elements/Stickers instead of after) — restoring hit-testing to match real visual z-order: an `overlay`-scoped World object correctly still wins over an overlapping sticker (verified, unchanged), while a `slide`/`frame`/`holder`/`element`-scoped one no longer steals clicks from Story content drawn on top of it. **The second symptom, investigated and found to be a real, disclosed structural limit rather than a bug**: `SceneEngine.bringStickerForward`/`sendStickerBackward`/`bringStickerToFront`/`sendStickerToBack` (`js/sceneEngine.js`) only ever reorder a sticker relative to *other stickers* in the same array — with exactly one sticker on the page (the reported case), every one of the four Order buttons is a correct, guarded no-op (`i===arr.length-1`/`i<=0`), since there's nothing else to swap with; Story-Author stickers and World-owned Layer Pack content are drawn in two structurally separate phases (stickers always after Scene elements, before `overlay`) and Order buttons have never reordered across that boundary — not touched, since doing so would be a real architecture change, not a bug fix, and wasn't what broke here. Verified via two new Playwright reproductions (scratch-only): `sticker_dragorder_bug.js` (a `git`-comparable A/B — reproduced the exact wrong-hit-test-id bug pre-fix, confirmed the sticker's own center now resolves correctly post-fix) and `sticker_dragorder_bug2.js` (confirms an `overlay`-scoped World object still correctly wins hit-testing when genuinely on top, then drives a real end-to-end `page.mouse` down/move/up drag on the canvas and confirms the sticker's real `x`/`y` actually change, not the locked World shape beneath it). Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged — the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_pushLayerObject`/concatenation step, no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change.)

- Unified Layer Ordering — the Object Strip Becomes a Real Reorder Control (a direct follow-up to the sticker drag/hit-test fix above: "as we are fixing creator one by one, i think we should fix this [layer order buttons]" — the user's own follow-up question, "can object strip be used as layering order? if we reorder objects there the layering reorder itself?", became the design. Investigated via a dedicated Explore pass (Plan Mode) before designing, confirming the real root cause was structural, not cosmetic: three completely separate, disjoint ordering mechanisms existed with no shared key — Scene blueprint elements (Frame/Decoration/Text-holder on Cover/Hook/End pages) order via a numeric `zIndex` (`SceneEngine.adjustZIndex`); Stickers order via plain array position (`SceneEngine.bringStickerForward`/etc., `js/sceneEngine.js`); World-owned Layer Pack objects order purely by containership scope. `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `render()` assembled the final hit-test/paint array as a **fixed concatenation**, never a true merge-sort — Scene elements always drawn first, then every Sticker unconditionally after, regardless of either's own ordering value — so a Sticker could never be reordered relative to a Frame/Decoration element on ANY page role (Cover/Hook/End included, not just Story), which is the real reason a lone sticker's "Front" button looked like it did nothing. **Fix, scoped deliberately after investigating the render pipeline's real constraints**: Scene blueprint elements and Stickers now draw as ONE interleaved, resolvable pass instead of two fixed loops. New `_naturalStoryOrder(s)`/`_resolveStoryOrder(s)` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) compute the reorderable group's order — natural (no override) is exactly the old fixed sequence, so every existing page/theme renders byte-identically until a Story Author actually reorders something; a new, additive `slide.metadata.layerOrder` array (`SceneEngine.getLayerOrder`/`setLayerOrder`, mirroring the existing override-bag "delete when empty" convention) lets that reordering persist. New exported `SlideRenderer.getReorderableIds(s)` is the one place both entry points read/write the current effective order from. Card Designer's three previously-separate Order button blocks (Sticker's 4-button row calling `SceneEngine[fn]`; Frame's 2-button row calling `_frameAdjustZ`→`adjustZIndex`; Decoration's 2-button row calling `adjustZIndex` inline) all collapse onto one shared `_reorderSelected(edge, commitFn)` helper (`js/cardDesigner.js`) — so "Bring Forward" on a lone sticker now genuinely moves it in front of a Frame/Decoration element too, and the buttons can never disagree with what the Object Strip shows, since both write the same `layerOrder`. `js/objectStrip.js` gained real HTML5 drag-and-drop on every card whose object is in the current reorderable set (`_wireReorderDrag`/`_performReorder`) — dragging a card left-to-right changes the object's actual paint/hit-test order (matching the strip's own existing left=back/right=front display convention), not just its own position in the list; a drop-indicator line and grab cursor (`css/style.css`'s `.object-card-draggable`/`.object-card-drop-before`/`-after`) make the affordance visible. **Scope, deliberately bounded and disclosed rather than forced** (this round): World-owned Layer Pack objects (moveable or not) are NOT part of this reorderable group — investigated directly and found that their rect for `frame`/`holder`/`element` scopes is only resolved at specific points inside Frame/Panel drawing, and their `slide`/`overlay` scopes draw at fixed points (before Frame/Panel, and after everything else) that existing themes (including the Sprint's own "Hosted by Scene" background mechanism) already depend on — unifying those safely would require deferred/two-pass drawing changes to the Frame/Panel rendering pipeline itself, a materially bigger and riskier change than this fix, so it's recorded as real follow-up work rather than attempted here (closed the same day — see the entry directly below); a locked/non-moveable object of any kind keeps showing in the Object Strip (still a real object on the page) but never gets a drag handle and can never have anything dropped past its fixed boundary position, matching that it was never independently reorderable before either. Verified via a new Playwright suite (`unified_layer_order_test.js`, scratch-only) against a real Cover-role page (real Scene blueprint decorations + Stickers, not a synthetic stand-in): natural order matches the exact old fixed sequence; clicking the Sticker section's real "Front" button moves a lone sticker to the very top of the now-unified order; clicking a Scene decoration's real "Forward" button three times moves it past two Stickers in that same order (the literal cross-mechanism reorder that was previously impossible); a real `dragstart`/`dragover`/`drop` sequence dispatched on actual Object Strip card DOM elements changes the persisted `layerOrder` to match the drop position; a synthetic locked World-owned object is confirmed absent from `getReorderableIds()`. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (20 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/sceneEngine.js`, `js/cardDesigner.js`, `js/objectStrip.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Unified Layer Ordering — Moveable World-Owned Shapes Join a Reorderable Group Too (a real, same-day follow-up: "ok so to test do i need to reauthor or just refresh the creator" led directly to a live repro screenshot of a real "My shapes" World — Background/Builder Ba…/First BG/Apple — where "reordering in object strip not happening." **Root cause, confirmed not assumed**: on that exact page, Builder Ba… and First BG are both moveable, non-overlay ('slide'-scoped) World-owned Decoration Shapes — the previous entry's own disclosed scope cut excluded ALL World-owned objects from the reorderable group, so with only the Apple sticker actually draggable and nothing else wired for drag/drop at all, dropping it anywhere was structurally a no-op; there was nothing else to combine it with. **Fix, deliberately narrower than the full cross-bucket generalization** (an `AskUserQuestion` call failed with the same transient `AbortError` seen earlier this session; proceeded with the lower-risk "Recommended" default rather than block on it, disclosed here rather than silently decided): a `moveable:true` Layer Pack object now joins a reorderable group of its own — but strictly WITHIN its own draw bucket, never crossing into another. Three buckets always draw in this fixed relative order: "earlier" (non-overlay World objects), "story" (the Scene-element/Sticker interleaved pass from the entry above), and "overlay" (overlay-scoped World objects). Two objects sharing a bucket (Builder Ba… and First BG, both 'earlier') can now be freely reordered relative to each other — exactly as safe as the Scene/Sticker merge, since only which one draws first within the one shared `_renderLayers` call changes; crossing a bucket boundary (a Shape moving in front of the Apple sticker) is still NOT attempted — that remains the deferred, bigger two-pass-drawing change. New `_applyOrderOverride(natural,order)` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) is the one resolution step both the Story bucket and the two World buckets now share, applied against the SAME page-wide `layerOrder` array — ids are unique across buckets, so a foreign id sitting in the override is simply invisible to a bucket that doesn't contain it, keeping the three buckets from ever interfering with each other despite sharing one list. `getReorderableIds(s)` now returns the union of all three buckets' current (already-resolved, not just natural) ids — a real bug caught and fixed mid-implementation via the test below: the first pass left `getReorderableIds`'s World-bucket helper reading only the natural push order, never applying the override, so a just-completed reorder would silently not show up on the next query even though `render()`'s own paint order was already correct; fixed by extracting one shared `_worldBucketOrder(s,wantOverlay)` that both `render()`'s bucket-splitting step and `getReorderableIds()` call, so both always agree. New `SlideRenderer.getReorderBucket(s,id)` reports which of the three buckets an id currently belongs to (`'story'`/`'earlier'`/`'overlay'`/`null`); `js/objectStrip.js`'s drag handler (`_sameReorderBucket`) uses it to refuse a cross-bucket drop outright — no drop-indicator line, no reorder — rather than silently accepting a drag that looked like it worked but moved nothing on the canvas. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`world_shape_reorder_test.js`, scratch-only) rebuilding the exact reported page shape (two moveable non-overlay Decoration Shapes + one Sticker): both Shapes are confirmed reorderable and share the `'earlier'` bucket; exactly 3 real draggable cards appear (2 Shapes + 1 Sticker, the synthetic Background/Artwork-Place cards correctly excluded); a real `dragstart`/`dragover`/`drop` sequence dragging one Shape onto the other actually swaps their resolved draw order; a same-sequence drag of the Sticker onto a Shape (different buckets) is correctly refused — `dragover` never calls `preventDefault()`, no drop-indicator class appears, and the Shape order is unchanged afterward. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (19 scripts, including the immediately-prior `unified_layer_order_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js` and `js/objectStrip.js`. A locked World object's own relative position among its bucket-mates can shift slightly alongside a freshly-reordered moveable sibling — it's simply never listed in the shared override, so it's always appended after every explicitly-reordered id (the same "last listed sits on top" convention the Story bucket's Sticker-append-on-top behaviour already established) — a disclosed, minor nuance, not a functional regression, since a locked object was never independently reorderable to begin with.)

- Unified Layer Ordering — Full Merge When There's No Frame/Holder Pipeline (a real, same-day follow-up: the previous entry's "own draw bucket" fix left a live "My shapes" World still broken — a screenshot showed the Sticker's Card Designer Order buttons still doing nothing, Object Strip drag still not reordering, and "I was able to move the builder background but not the shape (First BG)." **Root cause, confirmed via a direct diagnostic, not assumed**: `convergeSceneLayer`'s bucket-assignment heuristic (`isFullBleed`, `rect.w>=0.98 && rect.h>=0.98`) is designed for an unrelated concern (Hosted-by-Scene wall-level vs. foreground content) — a realistically-authored Shape with even a small margin (e.g. `rect:{x:0.08,y:0.08,w:0.84,h:0.84}`, matching the visible brown border around First BG in the user's own screenshot) lands in `'overlay'`, while a true full-bleed background lands in `'slide'` — two DIFFERENT buckets under the previous fix's scoping, so Builder Ba… and First BG could never be dragged onto each other, and the lone Sticker (in the separate `'story'` bucket) could never move relative to either. All three complaints traced to this one cause: on a page with no picture Frame at all, nearly every real object a Theme Author places ends up artificially split across these three buckets by an unrelated heuristic. **Fix**: investigated whether full interleaving is actually safe here and found it is, for exactly this page shape — a Scene explicitly converged with zero Places (`_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0`) or a Quote composition never runs the Frame/Panel drawing branch at all, so the `'frame'`/`'holder'`/`'element'` Layer Pack targets are never touched in that code path (their own `_renderLayers` calls live inside the branch that's skipped) — meaning 'slide' and 'overlay' Layer Pack objects and every Scene element/Sticker are the ONLY things such a page ever draws, with nothing else whose draw-order depends on Frame/Panel geometry. New `_noFramePipeline` flag (`(_composition==='quote')||(_activeLayoutHolders(s)===0)`, computed once early in `render()`) switches the whole pipeline into a genuinely merged mode for exactly this case: the previously-unconditional bulk `_renderLayers(_layerPack,'slide',...)` call (drawn before the composition branch) and `_renderLayers(_layerPack,'overlay',...)` call (drawn after Scene+Sticker) are both skipped, and instead every 'slide'/'overlay' Layer Pack entry is combined with the Scene-element/Sticker natural order into ONE list, resolved via the same `_applyOrderOverride(natural,layerOrder)` mechanism the Story bucket already used, and drawn in that single resolved order via a new `LayerEngine.renderOne(layer,rect,helpers)` (extracted from `render()`'s existing per-layer body, reused by both the bulk and the new per-layer call sites — never a second drawing implementation) exposed as `_renderOneLayer(layer,rect,s,target)` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`. Each drawn Layer Pack entry is popped straight out of the shared `_layerObjectBboxes` accumulator into `_lastSceneElements` at its correct interleaved position (rather than the old end-of-pass bulk fold, which is now correctly a no-op for these pages since nothing populates `_layerObjectBboxes` for `'frame'`/`'holder'`/`'element'` in this path). A page WITH a real Frame/Holder (Museum Gallery and every other existing theme) is completely untouched — `_noFramePipeline` is false there, so the exact previously-shipped 3-bucket behaviour runs unchanged, byte-identical. New `_lastRenderWasMerged` flag + `_mergedReorderableIds()` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) tell `getReorderableIds(s)`/`getReorderBucket(s,id)` that a merged-pass page has exactly ONE reorderable group (bucket name `'merged'`) read directly off `_lastSceneElements`'s own already-resolved order, rather than the old per-target `_layerObjectBboxes` scan (which would now find nothing, since every merged-pass entry is popped out immediately) — a real bug caught and fixed mid-implementation by the very first version of the new verification test, which showed the bucket check failing until this was added. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`merged_order_test.js`, scratch-only) rebuilding the exact reported page (a full-bleed 'slide' background, a margin-inset shape that genuinely converges to 'overlay', and a Sticker, all on a zero-Holder Layout): all three objects now share one `'merged'` bucket and all three ids are reorderable; the Sticker's real Card Designer "Back" button now moves it behind BOTH shapes (previously impossible, since it was alone in the old 'story' bucket); a real Object Strip drag of First BG onto Builder Background actually swaps their resolved order; a direct pixel sample at the canvas center confirms the real PAINT order changed (not just id bookkeeping) — the sampled colour matches Builder Background's `#3B2A1E` after the reorder, not First BG's `#E0A526`. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (21 scripts, including both prior Unified-Layer-Ordering tests) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — the fix is confined to `js/layerEngine.js` (new `renderOne`, `render()` refactored to call it) and `renderer/slideRenderer.js` (`_noFramePipeline`, the merged draw pass, `_lastRenderWasMerged`/`_mergedReorderableIds`); no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change. Crossing into a page that DOES have a real picture Frame/Holder remains the one still-deferred piece — reordering a 'slide'/'overlay' World object relative to Frame/Panel-interleaved content there would need the Frame/Panel drawing branch itself restructured, a materially bigger change intentionally left out of this pass.)

- Object Strip Becomes the ONE Reorder Control — Card Designer Buttons Removed + Lock Badge Added (direct product feedback after trying the shipped Object Strip drag-to-reorder: "i like the reordering function in object strip. 2 recommendations. 1st remove any reordering function from the right panel. 2nd for an object which cannot be reordered, put a lock or some kind of information show." **Recommendation 1**: Card Designer's Sticker/Frame/Decoration sections each still carried the pre-Object-Strip "Order" button row (Back/Backward/Forward/Front for Sticker, Backward/Forward for Frame/Decoration) — a second, now-redundant way to do the same thing the Object Strip's drag already does better, and a real UX inconsistency once both existed side by side. Removed all three button rows outright from `js/cardDesigner.js`, along with the shared `_reorderSelected(edge, commitFn)` helper they called (now genuinely dead code, not left orphaned) and `_frameAdjustZ` (Frame's own thin wrapper around it); `SlideRenderer.getReorderableIds()`/`SceneEngine.setLayerOrder()` — the actual mechanism — are completely unchanged, since the Object Strip's drag handler already reads/writes them directly. Also removed the now-unused `.sticker-layer-row`/`.sticker-layer-btn`/`.sticker-layer-glyph`, `.frame-layer-row`/`.frame-layer-btn`/`.frame-layer-glyph`, and `.decoration-layer-row`/`.decoration-layer-btn`/`.decoration-layer-glyph` CSS from `css/style.css` (careful to only strip the `-layer-` selectors out of combined rules like `.sticker-flip-row, .sticker-layer-row{...}`, leaving the still-used Flip Left↔Right/Up↔Down button styling completely untouched). **Recommendation 2**: a real object (has its own render-tree id) that ISN'T in the current reorderable set — a locked/non-`moveable` World-owned Layer Pack object — now gets a small 🔒 badge on its Object Strip thumbnail (`js/objectStrip.js`'s `_card()`, new `.object-card-lock-badge` CSS in `css/style.css`), positioned on the opposite corner from the existing ✏️ edit-capability badge so both can show independently (an object can be editable but not reorderable, or vice versa) — plus a `title="Can't be reordered"` tooltip. Deliberately gated on `opts.id` truthy so the two synthetic Background/Artwork-Place cards (page-level concepts with no real id, never reorderable to begin with) never show it — a lock badge there would answer a question nobody asked. Verified via a new Playwright test (`lock_badge_check.js`, scratch-only): a locked World-owned Shape shows the lock badge, a reorderable Sticker shows none, and the synthetic Background card shows none either. Two existing tests (`unified_layer_order_test.js`, `merged_order_test.js`) had their now-intentionally-broken button-click assertions replaced — one confirms the Order buttons are genuinely gone rather than clicking dead DOM, the other re-proves the exact same cross-mechanism reorder (Sticker moving behind both World Shapes) via a real Object Strip drag instead of a button click, since that's now the only way to do it. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (22 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder/rendering change; the fix is confined to `js/cardDesigner.js`, `js/objectStrip.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Click Empty Space Anywhere in Creator Deselects (direct product feedback: "any click in empty space anywhere in creator should get us out from any selected state. that is if apple is selected right now and i click in empty space in center pane, it should get deselected. this will ensure natural usage tendencies are respected." **Investigation confirmed a genuinely separate gap, not a duplicate of existing logic**: `js/app.js`'s `previewCanvas` `mousedown` handler already deselects when a click lands on empty CANVAS pixels — hit-tests, finds nothing, and clears `_selectedTextElement`/`_selectedSceneElement` — this has existed since before this sprint and needed no change. But `.preview-area` (the center pane) has real, separate clickable DOM space around the canvas itself: the flex gutter `.preview-wrapper` uses to center a fluid-sized canvas (`justify-content:center; align-items:flex-start`), and the Object Strip's own background beneath it — neither ever had a listener, so a click there silently did nothing, exactly the reported symptom. **Fix**: one new `mousedown` listener on `.preview-area` (`js/app.js`), guarded by `e.target.closest('#previewCanvas, .object-card')` so it never fires for a click the canvas's own hit-testing already handles, or for an Object Strip card click (which already selects/deselects via its own `onClick` routing into `PageRuntime.selectSceneObject`/`selectTextObject`/`clearSelection`) — only a genuine empty-background click reaches it, clearing both selection channels the same way the canvas's own fallback does. Verified via a new Playwright test (`deselect_empty_space_test.js`, scratch-only): a selected sticker is confirmed deselected by a real `page.mouse.click()` landing inside `.preview-area`'s bounding rect but outside `#previewCanvas`'s; a subsequent Object Strip card click ("Background") is confirmed to still work correctly and is unaffected by the new listener. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (22 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder/rendering change; the fix is confined to `js/app.js`. See `docs/CREATOR_PAGE_RUNTIME.md` §5's new "Deselect on empty-space click" subsection for the full account.)

- "Change Look" Left Stale Object Strip Content From the Previous Scene (a real, user-reported bug found authoring a real Landscape "Dual Holder" Scene in World Builder v2's test theme: after switching this page's Page Style to it via the Context Panel's "Change Look" shortcut, Creator showed the page as if it still had the PREVIOUS Scene's content — a Decoration Shape ("First BG") that belonged to an entirely different, zero-Holder Scene bled onto the newly-selected page, and "Artwork Place" (which should appear once the new Scene's Holder count is non-zero) was missing. **Root cause, confirmed via a real headless-Build + real-import reproduction, not guessed**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide()` (the function "Change Look" calls) correctly updates `slide.metadata.layout` to the new Representation's Layout id, and correctly called `window.redrawPreview()` — so the CANVAS pixels were, confirmed via pixel-sampling both before and after this fix, already rendering the right geometry (the correct landscape-shaped picture area, the correct wall tone) even in the buggy version. But it predates the Creator Page Runtime Sprint's `PageRuntime.notify()` dispatch (`redrawPreview`+`CardDesigner.refresh`+`ContextPanel.refresh`+`ObjectStrip.refresh`) and had never been updated to use it — it only ever called `redrawPreview`/`renderList`/`ContextPanel.refresh` directly, missing `ObjectStrip.refresh()` entirely, so Object Strip kept showing whatever Layer Pack objects the PREVIOUS Representation's Scene had converged, stale, until some unrelated action happened to trigger a refresh. **Fix**: `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide()` now calls `PageRuntime.notify()` (falling back to the original three calls plus the previously-missing `ObjectStrip.refresh()` if `PageRuntime` isn't loaded for some reason) — the same one dispatch every other selection/page-change path in Creator already routes through. **Two things investigated and confirmed NOT to be bugs, disclosed rather than silently "fixed"**: (1) the whole page canvas staying portrait-shaped (1080×1350) regardless of a Scene's authored Aspect Ratio is Engine V1's known, disclosed, structural canvas-model limitation (`docs/ENGINE_V2_PROMOTION_STRATEGY.md`'s own finding — "Engine V2 uses a genuinely different canvas model... Engine V1's always-fixed 1080×1350 logical canvas") — the picture FRAME area inside that fixed page correctly resolves to the Scene's own aspect (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveLayout`/`LAYOUT_RECT`, confirmed via pixel-sampling to already produce the exact landscape rect `{x:70,y:340,w:940,h:610}`), it's only the outer page shape that stays fixed; (2) the wall-tone colour filling the ENTIRE page behind a smaller picture placeholder is Sprint 9.7's own deliberate "wall-level" design (`_resolveWallTone`, resolved independently of the image-gated Picture Border pipeline, a gallery-room-paint concept distinct from the picture area itself) — not a rendering bug, confirmed identical before and after this fix. **A separate, disclosed, structural platform ceiling, not touched this session**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScene()` only ever converges the Scene's FIRST Place's Frame reference onto the compiled Representation's `defaultFrame` (its own code comment: "Engine V1 has exactly one Holder per page... a pre-existing, disclosed ceiling this sprint does not lift") — a Dual/Triple/Grid Holder Scene authored in Builder can only ever offer ONE artwork upload area in Creator, no matter how many Places exist; the `holders` count on the compiled Layout is used only to gate whether that one Artwork Place card/placeholder shows at all (zero vs. non-zero), never to render multiple independent picture regions. Lifting this would mean extending Engine V1's whole Representation/Holder model from one to many — a real architecture change requiring its own explicit approval, not something to attempt as a side effect of this bug fix. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`dual_holder_repro2.js`, scratch-only) building a real two-Scene World (a zero-Holder "First" Scene with a Decoration Shape, a Landscape "Dual Holder" "second" Scene with a Frame assigned to both Places) through the real `ProjectCompiler`, importing the real compiled package, and driving the real "Change Look" UI flow: before the fix, Object Strip showed `["Background","Background","First BG"]` (stale) after switching to "second"; after, it correctly shows `["Background","Artwork Place"]`. A companion pixel-sampling check (`git stash`-based A/B) confirmed the canvas geometry/wall-tone rendering was correct in both the buggy and fixed versions, isolating this fix to the Object Strip staleness alone. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (22 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder/rendering change; the fix is confined to one function in `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- Multiple Artwork Places Per Page (lifts the exact platform ceiling the entry directly above disclosed and deliberately did not touch: "than lets support as many holders as many authored by builder," approved via Plan Mode since this genuinely changes the core picture data model, rendering, hit-testing, Object Strip, and Context Panel/Card Designer. Until now, `renderer/slideRenderer.js` only ever resolved ONE picture area per page (`_panelRectFor(s)`) no matter how many Places (Builder's own "Holder" concept, renamed in Builder V3) a Theme Author built in World Builder v2 — a "Dual Holder" Scene compiled and rendered exactly like a single-Holder one, missing its second artwork area entirely. **Compile-time** (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScene()`): a new, purely additive `placeRects` array rides alongside the existing (unchanged) `holders` count and `representation.defaultFrame` — one entry per compiled Holder, carrying its own `id`/`name`/`position`/`size`/`shape`/`padding`/`fit`/`frame` (Frame Variation reference) exactly as Builder authored it; absent on every pre-existing compiled Layout (including Museum Gallery, which isn't Scene-authored at all) and on any `tools/world-builder/` (v1) output, which is deliberately left untouched. **Runtime** (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`): `_activeLayoutPlaces(s)` reads it (or returns `null`); `_placePixelRectFor(panelRect,place)` maps a Place's fractional rect onto the resolved panel rect; `_resolveBorder`/`_cardArtworkOverride`/`_resolveArtworkFields`/`_drawImage` all gained an *optional* trailing `placeId` parameter — omitted, every one of them is byte-identical to before this feature (Place 1's legacy `s.image`/`cardOverrides.image/.border/.artwork` fields, untouched); a real id resolves that Place's own storage instead. **The two-id-space design, deliberately kept separate**: a compiled Place carries its own Builder-authored id (e.g. `holder-2`); Creator mints its own, distinct SELECTION id (`'image-holder'` for Place 1, `'image-place-2'`/`'image-place-3'`/... by array position for the rest) — the key into `slide.metadata.placeContent[id]`/`slide._placeImages[id]` — never the Builder id, since a real Theme Author could rename/reorder Places between Builder sessions and Creator's own storage must stay stable against Creator's OWN position-based addressing, not Builder's internal ids; `_placeByExternalId`/`_placeIndexForId` translate one to the other. **A real correctness question resolved deliberately mid-implementation, not left arbitrary**: should Place 1 itself be subdivided by its own authored fraction once 2+ Places exist, or always stay at the full panel rect regardless? Keeping it always full-panel (the naive "byte-identical, no exceptions" reading) would make Place 1 draw across the ENTIRE panel while Place 2+ occupy fractional sub-rects beside it — visibly overlapping, defeating the entire point of a Dual-Holder layout; caught via direct pixel-sampling during verification (Place 1's sampled colour read as a wall-tone blend, not its own picture, because it was drawing full-bleed underneath Place 2's smaller inset rect).
