Resolved as: Place 1 stays at the full, untouched panel rect ONLY when 0 or 1 Places are authored (every existing theme, and a theme rebuilt post-feature with exactly one Place — a lone Place's own Builder-authored fraction has no reliable 1:1 correspondence to Engine V1's already-caption-aware panel rect, so it's deliberately not applied there); once 2+ Places are authored, Place 1 is subdivided by its own fraction exactly like every other Place, so a Dual Holder layout genuinely renders two side-by-side, non-overlapping picture areas as Builder intended. `getPlaceRects(s)` (the one function Object Strip/hit-testing/pixel-verification all consume) mirrors this exact same conditional so it always reports precisely what `render()` actually draws. **Per-Place storage**: `slide.metadata.placeContent[placeId]={dataURL,imageView,cardOverrides:{artwork,border}}` for every Place beyond the first (the identical shape `cardOverrides.image/.border/.artwork` already use, just relocated) — needs no `serialize()` change (already a wholesale `metadata` copy); `slide._placeImages[placeId]=<Image>` is the sibling runtime-only cache to today's `slide.image`, rehydrated by a new async loop in `ProjectManager.deserialize()` parallel to its existing `loadImageFromDataURL(p.image)` call. `js/pageOps.js`'s `duplicatePage()` gained one line copying `_placeImages` alongside its existing `image`/`metadata` copy. **Selection/hit-testing** (`js/app.js`): a new `_hitTestPlace`/`_placeImageFor` pair loops `SlideRenderer.getPlaceRects(s)` for the mousedown picture-pan gesture and cursor-hover check — index 0 keeps its exact existing id/behaviour, index ≥1 gets its own id and its own pan/zoom state, reading/writing that Place's own storage; selection `type` stays uniformly `'image-holder'` for every Place (only `id` varies) so Context Panel's existing dispatch needed zero changes to its own routing logic. `js/pageRuntime.js`'s `selectionIsValid()` generalized from an exact `'image-holder'` string match to also accept any `'image-place-N'` id. **Object Strip** (`js/objectStrip.js`): one card per Place — Place 1 keeps its exact existing "Artwork"/"Artwork Place" wording; extra Places show the Builder-authored Place `name` (e.g. "Place 2") or fall back to "Artwork Place N". **Context Panel + Card Designer**: `_currentPlaceId()` (undefined for Place 1, the id string otherwise) threads through `_applyImageResult`/`_replaceArtwork`/`_cropRotateArtwork` and through `_ensureView`/`_setMode`/`_setScale`/`_setImageProp`/the offset sliders/every reset, so Fit/Fill/Original + Bigger↔Smaller/Move controls edit exactly the selected Place and never bleed into another. **Deliberately scoped, disclosed limitations, not silently expanded**: `tools/world-builder/` (v1) is untouched — this is `tools/world-builder-v2/`-only, matching where all new Builder capability has landed this session; `js/pageDesigner.js`'s own older, largely-superseded per-role Image manager stays Place-1-only (Context Panel already covers every role's Replace/Crop/Frame needs); only Place 1 gets composition-aware caption placement (`_captionRectFor`'s `'right'`/Wide-layout behaviour) and only Place 1 renders `'frame'/'holder'/'element'`-scoped Layer Pack content (Museum Caption/Wax Seal-style entries) — extra Places never get a caption or Layer Pack content, since Builder V2's own compiled Scene Layers never target those three scopes anyway (confirmed: always `'slide'`/`'overlay'`), so this is a narrow, pre-existing non-gap, not a regression; Frame Look/Frame Style/Artwork Presentation's `WorkspaceBuilder`-driven theme controls stay Place-1-only for now, a disclosed, bounded follow-up. WYSIWYE holds for free — Thumbnail/Publish Studio/PDF export/Story Destinations all resolve through the identical `SlideRenderer.buildPayload`+`.render()` pair the editor canvas uses, so every Place renders correctly on every surface with zero code changes there; `buildPayload()` gained one line forwarding `slide._placeImages` onto the payload as `placeImages`. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright test (`multi_place_test.js`, scratch-only): built a real Dual Holder Scene with two DIFFERENT Frame Variations (distinct border colours) through the real `ProjectCompiler`, imported the compiled package into real Studio, and drove the real Change-Look UI to switch onto it — confirmed both Places render at pixel-distinct, non-overlapping rects with their own distinct picture colours AND distinct frame border colours (pixel-sampled, not merely inspected); Object Strip shows exactly 2 independently-selectable Place cards; Card Designer's Fit-mode toggle edits only the selected Place; a full `serialize()`→`deserialize()` round trip and a `PageOps.duplicatePage()` both carry every Place's picture over correctly; and the theme's OTHER, single-Place "first" Scene — captured before any multi-Place switching ever happens on that session — still resolves `holderCount===1`/`placeRectCount===1`, confirming zero behaviour change for the single-Place case. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (23 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Scene Viewport — the Page Itself Honours a Scene's Aspect Ratio (a direct, explicit follow-up: after shipping Multiple Artwork Places Per Page, the user confirmed the "portrait page shape" limitation that entry's own investigation had disclosed and deliberately left untouched was itself the next thing to fix — "we need to honour the commitments of builder." Until now, `renderer/slideRenderer.js` drew every page onto a fixed, module-level 1080×1350 logical canvas no matter what Aspect Ratio a Scene declared — a Layout's resolved aspect only changed the *inner* picture-panel rect's shape, never the outer page/canvas shape itself (`getCanvasSize()` always returned `{w:1080,h:1350}`). Planned via Plan Mode as a genuine architecture change (touches rendering, hit-testing, thumbnails, CSS); scope narrowed to **editor/page canvas shape only** after an `AskUserQuestion` call failed with a transient tool error twice — proceeded with the lower-risk default per this project's own established precedent, disclosing it rather than blocking: Publish/Export (`js/storyDestinations.js`/`js/publishStudio.js`/`js/pdfWriter.js`) keep their own fixed destination formats (Instagram Portrait/Square, PDF) completely unchanged, since those are a deliberate, separate destination-format menu — zero edits to those three files. **A real naming-forward-compatibility note, raised directly by the user before implementation began**: rather than name the new machinery around "canvas size"/"aspect ratio" specifically, every new construct is named around a general **Scene Viewport** concept — the resolved on-screen area a Slide's own content actually occupies — so this stays compatible with whatever a future generalized presentation-surface investigation lands on, without this vocabulary needing to change again; the pre-existing public `getCanvasSize(s)` keeps its exact name/signature (real callers in `js/app.js`/`js/thumbnails.js` today) but is now a thin wrapper over the new `_sceneViewportFor(s)` resolver. **Design**: a new `SCENE_VIEWPORT_BY_ASPECT` table (mirroring World Builder v2's own real `ASPECT_RATIOS` pixel values from `engineSchema.js` — `landscape:1350×1080`, `wide:1600×900`, `'full-bleed':1080×1920`, `portrait`/`quote` unchanged at `1080×1350`) resolves through the same `_resolvedAspectKey(s)` helper `_resolveLayout` already uses internally (extracted so the two tables can never disagree on a slide's aspect), explicitly gated on `SceneEngine.getRenderData(s)!==null` — Cover/Hook/End Scene-blueprint pages always get the portrait default regardless of what the active theme's own Layouts contain, a stronger guard than merely checking `slide.metadata.layout` is unset, since `_resolveLayout` was already found (during investigation) to silently fall back to the theme's `layouts[0]` for these pages too. Module-level `_viewportW`/`_viewportH` replace the old fixed `W`/`H` constants throughout the ~28 drawing-code call sites that referenced them (background fill, Layer Pack full-slide rects, safe-area guide, story-text centering, `_drawHandle`/`_drawFooter`/`_drawPageNumber` anchors); two sites needed more than a rename — `STORY_MAX_WIDTH` moved from a module-parse-time constant (which would have permanently cached the very first viewport ever seen) to a value computed fresh inside `_drawStoryText` on every call, and `_drawFooter`/`_drawPageNumber`'s baked-in bottom-anchor literals (`1285`, `1325`, `900`) were converted to their real `_viewportH-65`/`_viewportH-25`/`_viewportW-180` relationships so they scale correctly on a non-portrait page instead of anchoring to the old fixed page height/width. `init(cv,opts)`/`render(s)` cooperate via a new per-canvas-element sticky flag (`cv.__vihuAdaptiveViewport`, set only by `opts.adaptiveViewport`) rather than any new shared module state or call-site parameter: only `js/app.js`'s boot-time `SlideRenderer.init(previewCanvas,{adaptiveViewport:true})` and (see below) `js/thumbnails.js`'s own temp canvas ever opt in; every one of Publish's own throwaway export canvases (`js/storyDestinations.js`, `js/publishStudio.js`) never passes this option and their own canvas elements never carry a prior stamp, so `render()`'s new resize branch is never entered for them — **zero code changes needed in those files**, confirmed by tracing every `init()`/`render()` call site in each before implementation. `LAYOUT_RECT`'s `landscape` entry was re-authored to fit sensibly inside its own now-genuinely-wide 1350×1080 canvas (previously just a narrow placement rect inside an always-portrait page); a real, previously-dormant discrepancy was also fixed while touching this table — `LAYOUT_RECT['full-bleed']` had been authored assuming a portrait-shaped canvas (`{0,0,1080,1350}`) though World Builder's own `full-bleed` aspect is actually 1080×1920, a landmine no live theme had ever reached (Museum Gallery is explicitly trimmed to Landscape/Portrait/Quote only) — corrected to match. **A real bug found and fixed while wiring `js/thumbnails.js`, not assumed away**: the plan's original intent ("thumbnails.js already presizes manually, no opt-in flag needed") turned out to be wrong once traced through `init()`'s actual mechanics — `init()` has *always* unconditionally reset the canvas's backing-store size to the current default the instant it's called, regardless of whatever a caller manually presized the element to immediately beforehand (true in the original code too, just invisible there since `getCanvasSize()` with no argument was always the same fixed value anyway) — so a literal reading of the plan would have had `init()` silently clobber `thumbnails.js`'s own manual presize back to portrait on every call. Fixed by having `js/thumbnails.js`'s temp canvas *also* opt into `adaptiveViewport`, letting `render()`'s own resolution step size it correctly instead, exactly mirroring the live editor canvas's own mechanism — the downstream thumbnail-downscale math (already reading `temp.width`/`temp.height` *after* render, not before) needed no further change. Also added one small, self-contained `MutationObserver` in `js/app.js` (watching `.publish-studio-modal`'s `class` attribute) to resync the live editor canvas the instant Publish Studio's modal actually closes — a real gap found during investigation: Publish's own internal `init(editorCanvas)` "restore" call, made mid-export-loop, resets the canvas without ever re-rendering it, so a Scene-Viewport-resized live canvas could otherwise show a stretched/cropped page until the user's next unrelated interaction. **Backward compatibility, verified not merely asserted**: every existing `getCanvasSize()` caller (no argument) gets the byte-identical `{w:1080,h:1350}`; every theme with no `layouts`, and every Cover/Hook/End page regardless of theme, resolves to the portrait default; every existing `init(cv)`/`init(cv,{dpr:...})` call site in the three untouched Publish files resets to the exact canonical size it always has, since none of them ever pass `adaptiveViewport` and none of their (always brand-new) canvas elements ever carry a prior stamp. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright test (`scene_viewport_test.js`, scratch-only): built a real Landscape Dual Holder Scene through the real `ProjectCompiler`, imported the compiled package into real Studio, and confirmed the live `previewCanvas` genuinely resizes to 1350×1080 (not just an inner rect) with the correct inline `style.aspectRatio` set; both authored Places render at pixel-distinct, non-overlapping rects within the new wide canvas; a synthetic Cover-role page (real `SceneEngine` blueprint + `metadata.scene`) stays fixed at 1080×1350 regardless of the active theme's own Layouts; and switching back to the theme's other, single-Place portrait Scene reverts the canvas to exactly 1080×1350. **A real, pre-existing test-fixture bug was found and fixed in the same pass, not a product regression**: re-running the full existing regression suite surfaced `multi_place_test.js` failing — traced to that script's own pixel-sampler hardcoding `canvas.width/1080`/`canvas.height/1350` as its DPR-scale-factor divisor, an assumption that quietly broke now that a landscape page's logical size is genuinely 1350×1080; fixed by having it read `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize(slide)` dynamically instead, the same pattern `scene_viewport_test.js` already used correctly. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (24 scripts, including the corrected `multi_place_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/app.js`, and `js/thumbnails.js`.)

- Frame Look / Frame Style / Frame Variation Now Respect the Selected Place (a real, user-reported bug found hands-on testing the Multiple Artwork Places Per Page feature: "i selected first place and tried to give it round frame it was success. i selected second place tried to give it poloroid frame it applied to first place." This was the exact, disclosed scope gap that feature's own ship note named and deliberately deferred — "Frame Look/Frame Style/Artwork Presentation's `WorkspaceBuilder`-driven theme controls stay Place-1-only for now, a disclosed, bounded follow-up" — now closed. **Root cause confirmed by reading both sides of the pipeline**: the RENDER side (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveBorder`/`_cardArtworkOverride`/`_resolveArtworkFields`) already fully supported a per-Place border/artwork override at `slide.metadata.placeContent[placeId].cardOverrides.border`/`.artwork`, built for this feature from day one — but the WRITE side never used it: `js/cardDesigner.js`'s Frame Look preset buttons (`_applyFrameDesign`, e.g. Rounded/Polaroid) and every Frame Style slider/chip/toggle (`_ensureBorder`/`_readBorder`/`_pruneBorder`/`_commitBorder`/`_resetBorder`) always read/wrote the page-level `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.border` regardless of which Place was actually selected, and `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s Artwork Presentation controls (Frame Variation swatches, Presentation/Frame/Lighting/Caption/Paper/Mat dropdowns, all built on `_ensureArtwork`/`_readArtwork`) had the identical gap against `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork` — so no matter which Place was selected on screen, every one of these controls always edited Place 1's storage, and the renderer then correctly-but-misleadingly painted whatever Place 1 now held. **Fix, mirroring the exact `_ensureView`/`_readView` per-Place convention `js/cardDesigner.js`'s own Fit/Fill/Scale/Offset controls already used successfully**: `_ensureBorder`/`_readBorder`/`_pruneBorder`/`_resetBorder`/`_applyFrameDesign` all gained an optional `placeId` parameter — omitted (Place 1) is byte-identical to before; a real id reads/writes that Place's own bag under `slide.metadata.placeContent[placeId].cardOverrides.border` instead, reusing the pre-existing `_placeViewBag` helper. `_commitBorder`/`_refreshBorder` now resolve `_currentPlaceId()` themselves, and `_refreshBorder`'s `hasImage` gate was corrected to check the SELECTED Place's own picture (mirroring `_refreshImage`'s already-correct per-Place `hasImage` logic) rather than always Place 1's `s.image`. `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s `_ensureArtwork`/`_readArtwork` gained the identical optional `placeId` parameter, and `_buildSelectRow`/`_buildSwatchRow`'s default get/set now read it off a new `ctx.getPlaceId` callback (mirroring the existing `ctx.getSlide`/`ctx.onChange` convention) rather than hardcoding Place 1 — every one of `js/cardDesigner.js`'s four call sites building that `ctx` object (`_buildImageControls`'s initial "Artwork Presentation" build, `_buildBorderControls`'s initial "Frame Style" build, and both rebuilt in `_refreshFrameWorkspace` on every refresh) now passes `getPlaceId:_currentPlaceId` alongside. A control whose data doesn't live in the artwork bag (Layout, via its own explicit `store` override) is unaffected, since `store.get`/`store.set` bypass the default entirely. Verified via a new Playwright test (`frame_look_place_test.js`, scratch-only) reproducing the exact reported sequence end-to-end against a real Dual Holder Scene built through the real `ProjectCompiler` and imported into real Studio: selecting Place 1 and applying "Rounded" lands only on Place 1; selecting Place 2 and applying "Polaroid" lands only on Place 2 while Place 1's own Rounded design is confirmed unchanged (the exact bug scenario, now passing); a Frame Style slider (Round Corners) edits only the selected Place, with re-selecting Place 1 afterward confirming its own panel shows its own stored value, never Place 2's just-applied one. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (24 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `js/cardDesigner.js` and `js/workspaceBuilder.js`.)

- Frame Variation Seeding Now Re-Seeds Correctly on Every Representation Switch (a second, real, user-reported bug found in the same "authored two Frames" testing pass: "when i authored in builder i gave white and red borders to each frame ... it did not come to the creator." Investigated by reproducing the exact scenario rather than guessing — a Dual-Holder Scene's two Places DID both resolve correctly (confirmed via pixel-sampling: a genuinely white border is simply invisible against the near-white default wall/mat tone, not a bug), but the real defect surfaced in the OTHER common authoring shape: two separate single-Place Scenes/Representations, each with its own distinct Frame (white / red), switched between via "Change Look." **Root cause**: `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_seedDefaultFrameVariation()` writes a Representation's authored `defaultFrame` onto the page's `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation` — but only the FIRST time, guarded by `if(slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation) return; // never clobber a Story Author's own choice`. That guard can't tell an auto-seeded value apart from a genuine Story Author pick in Card Designer — both are just a plain string — so once the FIRST Representation ever seen had seeded its own Frame, every LATER Representation's own distinct Frame became permanently unreachable: the border stayed stuck on whichever Scene was seen first, exactly reading as "the border I gave the second Frame did not come to the Creator." **Fix**: a companion `_seededFrameVariation` field now travels alongside `frameVariation` in the same artwork bag, recording what THIS function itself last wrote; re-seeding is refused only when the current value has drifted from that recorded value — meaning a Story Author genuinely picked something different via Card Designer in between — so switching Representations any number of times correctly re-seeds each one's own Frame, while a real manual pick is still never clobbered. Verified via two new Playwright tests (`frame_color_repro2.js`/`frame_color_repro3.js`, scratch-only): the exact reported white/red two-Representation sequence, confirmed broken before the fix (`frameVariation` stuck on `"classic-white"` after switching to the Red Representation) and fixed after; a three-Representation white→red→blue sequence confirming re-seeding isn't a one-shot fix, with each switch's own border colour pixel-sampled and confirmed correct; and a direct manual-pick-preservation check confirming a genuine Story Author override survives a later Representation switch untouched. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (24 scripts, including the earlier Frame Look/Style per-Place fix's own test) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — the fix is confined to one function in `js/creationFlow.js`, no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change.)

- Scene Compile Order Now Respects "Reorder Scenes" Instead of Raw Creation Order (a real, user-reported bug found from a side-by-side screenshot comparison: the World Builder v2 Scenes Library showed the authored order First → Single Holder → Single Holder → second (the user had drag-reordered "second," originally created early — hence its name — down to the end via "Reorder Scenes"), but Creator's "Choose a Page Style" showed First → second → Single Holder → Single Holder instead, with "second" back in its ORIGINAL creation-order position. **Root cause**: `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`'s `convergeScenes()` iterates `projectLoader.getFilesInFolder('scenes')` directly, and that array is built by `js/projectCompiler.js`'s `loadIntoProjectLoader()` from `Object.keys(project.files)` — plain JS object key insertion order, i.e. the order each Scene file was first CREATED, completely bypassing `project.sceneOrder` (the array "Reorder Scenes"'s drag-and-drop, backed by `ProjectModel.moveScene`, actually writes to, and which `ProjectModel.scenes(project)` already correctly resolves everywhere else in the Builder UI). Since `builder.js`/`projectLoader` only ever see raw file Blobs — never the live `project` object with its own `sceneOrder` — the compiled Representation order silently reverted to creation order the moment a reordered World was Built, independent of anything in the Frame/Frame-Variation fixes shipped earlier this session. **Fix**: `loadIntoProjectLoader()` (the one adapter boundary that DOES still see the full, live `project` object) now re-sorts `folders.scenes` to match `ProjectModel.scenes(project)`'s own authored order immediately after building it from raw paths — a single, additive `.sort()` keyed off each path's own scene id looked up against `ProjectModel.scenes(project).map(s => s.id)`, touching nothing else in the frozen `builder.js` service. Applied identically to both `tools/world-builder-v2/` and its `tools/world-builder/` (v1) twin, which carries the identical `convergeScenes()`/`loadIntoProjectLoader()` code and was found to have the exact same bug. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (scratch-only) creating four Scenes in File-insertion order First/second/Single-Holder/Single-Holder, then calling the real `ProjectModel.moveScene()` (the same function "Reorder Scenes" drag-and-drop calls) to push "second" to the end — confirmed the compiled `theme.representations` order matched raw creation order (bug reproduced) before the fix, and matched the reordered Scenes Library display (First/Single-Holder/Single-Holder/second) after it, for both Builders. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including this session's own Frame Look/Style and Frame Variation reseed fixes, sticker-drag, and Object-Strip-reorder tests) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Scene Model change; the fix is confined to one function in each Builder's `js/projectCompiler.js`.)

- Clicking an Empty Artwork Place Now Selects It Instead of Deselecting Everything (a real, user-reported bug flagged earlier this session and now fixed: "in creator clicks between place 1 and 2 are not being managed properly." **Root cause**: `js/app.js`'s canvas mousedown handler only ever called `_setSelectedSceneElement(_placeHit.id,'image-holder')` *inside* the same `if(_placeHit && _placeImageFor(s,_placeHit.id) && ...)` guard that also starts the image-pan gesture — so selecting a Place was accidentally coupled to that Place already having a picture. Clicking an empty Place's placeholder box fell straight through to the "clicked empty space" branch at the bottom of the handler, which actively **deselected** whatever was selected instead of selecting the empty Place — pre-existing legacy behaviour for Place 1 too (an unfilled Place 1 was equally unclickable before Multiple Places existed), just far more noticeable once a page has several visually-identical empty boxes side by side (exactly the scenario in the user's own screenshots). **Fix**: split "select the Place" from "start a pan gesture" — `_setSelectedSceneElement` now fires for ANY real Place hit-test result, regardless of whether it has a picture yet (Story-role pages have no SceneEngine element for the picture, so this click is the only real target Context Panel/Object Strip can key "Artwork selected"/"Add Artwork" off); the pan gesture itself still only starts once that Place actually has an image to pan, exactly as before. Verified via a new Playwright test (`empty_place_click_test.js`, scratch-only) against a real Dual Holder Scene with NO pictures uploaded at all: clicking empty Place 1's placeholder now correctly selects `image-holder` (was previously a no-op/deselect), clicking empty Place 2's placeholder correctly selects `image-place-2`, Context Panel correctly shows "🖼️ Add Artwork" for the selected empty Place, and clicking genuine empty canvas background still correctly deselects (unaffected). Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (26 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — the fix is confined to one `if` block in `js/app.js`.)

- A Place With No Frame Chosen Now Renders With Zero Chrome, Matching Builder's Own Preview (investigated a real, user-supplied screenshot pair: Builder's Working View showing a nicely-framed artwork placeholder for a Scene with two Places, vs. Creator showing the same Scene as two plain flat white boxes. **Root cause, confirmed via debug instrumentation on a real compiled package, not guessed**: both Places had no Frame Variation assigned (`holder.frame:null`), and `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_resolveArtworkFields`/`_artworkBorder` always fell back to the World's own top-level `presentation:'gallery'` preset's System Default look (white background, white-mat frame, soft shadow, gallery lighting) for ANY un-Framed Place — correct per the Theme Language v2 architecture (Presentation Preset → Theme Overrides → System Defaults, Sprint 9.5), and confirmed to have zero visual effect on Museum Gallery's real, on-disk `.vtheme` (both its Showcase and Portrait Representations set a real `defaultFrame:'classic-white'`, so every real Place there already has explicit chrome; only Quote has `defaultFrame:null`, and Quote's composition skips the Frame/border pipeline entirely regardless) — but confirmed via a direct product decision (asked, not assumed) to be the wrong behaviour for a Place the Theme Author deliberately left un-Framed: "builder preview is correct. creator is wrong," applied "everywhere" per explicit follow-up. **Fix**: `_resolveArtworkFields` now computes one additive flag, `_hasExplicitChrome` — true when a Frame Variation resolves for this Place (`holder.frame`/a Story Author's own per-card pick) OR the Story Author made a manual per-card Presentation override via Card Designer's own Presentation/Frame/Lighting/Composition controls (Sprint 9.4); false when neither is true. `_artworkBorder` returns a genuine zero-chrome object (`fill:'none'`, `lineEnabled:false`, `shadowEnabled:false`, `design:null`, `_artwork:{}` so `_drawArtworkPresentation`'s paper/lighting checks and `_drawArtworkCaption`'s own gate all correctly no-op too) whenever `_hasExplicitChrome` is false, instead of resolving through `ThemePresets.resolveHolder`. `_resolveWallTone` is a deliberately separate resolution path (the gallery wall colour is a Slide-level concept independent of any one Place's own Frame choice, Sprint 9.7) and stays completely unaffected — a Scene's own wall tone/Scene-hosted background now correctly shows THROUGH an un-Framed Place instead of being covered by a fabricated white mat. Verified via Playwright: a real Dual-Holder Scene with a navy Scene-hosted background and no Frame assigned to either Place now shows the navy correctly through both Place areas (previously solid opaque white, confirmed via before/after pixel sampling); Museum Gallery's real `classic-white` Frame Variation still renders its white border chrome pixel-exact, completely unaffected. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (29 scripts) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — the fix is confined to two functions in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, no Theme Contract/Scene Model/Builder change.)

- Zero-Chrome Fix Was Being Defeated By a Dangling Frame Variation Reference (a direct, same-day follow-up: the user reported still seeing solid white Artwork Place boxes on their real "My shapes" World after the fix above shipped — confirmed deployed via the visible build-info footer, ruling out a stale deployment. **Root-caused by walking the user through a live browser-console dump of their real project's `slide.metadata`, not by guessing further**: `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.artwork.frameVariation` was the string `"classic"`, but the active theme's `frameVariations` was `null` — a stale, dangling seed from an earlier Builder state (a Frame the Theme Author has since renamed or removed) that survived on this already-existing Creator project. The previous fix's `_hasExplicitChrome` flag only checked whether *some* `frameVariation` id string was present (`!!frameVariationId`), never whether it actually resolved to a real entry in `theme.frameVariations` — so a dangling reference kept tricking Creator into treating the Place as "explicitly Framed" and falling back to the Presentation Preset's white System Default, exactly reproducing the reported symptom. **Fix**: `_resolveArtworkFields` now tracks whether the Frame Variation lookup genuinely found a matching entry with real `fields` (`frameVariationResolved`) and bases `_hasExplicitChrome` on that instead of the bare id string's truthiness — a stale/unresolvable reference now correctly falls through to zero chrome, matching a Place that never had a Frame Variation at all. Verified by reproducing the user's exact real-project state (a real Build via `ProjectCompiler`, then stripping `frameVariations` off the live theme record and seeding the identical dangling `frameVariation:'classic'` reference onto the slide): Place 1's edge pixel now reads the theme's wall tone (`234,231,226`), not solid white (`255,255,255`). Re-verified the prior fix's own navy Scene-background scenario and Museum Gallery's real `classic-white` Frame Variation are both still correct and unaffected. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — the fix is confined to `_resolveArtworkFields` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`.)

- Real Root Cause Found: Theme Was Applied to the Story Slot, Not the Artwork Slot (the genuine root cause behind the persistent white-box report, found via a live browser-console diagnostic — a temporary `SlideRenderer.debugResolveBorder` export — rather than further speculation. **Root cause**: `AppState.project.artworkTheme` was `null` on the user's real project, even though the Layout/Holder/Place/Frame-Variation geometry rendered correctly. Both are explained by the same fact: the World's theme had been applied into the **Story Theme slot** (`AppState.project.theme`), not the **Artwork Theme slot**. `_resolveBorder`/`_resolveWallTone` required `_artworkTheme(s)` (which only ever reads the Artwork Theme slot) to be non-null, found nothing, and fell straight through to the legacy `_drawPanel(t.panel.color,...)` fallback — painting the Story Theme's plain white/cream panel colour regardless of any earlier fix, since every one of those fixes lived inside the `_artworkTheme(s)` branch that never ran for this project. Layout/Holder/Place geometry rendered correctly anyway because `_activeLayoutHolders`/`_resolveLayout` already resolve through `_layoutTheme(s)`, which tries the Artwork Theme slot first and falls back to the Story Theme slot — exactly the fallback the chrome-resolution functions were missing. **Fix**: `_resolveBorder` (both the per-Place and Place-1 branches) and `_resolveWallTone` now use that same `_layoutTheme(s)` fallback instead of `_artworkTheme(s)` directly — whichever theme actually supplies Layout/Holder/Frame-Variation data now also supplies its own Frame chrome, consistent with what the rest of the Place system already does; for the normal case (a theme correctly applied via the Artwork Theme slot), `_layoutTheme(s)` prefers that real Artwork Theme first, so behaviour is byte-identical to before. Verified via Playwright by reproducing the exact real condition (`AppState.project.artworkTheme` forced `null`, `AppState.project.theme` pointing at the Layout/Holder/Frame-Variation-bearing theme): Place edge pixels now read the wall tone (`234,231,226`), not solid white (`255,255,255`). Re-verified Museum Gallery (correctly applied via the Artwork Theme slot) still renders its `classic-white` Frame Variation pixel-exact and unaffected, plus every prior fix's own reproduction (navy Scene background, dangling Frame Variation reference) still passes. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — the fix is confined to `_resolveBorder`/`_resolveWallTone` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`. The temporary `SlideRenderer.debugResolveBorder` diagnostic export added to chase this down is deliberately left in place as a small, permanent, non-invasive debugging aid rather than removed, since it has no behavioural effect on any real render path.)

- Guardrails — Artwork Places Become Moveable + Fully Reorderable (closes a real Builder-to-Creator wiring gap: World Builder's own per-Place permission block — "Can a Story Author move this?" / "...change this? (its Frame, once populated)" / "...see this at all?" — wrote correctly to `holder.permissions`, but `convergeScene` (`tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/builder.js`) never read it at all when compiling `placeRects`, sitting right next to `convergeSceneLayer`'s own proven `visible`/`moveable`/`editable` derivation for Scene Layers, which does exactly this correctly. **Fix**: `placeRects` now carries `visible`/`moveable`/`editable` per Place, mirroring `convergeSceneLayer`'s exact pattern (absent `permissions` → `true` at compile time, matching what `_ensureHolderDefaults` already stamps onto a live Holder). **Backward-compatible default asymmetry**: Creator's own render-time default for an ALREADY-compiled Layout is the OPPOSITE — absent `moveable`/`editable` → `false`/locked, absent `visible` → `true` — so every theme published before this fix (including Museum Gallery) keeps rendering exactly as before; `SlideRenderer.getPlacePermissions(s,placeId)`/`_resolvePlacePermissions` is the one shared resolver both the render path and Object Strip read, so the two can never disagree. Per the user's own explicit scope choices (confirmed via AskUserQuestion): **(1) a small grab-handle** appears on a selected, moveable Place (`_drawPlaceGrabHandle`/`getPlaceGrabHandleHitbox`) — dragging it writes a new position into the exact same generic `slide.metadata.elementOverrides` bag every other draggable object already uses (`SceneEngine.setPosition`, reused verbatim via `js/app.js`'s existing `_sceneDragState` machinery), completely independent of the pre-existing content-pan gesture (which still pans/zooms the picture itself); `_placePixelRectFor`'s three call sites (`_place1Rect`, the Place-N branch, `getPlaceRects`) all resolve through a new `_applyPlaceMoveOverride` so a moved Place's rect shifts everywhere consistently. **(2) Full cross-object reorder**: every Story-role page now ALWAYS uses the fully-interleaved merged pass (`_naturalStoryOrder`/`_applyOrderOverride`, previously only when `_noFramePipeline` — Quote/zero-Holder) so a Place, a Sticker, and a World-owned `slide`/`overlay` Layer Pack object can all be freely reordered together via Object Strip drag — not just Places among themselves; Cover/Hook/End pages (which never have Places) are completely unaffected, still using the merged pass only when `_noFramePipeline`, exactly as before. `_mergedReorderableIds()` gates a Place's own reorder-membership on its `moveable` flag specifically (unlike a locked Scene element/Sticker, which stays reorderable even while position-frozen) — matching the real bug report's own framing that "move" and "reorder" are the same guardrail for a Place. `js/objectStrip.js`'s Place-card loop gained real `id`/`draggable` wiring reusing the existing `_wireReorderDrag`/lock-badge machinery verbatim, plus a `visible:false` Place skip; a genuine duplicate-card bug (Places now living in the render tree for reorder purposes were ALSO being picked up by Object Strip's separate generic "every other object" loop) was found and fixed by excluding `isPlace`-marked entries there. **Two real, separate bugs found and fixed while verifying, not the feature itself**: (1) `js/app.js`'s `_canvasCoords` called `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize()` with no slide argument, always resolving the portrait default regardless of a page's real Aspect Ratio — every mouse hit-test on a non-portrait Scene was silently computed against the wrong logical size; fixed by passing the current slide through, exactly the same class of fix `js/thumbnails.js` already got in the Scene Viewport sprint. (2) A regression caught by full regression testing before shipping: the first cut of `_naturalStoryOrder`'s Place-inclusion logic required a real, populated `placeRects` array to include ANY Place at all — since every theme compiled before Multiple Artwork Places Per Page (every theme today except a freshly multi-Place-authored one, including Museum Gallery) has no `placeRects` array, this silently dropped Place 1 — and with it, Museum Gallery's own Frame-scoped Wax Seal/Museum Caption Layer Pack content, which only ever draws as part of Place 1's own atomic paint step — from rendering AND from Object Strip entirely; fixed by treating an absent/empty `placeRects` as exactly one implicit Place (`place:null`), matching the identical convention `getPlaceRects`'s own fallback already establishes elsewhere in this file. `_supportsResize`/`getResizeHandlesFor` exclude Places outright (`isPlace`) rather than inheriting the generic 8-corner resize handles a Scene blueprint's own `image-holder` type would otherwise trigger, since no size-override read exists anywhere for Places today and showing them would silently do nothing. `docs/THEME_PROJECT_SPEC.md`'s `placeRects` field table documents the three new fields and the compile/render default asymmetry. Verified via a new 7-assertion Playwright suite (permission resolution including the legacy-absent case; Object Strip lock-badge/draggable state per Place; a moveable Place and a Sticker sharing the same reorder bucket and a real cross-object drag changing their resolved order; grab-handle hitbox gating; a real mouse-driven drag repositioning a Place by the expected canvas-logical delta; a `visible:false` Place skipped from rendering/Object Strip/reorder entirely) plus full regression across the existing 31-script Creator/Builder Playwright suite (one script, `world_shape_reorder_test.js`, had its own bucket assertions intentionally updated — a Sticker and a World-owned Shape on any Story-role page now correctly share one "merged" bucket instead of the narrower "earlier"/"story" split that predates this feature, not a regression) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged, zero console errors.)

- Governing Rules Compliance Pass — Single-Place Geometry + Frame-Editable Guardrail (a direct, evidence-based follow-up to the Guardrails sprint above. After that sprint shipped, the user stated three permanent governing rules for the whole platform: **(1)** "When Scene shows up in Creator it is exactly as it was in Builder." **(2)** "Every object on Scene honors the guardrails." **(3)** "Creator can further refine the objects through options available in the right panel." A requested compliance audit (`three_rules_audit.js`) found two real, confirmed violations, both fixed here; a third check (World-owned Decoration guardrails) confirmed no regression. **Violation 1 (Rule 1)**: a single authored Place (not part of a Dual-Holder layout) had its Builder-authored fractional position/size silently discarded in favour of the full panel rect — a deliberate design decision made mid-implementation during the Multiple Artwork Places Per Page feature, reasoned (at the time) that "a lone authored Place's own fraction has no reliable 1:1 correspondence to Engine V1's already-caption-aware panelRect." Under Rule 1 this reasoning no longer holds — Creator must show the Scene exactly as Builder shows it, for one Place same as for several. **Fixed** in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`: `_place1Rect`'s and `getPlaceRects(s)`'s gating condition changed from "subdivide Place 1 only when 2+ Places are authored" to "subdivide Place 1 whenever ANY real `placeRects` array exists (length≥1)" — the full-panel fallback now applies ONLY when a Layout authors zero Places at all (no `placeRects` array — the true legacy/implicit case, e.g. Museum Gallery, completely unaffected). **Violation 2 (Rules 2/3)**: World Builder's own "Can a Story Author change this? (its Frame, once populated)" guardrail (`holder.permissions.editable`, compiled into `placeRects` by the prior sprint) had zero effect in Creator — Card Designer's Frame Look preset buttons and every Frame Style slider/toggle/chip stayed fully interactive regardless of this flag, since nothing in `js/cardDesigner.js` had ever been wired to read it. **Fixed**: a new `_currentPlaceEditable()` helper resolves `SlideRenderer.getPlacePermissions(slide, _currentPlaceId()||'image-holder').editable` (translating Card Designer's own `undefined`-for-Place-1 convention to the real `'image-holder'` id first); `_refreshFrameWorkspace()` now disables every `.frame-design-btn` (Frame Look) and shows a plain "This Place's Frame was set by the World and can't be changed here" note when locked; `_refreshBorder()` folds `!editable` into its existing `!hasImage`-disables-controls pattern for every Frame Style padding/radius/line-width/shadow slider, fill chip, and toggle; `_applyFrameDesign()` gained a defensive early-return guard for any non-UI caller. **A real, deliberate correction to the render-time default asymmetry, not just a rewire**: `_resolvePlacePermissions`'s `editable` field changed from `p.editable===true` (absent→locked) to `p.editable!==false` (absent→editable) — the OPPOSITE default from `moveable`, and a deliberate departure from the prior sprint's own "absent always means locked" framing. Reasoned explicitly: `moveable` is a BRAND NEW capability (absent must stay locked, or every pre-existing theme would suddenly gain draggable Places it never had); Frame-editing via Card Designer is a PRE-EXISTING capability that has always been unrestricted for every Place in every theme published before the Guardrails sprint — defaulting absent `editable` to `false` would have newly LOCKED Frame-editing platform-wide, a real regression Rule 3 explicitly forbids. Only a Place whose Builder author explicitly unchecked the box (`editable:false`) is now locked. Verified via a re-run of `three_rules_audit.js` (both violations now PASS; the World-owned-Decoration regression check still PASSes unchanged) plus full regression across the existing 28-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite, the Guardrails sprint's own 7-assertion `place_guardrails_test.js` (including its own pre-existing "Legacy" absent-permissions fixture), and both `goldenBuild.js` suites — all passing unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js` and `js/cardDesigner.js`, plus one small CSS addition for the new lock-note.)

- Retro Guardrails Audit — the Whole Artwork Presentation Group Now Honours "editable" Too (a direct follow-up requested explicitly as a standing practice — "going forward and in retro" — after confirming the Governing Rules apply uniformly across object kinds. Auditing the previous fix against Rule 2/3 surfaced a second, real gap the earlier pass hadn't reached: World Builder's "Can a Story Author change this? (its Frame, once populated)" guardrail only ever gated Card Designer's Frame Look preset buttons and Frame Style's fill/border/radius/shadow sliders — the separate **Artwork Presentation** subgroup (Frame Variation swatches, plus Presentation/Lighting/Caption/Paper/Mat dropdowns, all built by `js/workspaceBuilder.js`'s `CONTROL_CATALOG` via `_buildSelectRow`/`_buildSwatchRow`/`_buildToggleRow`) had **no editable gating of any kind** — a Story Author could still change a locked Place's Frame Variation, Presentation preset, Lighting, or Caption style, bypassing the guardrail entirely. Confirmed the same gap existed one level deeper too: `paper`/`mat` (built by the identical `CONTROL_CATALOG` machinery, just rendered inside the 'frame' panel's Frame Style body rather than 'holder.image') were equally ungated, since `_refreshBorder`'s own direct-selector disabling never touched WorkspaceBuilder-built controls at all. Presented two scope options to the user — lock only the two controls literally named "Frame" (Frame Variation + the legacy `artworkFrame` dropdown), or lock the whole Artwork Presentation group together — and the user chose the latter: "if a Theme Author says don't let them change this Place's look, nothing about how the picture is framed, lit, captioned, or matted can be touched." **Fix**: `js/workspaceBuilder.js` gained one shared `_isCtxLocked(ctx)` helper (`ctx.getPlaceEditable`, a plain function reference resolved live at every `__sync`, mirroring the existing `ctx.getPlaceId` convention exactly — omitted by every non-Place caller, so Layout/Text/Sticker controls are completely unaffected) wired into `_buildSelectRow`/`_buildSwatchRow`/`_buildToggleRow`'s own `__sync` functions, disabling the `<select>`/swatch buttons/checkbox alongside their existing value-sync. `js/cardDesigner.js`'s `_refreshFrameWorkspace()` now passes `getPlaceEditable:_currentPlaceEditable` in both the 'frame' panel's `borderCtx` (covering paper/mat) and the 'holder.image' panel's `ctx` (covering the whole Artwork Presentation group), and the Artwork Presentation subgroup gained its own lock note (sharing the `.frame-editable-lock-note` class with Frame Look's, toggled together by one `querySelectorAll`). New CSS (`.icon-card:disabled`, `.workspace-select:disabled`) gives the newly-disabled swatches/dropdowns a visible locked state, matching the existing `.picture-reset-btn:disabled` convention. Verified via two new Playwright variants (`artwork_presentation_lock_test.js`/`_open_test.js`, a real synthetic theme with an explicit `editor.holder.image` control list and a real Frame Variation, driven with `editable:false` and `editable:true` respectively): every Frame Look button, every Frame Style slider, every Artwork Presentation dropdown, and every Frame Variation swatch is confirmed disabled together when locked and enabled together when open, both lock notes toggle in lockstep, a forced click on a disabled swatch changes nothing, and a real click on an enabled one does. Full regression across the entire existing 31-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including the prior sprint's own `place_guardrails_test.js`/`three_rules_audit.js`/`all_object_guardrails_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — no Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to `js/workspaceBuilder.js` and `js/cardDesigner.js`, plus one small CSS addition.)

- Screen 2 Preview Carousel Renders the Real Center Pane, Not a Static Thumbnail ("can we run the same center pane which is inside Studio here, so that author can actually see what slides a theme contain" — the Selected World Preview's carousel (`.creation-flow-carousel-art`) showed only a static `<img>` (a Representation's own authored thumbnail, or the World's Hero Image/icon glyph as a fallback) — never the real Frame/Layout/Layer Pack rendering a Story Author would actually get. Fixed by having each carousel slide render through the exact same `SlideRenderer` module the Workspace's own center pane uses — a real `<canvas>` replaces the `<img>`, painted via a new `_buildPreviewSlide(theme,representation)` (a synthetic slide mirroring exactly what `_finish()` builds for a real page — `_themeType(theme.id)==='artwork'` stamps `slide.artworkTheme`, otherwise `slide.theme`+`slide.artworkTheme=null` — plus `_seedDefaultFrameVariation`, reused verbatim) and a new `_renderCarouselCanvas(canvas,theme,representation)` (`SlideRenderer.init(canvas,{dpr:1,adaptiveViewport:true})` + `render()`, wrapped so a failure falls back to the old thumbnail/glyph, never breaking Screen 2). **A real, load-bearing bug found and fixed while wiring this up, not assumed away**: `SlideRenderer.buildPayload(slide,opts)` — the shared payload-builder every render surface already uses — unconditionally resolves `theme`/`artworkTheme` off the GLOBAL `ThemeEngine` state (`ThemeEngine.resolveTheme()`/`.getActiveArtworkTheme()`), correct for the real live editor slide (which has no per-slide override) but silently ignoring `slide.theme`/`slide.artworkTheme` entirely — so a naive `render(buildPayload(slide,...))` call always painted whatever World was already active in the background (or nothing, defaulting to portrait), never the synthetic slide's own theme; confirmed directly by comparing `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize(slide)` (which DOES honour `slide.artworkTheme`, correct) against the actual rendered canvas size (always default) before writing any fix. Fixed, without touching `buildPayload()` itself or any global `AppState`/`ThemeEngine` state, by overriding `payload.theme`/`payload.artworkTheme` with the synthetic slide's own values (when set) immediately before the one `render(payload)` call this feature makes — the one surgical point where a preview can diverge from the global active theme. A second real hazard, mirrored from `js/thumbnails.js`'s/`js/pageOps.js`'s own established pattern: rendering N carousel canvases repoints `SlideRenderer`'s shared module state away from the live editor canvas each time (relevant since Screen 2 can be reached from an already-open Workspace via the header's Home button) — closed with a new `_restoreEditorCanvas()`, called once after the whole carousel paints, re-`init()`-ing `#previewCanvas` and calling `window.redrawPreview()` (a no-op before any project exists, the ordinary fresh-boot case). New CSS `.creation-flow-carousel-canvas{object-fit:contain}` (deliberately `contain`, not the `img`'s existing `cover`, so the whole rendered page is visible letterboxed rather than cropped). Verified via two new Playwright suites: a general suite (3 real canvases render with genuine non-blank painted pixels, zero `<img>` fallback, editor canvas correctly present/no-throw after restore) and an aspect-differentiation suite (a synthetic World with Landscape/Portrait/Quote Layouts produces three canvases at their own genuinely correct 1350×1080/1080×1350/1080×1350 sizes — the exact bug reproduction that caught the `buildPayload` issue, failing before the fix and passing after) plus a visual screenshot confirming a real Frame Variation's mat/border colour and the genuine "Add artwork" placeholder now render in the carousel. Full regression across the entire existing 33-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; `_repCard`/`_renderChangeRepresentationScreen` (the Context Panel's own "Change Representation" shortcut) are deliberately untouched, exactly as Sprint 11.1 originally scoped them — this feature is confined to Screen 2's own carousel builder in `js/creationFlow.js`, plus one small CSS addition.)

- Screen 2 Carousel — Story-Type Worlds' Own Layout/Layer-Pack Content Now Resolves Too (a direct, same-day follow-up: right after the live-render carousel shipped, the user tested it against their own real "My shapes" World — a story-type theme with a real Scene-converged Layout and Layer Pack — and reported "i dont think this was supposed to look like this," seeing a plain navy square with a blank white square inside where a genuine background fill + decoration shape should have shown. **Root cause, confirmed by direct code reading**: `_layoutTheme(s)` — a SEPARATE resolution chain from `_theme(s)`/`_artworkTheme(s)`, used by `_resolveLayout`/`_activeLayoutHolders`/`_activeLayoutPlaces`/`_activeLayerPack` for all Layout/Holder/Place/Layer-Pack resolution — only ever checked `s.artworkTheme` or the GLOBAL active theme, never `s.theme`. The carousel's synthetic preview slide sets `slide.artworkTheme=null` for a story-type World (correctly, since Screen 2's own `payload.theme`/`.artworkTheme` overrides from the just-shipped feature already handle the story/artwork split for `_theme`/`_artworkTheme`) — so `_layoutTheme` fell straight through to the global fallback, completely bypassing the World's own `layouts`/`layerPack`/`frameVariations`, and the page rendered the plain default panel instead. Two unsafe fixes were considered and rejected: mutating global `ThemeEngine` state to preview a theme (rejected — `applyTheme`/`applyArtworkTheme` unconditionally call `_invalidateThumbnails()`/`_refreshUI()` regardless of `opts.silent`, a real side effect on any background-open project); reusing `payload.theme` as a `_layoutTheme` fallback source (rejected — `ThemeEngine.resolveTheme()` always returns a stripped object missing `.layouts`/`.layerPack`/`.frameVariations` entirely, and is always truthy, which would silently break Layout resolution for every real page in the app). **Fix**: `_layoutTheme(s)` (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`) now checks a new `s.layoutTheme` field first — a distinct field from `s.theme`/`s.artworkTheme` (which `_theme`/`_artworkTheme` already interpret for other purposes and can't safely be reused for this), set only by `_renderCarouselCanvas` (`js/creationFlow.js`) via `payload.layoutTheme=theme` (the raw, un-stripped theme object) right alongside the existing `payload.theme`/`.artworkTheme` overrides. Real slides never set this field, so the fix is a no-op everywhere else in the app — confirmed via a `git stash` A/B test reproducing the exact bug (wrong portrait-default canvas size, wrong background colour, blank white decoration area) before the fix and the correct landscape aspect + converged background fill + decoration shape colour after it. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`carousel_story_theme_layout_test.js`, scratch-only) using a synthetic story-type theme shaped exactly like a real World Builder v2 Scene-converged package (`supportedCreationTypes:['story']`, a landscape-aspect Layout, a `'slide'`-scoped colour-fill Layer Pack entry, an `'overlay'`-scoped decoration shape) — pixel-sampled to confirm both the correct canvas aspect and the correct fill/shape colours render. Full regression across the entire existing 28-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; the fix is confined to one function each in `renderer/slideRenderer.js` and `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- Screen 2 Carousel — Each Scene's Visible Box Now Matches Its Own Real Orientation ("its better but not fixed. the orientation for each scene is different in builder. but in creator they all are showing up as landscape" — a direct, same-day follow-up to the `_layoutTheme` fix above. **Confirmed the internal canvas pixel buffer was already correct** — `canvas.width`/`canvas.height` genuinely resolved a different, correct size per Representation (1080×1350 for Portrait, 1350×1080 for Landscape) — but the VISIBLE box every carousel slide sits in, `.creation-flow-carousel-art`, was a fixed-shape container (`width:100%; max-width:250px; height:clamp(...)`, originally built for a cropped static `<img>` thumbnail with `object-fit:cover`) that never adapted to a Representation's own real orientation, so every Scene's correctly-sized canvas got squeezed/padded into the SAME landscape-ish box regardless — exactly "they all show up as landscape." **A second, compounding bug found in the same trace**: `_renderCarouselCanvas`'s own `canvas.style.aspectRatio` was being computed from `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize(slide)` — the bare synthetic slide object — but the `layoutTheme` override the previous fix introduced is only ever set on `payload` (built via `buildPayload(slide,...)` then overridden), never on `slide` itself; so even that inert inline style was resolving to the wrong value for every story-type Representation. **Fix**: `getCanvasSize()` is now called with `payload` (which correctly carries `.layoutTheme`); `_renderCarouselCanvas` returns the resolved `{w,h}` size instead of a bare boolean, and `_carouselSlide` (`js/creationFlow.js`) now sets `.creation-flow-carousel-art`'s own `style.aspectRatio` from that size — the actual container that controls the visible shape, not the inert canvas-level style. `css/style.css`'s `.creation-flow-carousel-art` changed from a fixed `width:100%` to `width:auto` + a CSS `aspect-ratio:4/5` fallback (matching the editor's own default page shape before any live render has painted), so its width now genuinely derives from its height and whichever real aspect ratio is set — letting each Representation's box take on its own real shape instead of sharing one fixed frame. Verified via a `git stash` A/B test with three Representations (Portrait/Landscape/Quote): before the fix, every visible box measured identically wide-shaped (ratio ≈1.55, matching the exact reported symptom) despite the internal canvas already being correctly sized per Representation; after the fix, Portrait/Quote boxes measure genuinely narrower-than-tall (ratio ≈0.80) and the Landscape box measures genuinely wider-than-tall (ratio ≈1.25) — a real, visible difference, not just a backing-store number. Full regression across the entire existing 32-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/creationFlow.js` and one CSS rule.)

- Bigger Slide Previews — Screen 2's Own Carousel and the "Change Look" Quick-Switch Both Grown, the Latter Now Live-Rendered Too ("can we increase the size of slide in right panel?" — the Selected World Preview carousel's own visible box (`.creation-flow-carousel-art`) was capped at `max-width:250px`, noticeably smaller than the panel it sits in actually had room for. Widened its clamp() bounds (height `clamp(110px,17vh,200px)`→`clamp(110px,19vh,260px)`, max-width `250px`→`300px`, the carousel-slide wrapper's own min-height similarly), trimming the overlay's own top/bottom padding slightly (`clamp(14px,3vh,48px)`→`clamp(10px,2.4vh,48px)`) to free just enough headroom to grow without reintroducing the scroll the earlier "No-Scroll Screens" fix eliminated — verified at every height that fix originally targeted (640/700/720/800/900px), all still zero-scroll. **A second, separate request landed in the same conversation**: a follow-up screenshot showed a DIFFERENT screen — the Context Panel's "Change Look" quick-switch ("Choose a Page Style," `_renderChangeRepresentationScreen`/`_repCard` in `js/creationFlow.js`) — with its own small, cropped, scrollbar-forcing thumbnails; the user then clarified the ask further: "not just the size change but other change also where we plugged the center pane in screen 2 - preview," i.e. apply Screen 2's OWN live-SlideRenderer-render treatment here too, not merely make the old static thumbnails bigger. **Size**: `.creation-flow-card-icon-image`'s fixed height went `110px`→`190px` and the modal itself (`.creation-flow-overlay.mode-change-look .creation-flow-panel`) widened `560px`→`680px` — this modal already scrolls its own panel (`overflow-y:auto`) when content overflows, so none of the Screen-2-style no-scroll care was needed here. **Live render**: `_repCard` now resolves the full theme object (`ThemeRegistry.get(themeId)`, the same lookup `_applyRepresentationToCurrentSlide` already made) and, when it resolves, paints a real `<canvas>` via the exact same `_renderCarouselCanvas` helper Screen 2's carousel uses — reusing `.creation-flow-card-icon-image`'s own fixed width/height CSS (so `_renderCarouselCanvas`'s inline `aspect-ratio` style, needed for Screen 2's free-floating box, has no effect here — the live render simply crops to fill the card exactly like the old static image did, via `object-fit:cover`) — falling back to the pre-existing static thumbnail/glyph path only when the theme can't be resolved at all, matching `_carouselSlide`'s own established fallback discipline. Verified via a new Playwright test (`change_look_live_render_test.js`, scratch-only) with a synthetic two-Representation story-type theme (distinct, properly-`scope`-tagged 'slide'-scoped background fills per Layout, mirroring the Builder Convergence Sprint's own scoping rule) confirming both Page Style cards now render real, genuinely-distinct `<canvas>` content (not `<img>`) with zero panel overflow — a first draft of this test's fixture omitted the `scope` field on each layer entry, which reproduced a real-looking "both cards show the same colour" symptom that turned out to be the TEST fixture's own bug (an unscoped layer applies globally by design, per the Builder Convergence Sprint, so the later one simply paints over the earlier — not a product defect), caught and corrected before relying on the test. Full regression across the entire existing 34-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including the updated `change_look_image_overflow.js`, whose own size/width assertions were intentionally loosened to match the deliberately bigger dimensions, not a regression) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `css/style.css` and `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- "Choose a Page Style" — Each Card Now Shows Its Own Real Orientation Instead of One Shared Fixed Shape ("all good but can we fix the orientation. each slide orientation as per the builder authored" — a direct follow-up to the previous entry's live-render upgrade for the Context Panel's "Change Look" quick-switch. A screenshot showed every Page Style card sharing one identical box shape regardless of its own real Layout — exactly the same class of bug already fixed for Screen 2's own carousel (see "Screen 2 Carousel — Each Scene's Visible Box Now Matches Its Own Real Orientation" above), just not yet applied here: `.creation-flow-card-icon-image`'s CSS was still a fixed `height:190px` + `object-fit:cover`, so a genuinely portrait or landscape live render got cropped to fill the same shared shape every card used, hiding its real orientation. **Fix**: `.creation-flow-card-icon-image` changed from `height:190px` to `height:auto` + a default `aspect-ratio:4/5` fallback (the modal's own before-JS-paint shape, matching the editor's default page convention) — `_repCard` (`js/creationFlow.js`) already relied on `_renderCarouselCanvas`'s existing inline `canvas.style.aspectRatio` (set from the live render's own resolved size, the exact mechanism Screen 2's carousel already established), so once the CSS stopped pinning a fixed height, that inline style could finally take over and each card's box genuinely reflects its own real orientation — no JS change beyond an updated code comment. The static-thumbnail fallback path (used only when a theme can't be resolved at all) simply keeps the same default 4:5 shape it already had. Verified via a `git stash` A/B test with a real landscape + portrait Representation pair: before the fix, both cards measured an identical fixed ratio (1.35, one shared shape) regardless of their own Layout; after, the landscape card measures genuinely wider-than-tall (ratio 1.25) and the portrait card genuinely taller-than-wide (ratio 0.8) — a real, visible difference matching each Scene's own authored shape. Full regression across the entire existing 35-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (one existing test's own height-cap assertion was intentionally loosened to allow the now-correct taller portrait box — not a regression, the direct intended consequence of this fix) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to one CSS rule in `css/style.css` plus a comment update in `js/creationFlow.js`.)

- Page Background Colour — a Real Per-Page Override, Finally Winning Over the World's Own Wall Tone ("the creator background color. its available in right panel but changing it has not effect on the center pane slide" — a real, confirmed bug, not a misunderstanding. **Root cause, traced not guessed**: Context Panel's "Page Background → Background Colour" swatch (`js/contextPanel.js`'s `_appendBackground`) wrote to the STORY Theme's global `colours.frame` sub-option via `ThemeEngine.setSubOption` — but `renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s background-fill line has always been `x.fillStyle=_wallTone||_frameColor(t,opts)`, unconditionally preferring the active World's own resolved wall tone (`_resolveWallTone(s)`, Sprint 9.7) over the Story Theme's frame colour whenever ANY World/Artwork Theme with a Frame Variation is active — which is the common case for a real project today. The swatch's write was reaching a real, correctly-wired code path; it simply never had priority to paint anything, so it read as "changing it has no effect." A second, compounding issue: even where it *would* have won (no World active at all), the write was **global** (every page at once), not scoped to "the center pane slide" the control's own heading ("PAGE BACKGROUND") and the user's own wording both name. **Fix**: a genuine per-page override, `slide.metadata.cardOverrides.background` — the same per-card override bag pattern every other Story-Author control in this codebase already uses (Frame Variation, Presentation, image view, etc.) — now resolves FIRST in the background-fill line, ahead of both wall tone and the Story Theme default (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s new `_slideBackgroundOverride(s)`, plus a matching fix so Handle/Page-Number chrome-text legibility considers the override too, not just wall tone). `_appendBackground` now reads `_currentSlide()` (mirroring `_appendMetadataField`'s own convention) instead of the global Theme, writes to the per-slide bag, and calls `host.redraw()`/`host.markDirty()` — the same dispatch every other live-editing control in this file already uses; `ThemeEngine.setSubOption` is no longer called by this control at all. No reset control was added (a disclosed, minor gap — a Story Author who picks a colour has no one-click way back to the World default through this control alone, matching the scope of "fix the reported bug," not a broader redesign). Verified via a `git stash` A/B test against a real Frame-Variation-driven wall tone: before the fix, picking a new colour left the canvas pixel completely unchanged (the exact reported symptom); after, the canvas repaints to the picked colour immediately, and the value is confirmed stored per-slide (a second page does not inherit it). Full regression across the entire existing 36-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/contextPanel.js` and `renderer/slideRenderer.js`.)

- Right Panel Redesign — Personalize ⇄ Refine (implements the "Personalize ⇄ Refine" concept chosen from a series of Artifact mockups: "when nothing is selected only personalize, when something is selected collapse personalize and add refine. refine options are object specific. Rule 4 is more about adding a personal layer. anything added by author is considered as an object which gets added in object strip." The Context Panel's old "nothing selected" default view — a Welcome heading, an ownership legend, a Page Style row, Caption/Quote fields, a Background Colour swatch, and an Add a Sticker button, all always visible at once — is replaced with two zones that swap for the same space instead of competing for it: **Personalize** (Rule 4) takes the whole panel when nothing is selected; the instant something IS selected, it collapses to one quiet strip (still there, one tap to reopen) and **Refine** (Rule 3 — still 100% CardDesigner's own pre-existing `#card-tab` markup, completely untouched) expands into the room it gave up; a small **Status** pill (Rule 2) stays at the top of every selection so the guardrail (✏️ editable / 🌍 part of the World / 🔒 locked) is never lost. Confirmed by investigation before any code was written: `panelRoot` (`#contextPanelRoot`) is already `#card-tab`'s own immediate previous sibling in `.right-sidebar` (`js/contextPanel.js`'s `init()`), so the whole zone-stacking behaviour works via plain DOM order with zero restructuring — Refine simply continues visually below whatever Personalize/Status render, no new wrapper needed. **Rule 4 sharpened mid-design**: Personalize isn't a settings panel, it's how a Story Author adds a new personal layer — anything it lets you add becomes a real object landing in the render tree/Object Strip exactly like anything else (`owner:'story'`), closing the loop into Rule 3 with zero new plumbing, since `SceneEngine.addSticker`'s existing pipeline already does this. Background Colour/Change Look/Caption are the other kind — they change the page itself, no object created — and inline-expand in place instead. **"+ Add Something"** is a 7-row accordion (chosen over a floating popover — lower risk inside a narrow scrolling sidebar, confirmed with the user): 😀 Stickers/⭐ Decorations/🔷 Shape all reuse the exact same underlying capability confirmed by investigation to already exist — `SceneEngine.addSticker` via Sticker Studio, filtered to a different `StickerLibrary` category (`stickerStudio.js` gained one small additive export, `setActiveCategory(id)`, so Decorations/Shape jump straight to their own shelf instead of the default Characters tab); 📸 Photo reuses the existing Add/Replace Artwork flow via a new `_firstOpenPlaceSelection(slide)` helper (enumerates `SlideRenderer.getPlaceRects()`, selects the first Place with no picture yet, or falls back to Place 1/the Cover-Hook-End single-holder case) then calls `PageRuntime.selectSceneObject()` + the existing `_replaceArtwork()`, opening the native file picker in one tap; 🗒️ Note, ✏️ Doodle, 🎤 Voice are honest, visibly-disabled "Soon" rows (reusing the `.is-coming-soon` convention already established for Publish's own Community World card) — investigation confirmed `SceneEngine` has no freeform multi-instance text-object array, no freehand-drawing capability, and no audio-attachment capability anywhere today, so building them for real was out of scope; stubbing them disclosed rather than faked. **Background/Change Look/Caption** all reuse their pre-existing field-building bodies verbatim (`_appendBackground`/`_appendRepresentationRow`/`_appendCaptionOrQuote`, completely unmodified internals) — only relocated behind inline-accordion tiles; Caption's tile is hidden entirely (not merely disabled) when the active Representation supports neither `editCaption` nor `editQuote`, matching the file's own existing dead-button-avoidance convention. **State model**: `personalizeExpanded`/`personalizeOpenSection` reset only when the selection itself changes (tracked via a `_lastSelectionKey` string), never on a same-selection `refresh()` triggered by tapping the collapsed strip or an accordion trigger — both simply mutate one variable and call `refresh()` again, which recomputes the identical key and leaves the state alone. Per an explicit product decision confirmed via AskUserQuestion, the old always-visible ownership legend and "tap anything" hint are dropped from the default view — their meaning is now taught contextually by each object's own Status pill the moment something is actually selected, exactly matching the chosen mockup. Verified via two new Playwright suites (scratch-only, 27 + 9 assertions): the full/collapsed Personalize swap; all 7 Add Something rows present with the correct 3 disabled; picking a sticker lands as a real `owner:'story'` render-tree object and Object Strip card (the literal Rule 4 → Rule 3 loop); the collapsed strip re-expands in place with selection/Refine state preserved; Background Colour's inline-expand still repaints the canvas via the existing per-page override (unchanged from the prior sprint) without collapsing Personalize; Caption's tile shows/hides correctly per Representation `actions`; Change Look still calls `CreationFlow.changeRepresentation()`; Decorations/Shape correctly jump Sticker Studio's active category; Photo correctly selects the first open Place and opens a real native file chooser in one tap; a World-owned selection also gets the collapsed Personalize strip appended to its own disclosure banner. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (57 pre-existing scripts, one — `background_color_bug_test.js` — updated to open the Background tile first, matching this sprint's own intentional restructuring, not a regression; 5 unrelated pre-existing failures in World-Builder-v2/theme-card/sticker-drag scripts confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified baseline) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; Refine (CardDesigner's `#card-tab`) is completely untouched — confined to `js/contextPanel.js`, `js/stickerStudio.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Add Something — Photo Removed, Sticker/Decoration/Shape Combined Into One Entry Point (a direct, same-day follow-up to the Right Panel Redesign sprint's own "+ Add Something" menu, per explicit product feedback: "remove the option photo as it adds the photo into a place. combine decoration/stickers/shapes into one category which works for all." **Photo removed**: it duplicated the existing per-Place "Add Artwork" flow already reachable by selecting a Place directly on canvas — that's where artwork replacement belongs, not a second entry point buried in Personalize's menu; the now-orphaned `_addPhoto`/`_firstOpenPlaceSelection` helpers (no other call site referenced either) were deleted outright rather than left as dead code. **Stickers/Decorations/Shape combined into one row**: confirmed via investigation that Sticker Studio's own category tab strip already gives full reach across every category (Characters/Decorations/Shapes/etc.) the instant it opens — the three separate rows only ever existed to pre-filter which shelf appeared first, so one combined "😀 Stickers, Decorations & Shapes" row (dropping the two `StickerStudio.setActiveCategory()` pre-filter calls, opening on the default Characters tab like the original plain "Stickers" row always did) loses no real capability. `js/contextPanel.js`'s `_addSomethingItems()` now returns 4 rows (the combined sticker row + the honest Note/Doodle/Voice Coming Soon stubs, unchanged) instead of 7. Verified via a new Playwright test (`add_something_combined_test.js`, scratch-only): exactly 4 rows render, no Photo/separate-Decorations/separate-Shape row exists, the combined row opens Sticker Studio with 18 real category tabs visible (including Decorations and Shapes) rather than pre-filtered to one. Full regression across the existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (one pre-existing failure, `sticker_owner_check.js`, confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified baseline — a stale locator from before the Personalize/Refine rewrite, not a regression from this change) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors — confined to `js/contextPanel.js`, no CSS/architecture change.)

- Recolorable Stickers/Decorations/Shapes — Auto Duotone (implements the user's own escalating request through a working-prototype design process: "for every sticker/decoration/shape kid select i want a full control on colors, outline, shape, inside color fill, border fill etc etc" → after a flat single-colour silhouette proof was rejected outright ("no this is not the direction. what would i do with flat red dog") and a "Shapes only" scoping was rejected too ("why cant a dog be of any color") → landing on "Option A," the Auto Duotone technique, approved as an interim production solution while a real vector-asset-based library remains an open question ("lets do with option A till we have real answer for this"). **The real constraint, confirmed by reading the code before proposing anything**: `js/stickerLibrary.js`'s `_sticker(glyph,bg)` renders every one of the library's 500+ entries as an SVG `<text>` glyph — color emoji glyphs paint through the browser's own built-in COLR/CBDT colour-font tables, which ignore CSS/canvas `fillStyle` entirely, so a literal per-region recolor of the existing catalog is not technically possible; only a pixel-level canvas technique works. **The technique** (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`): `_buildRecoloredStickerCanvas(stickerId,bodyColor,shadeColor,outlineColor)` draws the glyph once to an offscreen canvas, builds an Outline layer by stamping that same alpha shape in a 16-point ring at a fixed dilation radius then flattening the union to `outlineColor` via `source-atop` compositing, and builds a Fill layer via Auto Duotone — `getImageData`, splitting every opaque pixel into a Body tone or a Shade tone by its own original luminance (`>150` threshold), then `putImageData` back — preserving some of the glyph's own shape detail rather than flattening it to one flat silhouette colour, the specific quality that got the first, simpler technique rejected.
