Composites Outline behind Fill, cached per `stickerId+bodyColor+shadeColor+outlineColor` combination (`_stickerRecolorCache`, never caching a `null` result so a still-decoding source glyph correctly retries on the next repaint once `_ensureStickerImage`'s own `onload` fires). `_drawSceneSticker` branches on a new `st.recolorEnabled` instance field, drawing the recolored canvas instead of the natural glyph image/emoji-text fallback when set; `_stickerBbox` gained a matching `visual:{kind:'image',src:<dataURL>}` field (lazily cached via `_recoloredStickerDataURL`) so Object Strip's own pre-existing `visual`-aware thumbnail rendering shows the real recolored sticker instead of its plain catalog glyph, with zero Object Strip code changes needed — `_sceneObject`'s existing `Object.assign` normalizer already carries any extra field on a bbox through to the render tree verbatim. **Refine panel** (`js/cardDesigner.js`'s `_buildStickerControls`/`_refreshSticker`): a "🎨 Colour This" toggle (reusing the existing `_buildToggleRow` helper) plus three `<input type=color>` rows (Inside/Shade/Outline Colour) inserted after the Flip row — enabling the toggle seeds sensible defaults (`#E0432B`/`#8A1F10`/`#1D3457`) only the first time (`if(!st.bodyColor) changes.bodyColor=...`), so a later disable→re-enable cycle remembers whatever a child actually picked rather than resetting to the seed; every field writes through the existing generic `_stickerUpdate`→`SceneEngine.updateSticker` shallow-merge (no SceneEngine changes needed — it already accepts arbitrary new instance fields) and redraws live via the existing `_commitSticker` path. Works automatically on all 500+ existing catalog entries — and, per the Add Something menu's own same-day "combine Sticker/Decoration/Shape into one entry point" change, uniformly regardless of which shelf (Stickers/Decorations/Shapes) the object came from, since they're all the identical `type:'sticker'` instance shape — with zero new artwork required. Verified via a new Playwright test (`sticker_recolor_test.js`, scratch-only, using a real 'animals.dog' catalog entry): the toggle/3 colour inputs render on selection; toggling on repaints the canvas with the real default Body/Outline colours (pixel-sampled, not merely inspected); picking a custom Body colour repaints again and the old default colour is confirmed gone; toggling off reverts the canvas to the natural, un-recolored emoji; toggling back on remembers the previously-picked custom colour rather than resetting to the seed default; Object Strip renders a real recolored `<img>` thumbnail, not the plain glyph. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/cardDesigner.js`, and one small CSS addition. A real, richer vector-asset-based sticker library remains an explicitly open, deferred question — the user's own uploaded stock `.eps` sample was confirmed genuinely vector but unparseable in this sandbox with no available conversion tooling, and was set aside pending "a real answer," not pursued further this sprint.)

- Real Vector Shapes + Freeform Text — Personalize (implements two direct product requests together, per an approved plan: "can we get shapes like we have in world. outline shapes. geometry shapes, free style shapes." and "in personalization i would need text too. text should support all text related options. nice kid friendly font. it should also have something which resemble handwriting fonts." **The shared mechanism**: both land as `slide.metadata.stickers[]` entries — the exact same array/`type:'sticker'` shape every existing glyph sticker already uses — distinguished by a new `st.kind` field (absent/`'glyph'` unchanged, `'shape'`, or `'text'`). Investigation (3 parallel Explore agents) confirmed this is the lowest-risk reuse path: `js/app.js`'s hit-test is fully generic on bbox shape; its 4 `elementType==='sticker'` drag/resize checks already route any `type:'sticker'` object through `SceneEngine.updateSticker` (schema-free, any new field rides through with zero SceneEngine change); `js/contextPanel.js`'s `TYPE_TO_SECTIONS` already routes `'sticker'`→CardDesigner's sticker section; Object Strip is generic on bbox `visual`/`editable`/`owner`/`draggable`. Zero changes to `js/app.js`, `js/sceneEngine.js`, `js/objectStrip.js`, `js/pageRuntime.js`, or `js/projectManager.js`. **Real Vector Shapes**: `renderer/slideRenderer.js` already had the full 15-kind vector geometry (circle/rectangle/rounded-rectangle/triangle/diamond/pentagon/hexagon/octagon/star/cross/trapezoid/parallelogram/arrow/speech-bubble/banner, plus freehand `'custom'`) in `_layerDrawShape(d,rect)` — built for World-owned Layer Pack decorations, mirroring `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/engineRuntime.js`'s `_drawShape` byte-for-byte, but never reachable by a Story Author. New `_drawSceneShape(st)`/`_shapeBbox(st)` wrap it directly (zero geometry reimplementation) with early branches inside `_drawSceneSticker`/`_stickerBbox`; a new `SHAPE_KINDS` catalog in `js/stickerLibrary.js` mirrors Builder's own list (kept in lockstep by hand, per this codebase's established Decoration Shapes precedent). `js/contextPanel.js` gained a new, separate **"🔺 Shapes"** Add Something row (deliberately not folded into the existing combined emoji-glyph "Stickers, Decorations & Shapes" row — real vector geometry is a different capability from an emoji glyph, mirroring Builder's own two-parallel-grids precedent) opening a 16-tile picker (15 kinds + "✏️ Draw Your Own"); picking a preset creates the shape instance and selects it immediately, landing on its own Refine panel. `js/cardDesigner.js`'s sticker Refine panel gained a Shape controls group (Fill/Outline Colour+Opacity, Outline Thickness) plus an inline Draw pad for `shape:'custom'` (adapted from World Builder's own `_shapeDrawPad`, normalizing pointer drags to a 0..1 fractional `customPath`) — the existing "Colour This" duotone group and Flip row are hidden for shape kind (different/no-op concepts); Size/Rotation/Opacity/Lock-Duplicate-Delete stay shared. **Freeform Text**: no per-instance draggable text drawing existed anywhere (`resolveTextSource` only resolves fixed `slide.metadata` paths); new `_drawSceneText`/`_textObjBbox` reuse the existing `_wrapText` word-wrap utility, with height derived live from the real wrapped-line count (never stored) so the selection outline always hugs the actual rendered text, matching this codebase's own established "auto-size to rendered content" precedent (AV-006/AV-010). New `_ensureCanvasFont(fontFamily)` closes a real, disclosed gap — canvas `ctx.font=` draws are synchronous with no font-loading awareness anywhere in the renderer — using the Font Loading API (`document.fonts.check`/`.load()`) with the exact same request-once/redraw-on-ready discipline `_ensureStickerImage` already established for sticker images. **Fonts**: a new `assets/fonts/` folder (linked from `index.html`) with `fonts.css` + 4 self-hosted `.woff2` files, copied verbatim from the sibling `vihuplanet` product's own already-licensed, already-proven local-webfont set (Caveat/Kalam/Nunito, all Google Fonts/OFL, zero new licensing risk) — "Handwriting" (Kalam) and "Kid Friendly" (Nunito) are added to `js/cardDesigner.js`'s shared `FONT_FAMILY_OPTIONS` (with web-safe fallbacks in the stack) and, for consistency, `js/themeEngine.js`'s `FONT_CHOICES`. `js/contextPanel.js`'s disabled "🗒️ Note" row is promoted to a real, enabled **"🅰️ Text"** row — the exact gap its own prior code comment named ("no freeform text-object array... stubbed honestly as Coming Soon") — creating a `kind:'text'` instance and landing on its Refine panel: a Words textarea (wrapped with the existing `EmojiPicker.wrap(...)`, Sprint 9.6/AV-011 precedent), Font Family/Size/Weight/Style/Colour/Alignment/Width controls, all reusing `FONT_FAMILY_OPTIONS`/`FONT_WEIGHT_OPTIONS`/`_makeSliderRow` from the existing fixed-Text section. Doodle/Voice remain disabled, unrelated to this request. **Two real bugs found and fixed during implementation, not assumed away**: (1) `SceneEngine.addSticker`'s pre-existing guard requires a truthy `init.stickerId` — never touched by the new draw paths, but needed a synthetic value (`'shape.'+shapeId` / `'text.freeform'`) on creation to satisfy it without any SceneEngine change; (2) `EmojiPicker.wrap(el)` moves `el` into a new wrapper `box` and returns `box` — appending the raw element separately and calling `wrap()` for its side effect (as first written) silently detached the Words textarea from the DOM; fixed to match `js/pageDesigner.js`'s own established convention of inserting the wrapper's return value directly. A third, disclosed gap closed in the same pass: the new `.hidden`-toggled classes (`.sticker-shape-group`, `.sticker-text-group`, `.sticker-glyph-only`, `.sticker-hide-for-text`, `.shape-draw-pad-wrap`) had no matching CSS `display:none` rule — this codebase has no shared global `.hidden` utility, every usage is scoped per-component — so the toggle had zero real visual effect until the matching rules were added. Verified via a new Playwright test (`shapes_text_test.js`, scratch-only): the Shapes picker shows all 16 tiles and creates/selects a real `kind:'shape'` instance whose default and changed Fill Colour both pixel-sample correctly on the canvas; a real simulated pointer drag on the Draw pad persists a genuine `customPath`; the Text row creates a real `kind:'text'` instance; typing into Words persists; picking "Handwriting" persists `fontFamily` AND `document.fonts.check()` confirms the Kalam webfont actually loaded (not silently falling back); Weight/Style/Alignment/Colour/Width all persist and the canvas paints real non-blank text pixels; Object Strip shows both new objects with correct labels. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (one prior test's own row-count assertions updated for this sprint's own intentional new rows, not a regression) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/stickerLibrary.js`, `js/cardDesigner.js`, `js/themeEngine.js`, `js/contextPanel.js`, `css/style.css`, `index.html`, and the new `assets/fonts/` folder.)

- Doodle — A Real Multi-Stroke Freehand Drawing Capability (a direct, same-day follow-up: "i like this implementation, especially the draw your own. but draw your own is just filling shape it does not allow you to draw irregular shape. can we upgrade this. infact this has potential to become doodle." An AskUserQuestion offering two scope options — upgrade "Draw Your Own" in place, or promote it into a real standalone Doodle reachable from the Add Something menu's own already-stubbed row — was interrupted by the user's own direct answer: "the doodle implementation should live in doodle." **The real gap**: the Shape system's "Draw Your Own" custom path (`shape:'custom'`, `st.customPath`) has always captured exactly one stroke and unconditionally called `x.closePath()`+`x.fill()` on it (`renderer/slideRenderer.js`'s `_layerDrawShape`) — correct for its own purpose (an irregular but still closed, fillable silhouette shape), but incapable of real line art: a stick figure needs several separate, unclosed strokes (a head circle, a body line, two arm lines), not one forced-closed blob. **Doodle, a genuinely separate object kind** (`st.kind==='doodle'`), keeps Shape's own custom path completely untouched and adds new, additive machinery: `st.strokes` is an array of `{points:[{x,y}...],color,width}` — each point 0..1 fractional within the doodle's own w/h box, one array entry per pen-down..pen-up gesture on the Refine panel's Draw pad, so a single Doodle can freely mix any number of independent strokes, each in its own colour and thickness. New `_drawDoodleStrokes(strokes,rect,alpha)`/`_drawSceneDoodle(st)`/`_doodleBbox(st)` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js` render every stroke as an open, `lineCap:'round'`/`lineJoin:'round'` path — never closed, never filled — with `_drawSceneSticker`/`_stickerBbox` gaining one more early branch (`if(st.kind==='doodle')`) alongside Shape's and Text's, so the whole existing hit-test/drag/resize/lock/duplicate/delete/reorder/Object-Strip pipeline (already generic on `type:'sticker'`) needed zero further changes — the identical reuse path the Shapes/Text sprint established. `drawObjectThumbnail` gained a `visual.kind==='doodle'` branch reusing `_drawDoodleStrokes` directly (no second drawing implementation), and `js/objectStrip.js`'s thumbnail dispatcher was widened from `v.kind==='shape'` to `v.kind==='shape'||v.kind==='doodle'` to route through it. **Refine panel** (`js/cardDesigner.js`): a new Doodle controls group — 8 kid-friendly Pen Colour swatches plus a full custom colour picker, 3 Pen Thickness tiles (Thin/Medium/Thick, reusing the existing `.icon-card`/`.icon-row` visual language Text's own Style/Alignment rows already established), a 260px Draw pad (`_drawDoodlePad`, module-level like `_drawShapePad` beside it, live-previewing the in-progress stroke overlaid on every already-persisted one), and real Undo Last Line / Clear All buttons. Pen Colour/Thickness are deliberately transient "what will the next stroke look like" tool settings — plain closure locals, never written to the sticker instance until a stroke actually completes on `pointerup` (matching the Shape pad's own "persist only on release" discipline), so switching colour mid-drawing genuinely produces multi-coloured line art rather than retroactively recolouring earlier strokes. `_refreshSticker` gained the matching `isDoodleKind` branch (toggling `.sticker-doodle-group`, syncing the pad from `st.strokes` on selection, setting the selected-label to "Doodle") alongside Shape's and Text's existing branches. Add Something's previously-disclosed-as-unbuilt "✏️ Doodle" Coming Soon stub (`js/contextPanel.js`) is now a real, enabled row — `_addDoodleObject()` creates a `kind:'doodle'` instance with an empty `strokes` array and selects it immediately, landing on a blank pad ready to draw on; only Voice remains a disclosed stub (no supporting audio-attachment capability exists anywhere in this codebase). **A real, latent bug found and fixed while implementing this, unrelated to Doodle itself**: the earlier Shapes/Text sprint's own freeform-text drawer was named `_drawSceneText(st)` — an accidental exact-name collision with a real, pre-existing `_drawSceneText(s,el)` (~line 2700, drawing a Scene-blueprint `type:'text'` element) that JS's last-declaration-wins semantics let silently shadow; confirmed via a full-codebase grep that no blueprint anywhere actually creates a `type:'text'` element (only `'text-holder'` is real), so this had zero observed effect in production, but it was still a genuine correctness bug, not a stylistic nit — fixed by renaming the freeform-text function to `_drawFreeformText`, its one real call site, with a doc comment explaining the collision and why it stayed invisible until now. Verified via a new Playwright test (`doodle_test.js`, scratch-only): a real, enabled Doodle row exists with only Voice remaining disabled; clicking it creates and selects a real `kind:'doodle'` instance with an empty `strokes` array, landing on its own Refine panel; 8 pen swatches and 3 thickness tiles render; two real, separate mouse-driven pointer drags on the pad — with a pen colour/thickness change between them — persist exactly 2 independent strokes with their own distinct colour/width each (pixel-sampled on the pad to confirm both stroke colours actually painted, and — the whole point of this feature — that the blank space between/outside the two strokes stays pure white, never auto-filled the way Shapes' closed blob would be); Undo Last Line removes exactly one stroke; Clear All empties the array; Object Strip shows a real canvas thumbnail (not a generic icon); the live editor canvas itself (not just the small pad) actually paints the doodle. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (two prior tests' own stale Add-Something disabled-row-count assertions updated for this sprint's own intentional new row, not a regression; two additional pre-existing failures, `right_panel_redesign_test.js`/`right_panel_redesign_test2.js`, confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified baseline — stale locators from before the Personalize/Refine rewrite, unrelated to this change) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/objectStrip.js`, `js/contextPanel.js`, `js/cardDesigner.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Shapes "Draw Your Own" — Multi-Stroke Line/Circle Tool + Fill Shape Toggle; Doodle Panel Reorganised (two direct follow-ups landed together: "can we do same for shapes under draw your own. multi stroke. shapes stroke should be regular line or circular. give option for just outline shape of colored shape." and "the doodle right panel needs reorgnisation. the drawing area can be the first thing. the color selector can be just [swatches]." **Shapes multi-stroke**: `shape:'custom'`'s pad is upgraded from a single forced-closed freehand path into a real drawing tool — a Line/Circle Tool picker (`.shape-draw-tool-btn`, default Line) decides what the NEXT drag commits; each completed drag appends one `{type:'line'|'circle', p0, p1}` entry to a new `st.customStrokes` array (never replacing it), so a shape can freely combine several straight edges and circles — draw a few connected Lines to trace a polygon, or add a Circle for a round part, then keep going. New `_buildCustomStrokePath`/`_drawCustomStrokeShape` in `renderer/slideRenderer.js` build ONE combined path per shape: consecutive Line strokes whose endpoints touch chain into a real continuous subpath (so a closed loop of connected Lines fills correctly as one shape, not disconnected slivers), while a Circle stroke is always its own separate closed subpath (an ellipse inscribed in its own `p0`/`p1` drag rectangle) — deliberately a new, separate function rather than an extension of `_layerDrawShape` (left completely untouched, still the exact single-freehand-path renderer for any legacy `customPath` and for every World-owned Layer Pack decoration). `_drawSceneShape`/`_shapeBbox`/`drawObjectThumbnail` all gained a `customStrokes`-aware branch, routing to the new multi-stroke path only when present — zero behaviour change for every other Shape kind or any theme's own Decoration Shapes. **Fill Shape toggle**: closes "give option for just outline shape of colored shape" — a universal `st.fillEnabled` boolean (any Shape kind, not just custom) gates whether `_layerDrawShape`/`_drawCustomStrokeShape` call `x.fill()` at all (`fillEnabled!==false`, so every pre-existing Shape/World-owned decoration that never sets it keeps filling exactly as before); `js/cardDesigner.js`'s Refine panel gained a "🎨 Fill Shape" toggle (`_buildToggleRow`) wrapping the Fill Colour/Opacity fields in their own hideable `.sticker-shape-fill-fields` group — turning it off hides those now-irrelevant fields and genuinely skips filling (not merely a 0%-opacity trick), while Outline Colour/Opacity/Thickness stay always visible since the outline itself is never gated by this toggle. **Doodle panel reorg**: `js/cardDesigner.js`'s Doodle controls group DOM order changed to Hint → Draw pad → Pen Tools (swatches + thickness, one compact row) → Undo/Clear — the pad is now the group's own first, largest element instead of sitting below three rows of controls; per the literal "just swatches" wording, the separate custom `<input type=color>` colour picker is removed outright, leaving only the 8-swatch palette (a deliberate simplification, not an oversight — a child picks from the visible dots, never opens a native colour-picker dialog). Both the multi-stroke pad and the Doodle pad reuse the exact same shared geometry logic by hand in two places (the real renderer in `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, and each pad's own lightweight preview reimplementation in `js/cardDesigner.js`) — matching this codebase's own established "a Refine-panel preview never calls into the real renderer module, only mirrors its geometry" precedent, not a new pattern. Verified via a new Playwright test (`shape_multistroke_test.js`, scratch-only): the Tool picker defaults to Line; drawing 3 connected Line strokes that close back to their own start point renders as one real filled triangle (pixel-sampled); switching to Circle and adding a 4th stroke preserves the 3 Lines (genuine multi-stroke, not a replace); the composite renders with the correct default Fill Colour in both the triangle and the circle; Undo Last removes exactly the most recent stroke; toggling Fill Shape off persists `fillEnabled:false`, hides the Fill fields, and the triangle's own interior pixel genuinely stops being the fill colour (real outline-only rendering, not a UI-only change); Clear All empties `customStrokes`; Object Strip renders a real canvas thumbnail. `doodle_test.js` was extended with a DOM-order assertion (pad before pen tools) and its stale "custom colour picker present" check was corrected to "absent," both passing; `shapes_text_test.js`'s own older single-freehand-drag assertion (written before this upgrade existed) was updated to assert a Line stroke lands in `customStrokes` instead of a freehand `customPath`, since a plain drag on the upgraded pad now commits one Line stroke by design — the intended consequence of this sprint, not a regression. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (same pre-existing, already-disclosed failures confirmed via `git stash` against the unmodified baseline, unrelated to this change) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/cardDesigner.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Doodle Pen Circles, Add Something Regrouped, Selection Back Button, Transparent Shape Fill (four rapid, direct follow-ups landed together. **(1) "change these into sketch pens... try circular"**: the Doodle Pen Colour swatches and Pen Thickness buttons are real `<button>` elements, so they were caught by the same global-cascade bug this codebase has hit repeatedly (`css/style.css`'s `button{height:var(--button-height)}` + `button:not(...){width:100%;margin-bottom:12px}`) — each swatch had no explicit sizing of its own to out-rank that, so every one was silently stretched to the sidebar's full width and 40px tall, rendering as a vertical stack of ovals instead of small pen-tip dots (the exact class of bug already fixed once for `.object-card` and the Publish Studio close button, just never applied here). Fixed with the same proven pattern — explicit `!important` width/height/margin overrides plus `flex-shrink:0` — restoring true fixed-size circles (22px swatches, 28px thickness buttons), with a soft inset gradient (`box-shadow: inset ...`) added so each dot reads as a small marker/pen tip rather than a flat colour chip. **(2) "organise this better"** (the Add Something accordion, screenshotted mid-session): the 5-row stacked list (`.context-add-item`, full-width rows) is replaced with a compact 3-column icon-card grid (`.context-add-grid`/`.context-add-card`, mirroring the exact `.icon-card`/`.context-shape-tile` visual language already used elsewhere in this same panel) — each capability now reads as a tappable card with its own icon badge, and the disabled Voice card gets a distinct top-corner "Soon" pill instead of just another muted row in the same list; the combined Sticker/Decoration row's label was shortened from "Stickers, Decorations & Shapes" to "Stickers & Decor" to fit the card format (same capability, shorter text). **(3) "need back button to go to previous selection else every time have to reset it by clicking outside"**: `js/contextPanel.js` gained real browser-back-button semantics — a small `_selectionHistory` stack (capped at 20) records the selection state being LEFT every time the actual selection changes (tracked via the existing `_lastSelectionKey`/`refresh()` reset block, extended with a paired `_lastSelectionSnapshot`), and a `_navigatingBack` flag suppresses re-pushing the one transition Back itself causes, so Back/Forward can never ping-pong two entries against each other. A quiet "← Back" pill (`_appendBackControl`) renders above the Status pill on every real selection state (World-owned, Artwork/Place, ordinary Story-owned object) and on the default view too, shown only once real history exists; clicking it pops the last entry and re-applies it via the exact same `PageRuntime.selectSceneObject`/`selectTextObject`/`clearSelection` channels every other control in this file already uses — a "nothing selected" history entry correctly routes to `clearSelection()`, making Back do in one tap what used to require hunting for empty canvas space. **(4) "for all shapes give option of transparent fill color"**: the separate "🎨 Fill Shape" on/off toggle (shipped in the immediately-prior sprint) is replaced by a Transparent checkbox sitting directly beside the Fill Colour swatch, mirroring the exact Colour-section pattern Universal Experience Authoring already established for World Builder Experiences (Colour Picker / Opacity / Transparent checkbox) rather than a separate row above the fields — same underlying `st.fillEnabled` field, inverted meaning (checked = transparent = `fillEnabled:false`, genuinely skipping `fill()` in the renderer, not a 0%-opacity trick). Fill Colour/Opacity now stay visible at all times (just dimmed via a new `.is-transparent` class, `opacity:0.4;pointer-events:none` on the two inputs) instead of being hidden outright, so a child can still see and adjust the colour they'll get back the instant they un-check it. Verified via a new consolidated Playwright test (`four_fixes_test.js`, scratch-only) covering all four fixes end-to-end (grid geometry and card count, real circular swatch/thickness-button dimensions confirmed via `getBoundingClientRect`, the Transparent checkbox's default/checked states plus a genuine pixel-sampled proof the fill colour stops painting, and a full select→deselect→re-select→Back round trip confirming the correct prior selection is restored) plus a full regression pass across the existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite — `doodle_test.js`/`shape_multistroke_test.js`/`add_something_combined_test.js`/`right_panel_redesign_test.js` all had their own stale `.context-add-item`/`.sticker-shape-fill-toggle` selectors updated to match this sprint's real new markup (the intended consequence of items 2 and 4, not a regression); `sticker_owner_check.js` and `frame_variation_test.js` were confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified baseline, unrelated to this change — and both `goldenBuild.js` suites pass unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `css/style.css`, `js/contextPanel.js`, and `js/cardDesigner.js`.)

- Boot Flash Fix + Emojis Rename (a real, user-reported polish issue: "when am refreshing studio, this page loads for few seconds" — a screenshot showed the raw pre-Context-Panel tab bar ("Story / Card Designer / Stickers / World Designer") plus the dead "🤖 Vihu Buddy Coming Soon" placeholder visibly flashing on refresh. **Root cause**: `js/app.js`'s entire boot sequence — including `ContextPanel.init()`, which is what adds the `.context-panel-mode` class that hides this legacy chrome — lives inside one `window.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', ...)` handler; since none of `index.html`'s ~33 `<script src>` tags are `defer`/`async` (each blocks HTML parsing until it downloads+executes), the raw static markup — `.tabs` (`display:flex` by default) and `#story-tab`'s `.buddy-placeholder` (visible since `#story-tab` carries `class='tab-content active'` in the raw HTML) — is genuinely visible to the browser for however long all those scripts take to load, before `DOMContentLoaded` fires and JS hides them. **Fix**: since Context Panel is the permanent architecture with no real fallback path (`ContextPanel.init()` always runs, `.context-panel-mode` always gets added), `.tabs` and `.buddy-placeholder` are now hidden by DEFAULT in base CSS (`display:none`) rather than only via the JS-added class — they provide zero value before JS runs and are always hidden after, so hiding them unconditionally removes the "half-built, broken-looking" flash without touching script-loading architecture or execution-order risk (confirmed via grep that `.tabs` has exactly one usage in the whole codebase, `index.html`'s own right-sidebar tab bar). The underlying total boot time is unchanged — this only removes the ugly, confusing visual in the meantime. **Separately, "rename stickers and decoration to just emojis"**: the combined Add Something card (`js/contextPanel.js`) — previously "Stickers & Decor" — is now plain "Emojis"; the matching legacy tab-bar button label (`index.html`, part of the same now-hidden-by-default chrome) was updated to "✨ Emojis" too, for consistency. **A separate, real bug report was investigated and NOT reproduced**: "any changes am doing in objects are not reflecting on slides" — a dedicated Playwright reproduction (shape Fill Colour edit via the real UI input, Size-slider edits, dragging an object on canvas, typing into a Text object's Words field, and the same sequence immediately after using the new Back button) confirmed every edit path correctly updates both the model and the live canvas paint in the current code, with zero console errors; most likely explanation is a stale browser cache from immediately before/after the just-shipped build, not a real regression — flagged to the user to hard-refresh and re-report with specifics if it persists. Verified via the existing `four_fixes_test.js`/`add_something_combined_test.js` suite (updated for the new "Emojis" label) plus both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `css/style.css`, `js/contextPanel.js`, and `index.html`.)

- Page Background Colour vs. a Scene-Hosted "Background" Object (a real, user-reported bug with a screenshot: "i changed BG color it did not worked" — a "My shapes" World's Object Strip showed a real "Background" card marked 🎨 editable, yet Personalize's own "Background Colour" swatch had zero visible effect. **Root cause, confirmed pixel-by-pixel, not assumed**: the earlier "Page Background Colour" fix genuinely made this control's per-page override (`slide.metadata.cardOverrides.background`) win over the World's wall tone in the BASE canvas fill (`x.fillStyle=_bgOverride||_wallTone||_frameColor(...)`) — but a World-authored, Scene-hosted "Background" object (Builder's own "Hosted by Scene" Colour Experience, converged onto the theme's `'slide'`-scoped Layer Pack) paints AFTER that base fill, as part of the merged Scene Stack render every zero-Holder Scene now uses (Unified Layer Ordering's own "full cross-object reorder" pass) — so on any page with a real Scene-hosted Background object (an increasingly normal authoring pattern), the World's own full-bleed fill always painted right over the Story Author's swatch, silently. **Fix**: `js/contextPanel.js`'s `_appendBackground` gained a new `_sceneHostedBackgroundObject()` lookup — scans the render tree (`PageRuntime.getRenderedObjects().scene`) for an entry with `owner==='world'`, `target==='slide'`, and `visual.kind==='color'` (the exact fingerprint a Scene-hosted Colour fill leaves) — and when one exists, the swatch reads its live colour and writes through it directly via `SceneEngine.setContentOverride(slide,id,'fillColor',value)`, the identical mechanism Object Strip's own "Background" card edit control already uses (Honour World-Owned Object Commitments sprint) — so both entry points now agree and both actually change what a Story Author sees. When the object exists but isn't editable, the tile shows an honest "This page's background comes from the World and can't be changed here" note instead of a swatch that would silently do nothing. When no Scene-hosted background object exists at all (a plain Story Theme / wall-tone page, or a Museum-Gallery-style theme authored before this pattern existed), the exact original per-page-override behaviour is completely unchanged — the two paths are mutually exclusive, never both active. Verified via a new Playwright reproduction (`background_color_bug_test2.js`, scratch-only, reproducing the reported "My shapes" shape exactly — a zero-Holder Scene with a real `target:'slide'` Colour-fill Layer Pack entry): the canvas genuinely shows the World object's colour before any edit; the swatch opens showing that REAL current colour, not a stale/generic default; editing it updates both the model and the live canvas paint to the new colour; Object Strip's own edit control for the identical object shows the same just-edited value, confirming the two entry points stayed in sync. The pre-existing `background_color_bug_test.js` (the original fix's own regression test, no Scene-hosted object involved) still passes unchanged, confirming the fallback path is untouched. Full regression across the existing Creator/Builder Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors from the app itself (two unrelated network-noise console messages in the new reproduction's own test harness — a 404 and a sandboxed network restriction hit while importing the synthetic fixture package — confirmed via a parallel clean-test run to be test-fixture artifacts, not app-code errors). No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to one function in `js/contextPanel.js`.)

- Object Strip Scroll Polish ("this scroll can be better," a screenshot showing the Object Strip's plain native OS scrollbar — a boxy, arrow-capped bar with nothing in common with the app's own warm rounded design language. Replaced with round arrow buttons flanking the strip (`.object-strip-arrow`, matching the app's own established rounded-button visual language) plus a soft edge fade (`mask-image`) hinting at more content off-screen — the underlying scroll is still genuine native `overflow-x:auto` (touch/trackpad/click-drag all keep working exactly as before), only its own default chrome is hidden now (`scrollbar-width:none`/`::-webkit-scrollbar{display:none}`), with `scroll-behavior:smooth` and `scroll-snap-type:x proximity`/`scroll-snap-align:start` added for a satisfying settle. `js/objectStrip.js`'s `init()` wires the two new buttons (`#objectStripPrev`/`#objectStripNext` in `index.html`) to `listRoot.scrollBy({left,behavior:'smooth'})` by one page-width click, and a shared `update()` (called on every real scroll event and again after every `refresh()`, since new/removed cards change `scrollWidth`) disables each arrow at its real end — mirroring the exact arrow-disabled-state convention Screen 2's own carousel already established. Verified via a new Playwright test (`objstrip_scroll_test.js`, scratch-only, forcing real overflow with 10+ stickers): the native scrollbar is confirmed hidden (`scrollbar-width:'none'`), Prev starts correctly disabled at the true start (an 8px tolerance absorbs `scroll-snap-type`'s own sub-pixel settle, caught via a real failing run before adding it), clicking Next genuinely scrolls the row and Prev becomes enabled, and scrolling to the real end correctly disables Next. Full regression across the existing Creator/Builder Playwright suite (including `objstrip_check.js`/`zoom_objstrip.js`/`zoom_objstrip2.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `css/style.css`, `js/objectStrip.js`, and `index.html`.)

- Stylesheet Cache-Busting ("its still there" — a screenshot of the deployed GitHub Pages site (`dexprab.github.io/vihustudio/`) showed the "Vihu Buddy Coming Soon" placeholder still visible even though the Boot Flash Fix sprint had already shipped `.buddy-placeholder{display:none}` as an unconditional base-CSS rule, and the dev footer's own build stamp confirmed the browser HAD picked up the newer HTML/JS (Build 0153) — a real cache-mismatch, not a code regression: `css/style.css`/`assets/fonts/fonts.css` were linked with no version query string, so GitHub Pages/the browser's own HTTP cache could keep serving a stale cached copy of the same-URL stylesheet indefinitely, independent of whether the HTML document itself reloaded fresh. **Fix**: both stylesheet `<link>` tags in `index.html` now carry a `?v=0153` query string — a version bump changes the URL itself, forcing a genuine re-fetch regardless of the underlying cache mechanism (browser HTTP cache, GitHub Pages edge cache, an ISP proxy, etc.), the same class of fix any static site with long-lived cache headers needs. Established as a manual ritual going forward: bump `?v=` on both stylesheet links alongside any future CSS-affecting ship, mirroring the existing `build-info.json` version-bump discipline exactly. Verified via the existing Playwright regression suite (its own local test harness already strips query strings when resolving a requested file path, so this needed no test-harness change) — the app boots and renders identically with the versioned stylesheet URLs. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/rendering change; confined to two `<link>` tags in `index.html`.)

- "Book" Retired From Publish Copy + Read-Screen Corner Radius Fix (two real, user-reported issues from the Publish flow, addressed together. **(1) "we should not use book any more"** — every user-facing "book" string across `js/publishStudio.js`/`js/storyDestinations.js` is replaced with "Adventure": the Read screen's primary CTA ("Publish My Book" → "Publish My Adventure"), the Celebration screen's download button and ready-message ("Get My Book" → "Get My Adventure", "Your book is ready..." → "Your adventure is ready..."), the destination-aware Celebration headline ("Your story is now a real book!" → "...a real adventure!"), the Almost Ready headline/message ("Your book looks ready!" → "Your adventure looks ready!", "...publish your book anyway..." → "...publish your adventure anyway..."), the Make-Another-Story confirm dialog ("Your current book is already published..." → "Your current adventure is already published..."), and the Story Book destination's own display `label` (`js/storyDestinations.js`'s `BOOK.label`, "Story Book" → "Story Adventure" — shown on the Choose Story Destination screen). Deliberately scoped to the Publish flow only — internal identifiers (`dest.id==='book'`, `AppState.project.bookTitle`, the `#bookTitle` input) and the separate, established Theme Designer "Book Style"/"Book Title" vocabulary (`index.html`'s World Designer tab, Sprint 8.4.2, unrelated to this report) are untouched, since renaming those is a different, bigger surface not raised by this report. **(2) "published image has square corners while the one i was building has rounded corners"** — root-caused, not guessed: `#previewCanvas` (the live editor canvas) has always used `border-radius:var(--card-radius)` (16px), while `.publish-read-canvas` (Publish Studio's "Read My Story" preview canvas — the exact screen the report's screenshot showed) and `.publish-celebration-cover` both had a hardcoded `border-radius:6px` — a purely cosmetic CSS mismatch on the canvas element's own container, not a pixel-content rendering divergence (the actual painted bitmap was already identical, per the pre-existing WYSIWYE guarantee). Both fixed to `border-radius:var(--card-radius)`, matching the editor exactly. **A new, permanent Creator Governing Rule was added in the same pass, prompted directly by this bug**: "5. Publish Fidelity — Publish should honour the runtime view of center pane of Creator," formalizing that whatever the live editing canvas shows — every object, every edit, every guardrail-respecting placement — is exactly what Publish must produce, with no separate reconstruction or fallback rendering path ever allowed to diverge from it; this corner-radius bug is recorded as the kind of (narrowly cosmetic, but real) violation the rule exists to catch early. Verified via a new Playwright test (`book_to_adventure_test.js`, scratch-only): the Read screen's CTA reads exactly "Publish My Adventure"; the Read canvas and the editor canvas resolve to the identical computed `border-radius` (`16px` both); the Almost Ready headline carries no "book" wording; a full text-node walk of the Publish Studio modal confirms zero remaining "book" occurrences anywhere reachable in the flow. Full regression across the existing Creator/Builder Playwright suite (including `publish_stages.js`, whose own stale `:has-text("Publish My Book")` selector was updated to match the new label — the intended consequence of this rename, not a regression) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `css/style.css`, `js/publishStudio.js`, and `js/storyDestinations.js`.)

- Rule 5 (Publish Fidelity) Audit + Fix — Publish Honours the Center Pane's Real Aspect Ratio and Fonts (a direct, requested audit of the Publish pipeline against the just-added Governing Rule 5 ("Publish should honour the runtime view of center pane of Creator"), followed by fixing every real violation found. **Investigation confirmed every Publish render call site already routes through the same `SlideRenderer.buildPayload()`+`.render()` the editor uses — no second rendering implementation exists** — but found two real, confirmed divergences, verified with actual pixel evidence rather than code-reading alone. **Violation 1 (High severity, confirmed with real pixel evidence)**: `render()` only resizes a canvas to a Scene's own Aspect Ratio (Landscape/Wide/Square/etc., the Scene Viewport feature) when that canvas was `init()`'d with `{adaptiveViewport:true}` — the editor's live canvas does this; **none of the four Publish render call sites did** (Read screen, Almost Ready cover, Celebration cover, Story Book PDF/Story Carousel PNG pages, all in `js/publishStudio.js`/`js/storyDestinations.js`). A real Landscape Scene, rendered both ways, confirmed the defect directly: the editor-correct render is genuinely 1350×1080; Publish's actual render stayed stuck at fixed 1080×1350, with sampled pixels at x=1200/x=1330 returning `null` — content physically absent from the canvas, ~200px of the right edge silently cut off, plus ~270px of unintended extra canvas below the real content (also mispositioning bottom-anchored chrome like Handle/Footer/Page Number, which anchor off the same viewport height). **Not hypothetical** — Museum Gallery's own real Showcase Representation uses the Landscape Layout, so this affected the platform's actual flagship theme today. **Fixed with two different techniques matching two different situations**: the Read screen, Almost Ready cover, and Celebration cover (literal 1:1 page previews, no destination-format constraint) now pass `adaptiveViewport:true` to their `SlideRenderer.init()` calls, matching the editor exactly; two of the three (Read screen, Celebration cover) also needed their CSS wrapper's own `style.aspectRatio` set dynamically from `SlideRenderer.getCanvasSize(slide)` after render, since their canvas fills its wrapper at `width:100%;height:100%` — both dimensions already explicit — so the canvas's own inline aspect-ratio override (set automatically by `render()`'s adaptive branch) has no effect once both dimensions are set; the Almost Ready cover's own CSS (`width:200px;aspect-ratio:4/5;height:auto`) needed no such fix, since `height:auto` lets the inline override apply directly. Story Book PDF / Story Carousel PNG are different — those destinations have their own deliberate fixed output shape (a PDF page size, "Instagram Portrait" 1080×1350, "Instagram Square" 1080×1080, established Sprint 9.0 decisions) that naively adaptive-sizing would break; `storyDestinations.js`'s `_renderSlideInto` now renders the Slide correctly at its own real Aspect Ratio on a throwaway intermediate canvas first (`adaptiveViewport:true`), then fit/composites that correctly-shaped render into the destination's own fixed render coordinate space via a new `_fitCompositeInto` helper (contain-fit, centred, with letterbox bars filled from the Slide's own top-left corner pixel as a natural background-colour proxy — reliably background, never content, since every real panel/Frame carries its own margin) — `createCanvas`/`encodePage`/`finish` are completely untouched, since Rule 5 governs what gets rendered, not the separate, deliberate destination-format decision; a portrait Scene (the overwhelming common case, and every Scene authored before the Scene Viewport feature existed) hits a fast, byte-identical `drawImage` with zero extra compositing. **Violation 2 (Medium severity) — a custom font race, found and fixed at its actual root cause, not the symptom first assumed**: `_ensureCanvasFont`'s "not ready yet, redraw once loaded" callback only ever redraws the live editor canvas (`window.redrawPreview`), never any one-shot Publish export, since `document.fonts.load()` is async and a synchronous `render()` call never waits for it — confirmed directly (a synchronous render call does not wait for the Promise to resolve). Investigating why a fix attempt still failed uncovered the real, deeper, pre-existing bug: `_ensureCanvasFont` **checked** readiness at an implicit weight (`'16px '+fontFamily`, defaulting to CSS's implicit "normal"/400) but always **loaded** at a hardcoded `'700 16px '+fontFamily` — two different, separately-loadable `@font-face` weight variants in Chrome's font-loading model, so a normal-weight Text object's own check could never be satisfied by a load that only ever requested bold, in the editor as much as Publish; confirmed precisely (`document.fonts.check('700 16px Kalam')` reports `true` right after `document.fonts.load('700 16px Kalam')` resolves, while `document.fonts.check('400 16px Kalam')` stays `false`). Fixed by threading the object's real `fontWeight` through both the check and the load consistently (`_ensureCanvasFont(fontFamily, weight)`, `st.fontWeight` now passed at its one call site). A new exported `SlideRenderer.preloadFonts(slide)` scans a Slide's own freeform Text stickers for every distinct `{family, weight}` pair actually used and returns a Promise resolving once each is genuinely ready; `PublishStudio.open()` now fires this (fire-and-forget, for every slide) the instant Publish opens — well before the Almost Ready/Celebration/actual-export renders that matter — closing the race for any realistic usage without making every render call site async (which would risk its own out-of-order-page bugs on rapid page flips); confirmed directly that the targeted font is genuinely ready within 50ms of Publish opening. Verified via three new Playwright tests (scratch-only, `rule5_audit.js`/`rule5_carousel_fit_check.js`/`rule5_font_check.js`): a real Landscape Scene's Read screen and Almost Ready cover both now correctly resize to 1350×1080 and hold the real artwork with no clipping; the Carousel export's fit-composite shows genuine matching letterbox bars top and bottom with real content variation in between (not a flat, empty, or clipped canvas); the font race is closed, confirmed via the weight-matched check this investigation itself had to establish was the correct one to use. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder Playwright suite (including the Shapes+Text sprint's own `shapes_text_test.js`, confirming the weight-matching fix didn't regress the already-shipped Kalam/Nunito rendering) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `renderer/slideRenderer.js`, `js/publishStudio.js`, and `js/storyDestinations.js`.)

- Rule 5 Follow-Up — Transparent Padding + Baked-In Rounded Corners for Image Exports (a direct, user-clarified follow-up to the Rule 5 audit above, prompted by two real attached screenshots: a Landscape Scene's export showing letterboxed instead of genuinely landscape-shaped, and a downloaded PNG with plain square file corners next to an octagon-shaped test page. Resolved via the user's own explicit direction rather than guessed at: "export needs to match both. visible scene needs to be creator honoured. we can add transparent piece around the image to honour the publishing platform guidelines" — the destination's own fixed file shape (Instagram Portrait 1080×1350, Instagram Square 1080×1080) stays exactly as it was, satisfying the real platform requirement, but the padding around a non-matching Scene is now genuine alpha transparency instead of a filled letterbox bar, so the visible content reads as the Scene's own true, undistorted proportions with nothing fabricated around it. `_fitCompositeInto` (`js/storyDestinations.js`) gained an `opts.transparent` flag — skips its background fill entirely when set, letting the canvas's own default transparency show through; `_renderSlideInto` threads this through from a new `opts` parameter. Scoped deliberately per output format's real technical capability, not applied uniformly: `CAROUSEL.renderPage` passes `{transparent:true}` (PNG genuinely supports alpha); `BOOK.renderPage` (Story Book PDF, JPEG-encoded) is left completely untouched and still fills an opaque background, since a transparent canvas pixel composites to solid BLACK in a JPEG encode, not white — making the letterbox invisible there would have been a real visual bug, not a fidelity win. **Rounded corners baked into the actual exported pixels**: a new `_applyRoundedCorners(canvas)` clips a canvas to a rounded-rect path via `destination-in` compositing, matching the editor's own cosmetic `border-radius:var(--card-radius)` (16px) — a CSS-only effect that, unlike a downloaded PNG file, was never going to appear in the exported bytes on its own, unlike the earlier, narrower "in-app preview canvas corner-radius" fix from the previous Rule 5 sprint. Radius is proportional to the editor's own documented ~720 CSS px on-screen display width (see `#previewCanvas` in `css/style.css`) rather than a flat 16px against the export's much higher 1080px backing resolution, so the exported image's corners read at the same visual proportion the editor shows (`EXPORT_CORNER_RADIUS_RATIO=16/720`, ≈24px at 1080px width) instead of a barely-visible sliver. Applied only to `CAROUSEL.encodePage`'s final composited bitmap (the one real "downloaded image" surface both attached screenshots were examples of) — deliberately not applied to the Story Book PDF/JPEG path, since a printed page's corners are a fundamentally different, opaque physical-page concept where transparency has no real meaning, a disclosed scope decision rather than an oversight. Verified via two new Playwright tests (scratch-only): `rule5_carousel_fit_check2.js` confirms a real Landscape Scene's Carousel export shows genuine `alpha=0` transparency in both the top and bottom letterbox bands and at all four file corners, while the real content pixel stays fully opaque; `rule5_book_opacity_check.js` confirms the Story Book/PDF path is completely unaffected and still produces a fully opaque page. Full regression across the entire existing Creator/Builder Playwright suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/storyDestinations.js`.)

- My Projects — Reach an Existing Project Without Going Through "What Shall We Create Today" (a real, user-requested gap, confirmed via investigation before any code was written: Creator's own persistence (`js/projectManager.js`) has always been a single fixed `localStorage` slot (`'vihustudio-session'`) — one active project, restore-or-discard on reload, no way to see or reopen anything else without wiping that slot; the header's "Open"/"Save As" are file-import/file-download, not a project gallery. Confirmed with the user directly (`AskUserQuestion`) that the real fix — not a lightweight recent-list, not merely surfacing the existing restore modal — was wanted: a genuine multi-project store, mirroring World Builder's own proven `ProjectStore` pattern almost exactly. **New `js/creatorProjectStore.js`** (`CreatorProjectStore`) is purely additive bookkeeping riding alongside the existing single-session slot, never replacing it — `list()`/`get(id)`/`upsert(id,meta,data)`/`remove(id)`, one `localStorage` array (`'vihustudio-projects'`) of `{id,name,thumbnail,createdAt,updatedAt,data}` records, `data` being exactly `ProjectManager.serialize()`'s own existing payload shape, so reopening a record is just `ProjectManager.deserialize(record.data)` — no second project format. **`js/projectManager.js`** gained a small hook: `serialize()`/`deserialize()` now carry a `project.id` field through the payload (defaulting to `null`/unset for anything saved before this feature, handled gracefully); a new `_ensureProjectId()` lazily mints a real id (`CreatorProjectStore.newId()`) the first time any project is ever autosaved — covering both a brand-new Creation-Flow project and a legacy pre-feature session — and `_writeStorage()`'s existing debounced autosave path now also calls a new `_syncProjectStore(data)` on every successful write, upserting the current project (name from `bookTitle`/`title`, thumbnail from the first page) into `CreatorProjectStore` alongside its own unchanged single-session write; a new `openProjectRecord(record)` API wraps `deserialize()`+`_writeStorage()` for the "open from My Projects" case. **`js/creationFlow.js`** Screen 1 gained a small "📂 My Projects `<count>`" pill (`_myProjectsEntry()`) — rendered only when `CreatorProjectStore.list().length>0`, never a dead affordance on a brand-new install — sitting above the six Creation Type cards, reachable before any Creation Type is chosen (the literal "without going through what shall we create today" ask); tapping it opens a new `_renderMyProjectsScreen()` (its own Back-to-Screen-1 header, a 4-up card grid — thumbnail/name/"Edited X ago", newest-first via `CreatorProjectStore.list()`'s own sort, reusing a small `_timeAgo()` helper mirrored from World Builder's own) — tapping a project card calls the new `_openProjectRecord(record)`, which opens it and closes the Creation Flow overlay straight into the editor, bypassing Screen 1/2 entirely. **A real architectural nuance surfaced and correctly handled, not glossed over**: "Start Creating" a second time without a page reload (e.g. via the header's own Home → pick a different World) does NOT mint a second project — `_finish()`'s own pre-existing guard (`if AppState.slides.length===0`) only adds a first page when the current project is genuinely empty, so Home-then-Start-Creating on an in-progress project changes its World/theme in place, exactly as the Home button's own pre-existing, documented behaviour already promised; a project only becomes a second, independent `CreatorProjectStore` record the way any second project genuinely comes to exist today — a fresh page load (a new browser tab, or discarding/restoring the prior session) — which is also where `AppState.project.id` is naturally absent again, so the very next autosave correctly mints a new id rather than overwriting the previous project's record. Verified via a new Playwright test (`myprojects_test2.js`, scratch-only, using real page reloads between two separately-authored projects — not an in-session simulation, which an early draft of this test incorrectly used and which produced a false "same project overwrote itself" failure until corrected): two projects, authored across two real reloads with the restore modal discarded each time, produce two distinct `CreatorProjectStore` records with distinct ids, correct newest-first ordering, and correct names read from the real `#bookTitle` DOM field `serialize()` itself reads (not a bypassed `AppState` write, which an even earlier draft of this test used and which produced a second, separate false failure since `serialize()` has always preferred the DOM field over `AppState.project.bookTitle` directly); the My Projects entry is correctly absent with zero projects and correctly shows an accurate count once projects exist; reopening a project via its card lands on the exact correct project (verified by both its title and its preserved original id, confirming no duplicate record was minted); the pre-existing single-session restore-modal flow is confirmed completely unaffected and still functions independently. Full regression across the existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `baseline3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `book_to_adventure_test.js`, `rule5_audit.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to a new `js/creatorProjectStore.js`, `js/projectManager.js`, `js/creationFlow.js`, `css/style.css`, and one new `<script>` tag in `index.html`.)

- Magic Card Identity Evolution — Phase 1: The Awakening (implements the first slice of `docs`/Artifact "VihuStudio — Magic Card Identity Evolution" (Product Architecture & UX Design), a design document produced earlier in this same arc after an initial menu-driven "Access Card" implementation plan was explicitly rejected by the user and the whole effort was reframed: a Magic Card is never created during onboarding or from a settings menu — it "awakens" the moment a child completes their **first Publish**, and the child chooses whether to **claim** it. There is no sign-in, sign-up, email, password, or account-creation language anywhere; claimed vs. unclaimed is the only identity distinction, and the constellation IS the identity, not a decorative overlay on a separate credential. Phase 1, exactly as the design document's own §19 Product Recommendations scoped it: **"ship the awakening moment first, with claiming initially just meaning 'this device recognizes you' — no cross-device recall yet."** 100% local (`localStorage` only) — no Supabase, no schema change, no `card_type='creator'` mechanism; that remains real, disclosed future work, not built here. **The central design decision, "one constellation, two faces," made real**: new `js/magicCard.js` mints a claimed card's constellation pattern exactly once, at claim time, via `_placeConstellation` (geometry intentionally duplicated, not imported, from `js/cardPlatform.js`'s own version — a handful of small, pure, stable functions with zero Supabase entanglement) — the same pattern is simultaneously the decorative "sky" a child sees as their identity today and, in a future phase, the literal tap gesture that would recall their card elsewhere; nothing about "the sky growing" mutates this fixed core — `growthSignals()` derives purely presentational signals (companion-star count, glow) from real, already-available data (`CreatorProjectStore.list().length`, days since claim) with no counters/levels/leaderboards ever shown to the child. A genuine bug was found and fixed *during* implementation, not after: the first draft generated a separate, throwaway pattern purely for the ceremony's own visual reveal, independent from whatever `claim()` would separately persist — meaning the sky a child watched form during Awakening would not have matched their actually-claimed card's sky, a direct violation of the design's own central promise. Fixed by adding `MagicCard.generatePattern()` (generates without persisting) and widening `claim(nickname, precomputed)` to accept and use a pre-generated pattern verbatim, then threading that one `placed` object through every step of the ceremony chain in `js/magicCardUI.js` (`showAwakening` → `_runReveal` → `_runClaimPanel` → `_runNicknamePrompt` → the actual `claim()` call) — verified directly via Playwright by comparing the reveal stage's rendered star coordinates against the persisted card's own pattern. **Three real screens, one shared overlay** (`#magicCardOverlay`/`#magicCardContent` in `index.html`, mirroring `#creationFlowOverlay`'s own container pattern): the boot-time **Identity Gate** (Screen 2 Returning Creator / Screen 9 Shared Device, `checkIdentityGate`) — shown only when at least one card has ever been claimed on this device, a single card greets by nickname with "Continue My Journey" / "Not you?", multiple cards show a tile picker plus a permanent "🌱 Begin Exploring" non-claiming option; the **Awakening ceremony** (Screens 5-7, `showAwakening`) — triggered from `js/publishStudio.js`'s `_finalizePublish`, right before its pre-existing `_setStage(STAGES.CELEBRATION)` call, gated by `MagicCard.shouldOfferAwakening()` (true exactly once per browser — no claimed card yet, never offered before, regardless of whether that earlier offer was claimed or declined) — reveal → "This card wants to remember you" → Claim/Maybe Later/Just Exploring → nickname prompt → First Claimed Moment → hands off into the existing, completely unmodified Celebration stage; **Magic Card Home** (Screen 11, `openHome`) — reached via a new small header glyph (`#magicCardBadge`, hidden until a card is claimed, rendering a live 26px constellation), shows the active card's full sky, nickname, "Creator since [date]," and up to 8 of the child's own local projects read straight from `CreatorProjectStore.list()` (read-only, no new persistence). **Screen 1 (Welcome) and Screen 3 (Visitor Entry) are deliberately not built as separate code** — the design document itself specifies Screen 1 is skipped entirely with zero claimed cards, landing on Creator's existing, completely unmodified Creation Flow Screen 1; this is what makes the zero-card path (the common case until a family's first claim) genuinely zero-risk, confirmed directly via Playwright. **Boot wiring** (`js/app.js`): the original `bootstrapSession()` IIFE's body became a plain `_beginBoot()` function, unchanged internally; the IIFE itself now checks `MagicCard.list().length>0` and, only then, calls `MagicCardUI.checkIdentityGate(_beginBoot)` — otherwise `_beginBoot()` runs immediately exactly as it always has. **Disclosed Phase 1 limitation, stated plainly rather than glossed over**: the Shared Device picker is presentational/recognition-only — selecting a profile does not yet partition which local projects are visible, since `CreatorProjectStore` has no per-identity data separation today; real per-child separation is named in the design document's own Section 3/15 as later work, not solved here. CSS (`css/style.css`) is a deliberately distinct night-sky visual world — a fixed dark indigo/gold palette (new `--mc-*` custom properties scoped to `.magic-card-overlay`) regardless of the app's own light/dark toggle, mirroring the exact reasoning `.creation-flow-overlay`'s own `--cf-paper` tokens already established for the unrelated, equally distinct daytime Story Meadow; every real `<button>` in the new UI needed explicit `!important` width/height/margin overrides to escape this codebase's own established global `button{width:100%;height:var(--button-height)}` cascade rule — the identical class of fix this project has hit and fixed repeatedly for Object Strip cards, the Publish Studio close button, and Doodle's pen swatches. Verified end-to-end via two new Playwright suites (`magic_card_test.js`, 23 assertions; `magic_card_defer_test.js`, 9 assertions) driving a real, complete first Publish through the actual UI (Read → Almost Ready → Choose Story Destination → real destination/format selection → Publishing → the real `_finalizePublish` hook) rather than calling internals directly: the zero-card boot path is confirmed completely unaffected; a real first Publish triggers the Awakening overlay with a real rendered constellation; claiming persists a card whose sky is pixel-coordinate-identical to what the reveal stage showed; the header badge appears/opens Magic Card Home correctly; a second Publish never re-offers the ceremony; reboot with one claimed card shows the Returning Creator gate and "Continue My Journey" proceeds into normal boot exactly as before; a simulated second card shows the Screen 9 picker with a tile per card plus Begin Exploring; "Maybe Later"/"Just Exploring for Now" both mark the ceremony offered without ever creating a card and correctly never re-offer it on a later publish. Full regression across the existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `baseline3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `scene_object_test.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `book_to_adventure_test.js`, `myprojects_test2.js`, `diag_layerpack3.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors; two pre-existing failures (`myprojects_test.js`, `sticker_owner_check.js`) were confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified baseline, unrelated to this change. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to two new files (`js/magicCard.js`, `js/magicCardUI.js`) plus additive changes to `index.html`, `js/app.js`, `js/publishStudio.js`, and `css/style.css`. Phase 2 (real cross-device recall — a redeemer tapping a claimed card's own constellation to pull their identity onto a new device, via the `card_type='creator'`-style RLS mechanism the now-superseded plan already scoped) remains named, disclosed future work, not started here.)

- Magic Card Identity Evolution — Phase 2: Cloud Identity, Recall, and Two-Sided Card Art (closes the two real gaps Phase 1's own header already disclosed: "we should have identity cards on the superbase. this will essentially our signinless signin so need to safeguard this. also identify card shown during ceremony just had constellation pattern, a card should always have 2 sides and be downloadable, printable for kid." Confirmed via investigation, not assumed, that Phase 1 had zero cloud presence anywhere (`grep` across `js/magicCard.js`/`js/magicCardUI.js` found no Supabase reference at all) before any design work began. Two design decisions confirmed directly with the user via `AskUserQuestion` rather than assumed: **(1)** store the raw pattern on Supabase, safeguarded via RLS lockdown only — matching the exact precedent `cards`/`redeem_card()` already established (zero direct-SELECT exposure to anyone but the owning session; the only way to compare a tapped pattern against a stored one is a `SECURITY DEFINER` RPC that never echoes the secret back on any branch), deliberately not a second, different security model (e.g. hashing) for a very similar problem; **(2)** build the full tap-to-recall screen in this same pass, not just the storage foundation. **Architecture**: local stays authoritative everywhere; cloud is a continuous, fire-and-forget background mirror once a card is claimed — a Visitor (no claimed card) never triggers any network call at all, mirroring `tools/world-builder-v2/js/worldBuilderApp.js`'s own proven `_persist()`→`_scheduleCloudSync()` split. **Schema** (`supabase/schema.sql`, a disclosed, unexecuted draft — this sandbox cannot reach Supabase, the same standing limitation every prior schema change has disclosed): `magic_card_identities` (the identity itself — mirrors `cards`' exact zero-SELECT-exposure shape, minus every Vihu-Card-specific field that doesn't apply to a personal identity — no rarity/tries/duration/target-theme/revoked_at); a real, mid-implementation design correction from the plan's original `id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid()` to **`id text primary key`** (client-supplied, reusing the local `mc_...` id `js/magicCard.js` already mints) — a server-generated uuid would require capturing the Supabase-returned id and persisting it back into the local record after every claim, an unnecessary extra round trip; this matches `builder_projects`/`creator_projects`'s own established client-supplied-id convention rather than `cards`' server-generated one. `magic_card_recalls` (one row per successful recall — mirrors `card_redemptions` exactly, with one deliberate difference: no `expires_at`, since a Magic Card recall is permanent recognition, "coming home," not a time-boxed unlock like a Vihu Card; RLS enabled with zero insert policy for any client role — only the RPC's `SECURITY DEFINER` body can ever write a row). `recall_magic_card(p_pattern jsonb default null, p_typed_code text default null)` — a new `SECURITY DEFINER` RPC, structurally a near-mirror of `redeem_card()`, reusing the existing `_card_platform_sort_pattern()` helper verbatim for canonical set-comparison; compares the input against every stored identity (bypassing RLS internally — the only way this comparison can happen at all without a leaky SELECT policy), and on match updates `last_active_at`, inserts one `magic_card_recalls` row, and returns **only** `{ok, identity_id, owner_id, nickname, constellation, claimed_at}` — the pattern is never returned on any branch, verified via the same static leak-proofing technique already used for `redeem_card` (parsing every `jsonb_build_object(...)` call in the function body). `creator_projects` (Creator's first-ever cloud project backup, mirroring `builder_projects` exactly for owner-scoped CRUD) plus one additive cross-owner **SELECT-only** policy mirroring the exact "re-declare with an added `or exists(...)`" convention already used for `themes_personal_select`/`theme_assets_personal_read`, keyed off a live `magic_card_recalls` row joined through `magic_card_identities` — deliberately read-only for the recalling session, since a recalled project is always adopted as a brand-new local copy on the new device (fresh id, own subsequent row under the new device's own identity), never written back to the original owner's row, matching the "adopt-as-new-copy, never reuse the original id" precedent already established for World Builder's own Repository-Only Card cloning work. **`js/creatorProjectSync.js`** (new file) mirrors `tools/world-builder-v2/js/services/projectSync.js` near-verbatim (`isAvailable`/`push`/`list`/`remove`), plus one new function beyond the reference module, `listByOwner(ownerId)` (mirrors `ThemeRepositoryClient.loadPersonalByOwner`'s existing naming precedent) — what a successful recall calls to pull the original device's projects. **`js/magicCard.js` extended, not rewritten**: `claim()` fires an immediate (not debounced) best-effort push to `magic_card_identities` right after the existing local persist; `touch()`/`rename()` gain a shared, debounced (2000ms, matching `_scheduleCloudSync`'s own timing) background push via `_scheduleIdentitySync(id)`/`_pushIdentitySnapshot(card)`, since `touch()` fires on every `setActive()` call today and would otherwise spam Supabase on rapid navigation; new `recall(input)` calls the RPC (`{pattern:[[r,c],...]}` or `{typed:'ORION-00125'}`, mirroring `js/cardPlatform.js`'s `redeem(input)` structure exactly); new `adopt(remoteResult, pattern)` resolves a real subtlety found via investigation, not assumed — the RPC never returns the pattern (by design, same as `redeem_card`), but the recalling *client* already has it (it's exactly what was just tapped/typed and submitted), so `adopt()` threads that already-known client-side pattern together with the RPC's minimal response into a full local card record matching `claim()`'s own shape, then calls `_pullRecalledProjects(ownerId)` (via `CreatorProjectSync.listByOwner`), materializing each returned record into a new local `CreatorProjectStore` entry with a **freshly minted id** — never the original. **Recall UI** (`js/creationFlow.js`): new `_buildMagicCardRecallPanel()`/`_buildMagicCardRecallWidget()`, structurally parallel to the existing `_buildCardRedeemPanel()`/`_buildCardRedeemWidget()`, reusing `_cardBuildGrid`/`_cardRedrawLiveLines`/`_cardBoardKey`/`_cardCenterOfCell` **verbatim** (confirmed fully generic, zero World/card-type coupling in any of the four) — its own submit handler calls `MagicCard.recall({pattern})`/`.recall({typed})` instead of `window.CardPlatform.redeem(...)`, button text "✨ Come Home"/"Come home with code" rather than "Redeem"/Vihu-Card vocabulary. Two reachable entry points, both quiet/collapsed-by-default matching `_buildCardRedeemWidget`'s own toggle convention: Screen 1 (the zero-local-cards new-device case) and the Shared Device picker (`js/magicCardUI.js`'s `_renderPicker`, a second quiet tile "✨ Recall a different card" beside the existing "🌱 Begin Exploring") — bridged via a minimal one-shot `window.__magicCardAutoOpenRecall` flag (the picker sets it before closing back into boot; Screen 1's render consumes and clears it exactly once), since the two modules have no direct call path into each other's DOM and a heavier shared-state abstraction wasn't warranted for a quiet secondary entry point. **Two-sided card art** (new `js/magicCardArt.js`, Creator-only — no cross-tool sharing needed, since Magic Cards don't exist in World Builder at all, unlike the originally-proposed-but-never-built shared `js/cardArt.js` extraction): `CARD_ART_W/H=700×980` (same print-DPI reasoning as the Vihu Card system's own `CARD_ART_W/H`), `drawFront(canvas,card)` (night-sky gradient reusing `.magic-card-overlay`'s own existing `--mc-*` palette, decorative scattered stars, "✨ MAGIC CARD" kicker — no rarity, since none exists for a personal identity — fit-text nickname title, "Creator since {date}," `card.id` bottom-right, gold border), `drawBack(canvas,card)` (the real constellation plotted from `card.pattern` via the same grid/point/line/glow-star loop ported from the Vihu Card system's own `_drawCardBack`, constellation name, `card.id` again, tagline "Tap the stars to come home." — deliberately never "unlock," that's Vihu Card vocabulary — with an honest "No sky to show yet on this device." fallback for the disclosed typed-code-recall edge case where no pattern is locally known), `downloadDataURL`/`printCard` ported verbatim from the generic, already card-type-agnostic Vihu Card helpers, plus one new `.magic-card-print-sheet`/`@media print` CSS block mirroring `tools/world-builder-v2/css/world-builder.css`'s `.wb-card-print-sheet` exactly. **Wired into the ceremony and Home** (`js/magicCardUI.js`): `_showFirstClaimedMoment` replaces the old bare `_renderConstellation(...)` call with a new shared `_buildCardArtView(card)` (two real canvases, Front/Back labels, Download Front/Download Back/Print actions) — the literal "card shown during ceremony... should always have 2 sides and be downloadable, printable" ask, satisfied in the ceremony itself, not deferred to a separate later modal; `openHome()` gains a "🎴 View My Card" toggle opening the identical view for access any time after the ceremony. **Continuous project sync hook** (`js/projectManager.js`): `_syncProjectStore(data)` gains a new debounced (2000ms, its own separate timer mirroring `_scheduleCloudSync`'s exact shape) `_scheduleCloudProjectSync(id)` call, guarded on `MagicCard.getActive()` truthy — this is the one guard keeping a Visitor's projects 100% local forever, confirmed directly in the mocked test suite (zero network calls attempted while no card is claimed). Verified end-to-end via a new 23-assertion Playwright suite (`magic_card_phase2_test.js`, scratch-only, with a hand-built fake `window.ThemeRepositoryClient.getClient()`/`.getSession()` returning an in-memory fake Supabase client — this sandbox cannot reach a real Supabase project, the same standing limitation disclosed throughout this codebase's history): a real Publish → claim ceremony drives the actual UI (not internals); cloud push payload shape and timing confirmed correct (immediate on claim, debounced on rename); both card-art canvases confirmed to paint real, non-blank, front/back-distinct pixel content; a real browser download event confirmed for both sides; continuous project sync confirmed reaching `creator_projects` only once a card is claimed; and a full "simulate a new device" recall flow — wiping every local Magic Card / project `localStorage` key, calling `MagicCard.recall({pattern:knownPattern})` directly, confirming the identity is adopted with the same id and latest nickname, confirming exactly one project is adopted with a **fresh** id and the correct title, and confirming a wrong pattern correctly fails with `reason:'no_match'`. A static leak-proof check on `recall_magic_card`'s own SQL body (parsing every `jsonb_build_object(...)` branch) confirmed `pattern` is never returned under any outcome. Full regression across the existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright suite (including both Phase 1 suites, `magic_card_test.js`/`magic_card_defer_test.js`, unaffected) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. `docs/VIHU_CARD_PLATFORM.md` gained a new §6.2 clarifying that a Magic Card identity is **not** an instance of the reserved-but-unused `card_type='creator'` enum value — a deliberately separate, parallel system (own tables, own RPC) solving a genuinely different problem (personal/permanent signinless recognition + the recaller's own project recall, vs. a Vihu Card's shareable/disposable time-boxed unlock into someone else's published Theme) — so a future sprint that does build out the real Creator card type would be a third, still-separate thing, not a rename of either system. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; `tools/world-builder/` (v1) and `tools/world-builder-v2/` are untouched — Magic Cards remain a Creator-only concept. Live end-to-end verification against a real Supabase project remains explicitly deferred to the user's own browser, the same standing limitation disclosed for every prior schema change in this codebase.)

- Magic Card Identity Evolution — UI Polish Pass (a direct follow-up after the user ran Phase 2's schema live and screenshotted all four Magic Card screens: "i think we can do better work on UI and UX on these screens." Traced every visual complaint to a real, specific cause before touching CSS, rather than guessing. **The real bug, found in the reported screenshots**: `.magic-card-overlay` centered its content with plain `align-items:center` on a container that also scrolls (`overflow-y:auto`) — when a panel is taller than the viewport (Magic Card Home with the card-art view open, exactly what one screenshot showed), a scrollable flex container's `scrollTop` starts at 0, which shows the vertically-centered *middle* of the oversized content, permanently clipping everything above it, since scrolling further up isn't possible — the exact "two stars with lines cut off at the top of the screen" artifact in the report.
