Fixed with `align-items:flex-start; align-items:safe center;` (the second declaration only takes effect in browsers that understand the `safe` keyword — added to Chromium/Firefox — upgrading to true centering only when content actually fits and silently falling back to the safe `flex-start` baseline otherwise; an unsupporting browser simply keeps `flex-start`, never re-introducing the clipping bug). `.magic-card-home-panel`/`.magic-card-gate-panel` additionally gained their own `max-height:calc(100vh - 64px); overflow-y:auto;` so a genuinely tall panel scrolls internally as a self-contained modal card rather than the whole starfield backdrop scrolling — verified directly via Playwright diagnostics under a deliberately short 460px viewport with content measuring `scrollHeight:892` against `clientHeight:394`: the panel's own top element (`← Studio`) stays fully visible at `scrollTop:0` (`backTopY:53, backVisible:true`), the literal opposite of the reported bug. **A second real bug, found by reading `_renderPicker`'s own DOM-manipulation code**: clicking "Not you?" on the single-card Identity Gate correctly rebuilds the panel into a picker grid, but never removed the "Not you?" button itself — it stayed in the DOM as an orphaned, unstyled-looking underlined heading floating above the grid with no remaining purpose, exactly the stray artifact the third screenshot showed. Fixed in `js/magicCardUI.js`'s `_renderPicker()`: the stale `.magic-card-gate-notyou` button is now removed alongside the grid/welcome/continue/svg elements it already cleaned up, and a proper "Whose adventure is this?" heading is inserted when none already exists (the multi-card boot path's own "Continue Your Journey" title is left untouched, since it's already present by the time `_renderPicker` runs there). **Visual polish, not just bug fixes**: (1) the picker's two action tiles ("Begin Exploring"/"Recall a different card") previously read as a lesser, half-finished sibling next to a real card tile's rich constellation graphic — a new `_buildGateActionTile(icon,label,onClick)` wraps each emoji in a 44px icon-circle roughly matching a card tile's own visual footprint, with a stronger, visible dashed border (`rgba(255,255,255,0.24)` up from a near-invisible `--mc-line`) and a subtle background tint, so all three tiles now read as equal peers. (2) `js/magicCardArt.js`'s `drawFront()` — the Front face of the printable/downloadable card — devoted roughly 70% of its own canvas height to near-total blank space (confirmed directly: the nickname title only started at `CARD_ART_H-200`, i.e. 80% of the way down a 980px-tall canvas), reading as an unfinished card in the report's own screenshot; rebalanced with a deterministic (seeded, not `Math.random()`, so a re-download of the same card always looks identical) dense starfield plus a soft atmospheric radial glow filling the middle third, the nickname title moved to vertical middle (`CARD_ART_H*0.60`), and a quiet divider + tagline ("Every story adds a star to this sky.") giving the lower third real content instead of a long empty run down to the footer code — verified via a full-size render that the front now reads as a genuinely composed card, not a placeholder. (3) Screen 1's recall/redeem widget (`.creation-flow-card-redeem-panel`, shared by both the pre-existing Vihu Card redeem widget and the new Magic Card recall widget, so this fix improves both at once) previously had no background/frame of its own — the small dark "star matrix" tap board sat floating directly on Screen 1's own light meadow background with no visual relationship between the two, reading as pasted-in rather than designed; gained a warm paper-toned card frame (`background:var(--cf-paper-alt); border:1px solid var(--cf-line); border-radius:20px; box-shadow`) around the intro text/board/counter/status/button, and the board itself widened from `max-width:360px` to `420px` to better fill the available column width — the tap board now reads as a dark "night sky" nested inside a warm outer card, rather than an unframed dark box. Verified end-to-end via a new Playwright suite (`mc_ui_polish_check2.js`, scratch-only, with real network requests to any non-localhost origin aborted via `page.route()` so a live Supabase call fails fast instead of hanging the sandbox's proxy for 30s+): the picker fix (`stale NotYou present: false`, heading text, 2 action icon-circles present); the short-viewport clipping fix (diagnostics above); a full-size render of the enriched Front card art. Full regression across both Phase 1 suites (`magic_card_test.js` 23/23, `magic_card_defer_test.js` 7/7) and the Phase 2 suite (`magic_card_phase2_test.js` 21/21) passes unchanged, plus both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2) pass unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `css/style.css`, `js/magicCardUI.js`, and `js/magicCardArt.js`.)

- Magic Card — Decorative Sky vs. Recall Credential, a real security gap closed (a direct, user-raised question: "why are we showing the pattern on first screen, is that not something personal to kid. thats identification." Confirmed, then found to be far more widespread than the one screen first flagged. Every Magic Card's `pattern` is not just decoration — it's the literal credential `recall_magic_card()` checks against (order-independent, per `_card_platform_sort_pattern()`, so anyone who's merely SEEN the dots, in any order, can reproduce it on another device). A full audit of every `_renderConstellation()` call site in `js/magicCardUI.js` found the real pattern was being rendered on FOUR passive, ambient, zero-interaction surfaces, not the one the user first pointed at: the **header badge** (26px, permanently on-screen the entire time a card is active), **Magic Card Home's own top "sky"** (a separate display from the card-art view beneath it), the **"Welcome back" boot-time Identity Gate** (180px, shown automatically to anyone who opens the app, the specific screen the user flagged as worst), and the **Shared Device picker's own tiles** (70px each). Only two surfaces were ever meant to show the real thing: the Awakening ceremony's own one-time genesis reveal (watching the sky form, before it's bound to any identity) and Magic Card Home's explicit "View My Card" action — and even that second one had no protection of its own until this same pass (see below). **The fix, not a UI patch but a real data-model separation**: `js/magicCard.js` gained `decorativeSkyFor(card)` — a small, deterministic, string-seeded generator (`_seededRand`, a splitmix32-style PRNG seeded from `'decorative-sky:'+card.id`, explicitly NOT for anything security-sensitive) that reuses the *exact* existing `_placeConstellation` placement algorithm (refactored to accept an optional `rand` generator, defaulting to `Math.random` so every existing caller — `generatePattern()`, `claim()`'s own fallback — is byte-for-byte unaffected) to derive a SEPARATE constellation from the card's own already-public `id`, rather than fabricating a second secret or persisting anything new — recomputed fresh on every call, needing no storage/migration for cards claimed before this existed. All four ambient call sites in `js/magicCardUI.js` now render `MagicCard.decorativeSkyFor(card).pattern` instead of `card.pattern`; the two legitimate reveal moments are untouched. **Also closed in the same pass — the reveal-gate for "View My Card" that an earlier, mid-turn interruption had been designed but not yet written**: `_buildCardArtView(card,opts)` gained an `opts.gateBack` flag (set only by Magic Card Home's "View My Card" button, never by the ceremony's own First Claimed Moment, which stays the one legitimate "save it now" moment — the same shape 2FA backup codes use). When gated, the Back face — the real recall pattern — renders visually blurred (`filter:blur(13px)`) behind a "🔒 Tap to Reveal" overlay, with Download Back and Print disabled (both DOM-disabled and defensively guarded inside their own click handlers) until revealed; a warning note ("anyone who sees it can become you on another device") accompanies the gated view. A device left open on Magic Card Home can no longer silently hand over another child's recall credential with a glance or a stray tap. Verified via a new 9-assertion Playwright suite (`mc_pattern_leak_check.js`, scratch-only) confirming, by reading the actual rendered SVG star coordinates and comparing them against the card's real pattern: all four ambient surfaces now show a genuinely different set of points than the real credential; the same card shows the SAME decorative sky on every re-open (stable identity, not random noise, so "your sky" still feels personal and consistent); the reveal-gate button is present on Home's View My Card and, once tapped, the Back face still renders real, correct content (the deliberate reveal path still works). Full regression across all three existing Magic Card suites (51 checks total, Phase 1 ×2 + Phase 2) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged. A separate, adjacent finding was surfaced but deliberately NOT fixed in this pass, since it's a different bug with its own scope: the human-readable code printed on the card (`card.id`, the local `mc_...` string) does not match the format `recall_magic_card()`'s typed-code fallback actually expects (`CONSTELLATION`+5-digit server-issued serial) — the server never returns its generated `code`/`serial_no` back to the client after `claim()`'s bare `upsert()`, so the printed "code" and the RPC's typed-code check are checking two different things today; disclosed to the user, not silently patched. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/magicCard.js`, `js/magicCardUI.js`, and `css/style.css`.)

- Magic Card — the Printed Typed-Code Now Actually Matches What Recall Checks (fixes the adjacent bug the previous entry disclosed but left open: "Yes fix that too." `card.id` — the internal, locally-minted `mc_...` random string — was being printed on the card's Front and Back as "the code," but `recall_magic_card()`'s own typed-code branch checks `upper(constellation || lpad(serial_no::text,5,'0'))`, e.g. `CYGNUS00042` — a completely different value the client had never learned, since `magic_card_identities.serial_no` is a server-assigned `bigserial` with no way to be produced offline (the whole reason it's server-side: disambiguating two children who both happen to get "CYGNUS"). Typing the printed code back in would always have failed. **Fix**: `js/magicCard.js`'s `_pushIdentitySnapshot(card)` — the one shared function `claim()` (immediate), `touch()`/`rename()` (debounced) all already funnel every cloud write through — now chains `.select('serial_no,constellation')` onto its `upsert()` and, on a successful response, calls a new `_captureRecallCode(id,constellation,serialNo)` that computes `CONSTELLATION`+5-digit-zero-padded-serial and persists it onto the local card record as a new, additive `recallCode` field — matching `recall_magic_card()`'s own format exactly (verified directly, not assumed: a card claimed with a mocked `serial_no:42` response produces `recallCode:'LYRA00042'`, an exact match). Because every later `touch()` (fired on every `setActive()`, i.e. effectively every app boot) re-runs this same push, a card whose very first sync failed (offline, or simply raced ahead of the network) self-heals the moment any later push succeeds — no migration, no separate backfill job needed for cards already claimed before this fix. `js/magicCardArt.js`'s `drawFront`/`drawBack` now print `card.recallCode` instead of `card.id` — confirmed, not assumed, that `recallCode` is genuinely absent immediately after `claim()` returns (the async push hasn't had a chance to resolve yet at that exact synchronous moment) and only appears once the round trip completes; Front simply omits the quiet corner code until then (nothing worth showing yet), Back shows an honest "Code syncing…" in the same italic/muted style already established for the "No sky to show yet on this device" typed-recall fallback, rather than ever printing something that would fail if typed back in on another device. No RPC/schema change was needed — `recall_magic_card()`'s own typed-code comparison logic was already correct; the entire gap was the client never learning the one piece of data (`serial_no`) it needs to build the same value locally. Verified via a direct Node harness exercising the real promise chain end-to-end (mocked Supabase response, not merely inspected) confirming the exact pending-then-resolved sequence, plus full regression across all four existing Magic Card Playwright suites (Phase 1 ×2, Phase 2, the decorative-sky leak check) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites — all passing unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/magicCard.js` and `js/magicCardArt.js`.)

- Magic Card Home — One Constellation, Not Two (a real, user-reported bug: "my card is showing 2 constellations why?" — traced, not guessed. The previous entry's security fix introduced `decorativeSkyFor(card)`, a deliberately different, seeded stand-in pattern for every *ambient* surface — but Magic Card Home rendered BOTH that ambient sky (a small header block, connected with lines exactly like a real constellation) AND, further down the same panel, the "View My Card" action revealing the REAL `card.pattern` on the Back face — also connected with lines, also labelled with a real constellation name. Two genuinely different star shapes, both drawn as connect-the-dot constellations, visible on one screen — reading as a bug, because it was one: Home had silently broken the platform's own founding "one constellation, two faces" principle (`docs/magic-card-identity-evolution.md`'s central design decision) the moment the security fix swapped what the ambient half of that pair showed. Presented with the fix options, the user chose a third: "show me both sides of the identity card first" — lead Home with the real, two-sided card itself, rather than a separate decorative sky above it. **Fix**: `js/magicCardUI.js`'s `openHome()` no longer builds a standalone `skyWrap`/`growthSignals()`-driven ambient sky at all — `_buildCardArtView(active,{gateBack:true})` (the same reveal-gated Front/Back view the ceremony's First Claimed Moment already uses) is now the panel's own first real content, right after the back button, always rendered immediately rather than behind a "🎴 View My Card" toggle (which is removed, along with its now-redundant hidden host div). The Back face's reveal-gate is completely unchanged — nothing secret is exposed by default, only the *leading* content changed. `MagicCard.growthSignals()` and `_renderConstellation`'s `companionCount` option are left in place, unused for now rather than deleted, matching this codebase's own established "do not remove capabilities, disclose the gap" precedent (Canon Alignment Sprint) — a future pass could re-home the "growing sky" concept onto the card's own Front face instead of a since-removed second constellation. CSS cleanup: `.magic-card-home-sky`, `.magic-card-home-viewcard-btn`, and `.magic-card-home-art-host`(`.hidden`) are removed as genuinely dead rules; `.magic-card-home-name` picked up the small top margin the removed sky wrapper used to provide. Verified via a new 8-assertion Playwright suite (`mc_home_single_constellation.js`, scratch-only) confirming: no `.magic-card-home-sky` element exists anymore; the card art view renders with zero clicks; it is the panel's first real child; zero SVG "constellation" elements remain inside the Home panel itself (the header badge behind the overlay correctly keeps its own separate, unrelated, always-on ambient sky); the Back face is still reveal-gated by default and still reveals correctly on tap; the header badge's own decorative sky is unaffected. The two pre-existing suites that asserted the now-removed structure (`mc_pattern_leak_check.js`'s Home-specific checks, re-pointed at the header badge instead since Home no longer has an ambient surface to test; `magic_card_test.js`'s "Home renders the constellation" check, re-pointed at the card art view) were updated to match, not weakened — both re-verify the exact same underlying properties (a rendered identity, consistent across reopens) through the new, correct structure. Full regression across all Magic Card Playwright suites (Phase 1 ×2, Phase 2, the decorative-sky leak check, this fix's own new suite) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/magicCardUI.js` and `css/style.css`.)

- The Kid's Journey — First Screen to Publishing, With Real Screenshots (`docs/KID_JOURNEY.md`, a documentation-only addition — no application code changed. Answers a direct question: "do we have the journey of a kid documented from first screen till publishing with both roles visitor and creator?" Investigation found the pieces existed but nothing current and unified — `docs/STUDIO_CREATION_JOURNEY_V1.md` is canonical and in-repo but Sprint-11.0-era, written before Magic Card existed at all (zero Visitor/Creator distinction) and stale against Object Strip/Personalize-Refine/Creator V2; the Magic Card Identity Evolution design doc has real Creator/Visitor Journey sections but lives only in scratchpad, was never committed, and its own Phase 2/3 status table is stale. - Kid's Journey Review — Screen 1 Polish Pass (real, screen-by-screen product feedback: "the screen needs to be more lively. why do we have ? on top right. the bottom 2 options are not visualize properly." All three concrete, not vague. **The "?" was genuinely dead for the primary audience**: its own code comment disclosed it as "purely a tooltip (title attr)" — a plain HTML `title`, which never fires on a touch device (no hover state to reveal it), so a child on a tablet could never see its content at all. Fixed by making it a real, tap-to-open popover (`js/creationFlow.js`'s `_renderTypeScreen`, new `.creation-flow-help-popover`) with the same friendly orientation line, closed by a second tap — works identically on touch and desktop now. **The bottom two options genuinely weren't visualized properly**: `_buildCardRedeemWidget`/`_buildMagicCardRecallWidget` each rendered as an independent, identically-styled flat grey bar (`.creation-flow-card-toggle`, plain inline emoji + text) with its own separate dashed divider — no shared grouping, no visual hierarchy, blending into each other and into the meadow background. Fixed with a new shared `_buildOptionToggle(accentClass,icon,title)` helper giving each an icon circle (matching the six Creation Type cards' own visual language) + bold title + chevron, and a new wrapping `.creation-flow-secondary-options` section in `_renderTypeScreen` groups both under one "ALREADY HAVE SOMETHING?" label and one divider, laid out as two peer cards side by side (`.creation-flow-option-card`) with distinct accent tints (violet for the Vihu Card redeem, gold for the Magic Card recall) — two clearly different, clearly grouped options instead of two indistinguishable bars. **"More lively"**: the six Creation Type cards previously appeared all at once, fully static until the pointer actually reached one — a real, avoidable flatness given the illustrated Story Meadow scene around them is already animated. Added a staggered rise-and-fade entrance (`@keyframes creation-card-rise`, `nth-child`-delayed per card so the six arrive as a small ripple rather than a flat wall) and a genuine icon-level hover reaction (`.creation-flow-card-icon` now scales/rotates slightly on hover, independent of the card's own existing lift) — both respect `prefers-reduced-motion`. Verified via a new 11-assertion Playwright suite (`screen1_polish_check.js`, scratch-only) confirming the popover opens/closes correctly on tap with real content, exactly one shared secondary-options section groups exactly two distinctly-accented option cards each with a real icon circle, and the entrance/hover animations are genuinely wired (not just present in a stylesheet nobody applies). Full regression across the entire Magic Card/Vihu Card/Creator Playwright suite (`magic_card_test.js`, `magic_card_defer_test.js`, `magic_card_phase2_test.js`, `mc_pattern_leak_check.js`, `mc_home_single_constellation.js`, `regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `baseline3.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `myprojects_test2.js`, `book_to_adventure_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged, zero console errors. `docs/KID_JOURNEY.md`'s own Screen 1 screenshot and Stage 1 description were regenerated/updated to match, since it's meant to be a living doc kept in sync with real product changes. The same gap ran one level deeper: both panels' own intro copy said "Tap the stars shown on your card" (not "your Vihu Card"/"your Magic Card"), and — a real, confusing collision found while fixing this — both code-entry fallbacks said "Prefer to type the magic word instead?", literally using the word "magic" for the Vihu Card panel, one card system borrowing the other's name. **Fix, in `js/creationFlow.js`**: the toggle title is now "Have a Vihu Card? - Companion Engine Foundation — Sprint C1 (Lumo v1) (implements the first production-ready Companion Engine, per the sprint's own explicit framing: "Lumo is the canonical implementation. Every future companion... must use this same engine without requiring code changes." This sprint's own stated goal was NOT animation — it was establishing the Companion Package Contract, the Companion Runtime, and the State Engine; image swapping only, today. **The Companion Package Contract** — `assets/companions/lumo/companion.json` (`id`/`name`/`species`/`version`/`defaultState`/`states`, the 7-state vocabulary idle/wave/think/talk/celebrate/sleep/curious, each mapped to a PNG filename) plus 8 real PNGs (`hero`/`idle`/`wave`/`think`/`talk`/`celebrate`/`sleep`/`curious`, 480×480, transparent) — is pure data; the engine reading it knows nothing about any specific companion's identity. A real, disclosed gap: the spec described this folder as an already-existing, immutable input, but it did not exist in this environment — resolved by generating disclosed **placeholder production art** (a simple chibi Story Dragon built entirely from Canvas 2D primitives, matching this codebase's own established "reach for Canvas over hand-authoring binary assets" convention) via a headless-Chromium draw-and-export pipeline, rather than blocking on the user or fabricating a claim that real art exists; two real placeholder-art bugs (a mispositioned "spine plate" reading as a stray beard; raised arms for wave/celebrate/think drawn *behind* the head and therefore invisible) were found via screenshot review and fixed by regenerating. `assets/companions/README.md` documents the package folder shape following this repo's established asset-README convention, disclosing the art as placeholder. **`js/companionEngine.js`** (`window.CompanionEngine`) is the generic runtime — `load(id)` (fetches/validates/preloads every declared state image, rejecting cleanly on a missing/malformed package, never throwing synchronously or hanging; one broken image degrades gracefully rather than failing the whole load), `show()`/`hide()`/`isVisible()`, `setState(state)` (falls back to the package's own `defaultState` with a console warning on an unknown state, never throws), `getState()`, `speak(text)` (a rounded speech bubble, static text only, auto-hides after `speakDurationMs`), `destroy()`. The file's header comment explicitly documents the anti-pattern it avoids (`` `if (id === 'lumo')` ``) as prose — verified, not merely claimed, via a comment-stripped static scan confirming zero quoted `'lumo'` string literals anywhere in the file's real code. **`js/companionDirector.js`** (`window.CompanionDirector`) is the one file permitted to know Studio-specific moments — `companionId` is a plain configurable default (`opts.companionId||'lumo'`, the file's own only quoted `'lumo'` literal, statically verified) never a hardcoded behavioral branch — and translates each moment into generic `CompanionEngine` calls exactly per the spec's own choreography: Studio opens → `init()` (hooked once from `js/app.js`'s boot sequence) → `wave` + "Let's imagine!" → `idle` after 3s; user starts creating → `notify('story-started')` (hooked in `js/creationFlow.js`'s `_finish()`) → `think` + "I can't wait to see your story!"; user types → a document-level delegated capture-phase `input` listener (scoped to real Workspace text fields, 4s cooldown, never firing during Creation Flow itself) → `curious`; user inserts artwork → `notify('artwork-added')` (hooked in `js/contextPanel.js`'s `_applyImageResult`) → `celebrate` + "That's wonderful!" → `idle` after 2s; story published → `notify('published')` (hooked in `js/publishStudio.js`'s `_finalizePublish`) → `celebrate` + "Your story is ready!" → `idle` after 2s (my own reasonable extrapolation of a state trigger for "published," since the spec named it only as a speech example — disclosed in code comments); no interaction for 2 minutes → `sleep`; user interacts again → `wave` → `idle` after 2s. Every hook site is a single, defensive `try{ if(typeof CompanionDirector!=='undefined') CompanionDirector.notify(...) }catch(e){}` line, matching this codebase's established "thin hook into a dedicated module" pattern already proven for `PageRuntime`/`ObjectStrip`/`ContextPanel`/`MagicCard` — a missing companion.json, a broken image, or either script failing to load leaves Studio's boot sequence and every one of these call sites completely unaffected. New `.companion-*` CSS renders the widget bottom-right (`right:16px;bottom:40px`, `z-index:1200`) — repositioned there after a screenshot review found the original bottom-left placement collided with Screen 1's own decorative Story Meadow signpost (`.creation-scene-signpost`); the speech-bubble tail and mobile breakpoint were adjusted to match. **Future Ready, by construction**: every public method (`setState`/`speak`/`show`/`hide`) is written so a later version can add crossfade animation, sprite-sheet playback, sound, typewriter/TTS speech, or AI-sourced text without widening the public API — a future package's own extra `companion.json` fields are already treated as inert by `load()`/`_validatePackage()`. **Genuine multi-companion genericity proven, not just asserted**: a hand-authored second package (`nimbus`, carrying a `happy` state Lumo doesn't even have, never mentioned anywhere in `companionEngine.js`/`companionDirector.js`) was written directly to disk and loaded through the identical, unmodified `CompanionEngine`, correctly resolving its own name/species and correctly switching to its own unique state — then cleaned up. Verified via two new Playwright suites (43 assertions total: package-contract validation, the static zero-hardcoded-reference checks described above, the full live boot→think→curious→artwork→publish choreography driven through real UI actions — a real Start Creating click, a real dispatched `input` Event, real `notify()` calls — plus a full standalone `CompanionEngine` API test covering load/show/hide/setState/getState/speak/destroy/unknown-state-fallback/missing-package-rejection; sleep-after-2-minutes-idle and wake-to-wave-then-idle verified via Playwright's fake clock, `page.clock.install()`/`.fastForward()`, rather than a real 2-minute wait; the nimbus genericity proof) plus the full existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright regression suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `magic_card_test.js`, `magic_card_defer_test.js`, `magic_card_phase2_test.js`, `screen1_polish_check.js`, `card_naming_check.js`, `book_to_adventure_test.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites — all passing unchanged, zero console errors. `docs/COMPANION_ENGINE.md` is the new canonical reference (architecture, the full Contract, the public API, the complete choreography table, the placeholder-art disclosure, Future Ready extension points, the nimbus proof, and a Critical Files list). No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to two new modules (`js/companionEngine.js`, `js/companionDirector.js`), one new asset package, and single-line additive hooks in `index.html`/`js/app.js`/`js/creationFlow.js`/`js/contextPanel.js`/`js/publishStudio.js`/`css/style.css`.)

- Companion Platform v1 (Sprint C1, Lumo v1) (extends the prior sprint's Companion Engine Foundation into the full, frozen Companion Platform the follow-up spec asked for — "this sprint establishes the Companion Engine, Companion Package Contract, Runtime, State System, Event System, UI Integration, and Animation Foundation." **A 3-file Companion Package Contract**: `companion.json` (unchanged, required) plus two new optional sibling files — `personality.json` (traits/role/greetings/neverSays) and `animations.json` (a state → transition target and state → auto-revert duration table) — both best-effort loaded alongside `companion.json` in `load(id)`, neither required, so a bare `companion.json`-only package (the prior sprint's own shape, and any future companion that skips them) still loads and behaves exactly as before. **The frozen CompanionEngine public API**: `load`/`unload`/`show`/`hide`/`setState`/`getState`/`speak`/`wake`/`sleep`/`destroy` — `unload()` (new) discards the loaded package and hides the widget while keeping its DOM root mounted for instant reuse by a later `load()` (distinct from `destroy()`, which tears the DOM down entirely); `wake()`/`sleep()` (new) are semantic convenience wrappers (`wake()` → `setState('wave')`, `sleep()` → `setState('sleep')`). **Timing becomes genuinely package-driven, closing the gap the prior sprint's own Director-side hardcoded `setTimeout` constants left**: `setState(state)` now checks the loaded package's `animations.durations[state]`; if present, it schedules an automatic `setState(animations.transitions[state])` after that many ms, cancelled/rescheduled by any later `setState()` call — Lumo's own `animations.json` (`wave:3000→idle`, `celebrate:2000→idle`, matching the spec's exact values) means "Studio opens → wave → (3s) → idle," "artwork/published → celebrate → (2s) → idle," and (via `wake()`'s own `setState('wave')`) "user returns → wave → idle" all now resolve from the package's own data, not a Director-side timer; a `talk`-state package with no explicit duration instead settles via `speak()`'s own bubble-dismiss timer following `animations.transitions.talk` when declared, and `sleep` (declared with a transition but no duration) never times out on its own, ending only via an explicit `wake()`. `js/companionDirector.js` now has **zero** hardcoded companion-animation-timing constants (`BOOT_WAVE_MS`/`WAKE_WAVE_MS`/`CELEBRATE_HOLD_MS` are gone entirely, verified via a static scan) — only Studio's own genuinely separate policy constants remain (`IDLE_SLEEP_MS` 2 minutes, `TYPING_COOLDOWN_MS` 4s), correctly disclosed as Studio-owned, not companion-owned. The boot greeting now prefers a randomly-picked entry from Lumo's own `personality.json` `greetings` array (falling back to the one hardcoded default message only for a package with no `personality.json` at all) — genuine, disclosed personality-driven variety with zero Director knowledge of what the words say. `MESSAGES.artworkAdded` updated to this sprint's own re-spec'd wording ("That looks magical!," was "That's wonderful!"); a new `MESSAGES.idleWake` ("Welcome back!") is spoken on every wake. **Companion Registry**: new `assets/companions/registry.json` (`{companions:[{id,name,species,path}]}`) plus a new static `CompanionEngine.loadRegistry(assetsBase?)` (resolves `[]`, never rejects, on any failure) — `CompanionDirector.init()` now reads its default companion id from the registry's first entry when no explicit `opts.companionId` is given, with `'lumo'` kept as the one, final, disclosed literal fallback only if the registry can't be reached at all (still exactly one quoted `'lumo'` in `companionDirector.js`, statically verified) — adding a second companion (Nimbus, Moss, Nova) is now purely a new asset folder plus one `registry.json` entry, proven directly with two hand-authored throwaway test packages (one exercising a wholly different state vocabulary, one exercising the optional `blink` state below), neither ever referenced anywhere in `companionEngine.js`/`companionDirector.js`. **Companion UI, the spec's other major ask**: the widget is `pointer-events:none` except its portrait circle (the one draggable/hoverable surface, so it can float above Studio UI without ever intercepting a click meant for real controls); dragging switches it from its default CSS-anchored bottom-right corner to explicit clamped `left`/`top` pixel positioning, persisted to `sessionStorage` (`vihu-companion-widget-position`) and restored on a same-tab reload (a genuinely new tab correctly starts fresh, matching how `sessionStorage` itself is scoped by every browser — not a bug, confirmed via a reload-based test after an initial new-tab-based test attempt incorrectly expected cross-tab sharing); a window-resize listener re-clamps an explicitly-positioned widget back into the viewport. **"Automatically avoid overlapping dialogs or menus"**: `js/companionDirector.js` — the one file allowed to know Studio's own dialog system — runs a `MutationObserver` on `document.body` (debounced to one check per animation frame) watching a small, disclosed `BUSY_SELECTORS` list (`#restoreModal`, `#themePickerModal`, `.publish-studio-modal`, `#magicCardOverlay`, all following this codebase's own established "gains/loses a plain `.hidden` class" convention) and calls `engine.hide()` outright whenever any is open, restoring via `engine.show()` afterward only if the companion was visible before that dialog opened — the lowest-risk way to guarantee no overlap without needing to know any future dialog's exact geometry; Creation Flow's own overlay is deliberately excluded, since the companion is meant to stay visible there (that's where the boot wave/greeting happens). **Micro Polish**, all CSS/Canvas, no sprite animation: `show()`/`hide()` now fade via a real opacity/transform/delayed-`visibility` CSS transition (sequenced entirely in CSS, no JS timing) instead of the prior sprint's instant `display:none`; a continuous, subtle `companion-breathe` keyframe on the portrait (paused while dragging); a distinct `:hover` micro-interaction (a slightly larger, gently rotated portrait) separate from the constant idle breathing; a soft scale pulse while `talk` and a bounce while `celebrate`, both driven purely by a new `data-companion-state` attribute `_applyState()` sets on the widget root — the engine itself has zero knowledge that "talk" means "pulse" or "celebrate" means "bounce," that meaning lives entirely in CSS `[data-companion-state="..."]` selectors, so a future companion's richer state vocabulary automatically gets a plain, correct (if unstyled) image swap for any state this stylesheet doesn't yet style; a floating "💤" `.companion-zzz` indicator — a real sibling DOM element (not a `::after` pseudo-element inside the portrait, which would be clipped by the portrait's own `overflow:hidden` circular mask) — shown and animated only while `data-companion-state="sleep"`; and a future-ready, currently-inert random blink loop (`_scheduleBlinkLoop`/`_doBlink`, bypassing `setState()`'s own auto-transition machinery entirely since a blink is a visual flourish, never a real state change) that activates automatically only for a package declaring a `"blink"` state in `companion.json` — Lumo declares none today and the loop is proven completely inert for it via the test suite, ready the instant a future art pass adds one. All new animations respect `prefers-reduced-motion`. Verified via a new 46-assertion Playwright suite (all 3 package-contract files; static zero-hardcoded-companion-reference AND zero-hardcoded-timing-constant checks; the full live boot→think→curious→artwork→publish choreography including the updated message wording; a real mouse-driven drag persisting to `sessionStorage` and correctly restoring on `page.reload()`; sleep-after-2-minutes/wake-to-wave-then-idle via Playwright's fake clock, now correctly re-timed off the package's own 3000ms wave duration rather than the prior sprint's separate 2000ms Director constant; the full `unload`/`wake`/`sleep`/`destroy`/reload-reuses-the-same-DOM-root API surface; `CompanionEngine.loadRegistry()`; the blink-state proof plus Lumo's-own-inertness proof; and the dialog-occlusion hide/restore proof using a real `#restoreModal` open/close) plus the full existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright regression suite (12 scripts, including two that needed only an environment `NODE_PATH`/local-server fix unrelated to this sprint's own code) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites — all passing unchanged, zero console errors introduced by this sprint (the sandbox's own pre-existing, disclosed Supabase-CDN network-block noise, confirmed via direct request-failure inspection, is unrelated). No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; confined to `js/companionEngine.js`, `js/companionDirector.js`, `css/style.css`, `assets/companions/registry.json`, and Lumo's two new data files.)

- Companion Canon Freeze & Asset Integration (aligns the completed Companion Platform with the new VihuPlanet Companion Canon — deliberately a canon-alignment and asset-registration sprint, per its own explicit framing: "not about rebuilding the Companion Engine... purely a Canon Alignment and Asset Integration Sprint." `js/companionEngine.js` was **not touched, not one line** — confirmed via `git diff`, the strongest possible proof of "Existing Companion Runtime reused without architectural changes." **Canon 1 — Story Egg** and **Canon 2 — Lumo** are frozen in a new `docs/COMPANION_CANON.md`: a Visitor is not yet a Creator and has no companion — instead, every Visitor is represented by a **Story Egg** (no face, no limbs, never speaks, expressed only through pose — `hero`/`idle`/`curious`/`thinking`/`excited`/`sleep`/`hatching`), which "exists only until the first Creator ceremony" and "permanently disappears once the Creator is born." **Lumo is not the user's companion** — Lumo is the **Guardian of Story Companions**, the official mascot of VihuPlanet, owned by VihuPlanet, never claimable, appearing during Creator ceremonies and for returning Creators (poses updated to Canon 2's exact 7: `hero`/`idle`/`wave`/`curious`/`think`/`celebrate`/`sleep`, retiring the pre-canon `talk` pose). **Canon 3 — Creator Lifecycle** (`Visitor → Story Egg → Create → Publish → Magic Card → Lumo Ceremony → Creator → Future Personal Companion`) is now the platform's real, wired onboarding flow, not just a diagram. **Asset Registration**: Story Egg is registered as a real canonical platform entity (`assets/companions/story-egg/companion.json` + `animations.json`, both real) with its 7 PNGs genuinely still pending upload — disclosed, not fabricated, per the sprint's own explicit "treat those assets as the immutable canonical versions... rather than generating replacements" instruction (unlike the prior sprint's Lumo placeholder art, no interim art was drawn for the Egg); loading `'story-egg'` today succeeds (real `companion.json`) but every pose 404s to a broken-image glyph via the engine's own existing, unmodified graceful-degradation path until the real PNGs land, at which point **nothing else needs to change**. Lumo's `companion.json`/`animations.json`/`personality.json` were updated to match Canon 2 exactly (`hero` added as a real addressable state — previously a decorative, off-cycle file — `talk` retired and `talk.png` deleted, `role` updated to "Guardian of Story Companions"); `registry.json` gained a `role` field per entry (`guardian`/`visitor`) and a second entry for `story-egg`. **`js/companionDirector.js` rewritten around one small, data-driven `MODES` table** (`visitor`/`creator`) — Visitor vs. Creator is read from `MagicCard.getActive()` (Studio's own existing, unmodified Magic Card Identity Evolution state), and which registry entity actually loads is resolved generically by matching `MODES[mode].role` against each registry entry's own `role` field, **never a literal id branch** — confirmed via static scan: zero `if(id==='lumo')`/`if(id==='story-egg')` anywhere in either `companionEngine.js` or `companionDirector.js`, and exactly one disclosed `'lumo'` fallback literal remaining (used only when the registry itself is unreachable). Visitor mode boots the Story Egg with **zero speech bubbles ever** — enforced structurally via `MODES.visitor.speaks:false`, never left as an accident of Story Egg simply lacking a `personality.json` — and its own pose vocabulary for every existing Studio event (typing→`curious`, creating→`thinking`, artwork→`excited`→auto-idle after 2s, publish→`hatching`→auto-idle after 3s as a disclosed safety net); Creator mode keeps Lumo's exact pre-existing wave+greeting/think/celebrate/sleep choreography completely unchanged. **`notify('creator-born')`** (hooked into `js/magicCard.js`'s `claim()` and `adopt()` — the two real "Visitor becomes Creator" moments, whether freshly claiming or recalling on a new device) swaps the active entity from Story Egg to Lumo via the engine's own frozen `unload()`+`load()` pair on the *same* widget/DOM node — literally the mechanism the prior sprint's own docs named as ready for "a future switch companion UI with zero flicker" — then runs Lumo's boot choreography (wave + greeting) immediately; since this always fires from inside the Magic Card overlay's own open claim/recall flow, the pre-existing, unmodified dialog-occlusion watcher already keeps the whole swap invisible until that overlay itself closes, so no new "reveal" choreography was needed. **`notify('ceremony-closed')`** (hooked into `js/magicCardUI.js`'s `_finishAwakening()`, the ceremony's one true exit point regardless of outcome — Claimed/Maybe Later/Just Exploring) settles a Story Egg left mid-`hatching` back to `idle` when the ceremony closes without a claim, a real edge case since the Awakening ceremony only ever shows once per browser (`MagicCard.shouldOfferAwakening()`, unchanged) — without this, a Visitor who declined once and kept publishing would leave the Egg stuck mid-hatch forever. **Two real, disclosed bugs found and fixed while tracing this exact path, not assumed**: (1) `CompanionDirector.init()`'s call site moved from an unconditional top-level position in `js/app.js`'s boot sequence into `_beginBoot()` — which only ever runs *after* the Magic Card Identity Gate (`MagicCardUI.checkIdentityGate`) resolves — since introducing a real mode distinction this sprint made the previous ordering a genuine bug for the first time (the pre-canon Director always booted Lumo unconditionally, so timing relative to the async, user-gated Identity Gate never mattered before); mode detection now always reflects the gate's own settled outcome, not a stale snapshot from the instant the page merely loaded. (2) `js/magicCardUI.js`'s `proceed(cardId)` only ever called `MagicCard.setActive(cardId)` when `cardId` was truthy, so choosing "Begin Exploring" on a shared device silently left whatever card was *previously* active still marked active in `localStorage` — `MagicCard.getActive()` would keep reporting a Creator even after someone explicitly chose to continue as a Visitor; fixed to unconditionally call `MagicCard.setActive(cardId||null)`, which already correctly clears the pointer when passed `null` (the capability already existed, only the call was missing). Verified via a new 40-assertion Playwright suite (a real `git diff` proving zero `companionEngine.js` changes; static zero-hardcoded-id-branch checks; every Visitor Studio-event → pose mapping confirmed with zero speech at every step, including the 2s/3s package-driven auto-reverts; every Creator Studio-event confirmed unchanged including real speech; the real single-card and two-card Identity Gate UIs driven end-to-end, including a genuine `creator-born` mid-session entity swap and a real drive through the two-card picker's "Begin Exploring" tile proving both the timing fix — companion correctly boots as Story Egg only after the gate resolves — and the active-id bugfix — `localStorage`'s active-card key is confirmed actually cleared) plus the full existing 12-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright regression suite (`regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `screen1_polish_check.js`, `magic_card_test.js`, `magic_card_defer_test.js`, `magic_card_phase2_test.js`, `book_to_adventure_test.js`, `card_naming_check.js`, `mc_pattern_leak_check.js`, `mc_home_single_constellation.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites — all passing unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change, no Companion Runtime/Registry-mechanism/Package-Contract redesign; confined to `js/companionDirector.js`, three Magic Card integration hook sites (`js/magicCard.js` ×2, `js/magicCardUI.js` ×2 including the bugfix), `js/app.js`'s one hook relocation, Lumo's three data files, the new Story Egg package's two data files, `registry.json`, and documentation — zero CSS/`index.html` changes, so no cache-bust version bump was needed this sprint.)

- Companion Canon Freeze — Asset Path Correction (a same-day, immediate follow-up: the previous entry's own asset registration mistakenly nested the Companion Packages under `assets/companions/<id>/`, a misreading of the sprint's own package-*shape* diagram as if it also specified *location* — the sprint's own literal "Expected structure" was always flat, repo-root `assets/lumo/` and `assets/story-egg/`. Discovered the moment the user's real, immutable asset uploads landed via 3 GitHub-web-UI commits at exactly that real, un-nested location — `git fetch`/`git log --stat` on the diverged remote showed 8 real Lumo PNGs and 6 real Story Egg PNGs sitting at `assets/lumo/*.png`/`assets/story-egg/*.png`, never touching `assets/companions/` at all. **Merged cleanly first** (`git merge origin/main`, zero conflicts, confirmed via `git diff --stat` before merging that no file paths overlapped with the prior sprint's own work), then corrected the mismatch: `js/companionDirector.js`'s `init()` now constructs `CompanionEngine` with `{assetsBase:ASSETS_BASE}` (a new, disclosed, one-line module constant, `'assets/'`) and calls `loadRegistry(ASSETS_BASE)` to match — the one, deliberate override point; `js/companionEngine.js`'s own `'assets/companions/'` default stays completely untouched (re-confirmed via `git diff HEAD`, zero lines changed, same as every prior Companion Platform sprint), since the engine is meant to stay generic about where any caller's packages actually live. Every JSON data file the prior sprint authored (`companion.json`/`personality.json`/`animations.json` for Lumo; `companion.json`/`animations.json` for Story Egg; `registry.json`) was `git mv`'d to sit beside the real uploaded PNGs at their real top-level location; the prior sprint's own placeholder Canvas-drawn Lumo art (7 PNGs, no `talk.png`) and the now-fully-superseded `assets/companions/` folder were deleted outright. **A second, real correction, not just a path fix**: the real uploaded Lumo folder turned out to carry 8 poses — a genuine superset of Canon 2's own 7-pose list, including `talk.png` — which the prior sprint's alignment work had *retired* (deleted its own placeholder `talk.png`, dropped `talk` from `companion.json`'s `states` map and `animations.json`'s `transitions`) based on too narrow a reading of the Canon. Since this is real, immutable canonical art — not a placeholder to trim down to spec — `talk` was restored to both files (`companion.json`'s `states` map, `animations.json`'s `talk→idle` transition) rather than discarded a second time; `js/companionDirector.js`'s own `MODES` choreography still never sets `talk` directly, matching Canon 2's own frozen 7-pose vocabulary for what Director actively drives, while the engine's pre-existing, unmodified `speak()` settle-after-bubble mechanism (built in the earlier Companion Platform v1 sprint, generic to any package declaring a `talk`-linked transition) already understands the restored state correctly with zero further code change. Story Egg's real upload covers 6 of Canon 1's 7 poses — `hero.png` is the one file genuinely not yet uploaded, left declared in `companion.json` and disclosed, not fabricated, matching the engine's own existing graceful-degradation-for-a-missing-state-image behaviour; the upload's own leftover `assets/story-egg/temp` (a 1-line GitHub folder-creation placeholder) was deleted. New `assets/lumo/README.md` and `assets/story-egg/README.md` replace the old single `assets/companions/README.md` (deleted), each following this repo's established per-folder asset-README convention; `docs/PRODUCT_ASSETS.md`'s own Product Assets category table — which had never listed the Companion Platform's asset folder at all, a pre-existing gap from the original Companion Engine Foundation sprint, not introduced here — gained one row, `Story Companions | assets/lumo/, assets/story-egg/`, closing that gap while already touching the surrounding area. `docs/COMPANION_CANON.md` and `docs/COMPANION_ENGINE.md` (the two living technical/canon references) were both rewritten throughout to reflect the real, final paths and the real, final Lumo pose count — including a new "Asset Alignment correction" subsection in `docs/COMPANION_ENGINE.md`'s own changelog disclosing the mistake and its fix in full, rather than silently rewriting history. Verified via the existing 40-assertion Companion Canon Playwright suite, updated for the real paths/content (now 42 assertions — the `talk` restoration, the deleted `assets/companions/` folder, and the removed `temp` file each gained their own explicit check) — all passing, including every Visitor/Creator choreography check unaffected by the path change; full regression across the same 10-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform suite this sprint's own predecessor entry already lists, plus both `goldenBuild.js` suites — all passing unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change, no Companion Runtime/Registry-mechanism/Package-Contract redesign, no CSS/`index.html` change; confined to `js/companionDirector.js` (one new constant, two call sites), the relocated asset data files, two new per-folder READMEs, and documentation.)

- Story Egg Interaction & Presence (implements the sprint's own explicit brief — "not a redesign of the Companion Platform... purely about polishing the Story Egg experience" — as a widget-feel pass entirely confined to `js/companionEngine.js`/`js/companionDirector.js`/`css/style.css`: the Companion Runtime's own architecture, the Companion Registry mechanism, and the Visitor/Creator lifecycle's pre-existing pose vocabulary are all completely unchanged, verified via a static diff of every pre-existing Visitor/Creator pose mapping and every one of the Runtime's 10 frozen public method names. **Draggable, "living object" physics**: a small clamped rotation follows drag velocity via a `--companion-drag-rot` CSS custom property (one write per native pointermove event, never a JS animation loop); a throttled sparkle trail (`_spawnParticle('drag')`, at most one every ~90ms); the glow ring brightens while dragging; on release, a brief `.companion-settling` class plays a soft overshoot bounce; the pre-existing 3px drag-vs-click movement threshold now also distinguishes a genuine tap (which never opens a menu or shows dialogue) from a drag, triggering the click reaction below instead. **Idle presence**: a slow, randomized ambient sparkle loop (4-8s at the base richness level, 2.6-5.2s once richer); a breathing glow ring (opacity+scale only, never an animated `box-shadow`); a small "home" environment layer (a soft ground light, a patch of grass, two tiny flowers) rendered behind the portrait, purely decorative CSS/emoji, no images — "the egg should feel like it has a home." **Hover**: `.companion-hovering` brightens the glow ring and spawns occasional particles; a `--companion-tilt` custom property follows the cursor's horizontal position (clamped ±6°), feeding the pre-existing static hover-tilt transform. **Click**: a happy wiggle (a finite, non-looping keyframe) plus an immediate 3-particle sparkle burst — never a menu, never a dialogue/tooltip. **Crossfading pose transitions**: `_applyState()` now briefly dips the portrait image's opacity to 0 around a `src` swap (via the pre-existing `transition:opacity` rule, cleared on the very next animation frame) instead of an instant, abrupt cut — the `src` attribute itself still updates synchronously, so nothing that reads it needed to change. **Emotional presence** — two new, purely additive public methods, `setRichness(level)`/`boostGlow()`: `js/companionDirector.js`'s new `currentRichness()` derives a 0/1/2 level from `AppState.slides.length` (0-2 pages / 3-5 / 6+) and calls `setRichness()` after every page-count-changing event, brightening the glow ring and shortening the idle-sparkle delay range slightly — the engine only ever reacts to a plain numeric `data-companion-richness` attribute, never told what "richness" represents, the exact same discipline `data-companion-state` has used since Sprint C1. The very first `'artwork-added'` notification in a session additionally triggers the new one-shot `boostGlow()` ("user creates first artwork → brighter glow"); later artwork additions don't repeat it. **Studio event: "New Page" → `excited`** — added only to `MODES.visitor.poses.newPage` (Creator/Lumo's own poses are untouched, keeping this scoped to the Story Egg as the brief specifies); `js/pageOps.js`'s `insertBlankPage`/`addBefore`/`addAfter`/`duplicatePage` — the real page-creation call sites reachable from the "+ Add Page" button and the page ⋮ menu — each call a new, thin `_notifyPageAdded()` helper, matching this codebase's own established defensive-hook pattern. **"Wanders home"** (the sprint's own explicit "one additional suggestion"): after a real drag, a randomized 30-60s timer arms; if nothing else happens before it fires, a 70% probability check ("not every time") triggers a slow (1.4s), CSS-eased glide back to wherever the widget's own default `right`/`bottom`-anchored position would be — measured via a real, invisible, single-frame reflow rather than any pixel value hardcoded in JS, so it can never drift out of sync with the stylesheet's own `right`/`bottom` values; once settled, the remembered `sessionStorage` position is cleared and ordinary CSS-anchored positioning resumes. Never armed before a real drag has happened; skipped entirely under `prefers-reduced-motion`, along with every other new spawn/animate path in this sprint (idle/hover/drag/click particles, crossfade, wander-home) — genuinely skipped at the JS level, not merely hidden by CSS. **A real, disclosed bug found and fixed while touching this exact code path**: `notify('creator-born')` called `window.CompanionEngine.loadRegistry()` with no argument, silently falling back to the engine's own generic `'assets/companions/'` default (which no longer exists on disk since the prior sprint's own asset-path correction) instead of the real `ASSETS_BASE` every other registry lookup in the file already uses — harmless in practice only because the empty-list fallback still resolves to `'lumo'`, but a genuine defect in the registry-driven resolution path; fixed to pass `ASSETS_BASE` like every other call site. Verified via a new 55-assertion Playwright suite (static proof of the frozen public API/pose-lifecycle/zero-id-branch/untouched-canonical-PNG invariants; live coverage of environment/glow-ring/particle-container presence; click wiggle+burst+auto-clear with no menu/dialogue; hover glow+tilt+cursor with correct enter/leave; drag rotation+trail+glow+settle-bounce, plus real out-of-viewport clamping; the real `PageOps.addAfter()` UI call site — not just a manual `notify()` — reaching the pose change; crossfade dip-and-clear read synchronously within one `evaluate()` call to avoid a requestAnimationFrame race; richness progressing 0→1→2 with real page-count changes; the one-shot first-artwork glow boost firing once and never again; and a fully deterministic "wanders home" pass — a forced `Math.random()=>0` plus Playwright's fake clock installed *before* the drag so the real `setTimeout` `_armWanderHome()` creates is captured, fast-forwarded past the 30s delay, confirming the slow-glide class engages, the widget returns to CSS-anchored positioning, and the remembered position clears) plus a `prefers-reduced-motion` pass confirming zero particles spawn at all, plus the full existing 10-script Creator/Builder/Card-Platform Playwright regression suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites — all passing unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change, no Companion Registry-mechanism/Package-Contract redesign, no Visitor/Creator lifecycle redesign; confined to `js/companionEngine.js` (additive: drag physics, particles, glow ring/environment, crossfade, `setRichness`/`boostGlow`), `js/companionDirector.js` (the `newPage` pose mapping, `currentRichness()`, the `loadRegistry` bugfix), `js/pageOps.js` (4 thin hook sites), `css/style.css`, and documentation.)

- Story Egg Hatching / Lumo Ceremony Visibility Fix (a real, user-reported bug: "when we click on publish from studio the egg disappears why? the flow of egg hatching and lumo assisting in hatching is missing." Audited directly against `docs/COMPANION_CANON.md`'s own Canon 1/Canon 3 (the Story Egg's canonical `hatching` pose, and "Lumo Ceremony" as a real, named stage of the Creator Lifecycle) and found a genuine, confirmed gap between what the Canon documents and what a real Story Author ever actually saw. **Root cause**: Sprint C1's own occlusion watcher (`js/companionDirector.js`'s `BUSY_SELECTORS`, "automatically avoid overlapping dialogs or menus") was written before the Magic Card Awakening ceremony existed, and treated `#magicCardOverlay` as just another dialog to hide behind — but the ceremony always opens ON TOP OF an already-open `.publish-studio-modal` (itself a `BUSY_SELECTOR`, open through the whole Read → Almost Ready → Destination → Publishing flow), so the companion widget was hidden the instant Publish Studio opened and never became visible again until the entire flow closed. Two real, designed-for moments were consequently never seen by anyone: `notify('published')` setting the Story Egg's own canonical `hatching` pose (set correctly, just on a hidden widget), and `notify('creator-born')`'s live Egg-to-Lumo swap mid-ceremony (Canon 3's "Lumo Ceremony," also fired correctly, also invisible). **Fix, confined to the two files the occlusion mechanism already lives in**: `#magicCardOverlay:not(.hidden)` is no longer one of the plain `BUSY_SELECTORS` — it's now a separate `CEREMONY_SELECTOR` checked first in `isStudioBusy()`, forcing the companion visible whenever the Magic Card overlay is open, regardless of what else (Publish Studio) is open behind it; the Read/Almost Ready/Destination/Publishing stages keep hiding the companion exactly as before (unchanged, avoids clutter over functional UI), since the override only ever engages once the overlay itself is open. `css/style.css`'s `.companion-widget` z-index raised from 1200 to 1450 — being merely "not hidden" wasn't enough, since the Magic Card overlay's own full-bleed, fully-opaque background (z-index 1400) would otherwise still visually paint over a same-z-tier widget; 1450 sits above the overlay (1400) while staying below the restore-session modal (2000), the one dialog that should still fully cover it. No architecture change, no new choreography, no new assets — both `notify('published')`/`hatching` and `notify('creator-born')`/the live swap were already correctly implemented and firing; they simply had nowhere visible to render. Verified via a new Playwright suite (scratch-only): the companion stays correctly hidden during Read/Destination as before; becomes visible the instant the Awakening reveal opens, sitting in the corner throughout "It's yours, if you'd like it." and the Claim/Maybe Later/Just Exploring panel; on Claim, visibly swaps to Lumo (wave pose, real `assets/lumo/wave.png`, a real greeting speech bubble — "Ready to create?") right there beside the First Claimed Moment's two-sided card reveal, genuinely realizing "Lumo assisting" for the first time; on Maybe Later, correctly settles to `idle` (Egg, still Visitor) and returns to hidden once only Publish Studio remains open, then reappears correctly once Publish Studio itself is closed. Full regression across the existing Companion/Magic Card/Creator Playwright suite (`companion_canon_test.js`, `story_egg_polish_test.js`, `magic_card_test.js`, `magic_card_defer_test.js`, `magic_card_phase2_test.js`, `mc_pattern_leak_check.js`, `mc_home_single_constellation.js`, `regression.js`, `final_qa.js`, `runtime_pass_test.js`, `publish_stages.js`, `screen1_polish_check.js`, `card_naming_check.js`, `book_to_adventure_test.js`) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites passes unchanged; `companion_engine_test.js`/`companion_platform_v1_test.js` (stale, pre-Asset-Path-Correction paths) and 4 assertions in `companion_engine_test2.js` (stale, pre-Canon-Freeze Creator-only assumptions) were confirmed via `git stash` to already fail identically on the unmodified baseline, unrelated to this fix. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change, no Companion Registry-mechanism/Package-Contract redesign; confined to `js/companionDirector.js` and `css/style.css`.)

- Sparkle Trail / Settle Bounce Contrast Fix (a direct, same-session follow-up to a second user report: "throttled sparkle trail is not visible. neither the soft bounce." Investigated via real pixel-level evidence rather than trusting the JS/CSS mechanism alone — a first pass confirmed sparkles genuinely spawn and animate (real DOM elements, real non-zero computed `opacity`/`transform`/`color` sampled mid-drag) and the settle-bounce class genuinely applies with a real, measurable `translateY`/`scale` oscillation across sampled frames — but a real, zoomed (4x device scale) screenshot taken at that exact moment showed **zero visible sparkle**, confirming this wasn't "just hard to notice," it was a genuine contrast/scale defect: a 12px pale-gold (`#FFCB45`) glyph at 20-75% opacity has almost no luminance difference against this app's own light cream/white palette, so it was rendering essentially invisibly even though every mechanism underneath it was firing correctly. **Fix, in `css/style.css`**: `.companion-sparkle`'s base glyph size raised 12px→20px; its glow layered with a white halo underneath the existing gold one (`text-shadow:0 0 2px #fff, 0 0 5px rgba(255,255,255,.9), 0 0 8px rgba(255,203,69,.85)`) so it reads against any background — the light meadow, a white panel, or the dark ceremony overlay — rather than only one; every keyframe's peak `scale()` raised (idle 0.9→1.15, hover 0.8→1.05, drag start 0.55→1, burst end 1→1.3) so the effective rendered size is genuinely eye-catching instead of shrinking further via the animation's own math. The settle-bounce keyframe's amplitude was similarly widened (±3px/±2px `translateY`, scale 0.93-1.05 → ±7px/±5px, scale 0.87-1.1, plus a small extra settle beat) and its duration extended from .42s to .5s for a clearer "boing" on a ~92px object; `js/companionEngine.js`'s `SETTLE_CLASS_MS` constant bumped from 420 to 520 to match (the class must outlive the animation or it gets cut off mid-play). Verified via the same zoomed-screenshot technique that first caught the defect: post-fix, the sparkle is now a clearly visible bright white-gold burst near the widget in a real screenshot, not just a passing computed-style assertion. Re-ran the full existing 55-assertion Story Egg Interaction & Presence Playwright suite (all pass unchanged — none of it asserted exact keyframe pixel values, only presence/class/timing-window behaviour, which is untouched) plus the Companion Canon/Magic Card/Creator regression suite and both `goldenBuild.js` suites, all passing. A stray, untracked, empty `assets/companions/` directory — a leftover filesystem artifact from an earlier sprint's own folder relocation, invisible to `git status`/`git ls-files` since git never tracks empty directories, unrelated to this fix — was found and removed during this verification pass. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change, no Companion Registry-mechanism/Package-Contract redesign; confined to `css/style.css` and one constant in `js/companionEngine.js`.)

- Companion Canon V2 — Guardian & Creator Bond (a complete product-canon update, delivered by the product owner as a frozen specification with its own explicit governing instruction: "This sprint is a product canon update, not a feature implementation. Where existing code conflicts with the new canon, the canon takes precedence. Preserve the generic architecture, but align the experience to the finalized mythology of VihuPlanet." Corrects a real mythology mismatch the earlier Companion Canon Freeze sprint had baked into `js/companionDirector.js`: Lumo was wired as the permanent, ongoing entity for every claimed Magic Card (`MODES.creator` resolved by `role==='guardian'` match, forever) — the new canon makes this explicitly wrong. **Lumo is the Guardian of Story Companions**, VihuPlanet's own mascot — keeper of Creator Ceremonies, appearing *only* during a Creator Ceremony, never bonding with any Creator, never appearing on a Magic Card, never the ongoing Creator-mode presence. **Every Creator instead receives exactly one Story Companion, chosen for them, during their own Creator Ceremony** — "the Companion chooses the Creator," never a manual pick. Two design decisions were confirmed with the user directly before implementation: the ceremony renders as a real, new, big centered stage (not a reuse of the small corner widget); and, per the user's own follow-up ("am adding new companions. the system has to randomly select a companion for the kid. lumo does not bond with any kid"), two real, literal-from-spec Story Companion registry entries — **Nimbus (Dream Sprite)** and **Quill (Ink Spirit)** — were seeded this sprint so genuine randomness has more than one entry to prove itself against; matching the already-accepted precedent for Story Egg's own still-missing `hero.png`, **no placeholder art was generated for either** — both declare the full pose contract and disclosed-pending art, relying entirely on `CompanionEngine`'s existing, proven graceful degradation (a missing pose image 404s to a broken-image glyph, never crashes) — flagged explicitly in the approved plan as the one open call made on the user's behalf. **A third role joins the existing two-role model** (`assets/registry.json`): `visitor`→Story Egg (unchanged), `guardian`→Lumo (now used *only* inside the ceremony, never ambiently), `companion`→a bondable Story Companion (Nimbus/Quill today). **The Companion Pose Contract v2** — every Story Companion implements 12 poses (`hero, idle, wave, curious, think, happy, celebrate, sleep, sad, surprised, magic, hatching`), `hatching` mandatory and used only during the birth sequence, never re-triggered; Story Egg's own contract grows from 7 to 8 poses (`+magic`, used during the ceremony's Glow beat) while still never receiving emotional poses; Lumo's own 8-pose set is deliberately left unexpanded — a disclosed reading that the 12-pose contract governs Story Companions, not the Guardian, since Lumo never hatches and needs no `sad`/`surprised`. **Random bonding** (`js/magicCard.js`): new `assignBondedCompanion()` calls the existing `CompanionEngine.loadRegistry()`, filters to `role==='companion'`, and picks via `Math.random()` — isolated in one small function so a future smarter policy (avoiding repeats across siblings, seasonal weighting) can replace the picking logic with zero caller change, matching the canon's own "may initially use deterministic assignment... future logic can evolve without changing the canon." `claim()` calls this exactly once, at the moment a Visitor becomes a Creator, and the result is permanent — never re-rolled; a new `ensureBondedCompanion(cardId)` retroactively (and idempotently) bonds any legacy card claimed before this sprint the first time Creator-mode resolution needs one, persisting and cloud-pushing the result rather than crashing or silently defaulting to Lumo; cross-device recall (`adopt()`) never re-rolls either — it inherits the already-bonded companion fields from the recall RPC's own response, since the bond travels with the identity, not the device (`recall_magic_card()`'s success payload gains `companion_id`/`companion_name`/`companion_species`, still never the pattern on any branch, reverified via the same static `jsonb_build_object` leak-proofing every prior RPC change in this codebase has used). **`js/companionDirector.js`'s entity resolution was rewritten around the new model**, not merely patched: `MODES.creator` lost its `role` field entirely (Creator-mode resolution is now per-Magic-Card, never role-based) — a new `_resolveEntityIdByRole` (the shared role-match helper, holding the one remaining disclosed `'lumo'` fallback literal, used only if the registry itself is unreachable), `_resolveCreatorCompanionId` (async — reads the active card's `companionId`, falling back to `ensureBondedCompanion()` for a legacy card), and `_resolveIdForMode` (the shared dispatcher both `init()` and `notify('creator-born')` now call) replace the old always-Lumo lookup. **The Creator Ceremony becomes a real, reusable, data-driven orchestration** rather than the prior sprint's corner-widget-scale Awakening: new public `CompanionDirector.getCeremonySequence(companionId, companionName, companionSpecies)` returns a pure-data 7-beat array — Story Egg (`idle`) → Glow (Story Egg, `magic`) → Cracks (Story Egg, `hatching`) → Lumo arrives (`wave`, greeting speech) → Blessing (Lumo, `celebrate` + a real sparkle burst) → Companion Hatching (the just-bonded companion, `hatching`) → Companion Hero (`hero`, greeting speech) — with zero DOM/timer logic baked in, so a future companion needs zero code change to play through the identical sequence. Rendering lives entirely in `js/magicCardUI.js` (`_runCreatorCeremony`/`_playCeremonyBeats`/`_ceremonyResolveEntity`/`_entityLookupFor`/`_ceremonySparkleBurst`), a genuinely new big centered stage mounted inside the existing `#magicCardOverlay`, reusing the Story Egg Interaction & Presence sprint's own `companion-glow-breathe`/`companion-sparkle`/`companion-sparkle-burst` keyframes verbatim (styled via new `.magic-card-ceremony-*` CSS) plus one new keyframe (`magicCardCeremonyCrack`) for the Cracks effect. **A real, deliberate behavior change**: `MagicCard.claim()` no longer fires the instant the nickname prompt's "Continue" is clicked — it now fires only *after* the full ~14-second ceremony completes, with the random companion resolved right at the ceremony's own start, so "the sky the child watches form is guaranteed to match the sky/companion their card actually has afterward" — the established "one constellation, two faces" design principle, now extended to "one companion, two faces." "Maybe Later"/"Just Exploring" never reach the ceremony at all — `notify('ceremony-closed')` settles the Egg to idle exactly as before, unchanged. **The Magic Card becomes the permanent record of the Creator Bond**: the card record gains three permanent fields (`companionId`/`companionName`/`companionSpecies`, set once at `claim()`, never mutated); `growthSignals()` gains a derived `worldCount` (distinct `project.theme` values across `CreatorProjectStore.list()`) alongside the existing derived project count — "Stories Created"/"Worlds Created" are always computed live, never stored, matching the pre-existing derive-don't-duplicate convention; Achievements stay explicitly unbuilt, per the canon's own "(future)" marker. `js/magicCardArt.js`'s `resolveCompanionPortrait(companionId)` independently resolves a companion's `hero.png` via its own `fetch`, matching this codebase's established pattern of small, independently-duplicated asset-resolution helpers; `drawFront(canvas,card,opts)` gained an optional `opts` parameter for progressive, non-blocking portrait rendering plus the derived Stories/Worlds counts, with a real companion-portrait circle (top-right, a gold ring, a "✨" placeholder glyph for Nimbus/Quill's still-pending art) and a "with `<Name>`, your `<Species>`" line — dynamically-computed spacing keeps a companion-less legacy card's layout unaffected until it's retroactively bonded. `supabase/schema.sql` gains 3 new nullable columns on `magic_card_identities` (`companion_id`/`companion_name`/`companion_species`, both inline in the table definition and via idempotent `alter table ... add column if not exists` for already-deployed installs) — a disclosed, unexecuted draft, this sandbox cannot reach Supabase, the same standing limitation disclosed for every prior schema change in this codebase. **`js/companionEngine.js` was not touched — zero lines changed, verified via `git diff`** — the Companion Runtime remains fully generic, with no idea whether it's rendering a Story Egg, Lumo, or any Story Companion; it only ever receives a plain registered id and a plain pose name, matching every prior Companion sprint's own established discipline; there is still no `if(id==='lumo')`/`if(id==='nimbus')` anywhere in either `companionEngine.js` or `companionDirector.js`, reconfirmed via the same comment-stripped static scan this project's Companion sprints have used from the start. `docs/COMPANION_CANON.md` was rewritten in place to freeze V2 (the Guardian role, Story Companion canon, the species table, the 12-pose contract, the full ceremony sequence, the Magic-Card-as-Creator-Bond-record framing) and now explicitly documents Lumo as never the user's companion; `docs/COMPANION_ENGINE.md` was substantially updated (the new role/resolution mechanism, the ceremony orchestration's real location, the disclosed Nimbus/Quill art gap); `docs/WORLD_CARD_PLATFORM.md` §6.2 gained one clarifying paragraph distinguishing the new Creator-Companion Bond fields as a Magic-Card-only concept with no World Card equivalent. Verified via a new 40-assertion Playwright suite (registry resolves exactly 2 `role:'companion'` entries; `assignBondedCompanion()` picks across both over repeated calls, proving real randomness; `claim()` produces a card with real companion fields; a legacy card with no companion fields is correctly retroactively bonded on first Creator-mode resolution; the full ceremony renders all 7 beats in the correct order with the correct entity/pose/effect/speech at each boundary, including a real sparkle burst and a real hand-off into a companion-bonded First Claimed Moment card view; Nimbus/Quill's missing pose images degrade gracefully with zero console crash; every static invariant above) plus a full regression pass across the existing Creator/Builder/Card-Platform/Magic-Card/Companion Playwright suite — 2 stale assertions in `magic_card_phase2_test.js` (a fixed-timeout wait that assumed the old instant-claim behavior, now correctly waiting for the real ceremony to complete) and 3 stale assertions in `companion_canon_test.js` (the old 7-pose Story Egg count, and two Creator-mode "boots lumo" checks now correctly checking for the bonded companion instead) were updated to match this sprint's own intentional, disclosed behavior changes — confirmed via `git stash`/`git stash pop` comparison against the unmodified baseline that these 3 checks passed there and only fail with this sprint's changes applied, i.e. they were genuinely testing now-superseded behavior, not catching a regression; a handful of other pre-existing, unrelated test failures (`companion_engine_test2.js`'s stale message-text/state assertions, `companion_platform_v1_test.js`/`companion_engine_test.js`'s stale pre-Asset-Path-Correction paths) were confirmed via the same `git stash` technique to already fail identically on the unmodified baseline and were left untouched, disclosed rather than fixed. Both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2) pass unchanged, confirming zero impact on the unrelated Builder tooling. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder change; `tools/world-builder/` and `tools/world-builder-v2/` are untouched — Magic Card / Companion Canon remain Creator-only concepts; confined to `assets/registry.json`, `assets/nimbus/`, `assets/quill/` (new), `assets/story-egg/companion.json`, `js/companionDirector.js`, `js/magicCard.js`, `js/magicCardUI.js`, `js/magicCardArt.js`, `css/style.css`, `supabase/schema.sql`, and documentation.)

- Welcome-Back Gate — the Constellation Pattern Is Never Shown, Not Even the Decorative Stand-In (a real, user-reported bug with a screenshot: the boot-time "Welcome back, `<nickname>`" Identity Gate — the very screen the Magic Card — Decorative Sky vs. Recall Credential sprint had already flagged as "the worst possible surface to show the real recall pattern on" — was still rendering a connect-the-dots constellation graphic. Confirmed via code read, not assumed, that this was NOT a regression of that earlier fix: `checkIdentityGate`'s single-card branch and `_renderPicker`'s multi-card tiles both already correctly called `MagicCard.decorativeSkyFor(card).pattern` (the safe, non-secret stand-in derived from the card's own public id), never `card.pattern` (the real recall credential). The user's instruction — "the pattern is never to be shown" — was a stronger, simpler directive than the earlier fix implemented: a dot-and-line star map reads as "my secret code is on screen" to a viewer regardless of whether it's the real pattern or a decorative one, since the two are visually indistinguishable. **Fix**: both call sites now render a new `_buildGateIdentityGlyph(card,size)` instead of any constellation at all — a plain circular glyph showing the Creator's own bonded Story Companion portrait (resolved async via the existing `MagicCardArt.resolveCompanionPortrait(card.companionId)`, the same mechanism Companion Canon V2's card-art already uses) once it loads, falling back to a quiet "✨" glyph while loading, when no portrait is available (Nimbus/Quill's disclosed pending-art gap), or for a legacy card not yet retroactively bonded. `_renderPicker`'s own cleanup logic — which previously removed a stray leftover `svg.magic-card-constellation-svg` when switching from the single-card view to the picker — now removes the standalone `.magic-card-gate-glyph` instead, since that svg-specific cleanup no longer has anything to find on this screen. `_renderConstellation` itself is untouched and still correctly used on the two surfaces the earlier fix always intended to keep it on — the one-time Awakening ceremony reveal and Magic Card Home's own reveal-gated card view — plus the header badge, which was never part of this report and keeps its own decorative sky exactly as before.
