Verified via a new 13-assertion Playwright suite measuring real `getBoundingClientRect()` geometry (not just class presence) at rest, mid-Journey, and at Arrival — confirming the Gate wrap and its inner video frame both genuinely span 0,0 to the full viewport at rest, that `.gateway-panel` itself is truly viewport-tall, that Lumo stays visibly on-screen in front of the Gate at every zoom level including the massive Arrival scale, and that the same full-bleed coverage holds at a real 390×844 mobile viewport too — plus real screenshots at every beat confirming the composition reads well (the doors now genuinely dominate the frame, Lumo stands guard clearly on the right, the Egg is small and dim at bottom-left, and the Awaken beat's halo glow/magic sparks/Egg brightening are all still clearly visible layered atop the video). Full regression across every existing Gateway suite (the 21-assertion Traveller-path suite, the 7-assertion Returning-Creator-path suite, the tap-to-skip sanity check) passes unchanged, plus both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected — this sprint touches zero Builder files). No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `css/style.css`, with a matching cache-bust version bump on both stylesheet `<link>` tags in `index.html`.)

- Remove the Environment Elements (a direct, immediate follow-up on the just-shipped full-screen Gate: "ok i like the full screen thing but rest is not working out. remove the environment elements." The old illustrative ambient-sky decoration layer — `.gateway-scene`'s clouds/islands/birds/particles/rays/haze/sun/wind-streaks, plus Scene 5's separate `.gateway-journey-extras` streaming cloud/mountain/bird parallax bands — only ever clashed with a real, full-bleed cinematic Gate video: they'd bleed through visibly during the Gate's own 1.8s opacity fade-in (confirmed directly — a mobile screenshot taken 400ms after mount showed real cloud/bird shapes overlaid on the doors), and even once the Gate turned fully opaque, the whole layer was pure dead weight sitting behind it. **Removed entirely**: `index.html`'s `.gateway-scene` div (17 decorative child elements) is gone outright, leaving only `#gatewayContent` inside `#gatewayOverlay` — `.gateway-overlay`'s own background gradient is the sole remaining pre-video atmosphere, invisible the instant the Gate paints. `css/style.css` lost the full `.gateway-scene-*`/`.gateway-wind-streak` rule set (~150 lines: sky/haze/rays/sun gradients, 3 clouds with pseudo-element puffs, 3 islands, 3 birds, 6 particles, 3 wind streaks, and their 6 keyframes) plus the Journey's own `.gateway-journey-extras`/`-near`/`-far` parallax bands and 2 keyframes, plus every reduced-motion and `.gateway-hush` rule that referenced the now-removed selectors (the halo-dimming half of `.gateway-hush` is kept, since the Gate's own glow effect is unrelated and unaffected). `js/gatewaySequence.js`'s `playApproachLeadIn()` and `playJourney()` are simplified to match — the wind-rising/journey-active class toggles and the emoji-span construction in `playJourney()` are removed since they drove zero remaining CSS, while the underlying `WIND_RISE_MS`/`JOURNEY_MS` timing beats themselves (and their place in the six-scene pipeline) are kept unchanged, so overall pacing is unaffected. Verified via a full re-run of the existing 41-assertion Gateway Playwright suite (21 Traveller-path + 7 Returning-Creator-path + 13 full-screen-coverage geometry assertions, all unchanged since none of them ever depended on the removed decorations) plus a direct before/after mobile screenshot comparison confirming the exact cloud/bird bleed-through artifact is gone — the Gate now reads as a clean, uncluttered cinematic backdrop from the very first frame at every viewport size. Both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected) pass unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `index.html`, `css/style.css`, and `js/gatewaySequence.js`, with a matching cache-bust version bump on both stylesheet `<link>` tags.)

- Lumo's Arrival Becomes a Real Video, Not a Static PNG (a direct, explicit instruction on top of the just-shipped Gate work: "instead of static png portrait fly in this dragon" — pointing at a second, separate, newly-uploaded clip, `assets/video/gateway/lumo-flying.mp4` (1024×1024, H.264/no-alpha, 5.04s/121 frames, no baked-in gate/environment — an isolated Lumo character on a genuinely pure `(0,0,0)` black background, confirmed via `ffmpeg`+raw-pixel sampling before committing to a compositing technique). This is a different file from the earlier-uploaded, still-unwired `gate-sequence-01.mp4` (which shows Lumo flying INTO a mismatched gate design and dissolving into its light — a real, disclosed canon conflict with this file's own header comment, "Lumo never enters the Hall," left untouched pending the user's own explicit direction, exactly as the prior sprint's entry already recorded); this sprint touches only the new `lumo-flying.mp4`. **The technique**: `mix-blend-mode:screen` (pure CSS, zero per-frame canvas/JS processing) — a genuinely `(0,0,0)`-black backdrop composites to fully transparent under `screen`, so Lumo's own bright, saturated art shows while the black around it vanishes into whatever's behind it (the Gate). `mountLumo(lumo,reduced)` (`js/gatewaySequence.js`) is rewritten: the pre-existing static `<img class="gateway-lumo-portrait">` still settles Lumo into its guard post exactly as before, but now starts `.gateway-lumo-pending` (invisible) while a real `<video muted playsinline preload="auto">` (`LUMO_FLY_VIDEO_SRC`, classes `gateway-lumo-portrait gateway-lumo-flying gateway-lumo-flyvideo`) plays the arrival instead, reusing the exact pre-existing `.gateway-lumo-arrive` 1.8s CSS keyframe unchanged — only WHAT flies in changed, not the choreography flying it in. After `FLIGHT_MS` (4900ms, matching the clip's own real ~5.04s length with a small buffer), the video fades out (`.gateway-lumo-flyvideo-out`, a .25s opacity transition) and is removed from the DOM, while the static portrait becomes `.gateway-lumo-settled` and the stage's own pre-existing idle bob/blink/wing-flutter/cursor-tilt system takes over exactly as it always did — the two are never visible at once. Reduced motion skips the video path entirely, exactly matching the file's own established discipline: the static portrait is simply already settled, with zero video ever created or `.play()`'d. **A real gap found and closed during verification, not shipped blind**: sandbox screenshots at the video's own early/mid playback points showed nothing at all where Lumo should be — traced to two compounding, real reasons, not one: (1) this sandbox's headless Chromium genuinely cannot decode H.264 at all (the same already-documented limitation the Gate video hit earlier this session — confirmed here too via a spy-based `.play()`-was-called check, since `.paused` never flips despite a real, successful call), and (2) unlike the Gate video (which sets `video.poster=GATE_POSTER_SRC` as a fallback), the new flying video had no `poster` at all — so with no real frame ever decoding and nothing to fall back to, it painted nothing, period. Fixed by extracting a real frame-0 still (a clean, joyful waving pose, isolated on the same solid-black background) via `ffmpeg`, saving it as `assets/video/gateway/lumo-flying-poster.jpg`, and wiring `flyVideo.poster=LUMO_FLY_POSTER_SRC` — matching the Gate video's own established fallback discipline exactly, and giving both a slow connection and this sandbox's decode-incapable Chromium something real to show throughout the flight window. **A second, disclosed rendering caveat found while re-verifying with the poster wired in**: the poster now shows correctly, but as a visible black square with Lumo inside it rather than blending transparently — confirmed via direct `getComputedStyle` inspection that `mix-blend-mode:screen` genuinely computes as applied to the video element, so this is not a CSS authoring mistake; it's very likely a software/headless-rendering-specific quirk in how this sandbox's Chromium composites a `<video>` element's `poster`-fallback paint against `mix-blend-mode` (a well-established, widely-used web technique in real GPU-accelerated browsers), the same class of environment limitation as the H.264-decode gap itself — disclosed here rather than either quietly shipping unverified or over-engineering a canvas/chroma-key alternative to work around one sandbox's own rendering path. The settled, crossfaded-to static-portrait state (the actual steady-state look, reachable and screenshot-confirmed in this sandbox) composites correctly with no such artifact, since a plain `<img>` has no poster/decode-fallback state to trip over. Verified via a new 10-assertion Playwright suite (the video mounts with the correct real src; the static portrait stays pending/invisible the whole time it plays; `.play()` was genuinely called on this specific video, via a monkey-patched play-call spy; the video is removed from the DOM after the crossfade; the static portrait settles and becomes clearly visible; the stage reaches its idle state; zero unexpected console errors; reduced motion never creates the video at all and settles immediately) plus a full re-run of the entire pre-existing Gateway regression suite (41 assertions: 21 Traveller-path — with two of its own global `.play()`-call-count assertions, A7/A12/A13, re-scoped from a blanket call counter to a Gate-video-specific one, `window.__gatePlayCalls`, since the new Lumo video now also legitimately calls `.play()` early in Scene 2, well before the Gate's own Awaken-beat call — plus 7 Returning-Creator-path and 13 full-screen-coverage assertions, all passing unchanged since none of them depended on Lumo's own arrival mechanism) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected — this sprint touches zero Builder files). No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `js/gatewaySequence.js`, `css/style.css`, and one new poster image asset, with a matching cache-bust version bump on both stylesheet `<link>` tags in `index.html`.)

- Egg and Lumo Removed From the Gate Scene — Lumo Now Interacts With the Traveller Only After the Doors Open (a real, deliberate restructuring: "remove egg and lumo from the scene. let it be just the gate. welcome traveller and open the gate. in next scene let lumo interact with the traveller." The prior "Lumo Guards the Gate" model mounted the Gate, the Story Egg, and Lumo all together the instant the sequence began (Scene 2), with Lumo standing beside the Gate for the entire opening/journey/arrival/awaken sequence and the Egg brightening at Awaken alongside Lumo's own wing-raise — this sprint pulls both out of that scene entirely and gives Lumo a genuinely new, later scene of its own. **Scene 2 becomes Gate-only, and synchronous**: `mountGates(video)` dropped its `egg` parameter and all Egg DOM creation outright (`.gateway-egg-wrap`/`.gateway-egg-portrait` CSS removed as now-genuinely-dead code, including their reduced-motion counterparts); `resolveEgg()` — no longer called anywhere in this file — was deleted entirely, matching this codebase's own "if unused, delete completely" discipline (the Story Egg remains a real, separate concept, resolved independently by `js/companionDirector.js` once the Hall itself boots — this file never referenced it as anything but a cinematic presence within the Gateway to begin with, per its own header comment). Since nothing async needs resolving to show the Gate alone, the old `Promise.all([resolveLumo(),resolveEgg()])` wait is gone too — the Gate now mounts the moment `begin()` starts, with zero async delay before the very first paint, one step faster than before. **Scene 3's greeting/recognition lines are completely unchanged** (`GREETING_LINES`/`RETURNING_LINES`, still "Welcome, Traveller."/"Welcome home." etc.) — they now play as a voice heard, not witnessed, since nobody is on screen but the Gate itself; "the only difference is what happens before the gates open" still holds exactly as documented. **Scenes 4-6 (Approach/Journey/Arrival/Awaken) proceed with the Gate entirely alone** — `playGateAwaken(gateEls,reduced,onDone)` dropped its `lumoRef` parameter and the wing-raise/Egg-brighten toggles it used to fire; the magic sparks and rune-ignite halo pulse still fire exactly as before, now read as the Gate awakening and opening itself, with nobody beside it — "welcome traveller and open the gate," literally: the doors open on their own. **A new Scene 7 — Lumo Arrives**: once `playGateOpen` finishes (the real Gate footage's own opening motion has completed, via its genuine `ended` event or the existing duration-based fallback), the new `playLumoArrival(onDone)` — nested inside `begin()` so it can write into the same `lumoRef`/`cleanupLumo` closure every other per-scene element already uses, so a tap-to-skip mid-arrival still cleans up correctly — resolves Lumo via the unchanged `resolveLumo()`, calls the completely unmodified `mountLumo()` (the exact flight-video/settle mechanism built for the Lumo-video sprint, only WHEN it's called moved, not how it works), waits a short landing pause, then raises Lumo's wing (`.gateway-lumo-magic`, its CSS re-commented from "opens the gate" to "a welcoming gesture," since the Gate no longer needs Lumo's permission to open) and speaks one of two new, short, distinct arrival lines — `LUMO_ARRIVAL_LINES` ("Well met, Traveller." / "Come — your story is waiting.") for a first-time Traveller, `LUMO_ARRIVAL_RETURNING_LINES` ("It's good to see you again." / "Welcome back to your story.") for a Returning Creator, deliberately warmer and non-redundant with Scene 3's own earlier, unseen introduction. Only then does the existing `playThreshold` (camera dolly + final flash) run, followed by `done()` — the Hall is still never visible before that moment, for anyone, regardless of path, completely unchanged. Degrades gracefully straight to `onDone()` if Lumo's own art can't be resolved at all, matching every other resolution failure in this file. **The big header comment (Scenes 1-7) and every touched function's own inline comments were rewritten to describe the new structure accurately** rather than left describing the superseded "Lumo Guards the Gate" model. Verified via a new 24-assertion Playwright suite (replacing the prior sprint's own now-superseded assertions, which assumed Lumo/Egg mounted in Scene 2) confirming, in order: the Gate mounts alone with zero Egg/Lumo anywhere; the unchanged greeting plays with still nobody visible; Journey/Arrival/Awaken all proceed with no Lumo; magic sparks still fire at Awaken; Lumo mounts only after Scene 7 begins, raises its wing, and speaks the correct new arrival line; the sequence still completes cleanly; the Returning-Creator path shows its own unchanged recognition line and Creator Signature challenge with no Lumo present either, then Lumo arrives afterward with the distinct reunion line; tap-to-skip still completes near-instantly from any point; reduced motion still resolves in a few seconds. The pre-existing full-screen-coverage suite (13 assertions) was updated in the same spirit — its Lumo-visibility checks (previously made during Scene 2's resting state and mid-Arrival) moved to Scene 7, the only point Lumo now genuinely exists, while the Gate's own geometry checks (resting/Journey/Arrival/mobile) are completely unaffected since none of them ever depended on Lumo's presence. The pre-existing Lumo-flying-video suite (10 assertions) needed only its own mount-wait timeout widened to match the new, later mounting point — the video-crossfade mechanics under test are otherwise completely unaffected by when mounting happens. Both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected — this sprint touches zero Builder files) pass unchanged. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `js/gatewaySequence.js` and `css/style.css`, with a matching cache-bust version bump on both stylesheet `<link>` tags in `index.html`.)

- Traveller Path — Single-Video Gate/Lumo Pipeline (a real, hand-supplied clip, `assets/video/gateway/gate-sequence-final.mp4` — added via a direct GitHub upload, 1024×576/24fps/15.2s, its own AAC audio track stripped outright to match every other Gateway video's muted convention — shows the whole "doors alone → Lumo arrives carrying the Story Egg → lands and presents it → picks it back up and carries it through the now-open door" arc in one continuous shot, no compositing needed. `playVideoSegmentTo(video,toS,fallbackMs,reduced,onDone)` (plays from wherever the video sits to a target timestamp, then pauses and snaps `currentTime` exactly to it — `timeupdate` fires irregularly, so the snap guarantees a precise visual landing regardless of when the event actually fired); `playVideoSegmentToEnd(video,fromS,fallbackMs,reduced,onDone)` (seeks to a resume point and plays to the video's real natural `ended` event); both carry a duration-based fallback timer, matching this file's own established `playGateOpen`/`OPEN_FALLBACK_MS` safety discipline, so Studio's boot can never hang behind a stalled decode; `playFinalFlash(reduced,onDone)` (a brief flash reusing the existing `.gateway-threshold-flash` CSS, deliberately with **no** forward camera dolly this time — the video's own final seconds, Lumo carrying the Egg into the light, already read as a camera-through-the-light moment on their own, and stacking a CSS zoom on top would double up rather than add anything). `runTravellerGateway()` chains it all: an extended hold on the closed doors before any playback starts (`GATE_SETTLE_MS` + a new `GATE_HOLD_MS=2000`, added in direct response to "the gate hold can you extend it by 2 more seconds. i dont want lumo to enter as soon as the page has loaded" — ~2.6s total stillness before Segment 1 begins, with the footage's own natural ~2s of doors-alone-no-Lumo playback extending that further) → Segment 1 (0→5s, Lumo lands and sets the Egg down) → pause exactly at 5s, where `GREETING_LINES` now plays **in person**, witnessed over the held frame, rather than heard over an empty screen as it did before this sprint → Segment 2 (resumes at 7.5s, skipping the brief "Lumo crouches to pick the Egg back up" transition, plays to the real natural end) → the brief flash → hand-off. `begin()`'s own session-detection block now also decides which Gate video to preload, since the two paths use genuinely different footage — computed once, synchronously, before either video ever starts downloading. Verified via a new 15-assertion Playwright suite: the new video mounts with zero halo/particles/separate-Lumo-DOM-element; a direct `currentTime` check confirms the hold genuinely keeps playback at frame 0 for ~1.2s after mount; a `play()`-call spy (this sandbox's Chromium can't decode H.264 at all, a standing, already-documented limitation from earlier this session, so real `currentTime` advancement isn't observable — matching the established `lumo_video_test.js` testing pattern) confirms Segment 1 playback was genuinely requested once the hold ends; the pause lands exactly at `currentTime===5` with the greeting bubble showing "Welcome, Traveller."; no Creator Signature challenge appears for a first-time Traveller; resume seeks to exactly `7.5` and requests `play()` a second time; the final flash fires and the sequence hands off cleanly; zero console errors throughout; the Returning Creator path is independently confirmed, in the same suite, to still mount the old `gate-sequence.mp4` with its halo + 5 gather particles and its own unchanged "Welcome home." recognition line. (a 396px-wide bubble) vs 145px for the shorter "I am Lumo." (a 226px-wide bubble) — both genuinely ≈64% of their own bubble's measured width, confirming the scaling actually works even though a screenshot comparison alone hadn't made the difference obvious. - Traveller Greeting Polish — Bigger Type, Gradual Fades, No More Chopped-Off Egg Pickup (four concrete follow-ups on the shipped single-video Traveller pipeline: "make the text appear more polish. Increase the font. let it appear gradually and disappear gradually. right now its abrupts and running very quickly. there is jerk post last text and lumo seems to be abruptly flying. the sequence of him picking up the egg seems to be chopped off." **(1) Font size raised a full step** — `.gateway-greeting-bubble`'s clamp went from `clamp(19px,2.8vw,29px)` to `clamp(24px,3.6vw,38px)`, the subtitle from `clamp(13px,1.6vw,17px)` to `clamp(16px,2vw,21px)`, the mobile breakpoint's own fixed size from 18px to 23px. **(2) The fade itself was redesigned, not just retimed** — the old `gateway-line-in` keyframe spent only ~15%/18% of its own duration on the actual fade (a snap at 300ms/360ms out of a flat 2000ms); the new keyframe (`0%->26%` fade in, hold, `74%->100%` fade out) spends roughly a quarter of the line's own duration on each side, with a longer 18px drift instead of the old faint 10px nudge, and switched from `ease-out` to `ease-in-out` for a smoother glide. Frames 4.5s-6.0s all read as the identical held "standing, wings out, Egg on the ground" pose, so resuming from the exact same timestamp Segment 1 paused at (`RESUME_AT_S=PAUSE_AT_S`, no longer a separate later value) costs nothing visually during the dialogue pause and removes the hard seek entirely — `playVideoSegmentTo()` already snaps the video's own `currentTime` to `PAUSE_AT_S` when it pauses, so resuming from the identical value is a genuine no-op seek: the video simply un-pauses exactly where it left off and the crouch/grab/liftoff/flight now all play in full, continuously, for the first time. Verified via Playwright: font sizes measured directly (38px at a 1280px viewport, up from the old 19-29px range); the fade's own opacity was sampled across the transition window and confirmed to ramp gradually rather than snap; the animation's real computed duration matches `GREETING_LINE_MS` exactly; and — the core fix — the video's second `play()` call now fires with `currentTime===5` (not ~7.5 as before), confirmed via a `play()`-call spy across the whole sequence. The existing 15-assertion Traveller/Returning-Creator pipeline suite (re-timed for the new pacing and its own resume-point assertion corrected to expect the fix rather than the old skip) plus the completion/tap-to-skip sanity checks and both `goldenBuild.js` suites all pass unchanged, zero console errors. - Traveller Privacy — Clear My Projects on a Genuinely New Traveller Session ("another change if the system has identified its a traveller than all the caches should be cleared. traveller should not see projects of previous creators." Investigated the real gap before implementing: `CreatorProjectStore` ("My Projects") uses one flat `localStorage` key (`vihustudio-projects`) with zero scoping by identity — on a shared device, an unclaimed Traveller's own story really does stay visible to whoever opens the browser next, since `MagicCard.list().length===0` (the Traveller Gateway path) is true for both a brand-new device and a previous, still-unclaimed Traveller session. Confirmed the scope directly with the user before touching anything, given the destructive/hard-to-reverse nature of clearing data: **(1) timing** — "the cache clean should only be requested when its entry sequence" — only on a genuinely NEW browser session, never on an in-page reload of an in-progress story; **(2) scope** — My Projects list only, not the current session slot or companion state. Implemented via a new sessionStorage marker, `GATEWAY_SESSION_MARKER` (`'vihu-gateway-session-entered'`) — sessionStorage starts empty in every new tab/window but survives an in-page reload within the same one, exactly matching the required signal. `js/gatewaySequence.js`'s `begin()` now checks this marker immediately after computing `isReturning`: on a genuinely new session (marker absent) where the Traveller path was chosen (not Returning Creator), it calls a new `CreatorProjectStore.clearAll()` (added to `js/creatorProjectStore.js`, wiping the `vihustudio-projects` key outright) before anything else happens; the marker is then set unconditionally (both paths) so the rest of that tab session, including a Returning Creator boot, is correctly treated as "already entered." Verified via a new 5-scenario Playwright suite: a genuinely new Traveller session with a stale previous-Traveller project seeded in `localStorage` gets it wiped to an empty list, with zero console errors; a same-tab-session reload of an in-progress Traveller project is confirmed to NOT be cleared; a Returning Creator boot (a real Magic Card seeded) never clears My Projects under any circumstance. The existing 15-assertion Traveller/Returning-Creator pipeline suite, the completion/tap-to-skip sanity checks, and both `goldenBuild.js` suites all pass unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `js/gatewaySequence.js` and `js/creatorProjectStore.js`, no CSS touched, so no cache-bust bump was needed.)

Full regression across the entire existing Gateway/Magic-Card/Creator Playwright suite (`gw_final_video_test.js` 15/15, `gw_returning_unified_test.js` 18/18, `gw_completion_check.js`, `gateway_skip_check.js`, `gw_myprojects_clear_check.js` 5/5, `gw_smoke_handoff.js` 6/6) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected — this fix touches zero Builder files) pass unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; no CSS changes were needed, so no cache-bust bump was required this time; confined to `js/gatewaySequence.js` and `js/magicCardUI.js`.)

- Traveller Unpublished-Work Notice + World Card Constellation Crossing-Lines Fix ("1st for a traveller who once start creating. we need to tell if they do not publish their creation might get lost. this will help us in keeping data clean. second the star marker grid needs rework. it cannot mark any constellation which has crossing lines. check the stars assigned to vihupapa. the constellation is in shape of number 4." Two independent fixes. **(1) Traveller Save Notice**: new `js/travellerSaveNotice.js` — a small floating toast, deliberately NOT slotted into `.workspace`'s own fixed `calc(100vh - 64px)` grid (this codebase has hit that exact class of height-overflow bug more than once when a new sibling was added there) — shown only when ALL of: no Magic Card is active (`MagicCard.getActive()` falsy — a Traveller, not a Creator, who already has real Cloud Backup via their claimed card), the active project has at least one real page ("once start creating" — `AppState.slides.length>0`), it hasn't already been published this browser tab session, and it wasn't dismissed this tab session (`sessionStorage`, so it reappears on a genuinely new session, matching the exact "reappears next session" convention the Traveller Privacy sprint's own `CreatorProjectStore.clearAll()` already established rather than a permanent, one-time-forever dismiss). Reads "You're creating as a Traveller — publish your adventure (or claim your Magic Card) to make sure it's kept safe." with a "📖 Publish Now" button (clicks the real `#publishBtn`) and a dismiss "✕" — both buttons needed explicit `!important` width/height/margin overrides to escape this codebase's own established global `button:not(...){width:100%;margin-bottom:12px}` cascade rule, the same recurring bug class already fixed for Object Strip cards/the Publish Studio close button/Doodle's pen swatches. A thin host-binding module (`configure({...})`, matching the `js/objectStrip.js`/`js/contextPanel.js`/`js/pageRuntime.js` pattern) — wired in `js/app.js`, refreshed from `js/pageRuntime.js`'s own `PageRuntime.notify()` (the real choke point every meaningful Workspace mutation already calls, so no per-event wiring of its own was needed beyond one `configure()` call) and from `js/magicCardUI.js`'s `refreshHeaderBadge()` (every moment a Traveller may have just become a Creator — claim/rename/rehydrate/boot — needs this gate re-checked immediately, not on the next unrelated page notify); `js/publishStudio.js`'s `_finalizePublish()` calls `TravellerSaveNotice.markPublished()` the instant a real Publish succeeds, hiding it for the rest of the session since there's nothing left to nag about. **(2) World Card Constellation Fix**: a real, reported bug in `js/cardPlatform.js`'s and `js/magicCard.js`'s shared `CONSTELLATIONS` table — every connecting-line drawer in this codebase (`js/magicCardArt.js`'s `drawBack`, `js/magicCardUI.js`'s `_renderConstellation`) draws a straight line between each consecutive pair of points in the array's own order, and CYGNUS's original order (Top, Center, Bottom, Left, Right) drew its last segment (Left-to-Right) straight back through the Center point a second time — exactly the overlapping "number 4"-looking defect reported on a real claimed card. Confirmed via a real segment-intersection algorithm (orientation + `onSegment` checks, not eyeballed) before touching anything: the other four constellations (Orion/Cassiopeia/Ursa Major/Lyra) were already crossing-free in their base order and stayed that way — only CYGNUS had a genuine defect. Fixed by reordering to Top, Center, Left, Bottom, Right — traces the identical five points with zero self-crossing or vertex pass-through, verified (not just reasoned) to stay crossing-free across every one of `_placeConstellation()`'s 4-rotation × mirror-on/off combinations too, since a rotation/reflection/translation never changes whether two line segments cross. Both files kept in lockstep, matching this codebase's own established duplication discipline for this exact pair of modules. Verified via a new Node geometry script confirming: the original CYGNUS order reproduces a real, detected crossing; every constellation in both its base order and all 8 rotate/mirror combinations is crossing-free after the fix; a live Playwright screenshot of `MagicCardArt.drawBack()` rendering the fixed CYGNUS pattern shows a clean, non-overlapping kite/arrow shape instead of the old overlapping tangle. A new 15-assertion Playwright suite for the notice (a fresh Traveller with zero pages sees nothing; it appears once a real page exists; dismissing hides it and persists across an in-page reload but reappears on a genuinely new session; a claimed Creator never sees it even with real pages; `markPublished()` hides it) all pass, plus full regression across the existing Gateway/Magic-Card Playwright suite (`gw_final_video_test.js` 15/15, `gw_returning_unified_test.js` 18/18, `gw_completion_check.js`, `gateway_skip_check.js`, `gw_myprojects_clear_check.js` 5/5, `gw_smoke_handoff.js` 6/6, `gw_decline_choice_test.js` 11/11) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected — neither fix touches Builder files) pass unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to a new `js/travellerSaveNotice.js` plus `js/app.js`, `js/pageRuntime.js`, `js/magicCardUI.js`, `js/publishStudio.js`, `css/style.css`, `index.html`, `js/cardPlatform.js`, and `js/magicCard.js`.)

- Constellation Crossing-Lines Fix — Retroactive Repair for Already-Claimed Cards ("can you show me whats the pattern for vihupapa now" — while confirming the fix, found the `CONSTELLATIONS.CYGNUS` reorder only helps NEW claims: `MagicCard.claim()` stores a card's real pattern permanently at claim time (`js/magicCard.js`'s `pattern:placed.pattern`), never re-derived from the `CONSTELLATIONS` table on later renders, so an already-claimed CYGNUS card (like a real "vihupapa" card claimed before the previous fix shipped) would have kept showing the old, self-crossing order forever with no way to reach it. Fixed with a real, one-time repair: a new `_migrateCygnusOrder(cards)` runs inside `js/magicCard.js`'s `_readCards()` — every time cards are read from `localStorage`, any CYGNUS card with a 5-point pattern and no `constellationOrderFixed` flag gets its stored points reordered via `[p[0],p[1],p[3],p[2],p[4]]`, the exact same index permutation the base array's own Top/Center/Bottom/Left/Right → Top/Center/Left/Bottom/Right reorder applied — correct regardless of which random rotation/mirror the card got at claim time, since `_rotate`/`_mirrorHorizontal`/`_shiftToOrigin` are all plain `.map()` calls that never change array order (index 0 is always the transformed "Top" point, etc, for every card). Same stars, same position, only the connect-the-dots order changes — `recall_magic_card()` already matches a tapped pattern order-independently, so this can never affect whether a real device can still recall the card. Gated by the one-time flag so it runs exactly once per card and never re-touches an already-correct pattern from a claim made after the previous fix shipped (verified idempotent via two consecutive reads). Verified via a new Playwright check seeding a real pre-fix-shaped card (`constellation:'CYGNUS'`, the old defective pattern, no fix flag, nickname "vihupapa") and confirming: the migration runs automatically on load, the repaired pattern matches the corrected order exactly, a second reload doesn't re-touch it, and `MagicCardArt.drawBack()` renders the repaired card as a clean, non-overlapping kite/arrow shape (screenshotted) instead of the old "number 4" tangle. Disclosed honestly: I don't have access to the user's own real, live claimed card — Magic Cards are 100% client-side by design, stored only in the user's own browser — so this fix means the next time they open the app in their own browser, their real card's stored pattern gets silently, automatically, and permanently repaired with zero action needed from them. Full regression: `gw_decline_choice_test.js` 11/11, `traveller_save_notice_test.js` 15/15, `gw_returning_unified_test.js` 18/18, and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected — this fix touches zero Builder files) all pass unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `js/magicCard.js`.)

- Traveller Save Notice — Repositioned Out of the Object Strip's Way, Copy Corrected (two real, user-reported fixes on a real screenshot of a live Workspace: "we need to reposition this. or allow traveller to reposition this. also why we are saying claim magic card as there is no other way to claim the card." **(1) Reposition**: the notice originally rendered as a `position:fixed` toast anchored to the viewport bottom-center — the screenshot showed it visually colliding with the Object Strip's own cards and scroll-arrow buttons at the bottom of the canvas column. Rather than build a user-facing drag-to-reposition control (the alternative the user themselves floated, mirroring the Companion widget's own draggable behaviour), the simpler, more robust fix was to stop floating it at all: `js/travellerSaveNotice.js`'s `_ensureDom()` now mounts the notice as a normal, in-flow element — specifically the very FIRST child of `.right-sidebar` — instead of appending to `document.body` with fixed positioning. `.right-sidebar` already has `overflow-y:auto` (a safe container for new in-flow content) and the notice sits ahead of `#contextPanelRoot`, so it's never wiped by `ContextPanel.refresh()`'s own frequent `panelRoot.innerHTML=''` calls, which only ever touch `#contextPanelRoot`'s own children, not its siblings. A first attempt inserted the notice "right after `.tabs`" (mirroring where `ContextPanel.init()` itself inserts `#contextPanelRoot`) — this turned out to be a real, boot-order-dependent bug, caught by a Playwright DOM-order check before shipping: if `TravellerSaveNotice.refresh()`'s first call happened to run before `ContextPanel.init()` (which it does, in the real boot sequence), the notice would insert itself right after `.tabs` first, and `ContextPanel.init()`'s own later `insertBefore(panelRoot, tabsEl.nextSibling)` call would then insert `#contextPanelRoot` BEFORE the already-present notice — silently pushing the safety notice down below the entire Context Panel instead of above it. Fixed by dropping the `.tabs`-relative logic entirely in favour of always inserting as `.right-sidebar`'s unconditional first child — simpler, and immune to any future ordering change between the two modules' own initialization. `css/style.css`'s `.traveller-save-notice*` rules were rewritten from a floating toast (fixed position, translateX centering, a horizontal icon+text+buttons row) into a normal sidebar card (a `margin-bottom` sitting in the section-gap flow, a stacked icon+text+dismiss row on top with a full-width "📖 Publish Now" button beneath) — the same recurring `button:not(...){width:100%;margin-bottom:12px}` global-cascade override discipline this codebase has fixed repeatedly (Object Strip cards, the Publish Studio close button, Doodle's pen swatches) still applies to both buttons, just with different explicit widths now that the layout is vertical rather than horizontal. **(2) Copy correction**: the notice previously read "...publish your adventure (or claim your Magic Card) to make sure it's kept safe" — factually misleading, since there is no independent, separately-reachable way to claim a Magic Card; the ONLY path is `MagicCard.shouldOfferAwakening()`'s own ceremony, offered automatically the instant a first Publish actually succeeds (`js/publishStudio.js`'s `_finalizePublish`). Reworded to name exactly one real action: "You're creating as a Traveller. Publish your adventure to make sure it's kept safe." — no longer implying "publish OR claim" are two independent choices, since claiming is a downstream consequence of publishing, not an alternative to it. Verified via a new 12-assertion Playwright suite (`tsn_reposition_check.js`, scratch-only) confirming the notice mounts inside `.right-sidebar` (not `document.body`), is genuinely NOT `position:fixed`, has real non-zero layout size, does not visually overlap the Object Strip's own bounding rect, is the true first child of `.right-sidebar`, the corrected copy no longer mentions "claim your Magic Card" while still mentioning Publish, and both buttons (Publish Now / Dismiss) remain fully functional from the new location — plus a full re-run of the original 15-assertion `traveller_save_notice_test.js` suite (whose own `pushOnePageAndNotify` test helper needed one matching fix: it previously only hid `#creationFlowOverlay` without removing `body.creation-flow-active`, an incomplete stand-in for the real `_finish()`/`_closeOverlay()` sequence that never mattered while the notice was a fixed-position toast outside `#app`'s own `display:none` gating, but does matter now that the notice lives inside `.right-sidebar`, a real `#app` descendant) — all 15 pass unchanged. Full regression across the entire existing Gateway/Magic-Card Playwright suite (`gw_final_video_test.js` 15/15, `gw_returning_unified_test.js` 18/18, `gw_completion_check.js`, `gateway_skip_check.js`, `gw_myprojects_clear_check.js` 5/5, `gw_smoke_handoff.js` 6/6, `gw_decline_choice_test.js` 11/11) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected) pass unchanged, zero console errors. No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `js/travellerSaveNotice.js` and `css/style.css`.)

- Creator Signature Tap Board — Legible, Kid-Friendly Rework (a real, user-supplied screenshot showed the "Lumo, the Gatekeeper" constellation tap challenge with almost every one of its 100 grid cells fully invisible — "fix this screen also. very difficult to show the stars," followed by a direct product correction mid-fix: "think kids. its not easy for kids. they need fun not a test." **Root cause**: only a sparse, randomly-chosen ~22% subset of cells (`js/magicCardUI.js`'s `_gateBuildGrid`, the `--decoy` class) ever showed any glow at all — the remaining ~78% were fully `color:transparent`, so on a touch device (no `:hover` at all before the tap itself) a kid had no visual cue where most of the 100 tappable positions even were. **Fixed by making every cell visible, uniformly, at rest** — the sparse decoy/invisible split is removed entirely (`_gateBuildGrid` no longer computes a `decoySet` at all; every cell gets the identical base `.magic-card-tapgrid-cell` class), and `css/style.css`'s base cell rule changed from `color:transparent`/`font-size:15px` to a real, legible `color:rgba(255,255,255,.34)` with a soft `text-shadow` glow and `font-size:20px` — a genuine improvement on the original "camouflage" idea, not a trade-off against it: with every cell now identical at rest, there's no visible subset left to distinguish from "real" positions, so a shoulder-surfer watching a real tap sequence still can't tell a genuine tap from the rest of the now-uniformly-dim starfield around it. Added a real `:active` state (`rgba(255,255,255,.9)`, `scale(1.15)`) alongside the existing `:hover`, since touch devices often skip `:hover` entirely and need their own immediate tap feedback. The board's own width cap grew from 460px to 520px (`.magic-card-tapgrid-boardwrap`) for bigger, friendlier touch targets — safe to grow, since `_fitBoardToAvailableSpace()` already shrinks it back down on any viewport too short to fit it. Each cell also gained a gentle, randomized twinkle (`magicCardStarTwinkle`, a pure `opacity` keyframe independent of the `color` alpha channel so it never fights the hover/active/selected transitions; per-cell `animation-delay`/`animation-duration` set inline in `_gateBuildGrid` via `Math.random()` so the whole board twinkles out of sync like a real sky, not one flat uniform pulse; fully disabled under `prefers-reduced-motion`). **The "fun not a test" correction went beyond legibility into the interaction and copy itself**: (1) every subtitle on this screen ("Tap your stars, in order, to continue.") dropped "in order" — a real, previously-unnoticed correctness gap, not just a tone fix: both the local `_patternsMatch` check and the real `recall_magic_card()` RPC have always compared taps as an unordered SET, never a sequence, so telling a kid to remember a strict order was needless pressure for a rule that was never actually enforced. (2) the button and status copy were softened from clinical pass/fail wording to this screen's own established "sky" language (matching Magic Card Home's existing "your sky is alive") — "✨ Confirm" → "✨ That's My Sky!"; "Checking…" → "✨ Looking for your sky…"; "✓ Welcome back!" → "✨ Found it! Welcome back!"; "✗ Not quite — try again." → "Not quite — let's try again! 🌟" (no more ✗ marks reading as a wrong-answer buzzer); "Tap at least two stars first." → "Tap a couple of stars first! ✨". Verified via a new 16-assertion Playwright suite (`tapgrid_visibility_check.js`, scratch-only): all 100 cells render with real, identical, non-zero rest opacity (no invisible subset, no `--decoy` class anywhere); font-size genuinely bumped; the real tap-select/connecting-line/counter mechanics still work end to end; the subtitle no longer says "in order" while still mentioning stars; the confirm button uses the new "sky" wording; a real wrong-guess shows the softened error text with no ✗ mark; every cell carries the twinkle animation with genuinely randomized per-cell timing; zero console errors. Full regression across the entire existing Gateway/Magic-Card Playwright suite (`gw_final_video_test.js` 15/15, `gw_completion_check.js`, `gateway_skip_check.js`, `gw_myprojects_clear_check.js` 5/5, `gw_smoke_handoff.js` 6/6, `gw_decline_choice_test.js` 11/11, `traveller_save_notice_test.js` 15/15, `tsn_reposition_check.js` 12/12) and both `goldenBuild.js` suites (World Builder v1 and v2, unaffected) pass unchanged, zero console errors; `gw_returning_unified_test.js`'s own `button:has-text("Confirm")` selector needed updating to the stable `.magic-card-tapgrid-confirm` class — the intended, disclosed consequence of the copy rename, not a regression (18/18 after the fix). No Theme Contract/Engine V2 Scene Model/Builder/Creator Governing Rules change; confined to `js/magicCardUI.js` and `css/style.css`.)

## Locked Product Decisions

### 1. Workspace Simplification

- Hide Project Title, Author and editable Book Name from the editor.
- Preserve metadata in the project model.

### 2. Asset Pack System

- Decorations use installable packs.
- Local import first.
- Cloud repository later.
- Design for reusable pack architecture.

### 3. Card Designer

Reusable component supporting:

- Image scale
- Image position
- Fit modes
- Typography
- Card styling
- Theme defaults with per-card overrides

### 4. Audio Studio

- Per-card narration
- Record/import audio
- Audio linked to cards
- Foundation for narrated exports

### 5. Social-First Export

Priority:

1. Instagram Carousel
2. Instagram Reel

### 6. Creator Governing Rules

Five permanent rules for Creator, stated by the product owner and binding on every future Creator change. When something looks wrong in Creator, check it against these first — every real bug found and fixed since they were stated has mapped to a violation of one of them.

1. **Fidelity** — "When Scene shows up in Creator it is exactly as it was in Builder." Nothing about a Scene's geometry, layout, or content is silently discarded or substituted on the way into Creator.
2. **Guardrails** — "Every object on Scene honors the guardrails." Whatever the Theme Author marked moveable/editable/visible for an object is respected in Creator, with no exceptions.
3. **Refinement** — "Creator can further refine the objects through options available in the right panel." Whatever an object's guardrails do allow a Story Author to touch must have a real, reachable control in the Context Panel, not just a theoretical capability.
4. **Personalization** — "Creator provide options to personalize the scene." Beyond fixing what's broken, Creator's job is to give the Story Author genuine ways to make each Scene their own, within whatever room the guardrails leave.
5. **Publish Fidelity** — "Publish should honour the runtime view of center pane of Creator." Whatever the center pane (the live editing canvas) shows while a Story Author is working — every object, every edit, every guardrail-respecting placement — is exactly what Publish must produce. Publish is never allowed to reconstruct, reinterpret, or fall back to a different rendering path than the one the center pane already proved correct.

## Roadmap

1. Theme Designer Polish
2. Card Designer
3. Story Designer
4. Cover Designer
5. CTA Designer
6. Audio Studio
7. Asset Pack System
8. Export Studio
9. VihuPipe

## Development Rules

- Keep prompts minimal.
- Never refactor architecture without approval.
- Prefer extending reusable components.
- Preserve backward compatibility.
- Keep commits focused and atomic.
- Update CLAUDE.md whenever a major architectural or product decision is approved.
